# run-kit UI Patterns

## URL Structure

| Route | View | Component Pattern |
|-------|------|-------------------|
| `/` | Host-page host-console home | Standalone page (`HostOverviewPage`) — `flex-col h-full`. The root layout owns viewport height and the shared TopBar mounts once at the persistent root layout above the outlet, NOT pinned by this page — `HostOverviewPage` registers `isConnected: hostMetricsConnected` into the slot context (§ Chrome (Top Bar) → persistent root mount). Zones in order: HOST HEALTH → BOARDS → TMUX SERVERS → SERVICES (each a `[ LABEL▊ ]────` `SectionHeading`); the Host page's page identity is the solo `Host` heading in the top-bar center cell, plus the in-page `Host Overview` SectionHeading at the top of the scroll container (§ Page Overview Headings). No sidebar and no Shell grid. `/` carries live host data — the server-independent host-metrics subscription opens here (a `metrics` subscription on the shared state socket; no per-server subscription is attached, which is why the Host-page TopBar drives its connection dot from `hostMetricsConnected` rather than a per-server slice). The tile grid + count/loading line render from SessionContext's `servers`/`serversLoaded` so the "+" create path shares the pending-marker → `ServerWaiting` → auto-swap lifecycle (§ Create-server lifecycle). See § HOST HEALTH Zone, § BOARDS Zone, § Chrome (Top Bar). |
| `/$server` | Session-tiles density view | `AppShell` layout with `SessionTiles` content. SSE connected to the specified server. See § Session Tiles. |
| `/$server/$window` | Terminal / Iframe / Chat | `AppShell` layout. The second segment is the **numeric part** of the stable tmux **window ID** (`@N` sans `@`, e.g. `/testServer/0`) — the window ID (`@N`) is the identity everywhere in code/params/API, restored from the segment by the route's idempotent parse. `$session` is not in the route (`@N` is server-global, so the session is redundant); the session name shown in chrome is derived from the active window's SSE snapshot, not a URL segment. The address bar carries `/{server}/{N}` — the `@` is dropped for display, NOT percent-encoded. Old bookmarked `/{server}/%40N` deep links still resolve: the decoded segment `@N` passes through the idempotent parse unchanged (never `@@N`). Rendering branch: the renderer is selected by the **resolved view** — `chat` renders `ChatView`, `web` renders `IframeWindow` (URL bar + iframe), otherwise `TerminalClient` + `BottomBar` (see § Window Views (Lens Model)). The route also carries a validated `?view=web|chat` search param (per-viewer lens state). SSE connected. 3-segment `/$server/$session/$window` URLs are a hard break (no redirect shim). |
| `/board/$name` | Pane board (cross-server) | `BoardPage` shares the `<Shell>` grid wrapper with AppShell — sidebar / `<TopBar mode="board">` / pane-row content / shared `<BottomBar>`. Retains its own `<CommandPalette>` mount for board-route-only entries. Peer to `/$server`, NOT under it — boards aggregate windows across multiple tmux servers. Invalid `name` (fails `^[A-Za-z0-9_-]{1,32}$`) renders `NotFoundPage`. See § Boards View. |

Two-tier URL model (`/$server/$window`) with server always in path (no `$session` middle segment). URLs are fully shareable — copying a URL and opening it elsewhere on the same host opens the same server and window (the session is re-derived from the snapshot). TanStack Router uses nested routes: `/$server` is a layout route (`serverLayoutRoute`) whose component (`ServerShell`) wraps `SessionProvider` + `AppShell`; the terminal child route is `path: "/$window"` and uses the paired `params: { parse, stringify }` API to serialize the single `window` param (no `session`) as its numeric part in the URL. The two directions are the exported pure helpers `windowIdToUrlSegment` (stringify — strips the leading `@`) and `urlSegmentToWindowId` (parse — idempotently prepends `@`) in `router.tsx`; parse restores the `@N` form so every `params.window` consumer keeps receiving `@N`. Child routes (server index and terminal) are matched by the router but rendered conditionally by `AppShell` based on whether the `window` param exists. (`260529-jad6`, `260703-8mpy`)

**Canonical page names** — the spoken/documentation vocabulary for referring to each route. Use these names in conversation, PRs, and docs instead of the raw path patterns. A mirror of this glossary is a comment beside the `routeTree` definition in `app/frontend/src/router.tsx`. (`260702-nuup`, `260715-zs1y`)

| Route path | Canonical name | Component |
|------------|----------------|-----------|
| `/` | **Host** | `HostOverviewPage` (global home / server list; also the host-console HOST HEALTH zone, PR #290) |
| `/$server` | **tmux Server** | `ServerShell` (a single server's view; the `resolveServerView` route guard runs here) |
| `/$server/$window` | **Terminal** | *(inherited layout — no dedicated component)* (a specific window `@N`) |
| `/board/$name` | **Board** | `BoardPage` (lazy) (cross-server pane board) |
| not-found fallback | **Not Found** | `NotFoundPage` (root `notFoundComponent` catch-all — not a registered path) |

The `$server` / `$window` / `$name` segments are **route params** (actual server names, window ids, board names), not literal path segments.

**Vocabulary split** — **every** route surfaces a `PageType: name` identity heading in the top-bar CENTER cell (`Window: <window>` — static in every lens, `Board: <board>`, `tmux Server: <server>`, solo `Host`) — the canonical page type is the two-tone prefix, the instance name is the subject (§ Chrome (Top Bar) center cell). Page identity lives in the chrome, not the page body. The split reads: **the left breadcrumb ends at the PARENT** (server / session — *the trail to here*), **the centered heading is the current-page leaf** naming both the page type and the instance (*what & where you are*), so a name never appears twice in one bar (move-don't-copy — § Chrome (Top Bar), § Section Heading). The bracket idiom names the in-page **section** labels (the tmux Server page's `Sessions`, the four Host-page zones) via the shared `SectionHeading` (§ Section Heading). (`260702-6m46`, `260704-pr0p`, `260714-uco1`, `260715-zs1y`)

**Window identity is the tmux window ID (`@N`), not the index**, and **`@N` is the *only* window identity carried by the URL** — the URL *segment* carries only `@N`'s numeric part (`@N` sans `@`), restored to `@N` by the route's idempotent parse (see the `/$server/$window` route-table row above). The `$window` route param holds a stable `@N` string; all URL/API/relay/tmux layers address a specific window by this ID, while the window *index* is retained only for positional reorder/move. The owning **session name is derived from the active window's SSE snapshot** (locating `@N` within `sessions[].windows[]`), not read from the URL — `app.tsx` computes `currentSession = sessions.find(s => s.windows.some(w => w.windowId === windowParam))` and `sessionName = currentSession?.name`. Index-based bookmarked URLs (`/$server/$session/3`) AND session-bearing URLs (`/$server/$session/@N`) are a **hard break** — they do not resolve (no redirect shim; constitution §II — ephemeral URLs, no persistent state). See `architecture.md` § API Layer and `tmux-sessions.md` § Window addressing identity for the cross-layer contract. (`260529-chgz`, `260529-jad6`, `260703-8mpy`)

Server not found: if the `$server` segment doesn't match any known tmux server, a "Server not found" page renders with a link to `/`. A 3-segment URL does not match the 2-segment terminal route and falls through to the `NotFoundPage` / server-dashboard fallback.

**Three-way route guard (view / waiting / not-found)** — the `$server` segment is resolved by a pure exported helper `resolveServerView(server, servers, pendingServer, serversLoaded)` in `app.tsx` returning `"view" | "waiting" | "not-found"`. The branches: (a) `server` IN `servers` → `"view"` (render the server view); (b) NOT in list AND `server === pendingServer` → `"waiting"` (render `ServerWaiting`, a sibling of `ServerNotFound`); (c) NOT in list AND `server !== pendingServer` AND `serversLoaded` → `"not-found"` (render `ServerNotFound` immediately, so a typo'd URL still fails fast); (d) otherwise (e.g. before the first fetch resolves) → `"view"`, falling through to the server view / loading rather than flashing not-found. The guard keys on the explicit `serversLoaded` flag, **NOT** the `servers.length > 0` proxy (§ Design Decisions → Route guard keys on `serversLoaded`). The `pendingServer` waiting state applies only to the one server the user just created. `ServerWaiting` reuses `ServerNotFound`'s centered idiom (`flex flex-col items-center justify-center h-full gap-4 bg-bg-primary` — `h-full`, so these edge pages fit the content region below the persistent TopBar without overflow) + the shared `LogoSpinner`, showing a brief "Creating server… / Waiting for `<name>`" message. (`260602-3i5d`)

**Create-server → pending-marker → waiting-then-view lifecycle** — `SessionContext` (`app/frontend/src/contexts/session-context.tsx`) carries the transient state for this: `pendingServer: string \| null`, `markServerPending(name)` (an empty-string argument is the clear sentinel → sets `null`), and `serversLoaded: boolean` (set `true` in `fetchServers()`'s `finally`, so it counts as loaded even on an empty list or a caught fetch error — a permanently-false flag would hang the not-found branch forever). All three are threaded through the context type, the live provider value, and the `StandaloneSessionContextProvider` test fallback as safe no-ops/defaults. **BOTH server-create entry points drive this identical flow** — the waiting state is entry-point-agnostic: (1) the in-app **AppShell** "Server: Create" dialog (`handleCreateServer` in `app.tsx`), and (2) the `/` home-page **`HostOverviewPage`** "+ New Server" (`handleCreate` in `host-overview-page.tsx`). Each: calls `markServerPending(trimmed)` then navigates to `/$server`; its create `useOptimisticAction` fires `refreshServers()` from `onAlwaysSettled` (unmount-safe — the create dialog unmounts on navigation but the hook-owning component's root-level `SessionContext` stays mounted; the refresh touches only that) and clears the pending marker via `onAlwaysRollback` (`markServerPending("")`) so a failed create never strands the UI on the waiting state. `HostOverviewPage`'s displayed list reads SessionContext's `servers`/`serversLoaded` (the same source the guard reads, so page-display and guard-check cannot diverge) while keeping its local `ghostServers` optimistic tiles and the Host-page HOST HEALTH zone (§ HOST HEALTH Zone). `pendingServer` is auto-cleared by an effect **in SessionContext** (not in `app.tsx`) once the refreshed `servers` list contains it — event-driven on the list changing, with **no timer and no polling** (§ Design Decisions → No bounded-fallback timer on the waiting state). (`260602-3i5d`, `260701-f4e5`)

**Server-list fetch lifecycle**: the server list (`servers`, from `listServers()` → `GET /api/servers`) is a **one-time fetch on `SessionProvider` mount + explicit `refreshServers()`** — it is **NOT** part of the per-server SSE stream (SSE streams per-server *sessions*/order/metrics/board-changed only, never the list of servers). So a newly-created server does not appear until `refreshServers()` is called; the create flow above is what triggers that refresh. The `server-gone` event (below) is the symmetric *removal* trigger — it likewise drives a `refreshServers()` re-query rather than carrying the list inline.

Kill/not-found redirects go to `/$server` (server dashboard), not `/` (server list). The user stays in their server context.

### Server-Gone Reap → not-found flip (in-band `gone` event + connection-loss fallback)

The backend signals a server whose tmux socket is gone right before reaping it from the poll set — see `tmux-sessions.md` § SSE Poll-Set Lifecycle. This rides the state socket as an in-band `gone` frame (`{"op":"gone","kind":"server","key":"<server>","reason":"server-exited"}`; the `key` names the server since one socket carries every server). There is **no new HTTP endpoint or component** (Constitution IX) — it reuses the one state socket and the existing `not-found` route guard. (`260603-gs2t`, `260716-qf3j`)

`SessionProvider` (`app/frontend/src/contexts/session-context.tsx`) routes it through the `StateSocket`'s `onGone(key)` callback. The handler: drop the server from `ackedServersRef` (its dot goes disconnected) and from `subscribedServersRef`, call `socketRef.current.unsubscribeServer(key)` to **release the StateSocket ref-count** (so the diff effect can re-subscribe cleanly if the server is later restored while still attached — see `architecture.md` § State Socket → `onGone`), delete the server's slice from `slicesByServer`, then call `fetchServers()` (the `useCallback` that `refreshServers` aliases). The now-dead server is already absent from `GET /api/servers` (enumeration is socket-file-based and self-healing), so the refreshed list **shrinks**, and if the user is currently viewing that server `resolveServerView(server, servers, pendingServer, serversLoaded)` flips to `"not-found"` (`serversLoaded` is already `true` post-mount), rendering the existing `ServerNotFound` view. This extends the three-way route guard (§ above): the same `not-found` branch that catches a typo'd URL also catches a reaped server.

**Connection-loss fallback** (belt-and-suspenders): a catastrophic socket death the backend can't signal (no poll tick lands, or the daemon is mid-restart) is covered by the socket-level disconnect debounce — the state socket's `onConnectionChange(false)` clears each acked server's `isConnected` after the 3s debounce, and the provider's server-list refresh path (a `fetchServers()` on reconnect / list change) still shrinks the list, so the guard-flip path fires even with no `gone` frame. The two paths are idempotent and **first-to-fire wins**: the `gone` frame is the fast path (sub-second), the connection-loss refresh is the guaranteed-eventual path. If the server is in fact still alive, the refreshed list still contains it and no flip occurs.

### URL as Resumable Bookmark

**tmux is the sole source of truth for "current window" per server.** The URL is a **resumable bookmark** — consulted on initial mount (and reload), then treated as derived state that follows tmux. Two contracts:

1. **Mount-time alignment (one-shot)**. On the first SSE payload after a route mounts, `app.tsx` compares the URL's `$window` window ID (`windowParam`, a `@N` string) to `currentSession.windows.find(w => w.isActiveWindow)?.windowId`. If they differ, it fires exactly one `selectWindow(server, urlWindowId)` to align tmux to the URL — `selectWindow` takes `(server, windowId)`, no session, since a window ID is a self-contained tmux target (and the backend `/select` handler derives the owning session for group disambiguation; see `architecture.md` § API Layer). Guarded by `hasAlignedToUrlRef: useRef(false)` keyed on the `${server}|${windowParam}` key (window-id-only — `$session` is not in the URL, so it is not part of the alignment key). Subsequent route changes to the same window never re-fire alignment. This supports reload (URL=active is a no-op) and deep-link (URL≠active aligns tmux, then yanks any other tabs on the same server per multi-client convergence). Since the compared identifier is the stable `@N`, a reorder/kill that shifts indices never spuriously triggers re-alignment.

2. **URL writeback (continuous)**. A separate effect watches the SSE-derived `activeWindow` and calls `navigate({ replace: true, to: "/$server/$window", params: { server, window: activeWindow.windowId } })` whenever `activeWindow.windowId !== windowParam`. The writeback writes the **window id only** — there is no `session` param to write. No debounce — tmux truth wins always. The effect skips when `dialogOpenRef.current === true` to avoid focus-stealing re-renders mid-dialog (this gates the URL writeback only, not the underlying SSE-derived selection). Comparing `windowId` (not `String(index)`) means an index shift from reorder produces no phantom writeback navigation to a different window. (`260529-chgz`, `260529-jad6`)

**Sidebar clicks navigate optimistically AND mutate.** `navigateToWindow(windowId)` in `app.tsx` runs a `runSwitch()` body that fires an optimistic `navigate({ to: "/$server/$window", params: { server, window: windowId }, search: {} })` *and then* calls `selectWindow(server, windowId)` to bring tmux into agreement. This navigate **pushes** — a user-initiated window switch IS a navigation, so every switch routed through `navigateToWindow` (sidebar click, window-switcher ▾, command palette, keyboard shortcut, spawn-agent same-server branch) creates a distinct browser-history entry the top-bar ◀ ▶ arrows can retrace (see § Chrome → Browser-history arrows). **No dedup on distinct hops** — `w1→w5→w1` pushes three entries and Back retraces every hop (explicit no-dedup requirement). One early-return guard is NOT a history dedup: `navigateToWindow` early-outs when the target is a **redundant no-op** — BOTH the URL window AND tmux's active window (`isRedundantSwitch(windowId, windowParamRef.current, activeWindowRef.current?.windowId)` — a mobile-drawer dismissal tap, the palette's `"(current)"` entry). Such a click can change nothing (tmux emits no bytes, the event-driven SSE snapshot never re-confirms), so arming the pending-switch machinery would guarantee a spurious spinner mask at 300ms plus a false failure toast at 5s over the very terminal the user is on; the early-out keeps only the ergonomic drawer close. A genuine `w1→w5→w1` still pushes duplicates (each hop IS a real switch); only the degenerate self-click is inert. The two tmux/preference-driven navigates that MUST stay `replace: true` are the SSE URL-writeback effect (contract 2 above — tmux corrections aren't user intent, pushing would fight the Back button) and `switchView` (§ Window-View Lens — per-viewer lens toggles must not step through Back); `runSwitch` alone pushes. The optimistic navigate is what makes the terminal render immediately (including the first click from the `SessionTiles` density view and cross-session clicks the SSE writeback alone can't express); `pendingClickRef` suppresses the writeback's bounce-back until the SSE snapshot confirms the switch (typically sub-500ms with the tmuxctl control-mode subscription; see `architecture.md` § tmux Control-Mode Subscription). **SSE confirm is the PRIMARY, event-driven clear** — a single per-switch `CONFIRMATION_WINDOW_MS` (5s) failure-bounce timer BACKSTOPS it: on an explicit `selectWindow` POST rejection OR no confirmation within the window, the intent is cleared, the URL/heading bounce to tmux truth, and a failure toast shows (§ Window-Switch Slide Transition → Confirmation-gated motion). This timer fires ONLY on non-confirmation to un-stick a silent-failure limbo — never to prefer the click over an external event. Server-side overrides during a click (another agent or hook calling `tmux select-window` concurrently) resolve to whichever mutation tmux processed last — the confirmation timer does not contest a genuine external switch (SSE confirming ANY active window clears the intent). On mobile, `runSwitch` additionally closes the overlay sidebar after a destination tap. **Timing caveat:** on an *instant/fallback* switch — no View Transitions support, reduced motion, no outgoing window, or an unresolvable direction — `runSwitch` executes synchronously at click time. On an *animated* same-server switch the body runs INSIDE `document.startViewTransition`'s async callback, i.e. **≥1 frame after the click** (the browser first captures the outgoing snapshot, then invokes the callback); "navigate at click time" is precise only on the instant path; see § Window-Switch Slide Transition. (`260703-l4nf`, `260715-m4xy`, `260715-38kg`)

**Keyboard switch path via the command palette.** The window-switch path is also surfaced as `Window: Switch to <session> › <name>` palette entries — the `windowSwitchActions` useMemo in `app.tsx`, one entry per window across **every** session (built from `flatWindows`, the current server's merged sessions — not cross-server). Each entry reuses `navigateToWindow(fw.window.windowId)`, so it inherits the same `selectWindow` + URL-writeback + mobile-close + `pendingClickRef` suppression as a sidebar click — no separate `selectWindow` plumbing. The URL-active window (`fw.window.windowId === windowParam`) gets a `" (current)"` suffix, mirroring `Server: Switch to <name> (current)`. The `›` separator is U+203A (single right-pointing angle quote) for `<session> › <name>` palette labels. The block composes last in `paletteActions` (see § Boards Command Palette). (`260613-o20f`)

**Click-intent and URL-match key on `{server, @N}` — never the session name.** `pendingClickRef` is a `PendingSwitchTarget = { server: string; windowId: string }` (`src/lib/window-transition.ts`). Every consumer compares BOTH fields via the pure exported `isSamePendingTarget(pending, server, windowId)`: the writeback's `urlMatchesPending` is `isSamePendingTarget(pending, server, windowParam)` and `sseConfirmed` is `isSamePendingTarget(pending, server, activeWindow.windowId)`; the mount-alignment skip and `bouncePendingSwitch`'s guards use it too. See § Design Decisions → Pending-switch identity is `{server, @N}` for why the key excludes the session name and includes the server. (`260529-jad6`, `260715-38kg`)

**Sidebar selection follows the URL window ID, falling back to `isActiveWindow`.** `WindowRow.isSelected` derives from `currentSessionName === session.name && (hasUrlWindow ? currentWindowId === win.windowId : (!ghost && win.isActiveWindow))` in `app/frontend/src/components/sidebar/index.tsx`, where `hasUrlWindow = currentWindowId != null` and `currentWindowId` is the URL's `@N` window ID. When the route carries a window ID (the normal terminal-route case), selection is the stable `currentWindowId === win.windowId` comparison. The `isActiveWindow` term (set by the backend `WindowInfo.IsActiveWindow` from tmux's `#{window_active}`) drives selection only when no URL window is present — e.g., the dashboard route, or before the first navigation resolves. Because the URL window ID is written back from `isActiveWindow` (see contract 2 above), the two stay in lockstep with `tmux select-window` (external switches, `rk riff` window creation) without an index↔ID seam. Ghost windows (mid-creation, before the SSE snapshot includes them) match only via the `!ghost && win.isActiveWindow` fallback path when no URL window applies.

### Multi-Client Convergence

All clients viewing the same server's window route converge on the same window — the per-server invariant. When the SSE `event: sessions` payload changes which window is `isActiveWindow` for the currently-viewed session, every browser tab on `?server=<same>` and viewing `/$server/$window` navigates to the new window's `windowId` via `navigate({ replace: true })` (the URL writeback effect above).

Clients viewing `/board/$name` SHALL NOT navigate — the board route does not subscribe its URL to `isActiveWindow`. The SSE payload still arrives and `BoardPane` rendering still receives the updated `isActiveWindow` data; the route stays put.

Clients viewing different `?server=` values are independent — each server's SSE stream drives its own clients. Cross-server tabs never yank each other.

**Stale-URL tab yanks other tabs on mount**: when a new tab opens at `/$server/@7` while existing tabs are on `/$server/@2` (tmux active is window `@2`), the new tab's mount-time alignment fires `selectWindow(server, "@7")`. The resulting SSE snapshot then yanks every existing tab on that server to window `@7` via the writeback effect. This is intentional ("yanking is OK" per the change intake) — the new tab represents user intent to view that window, and existing tabs collectively reflect "what tmux is now doing." A URL whose `@N` no longer exists on the server simply fails to resolve a current window (no nearest-index arithmetic) — see § Kill-redirect.

## Session Tiles

The component is `app/frontend/src/components/session-tiles/session-tiles.tsx` (`SessionTiles`). The literal string "Dashboard" does not appear in the chrome — the no-window top-bar leaf is the server-name `aria-current` leaf (§ Chrome (Top Bar)).

`SessionTiles` is the **multi-agent monitoring-DENSITY view** — "what is every agent doing right now" at a glance, the differentiator vs single-session tools. It renders in the terminal area when no `$window` param is present: the `windowParam ? <TerminalClient/> : <SessionTiles/>` branch in `app.tsx` (`windowParam` is the `@N` window ID; `sessionName` is derived from the active window's SSE snapshot, not a URL segment). The empty `serverIndexRoute` (`router.tsx`) is componentless — rendering is done conditionally by `AppShell` based on whether `$window` exists (no new route — Constitution IV). (`260701-70a0`)

**The load-bearing constraint** — window previews are **static text**, NOT a live xterm/relay per tile. N live relays for N tiles would re-trigger the documented HTTP/1.1 6-per-origin connection-pool starvation (see the board-route entries in this domain). A tile upgrades to a real live terminal ONLY on click (navigate to `/$server/$window`, where the single relay opens). The preview mechanism is a periodic `tmux capture-pane` snapshot delivered over the existing SSE hub as `event: preview` — see `architecture.md` § Session-Tile Previews (`event: preview` + preview-scope) for the backend.

**Layout**: Outer wrapper `flex-1 min-h-0 flex flex-col`. The tmux Server page's page identity is the `tmux Server: <server>` heading in the top-bar center cell (§ Chrome (Top Bar)). A single scrollable tile area (`flex-1 min-h-0 overflow-y-auto ...`) whose first child is a page-level `<SectionHeading label="tmux Server Overview" />`; the grid below is preceded by a `<SectionHeading label="Sessions" side={"{N} sessions, {M} windows"} />` — the server-view stats ride the `side` slot, right-aligned after the rule (`[ SESSIONS▊ ]──── {N} sessions, {M} windows`; § Section Heading, § Page Overview Headings). The `<h2>` + TypedLabel typed-sweep live INSIDE the brackets. Only the tile area scrolls. (`260704-pr0p`, `260715-zs1y`)

**Session tiles grid**: `grid grid-cols-1 sm:grid-cols-2 lg:grid-cols-3 gap-3`. One tile per session (`bg-bg-card border border-border rounded`; `data-testid="session-tile-{name}"`), plus an always-visible dashed **New Session** tile at the end (calls `onCreateSession` → instant session creation, no dialog). A ghost/optimistic session tile gets `opacity-50 animate-pulse`.

**Session tile header**: A `<button>` toggling inline expansion (`aria-expanded`, `aria-label` "Expand/Collapse {name}"). Shows session name, window count, and activity summary (`{N} active, {M} idle`, derived from each window's `activity`). Chevron `▶`/`▼`. Multiple sessions may be expanded simultaneously. Expand state is local `useState<Record<string, boolean>>` keyed by session name.

**Window tiles** (inside an expanded session): each is a `<button>` (`rounded border border-border bg-bg-primary hover:border-text-secondary`; `data-testid="window-tile-{session}-{index}"`) that on click calls `onNavigate(win.windowId)` — the same `navigateToWindow` path a sidebar click uses (optimistic navigate + `selectWindow`; see § URL as Resumable Bookmark) — routing to the live-terminal route. NO preview relay is ever opened. A ghost window tile is `disabled` + pulsing. Each tile shows:
- A leading unified `<StatusDot win={win} />` (the SAME component as the sidebar row / pane panel / — see § Status Dot) + window name; a fab-stage badge (`bg-accent/10 text-accent`) when `win.fabStage` is set
- The **pane text preview** as a static monospace `<pre>` (`h-24 overflow-hidden whitespace-pre text-[10px] font-mono bg-bg-inset`, `data-testid="window-tile-preview-{windowId}"`) — the `capture-pane` snapshot for `win.windowId`, read from the context `previewsByServer.get(server)` map. Empty (`""`) until the first `event: preview` arrives for the expanded set — the view degrades gracefully to an empty preview area before the first snapshot. Never an xterm instance.
- Fab change ID + slug when present (`parseFabChange`)

**New Window button**: dashed-border button inside each expanded session (`onCreateWindow(session.name)`).

**Preview subscription lifecycle** (bounded to expansions): `SessionTiles` consumes `previewsByServer` and `setPreviewScope` from `useSessionContext()`. A `useEffect` keyed on the sorted+joined expanded-session-name key POSTs the current expanded set via `setPreviewScope(server, expandedNames)` whenever it changes (expand/collapse) and on server change. It opens NO live relay per tile and does NOT `setInterval`+fetch — previews arrive on the single existing per-server SSE stream. On unmount / server change the declared scope lapses naturally (the connection drop clears the server-side per-connection set — see `architecture.md`).

**Touch targets**: session tile headers and window tiles use `coarse:min-h-[44px]`.

## PR Status

Live PR status is exposed two ways: a **full one-line detail** (the Pane panel `PR` L3 register) and a **single status dot** (the unified `StatusDot`, see § Status Dot below). The detail surface is:

1. **Pane panel `PR` (L3) register** (the per-*selected*-window detail view; see § Pane Panel / `status-panel.tsx`). This is the **only** full-line PR surface. The `SessionTiles` window tile carries only the `StatusDot`; there is no `PrStatusLine` component, though its module `pr-status-model.ts` remains as the single source of the shared PR color vocabulary + the StatusDot's exported model (§ Shared PR vocabulary). (`260701-70a0`, `260706-y1ar`, `260715-jykd`)

The *dot* (a single colored dot, not the full line) reaches the remaining surfaces: the sidebar window-tree row and the `SessionTiles` window tile. The dense tree shows a single `StatusDot`, never the multi-part line. That single dot is the unified `StatusDot` driven by the palette-v3 **two-family ladder** (cool fab blue/green/purple, warm ad-hoc agent yellow/orange, gray floor; core hue = phase, shape = status, additive yellow halo = `waiting`), reused on all its surfaces (sidebar row, SessionTiles window tile, pane-panel header). See § Status Dot. (`260610-obky`, `260706-y1ar`)

### `PR` (L3) register — colored segments + open-first (`status-panel.tsx`)

> `WindowContent` renders the pyramid's **four orthogonal signal registers** (spec § Row Minimalism). See § Pane panel four-register view for the full L0/L1/L2/L3 model; this subsection covers the L3 `PR` register. (`260706-y1ar`)

The **`PR` (L3) register** shares the `tmx/cwd/git/fab` icon + value idiom but with an **open-first** interaction — it is the exception to the panel's "click row = copy" default. `getPrSegments(win)` returns `null` unless `win.prNumber` — the gate is **ungated from `fabChange`**: the L3 register shows the PR for ANY pane on a branch with a derived PR (universal derivation, Principle X; dot ownership is a separate family-gated concern — see § Status Dot D1). Otherwise it returns an array of colored `{text, color}` segments — `#<n>` (`text-text-primary`), `<state>[ (draft)]` (via `PR_STATE_COLORS`), and, for an `open` PR only, `checks <prChecks>` (`PR_CHECKS_COLORS`) and `review: <prReview→spaces>` (`PR_REVIEW_COLORS`). `state` can be `open`/`merged`/`closed` — the collector queries `states: [OPEN, MERGED, CLOSED]`, so a recently-merged PR shows `merged` (checks/review suppressed for non-`open`), see `architecture.md` § `internal/prstatus`. The three color maps are imported from `pr-status-model.ts` (single source shared with the sidebar dot — the shared vocabulary home, § Shared PR vocabulary), so segment coloring follows GitHub state per-segment (no whole-value red swap) — the color story lives in § PR Status (draft-follows-health) above. The PR icon (``) is the Nerd Font git-pull-request glyph, matching the other rows' accent icons.

**Open-first split** — the row body's interaction is open-first (`↗`), not copy. The segment JSX is single-sourced via a shared `segmentSpans` const in `WindowContent` (consumed by both branches below, so the two can't drift), and the row branches on `win.prUrl`: (`260703-41ks`)

- **URL present** → the row body is a file-private `PrLinkRow` — a real `<a href={win.prUrl} target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" title={win.prUrl} aria-label="Open PR #<n> in a new tab">` (NOT a `<button>` + `window.open`, so native middle-click / Ctrl-Cmd+click / right-click → "Copy link address" all work; mirrored the now-removed `PrStatusLine`'s anchor — the same anchor-not-button PR-link idiom). The anchor is a flex row: a `shrink-0` prefix span + PR icon span, then a `min-w-0 truncate` segment-text child, then an **always-visible** (not hover-gated) `shrink-0` inline `↗` sibling immediately after it — so the `↗` hugs the (possibly truncated) text end, is never eaten by truncation, and never floats to the far right of a wide row. The `↗` is the affordance that signals this row **opens** rather than copies; the existing row hover treatment (`hover:bg-bg-inset`, segment `group-hover:text-accent`) is kept as the row-level cue. Because the anchor is a flex container (whitespace-only `{" "}` text nodes between flex items are dropped and a trailing collapsible space trimmed), the inter-column gaps live as NBSPs INSIDE the prefix/icon spans — the at-rest prefix is `"pr"`+2×NBSP (4 monospace advances) matching `CopyableRow`'s `${prefix} ` (3 + gap = 4), and the `copied ✓`+NBSP feedback is 9 advances matching `CopyableRow`'s `copied ✓ ` — keeping the icon/content column-aligned with `tmx/cwd/git/fab` and the no-URL branch. **Copy is role-swapped, not dropped**: a sibling hover-revealed copy `<button aria-label="Copy PR URL">` (the `` clipboard glyph) sits in an absolutely-positioned right-side container reusing the **sidebar window-row icon-cluster gating** — the container is `pointer-events-none` at rest with `group-hover/pr:pointer-events-auto coarse:pointer-events-auto has-[:focus-visible]:pointer-events-auto`, and the button is `opacity-0 group-hover/pr:opacity-100 coarse:opacity-100 focus-visible:opacity-100` (revealed on hover / coarse pointers / keyboard focus; the anchor reserves `pr-6` so the icon doesn't overlap the inline `↗`/text). Its `onClick` does `e.preventDefault(); e.stopPropagation(); handleCopy("pr", win.prUrl)` — the button is a SIBLING of the anchor (not enclosed, so `<a>`-in-`<a>`/`<button>`-in-`<a>` nesting is avoided; `preventDefault` is belt-and-suspenders). Its color follows the window-row cluster precedent (`text-text-secondary hover:text-text-primary`), NOT `ICON_CLASS` (whose `text-accent-bright` would fight at equal specificity). The `copied ✓` feedback is unchanged — the copy still keeps the `copiedRow === "pr"` + `COPY_FEEDBACK_MS` mechanism, and since the row body is no longer a `CopyableRow`, `PrLinkRow` replicates the prefix swap (`pr` → `copied ✓`) inline. Both the anchor and the copy button are natively keyboard-focusable (Constitution V).
- **URL absent** (`prNumber` set, `prUrl` missing) → nothing to open, so the row stays a plain `CopyableRow` (prefix `"pr "`) copying the segment text (`prText`) on click — the row body IS the copy action, no anchor, no inline `↗`, no hover copy icon (unchanged from before).

`CopyableRow` has no `className` prop; its `title` prop is live (the `cwd` row uses it).

**Draft state-color follows health, not readiness.** `getPrSegments(win)` (the colored-segment variant used in the panel) does NOT force a draft PR's state-color to `text-text-secondary` — a draft's state segment follows `PR_STATE_COLORS[win.prState]` like any other (open → `text-accent-green`/green), under the "green = HEALTH, not merge-readiness" semantic. Checks/review are suppressed for `!open` (merged/closed) PRs, and `merged` is `text-purple-400`. The color story is one system across the sidebar dot and these status-panel segments (green = health, red = fail, purple = merged) driven by the shared `isFailish` predicate. The sidebar `StatusDot` keys off the lifecycle `PHASE_HUE`/shape model (§ Status Dot), rendering the PR phase as purple/red-center/green within that model rather than sharing literal color tokens with these text segments. (`260615-2olv`, `260615-0hsz`)

### Pane panel four-register view (`status-panel.tsx` `WindowContent`)

The pane panel's `WindowContent` renders the pyramid's **register view** — one line per signal layer, **orthogonal, never collapsed**, so the sidebar `StatusDot` is a pure function of what the panel shows and can be **mentally derived** from it. The four registers each render as absent when their layer is absent (a plain shell pane shows only `out`). All prefixes are the **fixed-width 3-char vocabulary** `out`/`agt`/`fab` (+ `tmx`/`cwd`/`git` identity rows), each followed by a single-space advance; only `PR` is 2-char + NBSP-padded to the same 4-advance column. (`260706-4h26`)

```
out  active · <command>   /   <command> — idle Xm since last output   (L0: activity + activityTimestamp)
agt  waiting 3m           /   active   /   idle 12m                    (L1: agentState + epoch duration)
fab  <id> <slug> · <stage>[ · <displayState>]                         (L2: fabChange · fabStage · fabDisplayState)
PR   #<n> · <state>[ · checks <c> · review: <r>]                      (L3: prNumber/state/checks/review, ungated)
```

- **L0 `out`** (`getOutputLine`) — ALWAYS rendered (the floor layer's precondition is "always"). Speaks about bytes, not intent. Its elapsed is **never muted** here — the register view is uncontested for space, so the **waiting-pierce rule is automatic** (the duration-mute rule that hides elapsed when output flows applies only to the tip's one-line summary, spec § Duration-Text Ladder). Icon: `BrailleSnake`.
- **L1 `agt`** (`getAgentLine`) — `null` when no `agentState`, else `${agentState} ${agentIdleDuration}` (or bare state when no duration). The rk-computed `agentIdleDuration` is present for `waiting`/`idle`, empty for `active`. Icon: `StarTwinkle`. This is where a waiting duration is always visible regardless of flowing output (the pierce rule).
- **L2 `fab`** (`fabLine`) — `<id> <slug> · <stage>[ · <displayState>]`; the `displayState` segment is appended when present (`fab pane map` may omit it on older binaries). Rendered as a `CopyableRow` (copies the change id). Icon: `ClockSpinner`.
- **L3 `PR`** (`getPrSegments`) — see § `PR` (L3) register above. **Ungated from `fabChange`** — shows for ANY pane with a derived `prNumber` (universal derivation, Principle X). The open-first `PrLinkRow` / `CopyableRow` branch on `win.prUrl` folds in here.

The identity rows (`tmx`/`cwd`/`git`) are pane metadata, orthogonal to these four signal registers, and render above them. The per-second `useNow()` tick lives in this leaf (`WindowContent`) — the bottom panel is a single instance, so its tick is negligible and never touches the memoized sidebar tree (§ Render Performance).

### Shared PR vocabulary — `pr-status-model.ts`

The module `pr-status-model.ts` carries no `PrStatusLine` component — it is the single source of the shared PR **color vocabulary** AND the lifecycle **status-dot model** (below), imported by 6 consumer modules (`status-dot.tsx`, `status-dot-tip.tsx`, `status-dot-label.ts`, `sidebar/status-panel.tsx`, `status-dot.test.tsx`, `status-dot-tip.test.tsx`) plus its own unit test (`pr-status-model.test.ts`). The PR text detail lives solely in the PANE panel's L3 `PR` register (`getPrSegments`, § `PR` (L3) register). (`260715-jykd`)

**Module surface** (colocated in `pr-status-model.ts` — all `export`ed except the file-private `hasFreshAgent`/`prOwnsDot`, which are internal helpers to `statusDotState`):

- **PR color vocabulary**: `PR_STATE_COLORS`/`PR_CHECKS_COLORS`/`PR_REVIEW_COLORS` (the per-segment GitHub-state color maps, consumed by the L3 register in `status-panel.tsx`) and `isFailish(win)` (`prChecks === "fail" || prReview === "changes_requested"` — the single fail predicate).
- **Status-dot model**: `PrDotState` (the `"merged" | "fail" | "pending" | "healthy" | "neutral"` union) and `prDotState(win)` (the first-match-wins precedence function, reusing `isFailish` for its `fail` branch — the single source of the fail definition, shared with the Pane panel). The palette-v3 dot model (`260615-2olv`, `260706-y1ar`): `DotShape` (`"ring" | "solid" | "failed" | "done" | "skipped"`), `DotPhase` (`"intake" | "apply" | "pr" | "agent" | "agentPr" | "none"`), `StatusDotState = { phase: DotPhase; shape: DotShape; waiting?: boolean }`, `fabPhase(stage)`, `fabShape(displayState)`, `prShape(win)` (reuses `prDotState`), `hasFreshAgent(win)`, `prOwnsDot(win)`, `PHASE_HUE` (phase→hue token map), and the two-family `statusDotState(win)` (see § Status Dot for the ladder + D1/D2).

The `StatusDot` component (`status-dot.tsx`, see § Status Dot) imports `statusDotState`/`PHASE_HUE`; `status-dot-tip.tsx` and `status-dot-label.ts` import `StatusDotState`/`DotShape`; `dotLabel` lives in its own `status-dot-label.ts` module (`260706-y1ar`, to break the dot↔tip import cycle). **`PR_DOT_COLOR` and `PR_DOT_LABEL` were DELETED by `260615-0hsz`** (zero-call-site once the redesigned dot stopped using them). `prDotState`/`PrDotState`/`isFailish` remain live (the L3 register + `prShape` use them; `prDotState` is reused by `prShape` and the `prDotState precedence` block in `pr-status-model.test.ts`, which `260715-jykd` preserved after dropping the `PrStatusLine`-render cases).

### Status Dot (`status-dot.tsx`) — palette-v3 two-family ladder + waiting halo

> Spec: `docs/site/status-dot.md` (+ `docs/img/status-dot-matrix.svg`) is the canonical reference for the full matrix and the palette rationale. Design authority: `docs/specs/status-pyramid.md`.

> Tooltip surface: the dot mounts a custom `StatusDotTip` hover-card (floating-ui based), not the native HTML `title`. See § Status Dot hover-card below. (`260616-37ub`)

`StatusDot({ win }: { win: WindowInfo })` (`app/frontend/src/components/status-dot.tsx`) is the **one** dot reused on all three surfaces — the sidebar window row (leading position, the row's ONLY status signal — see § Window rows / Row Minimalism), the `SessionTiles` window tile, and the pane-panel header. It is driven by the palette-v3 **two-family ladder** and is a **first-class consumer of `agentState`**, using **TWO orthogonal visual channels PLUS an additive attention overlay**: **core hue = phase** (which journey + position in it), **shape = status** (health, ONE shape vocabulary across fab AND PR), and **`waiting` → a ladder-exempt additive yellow halo** (see § Waiting halo below). (`260615-0hsz`, `260706-y1ar`)

**Ladder — two families joined at the top** (`statusDotState(win)` in `pr-status-model.ts`, palette v3). First precondition wins for the core hue + shape; `waiting = win.agentState === "waiting"` is computed independently and attached as `state.waiting` on every branch:

- **`fabChange` present → cool family (fab pipeline):** `prOwnsDot(win)` → `{ phase: "pr", shape: prShape(win) }` (purple); else `{ phase: fabPhase(win.fabStage), shape: fabShape(win.fabDisplayState) }` (blue if `intake`, else green).
- **no `fabChange` but a fresh `agentState` → warm family (ad-hoc agent):** `prOwnsDot(win)` → `{ phase: "agentPr", shape: prShape(win) }` (orange); else `{ phase: "agent", shape: agentState === "idle" ? "ring" : "solid" }` (yellow — a `waiting`/`active` agent is mid-turn → solid, only a resting `idle` agent is a ring).
- **neither → the gray L0 floor:** `{ phase: "none", shape: win.activity === "active" ? "solid" : "ring" }`.

The result type is `StatusDotState = { phase: DotPhase; shape: DotShape; waiting?: boolean }`. `hasFreshAgent(win)` is `agentState ∈ {active, waiting, idle}` — #314 already clears stale/shell-reconciled values server-side (the reconciler + rollup omit a plain-shell pane), so a non-empty rolled-up `agentState` on the window IS fresh; no client-side staleness heuristic (R4).

**D1 — per-family PR ownership**: `prOwnsDot(win)` is `!!win.prNumber && win.prState !== "closed"`. PR ownership is PER-FAMILY — **purple requires `fabChange && prNumber`, orange requires `fresh agent && prNumber`**. A **plain floor pane never lets its PR own the dot**: with no fab change and no fresh agent it stays gray even when its branch has a derived PR. The PR still shows everywhere derivation reaches — the PANE panel's L3 register and the StatusDotTip "Open PR" link — but never as a mystifying floor-pane dot (Principle X: derivation is universal; dot ownership is a separate, family-gated concern).

**D2 — merged/closed PR ownership**: a **CLOSED-unmerged** PR never owns the dot (`prState !== "closed"` in `prOwnsDot`) — the pane falls through to its underlying tier (a live-change window shows its green working stage, not a dead PR's skipped ring — decision-table row 20). A **merged** PR (served durably by the backend's `--state all` branch derivation — no grace clock; see [architecture](/run-kit/architecture.md) § Branch→PR Derivation) still owns the dot as the purple/orange done square. The frontend `prState === "closed"` drop and the backend's stateless/restart-proof merged durability are the two halves of D2. (`260706-y1ar`, `260706-4h26`)

**Waiting halo — additive attention overlay, ladder-exempt** (R2): when `state.waiting`, `StatusDot` appends the `rk-waiting-halo` class to the dot element — a **constant-yellow pulsing box-shadow ring** layered around it (the `rk-waiting-halo` keyframe in `globals.css`). It is **ADDITIVE** — the core hue AND shape are untouched (a blue intake dot keeps its blue core; a green failed dot keeps its failed shape; a waiting `done` square keeps sharp corners). NEVER a hue-flip — family identity must survive attention. The class rides the dot element itself (box-shadow renders outside the border-box, disturbing neither size nor hue), so the floating-ui `setRef` stays on one element. Under `prefers-reduced-motion` the halo is a **static yellow ring** (no pulse). The glance rule: **cool core = my pipeline, warm core = my ad-hoc agents, gray = just a terminal, yellow HALO = needs me now.**

**Hue = phase** — palette v3, TWO families + floor (spec § The Channel Model). Every fab stage after `intake` (apply/review/hydrate/ship/review-pr) collapses to the single green `apply` phase. `fabPhase(stage)`: `intake`→`intake`; everything else (incl. unknown/absent)→`apply`. The purple `pr` phase is chosen in `statusDotState`, never in `fabPhase`. `DotPhase = "intake" | "apply" | "pr" | "agent" | "agentPr" | "none"`. `PHASE_HUE: Record<DotPhase, string>` maps phase→core-hue token:

| Phase (`DotPhase`) | Family / source | Hue token |
|--------------------|-------------------|-----------|
| `intake` | cool fab — `intake` stage | `text-blue-400` |
| `apply` | cool fab — every other stage (green collapse) | `text-accent-green` |
| `pr` | cool fab — the live PR (`fabChange && prNumber`) | `text-purple-400` |
| `agent` | warm ad-hoc agent — working (no PR) | `text-yellow-400` |
| `agentPr` | warm ad-hoc agent — its PR (`fresh agent && prNumber`) | `text-orange-400` |
| `none` | gray L0 floor (no journey) | `text-text-secondary` |

> **Why the green collapse**: the old ship/review-pr green barely rendered — `/git-pr` creates the PR mid-ship, so purple takes the dot the moment `prNumber` exists. Collapsing apply→review-pr to one green frees the palette to give the ad-hoc agent tier its own warm hues (yellow/orange) and reserves purple for the PR endpoint. This is the deliberate break from fab-kit's README 4-phase grouping (Intake/Execution/Completion/Shipping) — noted in `docs/site/status-dot.md` and the matrix SVG.

**Shape = status** — ONE vocabulary, five shapes, rendered by `StatusDot` from `{phase, shape}` with `color = PHASE_HUE[phase]` (except `skipped`, which forces `text-text-secondary` regardless of phase); the halo is layered on top when `state.waiting`:

| Shape (`DotShape`) | fab `fabDisplayState` / PR equivalent | Rendering |
|--------------------|----------------------------------------|-----------|
| `ring` | `pending` (PR: checks running) | hollow circle, `1.8px solid currentColor` border in phase hue, transparent fill |
| `solid` | `active`/`ready` (PR: open/healthy) | filled circle (`backgroundColor: currentColor`, `border: none`) in phase hue |
| `failed` | `failed` (PR: checks fail / changes requested) | **dotted ring** (`1.2px dotted currentColor`, transparent) in phase hue + a centered small **red** `bg-red-400` dot (`w-[3px] h-[3px]`) |
| `done` | `done` (PR: merged) | filled **sharp-cornered square** (`rounded-none`, `backgroundColor: currentColor`) in phase hue |
| `skipped` | `skipped` (PR: closed unmerged) | gray hollow ring (hue FORCED to `text-text-secondary`) |

Every shape EXCEPT `failed` renders at one uniform 7px footprint (`DOT_SIZE = "w-[7px] h-[7px]"`), so the filled square and the hollow circles read as the same size in the dense sidebar — the square is distinguished by its sharp `rounded-none` corners, not by being larger (at 7px even a 1px radius blurs the square-vs-circle distinction). The **`failed` dot is the lone size exception** — a slightly larger 9px footprint (`w-[9px] h-[9px]`): a CSS `dashed` border can't control its dash count and at 7px fits only ~4 dashes that read as flower petals, so it uses a `1.2px dotted` border at 9px, which renders as a delicate bead ring, with a `3px` red center sitting inside the 9px ring's ~6.6px hole (the earlier `dashed`/7px/4px-center description is superseded).

**Shape mappings**:
- `fabShape(displayState)`: `pending`→`ring`; `active`,`ready`→`solid`; `failed`→`failed`; `done`→`done`; `skipped`→`skipped`; unknown/absent→`solid` (a live fab window with a future/unrecognized state still reads as a live dot, not gone).
- `prShape(win)`: reuses `prDotState(win)` so the PR surfaces stay in lock-step — `merged`→`done`, `fail`→`failed`, `pending`→`ring`, `healthy`→`solid`. Its `neutral` catch-all **splits on `prState`**: a **closed-unmerged** PR → `skipped` (the gray hollow ring, labelled "PR — closed"), an open / aged-out-merge → `solid`. The `win.prState === "closed"` check lives in `prShape` on the `neutral` fall-through only — `prDotState`'s own behavior is UNCHANGED (still returns `neutral` for closed). Note: post-D1 a closed PR never reaches `prShape` from the dot ladder anyway (`prOwnsDot` excludes `prState === "closed"`), so the closed→skipped branch is exercised only by direct-call tests — flagged as a deletion candidate.

**Red is used in exactly ONE way** across the whole system: the small center dot of a `failed` dotted ring. A failure reads as a dotted ring **in its phase hue** with only the red center — no whole-dot red tint, no solid-red PR `fail` dot.

**Gray L0 floor** (`phase: "none"`, lowest precedence, no fab change + no fresh agent) is **monochrome gray** — color is reserved for the two journeys: `activity === "active"`→gray `solid` filled circle, else gray `ring`. No phase hue is ever applied here.

**Full stage × status matrix** (rows = phase/hue, cols = status/shape). The **waiting halo overlays ANY cell** — it is an overlay applicable to every tier, not a matrix row (spec § The Channel Model):

| Phase (hue) | pending | active/ready | failed | done | skipped/closed |
|-------------|---------|--------------|--------|------|-----------------|
| intake (blue) | blue ring | blue solid | blue dotted-ring + red center | blue square | — |
| apply→review-pr (green, collapsed) | green ring | green solid | green dotted-ring + red center | green square | gray ring |
| PR — fab (purple) | purple ring (checks pending) | purple solid (open/healthy) | purple dotted-ring + red center (failing) | purple square (merged) | *(closed never owns the dot — D1/D2)* |
| agent — warm (yellow) | — | yellow solid (active/waiting mid-turn) | — | — | yellow ring (idle) |
| PR — agent (orange) | orange ring | orange solid | orange dotted-ring + red center | orange square | *(closed never owns the dot)* |
| plain (gray floor) | — | gray solid (active) | — | — | gray ring (idle) |

**Accessibility** — every dot carries `role="img"` + `aria-label` composed from journey + status + **additive attention suffix**, never color alone (colorblind a11y + Constitution V). The dot is wrapped by the custom `StatusDotTip` hover-card, which carries the same label text; `role="img"`/`aria-label` are the accessible name, and `tabIndex={0}` opens the card on focus (§ Status Dot hover-card below; `260616-37ub`). `dotLabel(win, state)` lives in its OWN module `status-dot-label.ts` (so both `status-dot.tsx` and `status-dot-tip.tsx` import it without an import cycle; `status-dot.tsx` re-exports it, keeping its public surface stable). It composes a **core label + additive `— agent waiting {dur}` suffix** (`coreLabel` + the `state.waiting` suffix): (`260706-y1ar`)
- **fab PR tier** (`phase === "pr"`) / **agent PR tier** (`phase === "agentPr"`): PR-native words via `PR_SHAPE_LABEL` (`ring`→"checks running", `solid`→"open", `failed`→"failing", `done`→"merged", `skipped`→"closed") — e.g. `"PR — merged"`, `"PR — open"`.
- **fab non-PR tier** (gated on `win.fabChange`, NOT phase — so a fab window with an unknown/absent stage still reads `{stage-or-fab} — {status}`, never a bare agent/tmux word): the real stage word via `SHAPE_LABEL` (`ring`→"pending", `solid`→"active", `failed`→"failed", `done`→"done", `skipped`→"skipped") — e.g. `"apply — active"`, `"review — failed"`, `"intake — pending"`.
- **warm agent tier** (`phase === "agent"`): agent-native words via `AGENT_SHAPE_LABEL` — the idle `ring` reads **"idle"** (NOT the fab-stage "pending") and `solid` reads "active" — e.g. `"agent — active"`, `"agent — idle"`. (T002 rework: the ring must read "idle" per the module doc + docs/site, not "pending".)
- **L0 floor**: the bare tmux activity word (`"active"`/`"idle"`).
- **Waiting suffix**: when `state.waiting`, append `" — agent waiting {dur}"` (duration from the rk-computed `agentIdleDuration`, present for `waiting`/`idle`) — so a review-failed waiting window reads `"review — failed — agent waiting 3m"` (R3).

**Impl symbols** — in `pr-status-model.ts` (colocated, see § PR Status exports): `DotShape`, `DotPhase` (`"intake" | "apply" | "pr" | "agent" | "agentPr" | "none"`), `StatusDotState = {phase, shape, waiting?}`, `fabPhase`, `fabShape`, `prShape`, `hasFreshAgent`, `prOwnsDot`, `PHASE_HUE`, and the two-family `statusDotState`. In `status-dot-label.ts`: `dotLabel` + the file-private `coreLabel` + the `SHAPE_LABEL`/`PR_SHAPE_LABEL`/`AGENT_SHAPE_LABEL` maps. In `status-dot.tsx`: `DOT_SIZE`, the `renderDot` shape markup (incl. the `rk-waiting-halo` class append), the `StatusDot` component, and a re-export of `dotLabel`; it imports `statusDotState`/`PHASE_HUE`/`DotShape`/`StatusDotState` from `pr-status-model.ts` and `dotLabel` from `status-dot-label.ts`. In `status-dot-tip.tsx`: `StatusDotTip` + the pure `dotTipContent(win, state)` resolver (now also carrying an `agent` line — see § Status Dot hover-card) + `DotLink`/`DotTipContent` types.

> **No `PR_DOT_COLOR`/`PR_DOT_LABEL` maps.** The dot renders from `PHASE_HUE` + the shape maps + `SHAPE_LABEL`/`PR_SHAPE_LABEL`/`AGENT_SHAPE_LABEL`. (`prDotState`/`PrDotState`/`isFailish`/`PR_STATE_COLORS`/`PR_CHECKS_COLORS`/`PR_REVIEW_COLORS` serve the Pane-panel L3 `PR` register + its segments, and `prShape` reuses `prDotState`; see § Shared PR vocabulary.) (`260615-0hsz`)

**Why this shape** (`260706-y1ar` design decisions): (1) two families let a glance separate "my fab pipeline" (cool blue/green/purple) from "my ad-hoc agents" (warm yellow/orange) from "just a terminal" (gray) — the user's own two-journey framing. (2) the additive yellow halo keeps family identity intact when attention is highest — a hue-flip (rejected) would destroy exactly the signal the user is scanning for; a self-colored halo (rejected) vanishes in the reduced-motion static form. (3) D1's per-family PR ownership keeps derivation universal (PR in register/tip/line everywhere) while a plain shell never shows a mystifying PR dot. Rejected: fuchsia attention hue (the motivating amber collision is gone with the green collapse); hue-flip and self-colored halo (see above).

**Call sites** — the three surfaces are bare `<StatusDot win={win} />` (the hover-card lives inside `StatusDot` via the `renderDot` callback): (1) sidebar `WindowRow` — ONE leading dot, the row's ONLY status signal (§ Window rows / Row Minimalism); (2) the `SessionTiles` window tile — leading dot before the window name (dot + name + fab-stage badge + text preview); (3) pane panel `WindowPanel` `headerRight` — `<StatusDot win={win} />` before `{win.name}`. The dot's inputs (`agentState`, branch-derived `prNumber`/`prState`, `fabChange`/`fabStage`/`fabDisplayState`) all already ride `WindowInfo` via SSE; the halo keyframe is the only new CSS (`globals.css` `rk-waiting-halo`). Tests: `status-dot.test.tsx` (enumerates the decision-table rows across floor/agent/fab families × shapes + the additive halo on blue-core and green-failed cores + a11y label composition incl. the waiting suffix); `pr-status-model.test.ts` covers the ladder + `prShape`; the reduced-motion static-ring form is asserted via the `agent-next-waiting.spec.ts` e2e (jsdom can't evaluate `globals.css` media queries).

### Status Dot hover-card (`status-dot-tip.tsx`) — custom floating tooltip

The dot's tooltip is a custom `StatusDotTip` hover-card, built on `@floating-ui/react` (`app/frontend/package.json`), not the native HTML `title`. Native `title` cannot be styled, has a browser-fixed open delay, and **cannot contain links** — the dot needs interactive affordances (open the PR, jump to the docs explaining the state vocabulary). It renders on all three StatusDot surfaces (it lives inside `StatusDot`, so the call sites are untouched). (`260616-37ub`)

**Wiring** — `StatusDotTip({ win, state, renderDot })` wraps the dot via a `renderDot(setReference, referenceProps)` callback: `StatusDot` owns the dot's shape/color markup and spreads the floating reference setter + interaction props onto its `<span>`, keeping the dot the floating anchor. `useFloating` (`placement: "top"`, middleware `offset(6)` / `flip()` / `shift({ padding: 8 })`, `whileElementsMounted: autoUpdate`) + `FloatingPortal` (renders to `document.body`, escaping the sidebar's `overflow:hidden` clip). Interactions: `useHover` (`delay: { open: 150, close: 100 }`, `handleClose: safePolygon()` — the bridge so the pointer can travel dot → card to click a link), `useFocus` (keyboard-first open, Constitution V), `useDismiss` (Escape / blur). The card surface uses the shared theme tokens (`bg-bg-primary border border-border rounded-md shadow-lg`, monospace) — no new color tokens. (SwatchPopover shares the `bg-bg-primary border border-border` base but is zero-radius with a hard offset shadow, not `rounded-md shadow-lg` — the two surfaces are not token-identical.)

**Deliberately NO `useRole({ role: "tooltip" })`** (§ Design Decisions → No `role="tooltip"` on the StatusDot hover-card). The dot's accessible name stays on its own `aria-label`; the links are real Tab-reachable controls, so no extra ARIA role is added.

**`tabIndex={0}` on the dot** is the focus-open tab stop (the floating-ui reference props don't add one). Accepted tradeoff (reviewed): on the sidebar the dot sits inside the row button/treeitem, so it becomes a second tab stop ahead of the row — but a `<span role="img" tabindex="0">` is focusable yet NOT "interactive content" in the HTML button content-model sense (valid markup), and the sidebar tree keydown handler still anchors on `closest('[role="treeitem"]')`, so arrow-nav works from a focused dot.

**Content** — the pure `dotTipContent(win, state) → { label, agent, links, fetchedAtEpoch }` resolver: `label` REUSES the exported `dotLabel(win, state)` (single source of truth shared with the dot's `aria-label`, imported from `status-dot-label.ts`). It also carries an **`agent` line** (`agent: waiting 3m` / `active` / `idle 12m`; `null` when no `agentState`) rendered on EVERY tier (fab, PR, warm, or floor) — the tip is the recovery path for the Row-Minimalism-removed row stage word + durations (R7). Any window with a `prUrl` gets one `"Open PR #N"` link — on ANY tier including the gray floor: PR-dot OWNERSHIP is family-gated (D1) but the derived PR itself is UNIVERSAL (Principle X / decision-table row 10), so the tip surfaces the link wherever a `prUrl` exists, exactly like the PANE panel's L3 register. (`onClick` `stopPropagation` so opening the PR doesn't also select/navigate the underlying sidebar row.) **Every** card additionally renders a fixed docs-link icon (NOT part of `links[]`) → `https://github.com/sahil87/run-kit/blob/main/docs/site/status-dot.md` (GitHub blob, top of doc — `docs/site` is not served locally, matching `top-bar.tsx`'s `NOTIFICATIONS_HELP_URL` convention).

**Freshness line — "checked Xs ago"**: `dotTipContent` carries a fourth field `fetchedAtEpoch: number | null` — the window's `prFetchedAt` (the collector-join `PrFetchedAt` timestamp, architecture.md § PR-Status SSE Join) parsed to **epoch SECONDS** (`Date.parse(win.prFetchedAt)` → `Math.floor(/1000)`), or `null` when `prFetchedAt` is absent OR unparseable (`Date.parse` → `NaN`), so the card omits the line rather than rendering "checked NaNs ago". Rendered by a dedicated **`FreshnessLine` leaf component** (NOT inline in `StatusDotTip`): it owns a live `useNow()` clock (epoch seconds) and displays `checked ${formatDuration(nowSeconds - fetchedAtEpoch)} ago` (`data-testid="dot-tip-checked"`, styled like the agent line) — reusing `formatDuration` (`lib/format.ts`, the Ns/Nm/Nh convention) rather than adding a relative-time formatter, and returning `null` when `fetchedAtEpoch === null`. **Why its own component**: `FreshnessLine` is mounted ONLY inside the open hover-card (`{open && …}`), so its per-second `useNow()` re-render is leaf-scoped to a card that is actually open — the dot wrapper never ticks (the leaf-scoped-`useNow` contract, § Render Performance / use-now.ts). After a manual refresh the timestamp visibly resets — the ambient version of the same trust signal the refresh-button checkmark gives, useful without clicking. (`260715-nwla`)

**Tests** — `status-dot.test.tsx` covers `dotTipContent` (PR-phase → one link with correct `href`; fab/tmux → zero links; `label === dotLabel`) and asserts the dot has no `title` (`aria-label` instead). `status-dot-tip.test.tsx` (added `260715-nwla`) covers the freshness line: the "checked Xs ago" line renders with the formatted relative time when `prFetchedAt` is present and is omitted when absent/unparseable. New e2e `tests/e2e/status-dot-tip.spec.ts` (+ sibling `.spec.md`) proves hover-open, focus-open, Escape-dismiss, PR-link + docs-icon presence, and link click-through.

## Attention Surfacing (`waiting` rollups + nav)

The per-window `waiting` overlay (agent blocked on a human) propagates UP the hierarchy as **count badges** and drives a **keyboard-first navigation** action and a **board-pane seam**. This is the UI half of #314's three-state `agentState` — see [agent-state](agent-state.md). All counts derive from the existing SSE session data already in the client — **no new endpoint, no `setInterval`/fetch** (Constitution II / code-quality anti-patterns).

**Shared rollup helpers** (`lib/waiting.ts`) — the single source of truth so every surface counts identically: `isWaiting(win)` (= `win.agentState === "waiting"`, keyed on the server-side window-level rollup that already applies `waiting > active > idle` across panes), `countWaitingWindows(windows)`, `countWaitingInSessions(sessions)`. Pure functions over the streamed `WindowInfo`/`ProjectSession` shape.

**`WaitingBadge`** (`components/waiting-badge.tsx`) — a small count chip mounted unconditionally; **renders `null` when `count <= 0`** (attention badges are present only when they mean "something needs you"). Styling follows the existing count-chip vocabulary but in the **constant yellow** of the waiting overlay (`bg-yellow-400/15 text-yellow-400`, theme-independent — the same "yellow = an agent needs you now" glance language as the status-dot halo), plus a `⚠` glyph. It is TEXT, not motion (the pulse lives on the per-window dot/seam) — legible via color + count + `aria-label`, never color-only. Mounted on four surfaces:

- **Session row** (`sidebar/session-row.tsx`) — count of the session's waiting windows (`countWaitingWindows(session.windows)`), rendered after the session name button (R8).
- **Host-page TMUX SERVERS server tile** (`host-overview-page.tsx`) — per-server count summed over the server's sessions (`countWaitingInSessions(sessionsByServer.get(name) ?? [])`), absolutely positioned top-right on the tile. One glance at `/` answers "does anything need me" (R9). Only attached servers stream windows, so an unattached server's count is 0 (badge absent) — never a wrong count.
- **Board header** (top-bar `BoardModeInfo`, `top-bar.tsx`) — count of the board's waiting panes (`waitingPaneCount` prop), rendered in the board-mode left info between the pane/server counts and the `⌘[⌘] cycle` hint (R10).
- **Sidebar SERVER-panel server tile** (`sidebar/server-panel.tsx`) — the fourth server-level surface, per-server count over the server's sessions. Placement **differs** from the Host-page tile: it rides the **same flex row as the tile's "N sess" count, right-aligned** (`flex items-center justify-between`) rather than absolute top-right, because the sidebar tile already occupies its top-right with a hover-revealed palette/kill action cluster (`top-1 right-1 z-10`) — the Host-page tile's `absolute right-2 top-2` would collide. `ServerTile` takes a plain `waitingCount: number`; `ServerPanel` takes the optional `waitingCounts?: Map<string, number>` and forwards `waitingCounts?.get(name) ?? 0` per tile, keeping the presentational panel decoupled from session data. The Sidebar computes the map in `sidebar/index.tsx` via `useMemo(() => …, [sessionsByServer])` over the already-consumed `sessionsByServer` (same `countWaitingInSessions` helper). Attached-server-only by construction (an unattached server is absent from `sessionsByServer` → count 0 → badge absent), the same accepted caveat as the Host-page tile — no eager attach-all: lazy-attach is deliberate, so an unattached server shows no badge. (`260708-4li7`)

**Board-pane waiting seam** (`board/board-pane.tsx` + `board-page.tsx`) — a waiting board pane gets a **3px pulsing yellow seam** (border-width system; the `rk-waiting-seam` class + `border-[3px]`), the board-pane form of the status-dot halo. Border precedence: a `waiting` pane always shows the seam (attention is the highest-priority signal); a focused-AND-waiting pane layers the accent focus shadow on top so it reads both. Under `prefers-reduced-motion` the seam is static yellow (`globals.css`). `BoardEntry` is a thin shape with no `agentState`, so `BoardPageContent` **joins each pinned pane back to its live `WindowInfo`** via `(server, windowId)` against the streamed `sessionsByServer` (use-boards attaches every board server, so window data incl. `agentState` is flowing) — a `waitingWindowIds` set (`${server}:${windowId}` keys) drives both the per-pane seam and the header count; a pane whose window is not yet in the snapshot is simply not waiting (no wrong signal).

**`Agent: Next waiting` palette action** (`app.tsx` `agentActions`, R11 — keyboard-first, Constitution V): cycles focus through windows whose rolled-up `agentState` is `waiting`, **current server first** (in sidebar order, from `flatWindows`) then other **attached** servers (from a live `sessionsByServerRef.current` read — unattached servers' window data isn't streamed, a known constraint). No-op with a `"No agents waiting"` toast when none. The cycle arithmetic is the pure `nextWaitingTarget(ordered, currentServer, currentWindowId)` helper (`lib/palette-agent-nav.ts`, unit-tested): empty → `null`; current window not in the list → first target (jump in); current IS a target → the next one **with wraparound** (`(idx+1) % len`). This is a deliberate contrast with `palette-move.ts` (reorder arithmetic, which does NOT wrap) — do NOT extend that module. Same-server targets navigate via `navigateToWindow`; cross-server targets `navigate({ to: "/$server/$window" })` (and close the mobile drawer). The action is appended to `paletteActions` as `agentActions`.

## Iframe Window (the `web` lens renderer)

`app/frontend/src/components/iframe-window.tsx` — the renderer for the **`web` lens** (§ Window Views (Lens Model)). It is selected by the window's *resolved view*, NOT by `@rk_type` identity — `app.tsx` renders it when the resolved view is `web`: `resolvedView === "web" && currentWindow?.rkUrl ? <IframeWindow …/> : <TerminalClient/>` (`resolveView` bakes in availability, so an iframe-typed window with no `rkUrl` resolves to `tty`). Bottom bar is NOT rendered for the web lens (no terminal to send keys to). The component is **presentational** — it takes `windowId`, `rkUrl`, and an `onSwitchToTty: () => void` callback and owns NO view/URL/localStorage logic (that lives in `window-view.ts` + `app.tsx`); it does not import `updateWindowType` (§ Window Views → decoupling). (`260714-t97o`)

**Layout**: Outer wrapper `flex flex-col flex-1 min-h-0` with two children: URL bar (`shrink-0`) and iframe (`flex-1`).

**URL Bar**: Thin toolbar above the iframe (`border-b border-border bg-bg-primary`). Four elements:
- **Refresh button** (↻ `&#x21bb;`) — forces iframe reload by clearing `src` to `"about:blank"` then re-setting it via `setTimeout(0)`. Styled: `w-7 h-7 rounded hover:bg-bg-card text-text-secondary`
- **URL input field** — shows current `rkUrl`, editable. On Enter, calls `updateWindowUrl(server, windowId, url)` which delegates to the unified `setWindowOptions(server, windowId, { "@rk_url": url })` → `POST /api/windows/{windowId}/options` (partial-merge — only `@rk_url` is touched). On API failure, reverts input to the SSE-confirmed `rkUrl`. Styled: `bg-bg-card text-text-primary text-sm px-2 py-1 rounded border border-border`. **This is the one POST the web lens fires** — editing the content ADDRESS is *substrate* state (shared, POSTed, everyone sees it — spec R7), distinct from switching which lens you look through (per-viewer, no POST). (`260529-jad6`)
- **Submit indicator** (⏎ `&#x23ce;`) — decorative visual affordance (`text-text-secondary text-xs`)
- **`>_` switch-to-terminal button** (`aria-label="Switch to terminal"`) — it calls the injected `onSwitchToTty()` prop (which runs `app.tsx`'s `switchView("tty")` → drops `?view=` + writes localStorage), **NOT** `updateWindowType(server, windowId, "")`. It is a per-viewer *view switch*, so flipping to the terminal and back preserves the window (no `@rk_type` mutation, no global flip — the e2e asserts zero `/options` POSTs across a flip). (`260714-t97o`)

**SSE Sync**: A `useEffect` on `rkUrl` syncs both the URL bar text and iframe `src`. Uses a `currentSrcRef` to avoid re-setting iframe `src` when the URL hasn't actually changed (prevents unnecessary reloads on identical SSE ticks). When `rkUrl` changes externally (Claude or another process runs `tmux set-option`), the URL bar updates and iframe navigates automatically.

**Proxy URL conversion**: `toProxySrc(url)` converts localhost URLs to proxy paths: `http://localhost:8080/docs` -> `/proxy/8080/docs`. Non-localhost URLs pass through unchanged. Pattern: `^https?:\/\/(?:localhost|127\.0\.0\.1):(\d+)(\/.*)?$`.

**Iframe attributes**: `sandbox="allow-same-origin allow-scripts allow-forms allow-popups allow-modals"`, `title="Proxied content"`, `border-0`.

**Window creation**: "Window: New Iframe Window" command palette action (id `create-iframe-window`) opens a `Dialog` with two inputs: window name (autofocused, Enter focuses URL input) and URL (Enter creates window). Create button disabled until both fields non-empty. Calls `createWindow(server, session, name, undefined, "iframe", url)` — the extended API client function passes `rkType` and `rkUrl` in the POST body. Backend uses `CreateWindowWithOptions` for atomic `\;`-chained tmux command. Only shown when a session is active. Synthetic iframe windows are created this way; `@rk_type=iframe` means "**default view = web**" (a creation-time hint, § Window Views → `defaultView`), not a locked identity. (`260714-t97o`)

## Window Views (Lens Model)

The model (`docs/specs/window-views.md`, rules R1–R7): **a window ROW is a substrate** (a supervised tmux pane); **a VIEW is a lens** over one derivable output of that pane (the tty is a lens; an iframe of the pane's HTTP service is a lens; the parsed agent transcript is a lens; later: desktop). **Which lenses a window offers is a derived capability set; which lens YOU look through is per-viewer client state** carried in the URL + localStorage — never a server-side `@rk_type` mutation, never part of the window's identity. Both the iframe (`web`) and chat (`chat`) lenses run on this same generalized switcher machinery (spec R4). Frontend-only; no Go/API changes (`@rk_type`/`@rk_url`/`@rk_chat` plumbing and `POST /options` are untouched — the SSE payload already carries `rkType`/`rkUrl`/`chatProvider`). (`260714-t97o`, `260714-r7rq`)

Three lenses are implemented: `tty` (always available, `TerminalClient`), `web` (available when `rkUrl` is non-empty, `IframeWindow`), and `chat` (available when `chatProvider` is non-empty, `ChatView` — the read-only transcript renderer, § Chat View). Capabilities are orthogonal and STACK (spec R5): one window can offer `tty`+`web`+`chat` at once. The registry is open-ended — `desktop` adds a `ViewName` member, an availability clause, a `defaultView` hint, and a `ViewSwitcher` segment, NOT a new component/route/window-type.

### Pure view-model helper — `lib/window-view.ts`

The single source of view logic — pure, DOM-free, colocated `window-view.test.ts` (the same pattern as `window-transition.ts`/`navigation.ts`). Both the `app.tsx` render branch AND the window-switch transition classification (§ Window-Switch Slide Transition) call `resolveView`, so it MUST live in one place (no drift). Helpers take a minimal structural `{ rkType?, rkUrl?, chatProvider? }` shape (assignable from `WindowInfo`):

- **`ViewName = "tty" | "web" | "chat"`** — the lens union.
- **`hasWebUrl(win)` / `hasChat(win)`** — the single-source availability predicates: `rkUrl` non-empty after `.trim()` (whitespace-only `@rk_url` is NOT web — no blank-src iframe); `chatProvider` non-empty (mirrors the backend `resolveWindowChat` gate).
- **`availableViews(win): ViewName[]`** (spec R1/R3) — `["tty"]`, plus `"web"` when `hasWebUrl`, plus `"chat"` when `hasChat`. **Availability is decoupled from `@rk_type`**: an iframe-typed window with no URL offers only `tty` (matches the old render gate's AND-condition). Returned in the registry's fixed order (`chat > web > tty`) via a `HINT_ORDER` filter — so a stacked window yields `["chat","web","tty"]`.
- **`defaultView(win): ViewName`** (spec R5) — the window's default lens, applied ONLY when the URL and localStorage carry no choice: `"web"` when `rkType === "iframe"` AND `rkUrl` is set, else `"tty"`. `@rk_type=iframe` is **demoted from identity to a creation-time default-view hint** (no data migration). Structured as spec R5's ordered hint precedence `desktop > chat > web > tty` (module const `HINT_ORDER`, only `web`/`tty` wired) so later lenses add a hint clause, not a branch. **`chat` sits in `HINT_ORDER` for capability ORDERING only — it contributes NO default hint**: a chat-capable window still defaults to `tty` unless the viewer chose chat (preserves `260714-r7rq`'s terminal-default; a chat-capable window opens on the terminal, chat is one click / `Ctrl+\`` away).
- **`resolveView(searchView, stored, win): ViewName`** (spec R2) — precedence **URL `?view=` (if that view is available) → localStorage (if available) → `defaultView(win)`**. Any unavailable value falls through; the chain always bottoms out at `tty`, so an unavailable `?view=web` deep link (window with no `rkUrl`) OR `?view=chat` on a chat-less window renders the terminal, never a broken iframe / empty chat shell. `searchView`/`stored` are untrusted strings validated against the capability set here — callers pass raw values.
- **`nextView(available, current): ViewName | null`** — the cycle successor (wraps); `null` when < 2 views or `current` is absent. Powers the `Cmd/Ctrl+.` chord (pure so the order is unit-testable).
- **`shouldSuppressViewChord(target): boolean`** — the input-gating predicate for the chord, **byte-for-byte the same rule as `shell.tsx`'s `⌘\` sidebar toggle**: suppress only inside a NON-xterm INPUT/TEXTAREA/contenteditable (xterm's hidden helper textarea is the terminal's normal focus, so it must NOT be suppressed — `target.closest(".xterm") != null` is the exception). jsdom-safe (`contentEditable` attribute fallback for the missing `isContentEditable` getter).
- **localStorage helpers** — **value-bearing** key `runkit-window-view:{server}:{windowId}` storing the view NAME, including `"chat"` (absent = default). `windowViewStorageKey`/`readStoredView`/`writeStoredView`, try/catch-noop per `chrome-context.tsx`. Value-bearing generalizes past two states (spec R2).

### `?view=` search param — `router.tsx`

`view` is a **validated search param** on `terminalRoute` (spec R2, Constitution IV: no new route — it is the codebase's first `validateSearch`). The exported pure `validateTerminalSearch(search): { view?: "web" | "chat" }` accepts `view === "web"` or `view === "chat"` and **drops any other/unknown/non-string value** (returns `{}` — treated as absent, NEVER errored), so a stale/garbage deep link degrades to the default view. It is wired as the route's `validateSearch` (ONE key — the merge briefly had two) and unit-tested directly in `router.test.ts` (accepts `web`/`chat`, drops `?view=bogus`/non-string/absent without throwing). The `declare module "@tanstack/react-router"` `Register` block types `.view` as `"web" | "chat" | undefined`, so `useSearch({ strict: false })` in `app.tsx` reads it **with no `as` cast** (code-quality type-narrowing — `tsc --noEmit` clean).

### `app.tsx` integration — resolution, `switchView`, render branch

`app.tsx` (terminal route) computes `searchView = useSearch({ strict: false }).view`, `storedView = readStoredView(server, windowParam)`, `currentViews = availableViews(currentWindow)` (memoized), and `resolvedView = resolveView(searchView, storedView, currentWindow)`. There is ONE view-state block. It owns one stable `switchView(view)` callback (deps `server`/`windowParam`/`navigate`):
- writes localStorage (`writeStoredView`),
- `navigate({ to: "/$server/$window", params, search: view !== "tty" ? { view } : {}, replace: true })` — **`web`/`chat` ride the URL (`?view=web` / `?view=chat`); `tty` DROPS the param** (clean URL; tty is the always-available default). The URL is the shareable/deep-linkable seam (push-notification-ready); localStorage is the per-window stickiness that survives R6's param-drop on a window switch. Both seams are required.

The **render branch** selects the renderer by resolved view — `chatViewActive ? <ChatView …/> : resolvedView === "web" && currentWindow?.rkUrl ? <IframeWindow onSwitchToTty={() => switchView("tty")} …/> : <TerminalClient/>`, where `chatViewActive = resolvedView === "chat"` (`resolveView` already bakes in the `chatProvider` availability gate, so a chat-less window never resolves to chat — no separate `chatAvailable` guard).
