NOT by `rkType === "iframe" && rkUrl`. The **tty-branch "Switch to iframe view" `</>` hint bar** (a SECOND `@rk_type`-mutation site that called `updateWindowType(..., "iframe")`) is **removed** — switching to web is now the ViewSwitcher/palette/`>_` job, none of which mutate `@rk_type` (spec R7).

### ViewSwitcher chip — `components/view-switcher.tsx`

The ONE switcher UX all lenses share (spec R4) — a generic segmented chip: props `{ views: ViewName[]; active: ViewName; onSelect }`. It is the **first candidate of the right-cluster overflow registry** (see § Right cluster → overflow chevron menu). As the FIRST `rightItems` entry it keeps its leftmost in-bar position but is the **first control to yield** under width pressure (before any L1 split), collapsing into the "More controls" chevron menu as per-view rows (`ViewSwitcherMenuRows`) so the center heading regains its space on narrow viewports (the common phone case). Fed via the `useRegisterTopBarSlot` slot context (`availableViews`/`activeView`/`onSelectView` are the ONLY view fields on the slot). Renders `null` when `views.length <= 1` (both the chip and the caller gate on this, so a tty-only window shows no chip). Presentational — owns no view logic. (`260717-6anu`)

- **Segment DISPLAY order is `[tty|web|chat]`** via a component-local `DISPLAY_ORDER = ["tty","web","chat"]`, **deliberately decoupled from `window-view.ts`'s `HINT_ORDER`** (`chat>web>tty`, which governs only default/capability precedence — the two orderings answer different questions). Any view not in `DISPLAY_ORDER` sorts to the END (defensive — a future lens still renders). The tty-first ordering is applied by a shared module-local helper `orderViews(views)` (listed-in-`DISPLAY_ORDER` first, unlisted appended) used by BOTH the in-bar pill AND the overflow `ViewSwitcherMenuRows`, so bar↔menu ordering can never drift. (`260717-6anu`)
- Active segment is **inverse-video** (`bg-accent-green text-bg-primary`); house `rk-glint` hover vocabulary (reduced-motion-safe — the glint is a CSS media-query no-op, no JS animation). `role="group" aria-label="Window view"` + `data-testid="view-toggle"` + per-segment `aria-pressed`/`aria-label` (`Terminal view`/`Web view`/`Chat view`). **No `hidden sm:*` breakpoint gate** (`inline-flex`) — visibility is **space-driven via the overflow registry**: the pill renders inline while the right cluster has room and otherwise collapses into the chevron menu as `ViewSwitcherMenuRows` (`260717-6anu`). Because it is the FIRST candidate it is the first to yield, so on a phone width (and on a squeezed desktop pane) a long-named multi-view window's pill is in the menu, not inline — while a very short heading legitimately keeps it inline (no crowding exists then). Segment glyphs are the **lowercase view names** `tty`/`web`/`chat` (spec R4's `[tty|chat]` style).
- **Overflow representation — `ViewSwitcherMenuRows`** (`260717-6anu`, exported from `view-switcher.tsx`, same `{views, active, onSelect}` props): when the `view-switcher` registry entry overflows, the pill is represented as **one `role="menuitem"` row per available view** in the shared `orderViews()` tty-first order, labeled `View: {VIEW_LABEL[view]}` (`View: Terminal` / `View: Web` / `View: Chat` — the palette's `View:` vocabulary). The **active** row is inverse-video accent-green (matching the pill's active segment) and carries `aria-pressed`, so the menu keeps the lens-indicator role while the pill is collapsed; clicking a row calls the same `onSelect(view)` and the menu's role-keyed handler closes the panel. Row styling composes the shared `MENU_ROW_BASE` + `MENU_ROW_REST`/`MENU_ROW_ACTIVE` variants hosted in `top-bar-overflow-menu.tsx` (`tabIndex={-1}` per the menu's roving-focus model), so it stays in lockstep with every other overflow-menu row. Returns `null` for a single-view window (mirrors the pill). Follows the multi-row `NotificationMenuRows` `menuRender` precedent. No NEW inline lens indicator is added while collapsed — the marked row + the view content itself (chat bubbles vs. terminal) carry lens identity, and the heading stays the static `Window:` in every lens (§ Heading is a static `Window:`).

### Palette parity + keyboard shortcuts (Constitution V)

- **`View: Terminal` / `View: Web` / `View: Chat` palette actions** (AppShell `viewActions` in `app.tsx`), each visible only when its view is **available AND not the current** view — the gating + label + shortcut-hint composition live in a pure builder `buildViewActions(available, resolved, onSwitch)` in `lib/palette-view.ts` (mirrors `lib/palette-move.ts`/`palette-update.ts`, unit-tested in `palette-view.test.ts`). The per-entry `shortcut` hint tracks the binding that reaches it: `View: Chat` (and `View: Terminal` when LEAVING chat) show `` Ctrl+` `` (the chat toggle); every other switch shows `⌘.` (the cycle). One `buildViewActions` call feeds them; there is no `@rk_type`-mutating `toggle-iframe-terminal` action.
- **`Cmd/Ctrl+.` cycles the current window's lenses** — a window-level `keydown` effect in `app.tsx` that `preventDefault()`s (so xterm doesn't also receive it), gated by `shouldSuppressViewChord` and calling `switchView(nextView(views, active))`. No-op when < 2 views. Live view/window values read via a `viewCycleRef` so the listener is stable across SSE ticks. Chosen against the live chord registry (`⌘K` palette, `⌘\` sidebar, `⌘]`/`⌘[` board pane-cycle) — a free binding in the `⌘<punctuation>` family; `Ctrl+.` is inert in readline (unlike `Ctrl+/`→undo). Documented in the **App section of the Keyboard Shortcuts dialog** (`ShortcutRow label="Cycle view" keys={["⌘."]}`).
- **`` Ctrl+` `` toggles tty↔chat** (`use-chat-view-shortcut.ts`, § Chat View → shortcut) — the VS-Code "toggle terminal" binding, speaking `ViewName` (`"tty"`, not `"terminal"`), enabled when `currentViews.includes("chat")`, toggling via `switchView`. Documented as `ShortcutRow label="Toggle chat / terminal" keys={["Ctrl+\`"]}`.

### Heading is a static `Window:` in every lens (spec R4 reversal)

The top-bar center `PageType: name` heading on the terminal route reads a **static `Window: <window>` in every lens** (tty / web / chat) — it does NOT follow the active view (§ Window Heading). A single `WINDOW_PREFIX = "Window:"` constant (`top-bar.tsx`) is passed as a constant `prefix` into `WindowHeading` at the terminal-mode center cell; there is no lens-following `terminalHeadingPrefix()` helper and no `WEB_PREFIX`/`CHAT_PREFIX` constants. The heading identifies the WINDOW (the substrate); which lens you look through is shown by the `ViewSwitcher` (the overflow-registry chip — or its `View:` menu rows when collapsed), not the heading (§ Design Decisions → Heading identifies the window, not the lens). The name's anchor does not jump on a lens switch, since the prefix width does not change with the lens (§ Center-heading stable anchor + nav affordances). The click-to-rename affordance and boot-sweep treatment apply. (`260714-uco1`, `260717-6anu`)

### `?view` drops on window switch (spec R6)

Navigating to a DIFFERENT window carries NO `view` param — each destination window resolves its own last-view/default independently. Client-side navigations (sidebar/palette/breadcrumb via `navigateToWindow`, plus the window-death redirect and SSE-writeback switch) omit/clear `search`, and TanStack Router's `final` search middleware returns `{}` when `dest.search` is absent, so an outgoing `?view=web`/`?view=chat` does not leak onto the target. (Simplest semantics — per-window localStorage covers the intent; the web-view-lens e2e persistence case exercises this through a real sidebar-click navigation to guard against a future `retainSearchParams`/router-upgrade regression.) The one exception is the `Agent: Next waiting` / WaitingBadge deep-link, which INTENTIONALLY sets `?view=chat` for a chat-capable target (§ Chat View → WaitingBadge).

### Window-switch transition classification (one rule)

The window-switch slide transition's `switchTransitionRef` carries a SINGLE `ungatedIds` set: window ids whose EFFECTIVE resolved view is **not `tty`** — i.e. they render `<IframeWindow>` (web) or `<ChatView>` (chat), neither of which has the terminal's xterm first-write receipt seam, so they use the transition's **ungated capture** (a first-write gate would never release for a non-xterm surface → stuck transition / blank pane). Computed at render time from `resolveView(undefined, readStoredView(server, id), win) !== "tty"` (URL is unknown for a not-yet-navigated target, so only localStorage + default hint decide) — the same "keyed on resolveView, not `@rk_type`" invariant as the render branch (§ Window-Switch Slide Transition).

### e2e — `web-view-lens.spec.ts` / `chat-view.spec.ts` (+ `.spec.md`)

`web-view-lens.spec.ts` drives real tmux (own session, `window-heading.spec.ts` pattern), setting `@rk_url`/`@rk_type` via `tmux set-option -w`. Its `describe` defaults to a wide **1440px** desktop width (the 1280px "Desktop Chrome" default sits right at the drop threshold once the pill is a candidate, so 1440px is used to clear the whole cluster deterministically). Covers: chip appears only on web-capable windows; flip to web then back preserves the window and fires **zero `/options` POSTs** (asserted via `page.on("request")`); deep link `?view=web` cold-loads the iframe (lens proven by the web chip / iframe + the `?view=web` URL — the heading stays the static `Window:` prefix); `?view=web` on a URL-less window falls back to the terminal; legacy `@rk_type=iframe`+url defaults to web with the chip present; last-view persistence across a real client-side window switch away and back. The 375px behavior follows the space-driven registry contract: at 375px with a realistically long window name the pill **overflows into the "More controls" chevron menu** (assert the `View: Terminal`/`View: Web` rows + no horizontal overflow), and at desktop width it returns to the bar as the inline chip. `chat-view.spec.ts` covers the chat lens through the SAME unified chip (`view-toggle`, `Chat view` segment): chip gated on `chatProvider`, flip to chat (lens proven via `view-toggle`/`chat-view` presence + `?view=chat` URL, not the heading prefix), the `` Ctrl+` `` toggle, `?view=chat` cold-load, the bubble/tool-card/pending renderer, reduced-motion — and the 375px "single-line top bar" test asserts the **collapsed-pill contract** (long window name → pill in the chevron menu as `View:` rows, heading room, single line, no horizontal overflow). It drives chat over the state socket, NOT SSE: it uses the extended `_state-socket-mock.ts` (answers a `kind:"chat"` subscribe with an offset-bearing ack + optional `chat`/`chat-state`/`chat-reset` emits) plus a plain `GET /api/windows/*/chat*` backfill `page.route`; the terminal stub stays on `/ws/terminals` (memory `relay-mux-stale-ws-stub-class` — no `/relay/` or SSE stubs). `connection-budget.spec.ts` uses the any-route ≤2 WS + 0 SSE form with a chat-lens case (architecture.md § Testing). (`260714-uco1`, `260717-6anu`, `260717-vhvz`)

## Chat View

A **read-only HTML chat view over the SAME agent pane** — a second view over the tmux pane, never a substrate (the pane stays the agent's parent, Constitution VI; the view only renders the streamed transcript). It is the **`chat` lens** of the window-view model (§ Window Views (Lens Model)) — addressed by `?view=chat` on the existing `/$server/$window` terminal route (Constitution IV, no new route). **All view-state plumbing — the `?view=` param, availability gate, the ViewSwitcher chip, localStorage persistence, palette parity, the `` Ctrl+` `` shortcut, and the switch-transition classification — is the UNIFIED machinery** described in § Window Views (Lens Model); this section owns only what is chat-SPECIFIC: the `chatProvider` gate, the connection-dot semantics, the renderer/stream, and the WaitingBadge deep-link. (The heading is a static `Window:` in every lens, § Heading is a static `Window:`.) The renderer + data layer live in `architecture.md`/[chat](/run-kit/chat.md) § Chat View Frontend. The chat stream is a `kind:"chat"` subscription on the shared state socket (NOT an `EventSource`) — the owner hook is `use-chat-subscription.ts`, and the connection dot below derives from socket-connected AND chat-acked, not `EventSource` health. (`260714-uco1`, `260717-vhvz`)

**The `chatProvider` gate.** `WindowInfo` carries `chatProvider?: string` + `chatSessionRef?: string` (`types.ts`) — the window-level `@rk_chat` rollup the backend emits (typed, not newly parsed). **A non-empty `chatProvider` is the SOLE availability gate** for the chat lens (`hasChat(win)` in `window-view.ts`) — mirroring the backend's own `resolveWindowChat` gating — so it transitively gates every chat affordance: the ViewSwitcher chat segment, the `View: Chat` palette action, the `` Ctrl+` `` shortcut (enabled iff `currentViews.includes("chat")`), the `<ChatView>` renderer, and the deep-link append. (The heading is NOT among them — it is a static `Window:` in every lens, § Heading is a static `Window:`.) There is NO separate `chatAvailable` variable — `resolveView`/`availableViews` fold the gate in.

### View state = the unified lens machinery (NOT a chat-specific mechanism)

The chat lens runs entirely on the unified lens machinery (§ Window Views (Lens Model)), with no chat-specific view-state module:
- Resolution is `resolveView` (URL→localStorage→default); `router.tsx`'s single `validateTerminalSearch` accepts `web`|`chat` (§ Window Views → `?view=`). There is no `lib/chat-view-resolve.ts`.
- Persistence is the value-bearing `runkit-window-view:` key (which also stores `"chat"`). There is no `runkit:chat-view:` key-presence pref hook.
- The chip is the generic `ViewSwitcher` (`[tty|chat]` segments for a chat-only-capable window); flipping is `switchView("chat")`/`switchView("tty")`. There is no `SegmentedViewToggle`.
- `chatViewActive = resolvedView === "chat"` is the render + stream gate (`resolveView` already gated on `chatProvider`).

### Center heading `Window: <window>` (static in the chat lens too)

The `chat` lens does NOT change the heading prefix — the top-bar heading is a static `Window: <window>` in every lens (§ Heading is a static `Window:`; § Window Heading for the boot-sweep/rename mechanics). The `<ChatView>` renderer preserves the inline-rename affordance (the heading IS the rename surface, especially on mobile) — the same parametrized `WindowHeading`, no fork. (`260714-uco1`)

### Renderer swap + chat stream (`app.tsx`)

In the `windowParam` render arm, `chatViewActive` selects `<ChatView>` AHEAD of the web-vs-terminal branch (`chatViewActive ? <ChatView> : resolvedView === "web" && rkUrl ? <IframeWindow> : <TerminalClient>`). `AppShell` owns the single owner-hook call — **`useChatSubscription(server, windowId)`**, opened only when `chatViewActive` (else passed empty strings so the hook idles) — and passes `{events, pending, connected, error}` into `ChatView`. ONE chat subscription on the shared state socket feeds both the renderer and the connection dot (below). The chat pane joins the switch-transition **ungated capture** through the unified `ungatedIds` classification (any non-`tty` resolved view; § Window Views → Window-switch transition classification) — `<ChatView>` has NO xterm first-write seam, so a first-write gate would never release. (`260717-vhvz`)

### Connection dot = chat stream health in chat mode (R9)

"Dot-everywhere = per-page live-data health" (§ Chrome (Top Bar) → connection dot). In chat view, the `isConnected` `AppShell` registers into `TopBarSlot` reflects the **chat subscription's** health instead of the per-server sessions slice: `dotConnected = chatViewActive ? chatStream.connected : isConnected`. **Since `260717-vhvz` `chatStream.connected` = (state socket connected) AND (this window's `kind:"chat"` subscription acked)**, keeping the established 3s disconnect debounce (from `use-chat-subscription`, was the `EventSource`-health form in `use-chat-stream`). In terminal/web view the value is unchanged.

### WaitingBadge click + `Agent: Next waiting` deep-link into `?view=chat`

`WaitingBadge` (`components/waiting-badge.tsx`) gained an **optional** `onClick` prop: when passed, the badge renders as a `<button>` (rk-glint hover, `stopPropagation` so it doesn't bubble to the parent row) that navigates to the next waiting window in its scope; when absent, it keeps today's **display-only** `<span>` (so the board-header / Host-page-tile / server-panel mount sites, which pass no onClick, are unchanged). It is currently wired ONLY at the **sidebar session row** (`session-row.tsx` → `sidebar/index.tsx` → `AppShell`'s `handleWaitingBadgeClick`) — the one surface with a navigable per-session scope.

`handleWaitingBadgeClick(srv, sess)` (`app.tsx`) builds the clicked session's ordered waiting windows and calls **`nextWaitingTarget(ordered, server, windowParam)`** (`lib/palette-agent-nav.ts` — REUSED, not re-implemented; the R12/A-024 review-rework fix: the first cut picked the session's FIRST waiting window via `windows.find(isWaiting)`, so clicking the badge while already ON its first waiting window was a no-op instead of advancing to the next). It appends `?view=chat` via the pure `chatSearchForTarget(hasChat)` helper (`lib/palette-agent-nav.ts`, unit-tested) — `{ view: "chat" }` iff the target window has a `chatProvider`, else empty search (the target resolves its own pref). This is the ONE intentional `?view=` carry across a window switch (§ Window Views → `?view` drops). The existing `Agent: Next waiting` palette action gets the **same** `chatSearchForTarget` append rule for any target it navigates to.

### Connection dot = chat stream health in chat mode (R9)

"Dot-everywhere = per-page live-data health" (§ Chrome (Top Bar) → connection dot). In chat view, the `isConnected` `AppShell` registers into `TopBarSlot` reflects the **chat subscription's** health instead of the per-server sessions slice: `dotConnected = chatViewActive ? chatStream.connected : isConnected`. **Since `260717-vhvz` `chatStream.connected` = (state socket connected) AND (this window's `kind:"chat"` subscription acked)**, keeping the established 3s disconnect debounce (from `use-chat-subscription`, was the `EventSource`-health form in `use-chat-stream`). In terminal/server view the value is unchanged.

### WaitingBadge click + `Agent: Next waiting` deep-link into `?view=chat`

`WaitingBadge` (`components/waiting-badge.tsx`) gained an **optional** `onClick` prop: when passed, the badge renders as a `<button>` (rk-glint hover, `stopPropagation` so it doesn't bubble to the parent row) that navigates to the next waiting window in its scope; when absent, it keeps today's **display-only** `<span>` (so the board-header / Host-page-tile / server-panel mount sites, which pass no onClick, are unchanged). It is currently wired ONLY at the **sidebar session row** (`session-row.tsx` → `sidebar/index.tsx` → `AppShell`'s `handleWaitingBadgeClick`) — the one surface with a navigable per-session scope.

`handleWaitingBadgeClick(srv, sess)` (`app.tsx`) builds the clicked session's ordered waiting windows and calls **`nextWaitingTarget(ordered, server, windowParam)`** (`lib/palette-agent-nav.ts` — REUSED, not re-implemented; the R12/A-024 review-rework fix: the first cut picked the session's FIRST waiting window via `windows.find(isWaiting)`, so clicking the badge while already ON its first waiting window was a no-op instead of advancing to the next). It appends `?view=chat` via the pure `chatSearchForTarget(hasChat)` helper (`lib/palette-agent-nav.ts`, unit-tested) — `{ view: "chat" }` iff the target window has a `chatProvider`, else empty search (the target resolves its own pref). The existing `Agent: Next waiting` palette action gets the **same** `chatSearchForTarget` append rule for any target it navigates to.

## Boards View

`/board/$name` renders a horizontal pane dashboard for windows pinned to a named board (see `tmux-sessions.md` § Pin Sessions / § `@rk_board` for storage and `architecture.md` § Boards Feature for the route placement rationale). The board view does NOT mount AppShell, but it shares the same root-mounted multi-server `SessionProvider`, the same unified `<Sidebar>`, and the same `<Shell>` grid wrapper — the sidebar's per-server session groups stay populated across the route switch because the provider lives at the root. (`260509-17m3`)

### SESSIONS + BOARDS dual presence (a pinned window is LINKED, not moved)

Pinning a window **links** it (`tmux link-window`) into a single-window pin-session (`_rk-pin-<id>`) while it stays a member of its home session, so a pinned window appears on **both** surfaces at once — in the SESSIONS sidebar at its real home index AND as a pane on the board. This is honestly tmux-derived (Constitution II): the SSE session snapshot lists the window under its home session (only the `_rk-pin-*` session name is filtered at the `parseSessions` chokepoint, not the window), so the sidebar shows it with no frontend synthesis. Two ambient dual-residence affordances make the second home legible: the board pane header shows a `{session} › {window}` home crumb (§ Board Tile Header) and the sidebar pin indicator surfaces a "Go to {board}" navigation row (§ Sidebar Pin Icon on Window Rows). The pin-icon filled state and the active-board accent (below) are the board-aware affordances on a SESSIONS row, which stays visible while pinned. (Legacy move-based pins do not appear in SESSIONS while pinned — the window isn't in its home session under the old model; they convert to dual presence on unpin + re-pin.) (`260718-co9z`)

### BoardPage Layout (`app/frontend/src/components/board/board-page.tsx`)

BoardPage uses the shared `<Shell>` wrapper. The Shell grid carries NO `topbar` row — the desktop grid is `grid-template-areas: "sidebar content" / "sidebar bottombar"` (rows `1fr auto`; collapses to single-column `"content" "bottombar"` on `< 640px` with the sidebar overlay); the TopBar is mounted once at the persistent root layout above the Shell, not as a grid child (see § Shell Grid Layout / § Chrome (Top Bar) → persistent root mount). Children are placed into named grid areas: (`260707-4vq2`)

- **Sidebar** (`gridArea: "sidebar"`) — the unified `<Sidebar currentServer={null}>` (same component as AppShell). No per-server group is marked current on board routes. Per-server session groups + Boards section + ServerPanel + bottom panels render as on AppShell. Mobile (`< 640px`) renders the sidebar as a Shell-level overlay whose grid child spans `gridRow: "1 / 3"` (content + bottombar; the Shell grid has no topbar row) — same overlay implementation as AppShell (`260707-4vq2`)
- **TopBar** — NOT a Shell grid child. `BoardPageContent` registers the board extras (`boardName: name`, `paneCount: entries.length`, `serverCount`, `waitingPaneCount`, `boards`, `focusedPane` (the focused-tile split target), `onRequestKill: requestKillFocused` (the top-bar ✕ opens the kill confirm dialog; post-kill refetch rides `executeKillWindow`'s own `onSettled`, not a top-bar callback), `isConnected: boardConnected`, `sidebarOpen`, `onToggleSidebar`) into the slot context via `useRegisterTopBarSlot` (keeping the `HELP_URL` import for its palette action). The persistent `RootTopBar` derives `mode="board"` + `boardName` from the route and renders the board bar fed by those extras (see § Board and § center cell for the current board rendering) (`260707-4vq2`, `260718-co9z`)
- **Content** (`gridArea: "content"`) — the `DesktopRow` (desktop) / `MobileCarousel` (mobile) horizontally-scrollable container of pane "cards" sorted by `orderKey`. Each card is a `BoardPane` with a `BoardHeader` (the `{session} › {window}` home crumb — see § Board Tile Header — + the pin-glyph unpin button) and an embedded `TerminalClient` streamed over the shared `/ws/terminals` mux keyed by `windowId` (one stream per pane) — **the same `TerminalClient`/relay path as the normal terminal route**. The relay attaches the window's `_rk-pin-*` pin-session server-side (the pin-session-first attach preference), so `BoardPane`/`board-page.tsx` need no structural change for the attach — `BoardEntry` shape unchanged. The horizontal-scroll viewport begins at the `content` grid area's left edge — flush with `sidebar.right` (or page.left when `sidebarOpen === false`); no left gutter for board-level chrome (`260717-803u`, `260718-co9z`)
- **BottomBar** (`gridArea: "bottombar"`) — the shared `<BottomBar>` (NEW on this route — board route had no BottomBar pre-rotation). Byte-identical to AppShell's invocation: same three callbacks (`onOpenCompose`, `onFocusTerminal`, `onScrollLockChange`). `onOpenCompose` is `toggleComposeStrip` (the `>_` chip toggles the docked compose strip preference — § Docked Compose Strip); `onFocusTerminal` invokes a ref-tracked `focusFocusedPaneRef.current()` that re-focuses the currently-focused board pane via its `paneRefs[focusedIndex].focus()`; `onScrollLockChange` plumbs through `DesktopRow`/`MobileCarousel` → `BoardPane` → `TerminalClient.scrollLocked`. Input target is the focused pane's wsRef (read from `FocusedTerminalContext.focused?.wsRef`). The docked compose strip renders in this footer above `<BottomBar>` when the preference is on (`{composeStripEnabled && <ComposeStrip />}`)
- **Own `<CommandPalette>` mount** — BoardPage retains its own palette mount because board-route-only entries (Switch / Leave Board View / Cycle Pane Focus →/←) need a registration site, and the AppShell palette doesn't mount on `/board/<name>`. The mount is preserved through the rotation

Empty / non-existent board (`name` exists in URL but `getBoard` returns `[]`): shows "No panes pinned to this board yet. Pin a window from the sidebar." with a back link.

### Pane Cards (Desktop)

- **Default width 480px**, drag-resizable between 280px (min) and viewport-minus-sidebar (max). Resize handle hidden on coarse-pointer devices
- **Persisted per-board** in `localStorage["runkit:board-widths:<name>"]` as `Record<windowId, number>`. `usePaneWidths(boardName)` encapsulates read/write/clamp; missing entries fall back to 480px; malformed JSON is ignored silently. Pane widths are intentionally browser-local view state — they do NOT cross devices (pin state in tmux does)
- **Click-to-focus** transfers focus to the pane's xterm via a `useImperativeHandle`-exposed `focus()` method on `BoardPaneHandle`. **Hover-to-focus is OFF in v1** (no hover handler attached)
- **Visual focus indicator** — focused pane has a distinct border/glow; unfocused panes are de-emphasized
- **Keyboard pane cycling** — `Cmd+]` / `Ctrl+]` next (wraps), `Cmd+[` / `Ctrl+[` previous (wraps). Bound via a `useEffect` keydown listener on the BoardPage component
- **Autofit override** — when the per-board autofit toggle is ON, desktop panes ignore the stored pixel width and become equal-share flex items, and the resize handle is hidden. See § Board Autofit Toggle. Autofit never mutates `runkit:board-widths:<name>`, so toggling off restores the exact hand-tuned widths above.

### Board Kill Confirm Dialog + Verb Discipline

The board surfaces two distinct destructive-vs-safe actions with disciplined verbs — **Unpin** (safe, reversible — removes the window from the board, it stays in its `{session}`) and **Kill** (destructive — closes the window everywhere, including its home session). Board surfaces (tooltips, aria labels, palette entries) do not use the "close"/"close pane" verb; sidebar and terminal-mode ✕ vocabulary/semantics are out of scope.

**Kill is confirm-gated** (`board-page.tsx`). The board top-bar ✕ (via the slot's `onRequestKill`) and the `board-kill-focused` palette entry both call `requestKillFocused`, which captures the focused entry as `killTarget` (`{server, windowId, windowName, home}`) and opens a `Dialog` — they never fire immediately:

> **Kill `{window}`?** This closes it everywhere — including session `{home}`.
> `[Unpin instead]` `[Kill]` `[Cancel]`

- **`{home}` derivation + fallback**: `home` is resolved at open time from the `homeSessionByKey` snapshot join (§ Board Tile Header — the same `ctx.sessionsByServer` join the header crumb uses), read through a ref (`homeSessionByKeyRef`) so `requestKillFocused` (declared above the memo) sees the current map. When `home` is not derivable (legacy pin / home died — window absent from the snapshot) the copy falls back to window-only ("This closes the window everywhere.").
- **Default focus on the SAFE action**: `[Unpin instead]` is the FIRST focusable element, so `Dialog` auto-focuses it; the dialog is fully keyboard-operable (Escape/Tab/backdrop via the shared `Dialog`).
- **Confirmed Kill is a WINDOW-kill**: `[Kill]` calls `executeKillWindow` (`useOptimisticAction` over `killWindow` → `POST /api/windows/{id}/kill`), destroying the window entity everywhere (home + pin links) in one call. Its `onSettled` schedules the board refetch (the self-heal for the no-`board-changed`-on-kill gap).
- **`[Unpin instead]`** invokes the shared unpin path (`unpin(server, windowId, board)`), the same reversible action the tile-header pin-glyph and `Board: Unpin Focused Pane` use — no confirmation.

The tile-header pin-glyph unpin stays **unconfirmed** (unpin is cheap to reverse). See § Chrome (Top Bar) → Close pane button for the top-bar ✕'s `onRequestKill` routing and § Boards Command Palette for the `board-kill-focused` entry.

### Board Autofit Toggle

A per-board **desktop** toggle that stretches panes to fill the row instead of using explicit pixel widths — the minimal-surface answer (Constitution IV: one button + one palette action, no settings page) to boards chronically under-using screen width with 2–3 panes on a wide monitor. Desktop `DesktopRow` only — the `MobileCarousel` is already one full-width `w-full` pane, so autofit is a **no-op on mobile** (no branch there).

**Persistence — `useBoardAutofit` (`app/frontend/src/hooks/use-board-autofit.ts`)**, mirroring the guard discipline of `use-pane-widths.ts`:

- Key `runkit:board-autofit:<board>` (exported prefix `BOARD_AUTOFIT_LOCALSTORAGE_PREFIX = "runkit:board-autofit:"`), **per-board** — enabling autofit on board A does not affect board B, and switching `board` reloads state via a `useEffect`-on-`board` (the same reload seam `usePaneWidths` uses).
- **"on" sentinel with key removal on off**: the literal string `"on"` is the ONLY value that reads as on; anything else (absent, malformed) reads off (window-undefined bail + `try/catch`, malformed-tolerant like `use-pane-widths.ts`). Turning autofit OFF **removes the key** (`localStorage.removeItem`) rather than storing `"off"` — the read is `getItem(...) === "on"`, so there is no `"off"` state to persist.
- **Default off** (no key stored → current per-pane-width behavior); the key is untouched until the setter runs.
- API: `useBoardAutofit(board) → { autofit, toggleAutofit }`; `toggleAutofit` flips + persists and round-trips across a fresh hook instance / reload.

**Layout branch — `DesktopRow` / `BoardPane` (`board-page.tsx`, `board-pane.tsx`)**. `BoardPage` owns `useBoardAutofit(name)` and passes `autofit` down to `DesktopRow`, which forwards it to each `BoardPane` and passes `showResizeHandle={!autofit}`:

- **Autofit ON**: `DesktopRow` passes **no pixel `width`** (`width={autofit ? undefined : getWidth(entry.windowId)}`); each pane root becomes `flex: 1 1 0` with `min-width: max(BOARD_PANE_MIN_WIDTH, calc(25% - 3px))` (import the `BOARD_PANE_MIN_WIDTH` constant from `use-pane-widths` — 280px — never hard-code) inside the existing `overflow-x-auto flex gap-1 p-1` row. Classes drop `w-full`/`shrink-0`; the flex+min-width in `style` drives sizing. Result: ≤4 panes stretch to share the row equally with no horizontal scrollbar; >4 panes floor at the 25% arm and the row scrolls exactly as today. Pure CSS — **no ResizeObserver on the row** — so window resize reflows live for free.
  - **Gap-adjusted floor** (DD): the literal `max(280px, 25%)` from the backlog would force `4×25% + 3×4px (gap-1) > 100%` → a 12px scrollbar at exactly 4 panes, contradicting the "max 4 visible" intent. `calc(25% - 3px)` (3 gaps × 4px ÷ 4 panes) makes exactly 4 panes fit flush.
  - **Verified** the percentage `min-width` resolves against the flex container's content box (the scrollport), NOT the scrolled content width — the containing block of a flex item is its flex container's content box, and `overflow-x: auto` does not change that. The backlog's JS-measurement fallback is therefore unneeded; the e2e asserts the resulting widths as a safety net.
- **Autofit OFF**: **exactly** the prior per-pane-width behavior — explicit pixel widths from `usePaneWidths.getWidth`, `shrink-0`, resize handles present.
- **Non-destructive round-trip**: the stored `runkit:board-widths:<board>` map is **never touched** by autofit (the `width` prop is merely not passed while on; `getWidth`/`setWidth` are not called through the autofit branch), so toggling OFF restores the exact hand-tuned layout.
- **`autofit?: boolean` prop on `BoardPane`** (not a wrapper div — DD): the pane root is the row's direct flex child AND the `rootRef` IntersectionObserver target (§ Desktop Relay-Connection Suspension), so a wrapper would break both contracts; the flag follows the existing optional-`width` pattern.

**Controls (Constitution V parity)** — a top-bar button and a palette action flip the same state:

- **Top-bar `BoardAutofitToggle`** (`top-bar.tsx`): a **board-only** L2-cluster toggle **between `Aa` (`TerminalFontControl`) and `✕` (`ClosePaneButton`)**, gated `mode === "board" && onToggleAutofit` (unlike Aa/✕ which are terminal+board). Mirrors the `FixedWidthToggle` vocabulary — `aria-pressed={autofit}`, `rk-glint` CRT-glint hover, `coarse:` touch sizing. See § Chrome (Top Bar) → Right cluster (L2).
- **Palette action** `Board: Toggle Autofit (on/off)` (`id: "board-toggle-autofit"`, `boardRouteActions` in `board-page.tsx`, label reflects state) → `toggleAutofit`.
- **State plumbing** — `BoardPage` publishes `autofit` + `onToggleAutofit: toggleAutofit` into the top-bar slot context (`useRegisterTopBarSlot`, the same channel carrying the board `focusedPane` + `onRequestKill` kill-dialog seam); `top-bar-slot-context.tsx` carries two optional board-mode fields `autofit?` / `onToggleAutofit?`; `RootTopBar` (`app.tsx`) maps `slot?.autofit`/`slot?.onToggleAutofit` → `TopBar` props (tolerant-empty — absent ⇒ no toggle rendered). (`260718-co9z`)

**Alignments (no code change)**:

- **`MAX_LIVE_RELAY_PANES = 4`** (§ Desktop Relay-Connection Suspension) equals the 4-visible max the 25% floor produces, so on plaintext origins autofit never forces a visible-but-paused pane; the focused pane is exempt from the cap anyway (`selectLivePanes`). >4 panes still overflow horizontally and off-screen panes still suspend.
- **xterm refit rides the existing `terminal-client.tsx` ResizeObserver** (no autofit-specific wiring): a container `ResizeObserver` rAF-debounces `fitAddon.fit()` + a paired `{type:"resize",cols,rows}` WS message; flex reflow (window resize, pin/unpin, toggle flips) changes each visible pane's size and fires that observer per pane.

**Tests**: unit `use-board-autofit.test.ts` (default-off, "on"-sentinel round-trip + key removal, per-board isolation, board-switch reload, malformed tolerance); Playwright `tests/e2e/board-autofit.spec.ts` + companion `.spec.md` (equal-fill/no-scroll at 2–3 panes, ~25%-floor/scroll at 5+, per-board persistence across reload, handles-hidden-while-on, top-bar button + palette action parity) — run via `just test-e2e`/`just pw` only.

### Board Pane Reorder

Desktop board panes are drag-reorderable, with full Cmd+K keyboard parity (Constitution V). Panes render in server `orderKey` order (`GET /api/boards/{name}`); reorder writes a new fractional-index key via `POST /api/boards/{name}/reorder` (see `architecture.md` § Boards Feature). **`MobileCarousel`** — swipe is navigation there, not reorder.

**Adapts the § Server-tile drag reorder pattern** (`use-server-reorder.ts`) into a sibling hook `useBoardPaneReorder(entries, board, reorder)` (`app/frontend/src/hooks/use-board-pane-reorder.ts`), inheriting its two hard-won fixes (derive-over-store override, self-target dragover acceptance). Key differences from server/session reorder:

- **Custom MIME `application/x-board-pane-reorder`** (`BOARD_PANE_REORDER_MIME`) — must not collide with `application/x-server-reorder`, `application/x-session-reorder`, or the window-move default-JSON payload. Guarded FIRST, before any acceptance (the shared guard-order invariant — see § Server-tile drag reorder).
- **Composite `server:windowId` key** — a board spans servers, so `windowId` alone is ambiguous; the override array, the drag payload, and the DnD/palette bookkeeping all key by `server:windowId` (matching the `key={`${entry.server}:${entry.windowId}`}` in `DesktopRow`).
- **Split handle/drop props** — `getHandleProps(server, windowId)` returns `{ handle, drop }` separately: `handle` (`draggable` + `onDragStart`/`onDragEnd`) goes on the pane HEADER only (`BoardHeader`) so a live xterm terminal never hijacks the drag or becomes the drag image; `drop` (`onDragOver`/`onDrop`) goes on the pane ROOT (`BoardPane`) so the preview updates and a release commits anywhere over a pane, not only the ~24px header strip. The header unpin button (a pin-glyph, § Board Tile Header) opts out (`draggable={false}` + `stopPropagation`) and the resize handle lives on the pane root outside the header, so neither is shadowed by the drag handle.
- **ONE `reorderPin` POST per move, no debounce** — fractional indexing means one authoritative call per completed move (`before`/`after` = the moved pane's new neighbours' windowIds, `null` at edges), so the drop is the single commit point. This is the deliberate contrast with server/session reorder's 250ms debounced full-order writes + drop-flush (there is no full-order sweep to coalesce). The `board-changed` SSE echo (refetched by `useBoardEntries`, 50ms debounce) reconciles the override away.
- **Committed-drop flag drives cancel-revert** — `committedRef` is set true only when `onDrop` fires the POST. `onDragEnd` clears the override when uncommitted (Escape / release outside any pane = revert to authoritative order, no phantom unpersisted order) but keeps it when committed (no snap-back — the SSE echo reconciles it). This is the one place the board hook diverges from the no-drag-end-clear discipline of server/session reorder: with drop as the single commit point, native HTML5 cancel semantics = revert, so the no-snap-back rule applies only to committed drops and SSE reconciles.
- **Rollback on POST rejection** — `usePinActions().reorder` shows its toast AND **rethrows** (pin/unpin swallow — they have no client-side optimistic order to revert); the DnD hook `.catch()`es to clear the override and the palette move `.catch()`es to avoid an unhandled rejection, so a rejected reorder reverts the display to the authoritative order instead of leaving the failed order rendered.
- **`onDrop` derives neighbours inline from the final override order** (not from `computeReorderNeighbors` over the authoritative list) — the override is what the user sees and is robust to mid-drag entry churn where index arithmetic over the authoritative array is not. The pure `computeReorderNeighbors`/`computeMoveNeighbors` helpers (`src/lib/board-reorder.ts`, mirroring `palette-move.ts`) are the PALETTE path's arithmetic (`computeReorderNeighbors` has one live caller, `computeMoveNeighbors`, so it is kept with a doc comment, not dead).

**Palette parity** — `Board: Move Focused Pane Left/Right` (`boardRouteActions`, boundary-hidden per § Boards Command Palette) act on the focused pane, compute neighbours via `computeMoveNeighbors`, and fire the same single-POST path as DnD. No wraparound (hidden, not disabled, at the edges).

**Focus tracked by `server:windowId` key + a user-intent gate** (`board-page.tsx`, the load-bearing seam):

- Focus is tracked by the focused pane's **`server:windowId` key** (`focusedKeyRef`), NOT by positional index. A single focus-authority effect reconciles `focusedIndex` from `focusedKeyRef` on every order change (via `focusedIndexForKey`) so the focused pane's identity survives reorders — own palette move, own drop echo, AND a reorder arriving from another client (key-follow, not index-follow). The palette `moveFocusedPane` deliberately does NOT bump `focusedIndex`; the reconcile does it once the new order settles (§ Design Decisions → Board pane focus tracks by key, not index).
- **Imperative `.focus()` fires only on a TRUE user-intent flag** — this is the board-route form of the "SSE must not steal focus" invariant, mirroring the sidebar tree's `focusMovedRef` gate literally (see § Keyboard Navigation & Tree ARIA). `useBoardEntries` refetches a fresh `entries` array on EVERY `board-changed` SSE from ANY board on ANY server, so gating focus on *index change alone* is insufficient: a remote-driven reconcile (a `board-changed` from another client whose reorder/pin/unpin ahead of the focused pane shifts its index) changes the index without any local user intent and would steal DOM focus into the xterm while the user types in the docked compose strip / pin-popover / palette / another surface. The gate is `shouldFocusPane(focusIntentRef.current, prevFocusedIndexRef.current, focusedIndex)` (`focusIntentRef` = the user-intent flag beside `focusedKeyRef`): it fires `paneRefs.current[focusedIndex]?.focus()` only when a user-driven action set the flag AND the index genuinely changed. A passive `board-changed` refetch never sets the flag, so a remote reconcile reconciles the index but never moves DOM focus; board load never auto-focuses pane 0 (no intent, seed index unchanged).
- **Intent sites set the flag; same-index actions focus imperatively without it.** `focusIntentRef.current = true` is set at each user-intent site that will change `focusedIndex`: keyboard cycle (`Cmd/Ctrl + ]` / `[`), the two palette cycle actions (`Board: Cycle Pane Focus →` / `←`), and `handlePaneClick` on a *different* pane — each guarded so the flag is only set when the index will actually change (the single-pane modulo cycle is guarded by `entries.length >= 2`; clicking the *already-focused* pane focuses its terminal imperatively at the call site WITHOUT setting the flag, since no state change would consume it). The flag is cleared on the settled pass whenever it runs with the flag set (regardless of index change), so a set flag can never linger past its triggering render; the `orderChanged` key-reconcile early-return pass leaves the flag untouched so it survives to the re-entered settled pass.
- **The own-move follow is preserved through the async echo via `reorderWithFollow`** — a board-page-level callback wrapping `usePinActions().reorder` that sets `focusIntentRef.current = true` before delegating and clears it (`false`) in the `.catch` failure path (no echo will arrive). BOTH own-move paths route through this single seam: the palette `moveFocusedPane` and the `reorder` prop threaded to `DesktopRow` (DnD drop). An own move has no synchronous index change — the display reorders only when the `board-changed` echo arrives — so the flag is deliberately set *ahead* of the echo: the echo's reconcile bumps the index (early-return pass, flag untouched), the re-entered settled pass consumes the flag, and the moved pane is focused. The accepted residual is a one-echo-round-trip race window: a remote event interleaving before the own echo could consume the flag early, producing a single benign own-pane focus-follow (not a focus steal). `shouldFocusPane`/`focusedIndexForKey` are unit-tested in `board-reorder.test.ts`.

**e2e** (`app/frontend/tests/e2e/board-reorder.spec.ts` + `.spec.md`) mirrors `server-reorder.spec.ts`: it exercises the reorder ENDPOINT + `board-changed` SSE echo + a reload-free GET-order assertion against the live backend, NOT a native HTML5 drag simulation — synthetic Playwright DnD is unreliable (the session-reorder drag spec is `test.fixme`, never passed) and `page.reload()` does not commit under the SPA's long-lived SSE. The drag handlers, MIME guard, reconcile, cancel-revert, failure-rollback, and neighbour arithmetic are Vitest-covered (`use-board-pane-reorder.test.ts`, `board-reorder.test.ts`). Backend cross-server neighbour resolution is Go-tested (`router_test.go` `TestLookupNeighbourKeys_*`).

### Desktop Relay-Connection Suspension

On plaintext origins, `DesktopRow` suspends off-screen panes' terminal streams so the live count stays bounded — the desktop analogue of the mobile carousel's `paused={idx !== carouselIndex}` pause. The mechanism mirrors the mobile pause: a paused pane unmounts its `TerminalClient`; scroll-back re-mounts and re-opens, replaying terminal content. Suspension is NOT a closed WebSocket per pane — all panes share the ONE `/ws/terminals` socket, so a paused pane's `TerminalClient` unmount sends a `close` **control op** for its stream (not a socket teardown) and a resumed pane sends a fresh `open` op. This avoids the board pane-resize suspension-drop reconnect cost (memory `board-pane-resize-suspension-drop`). The mux + state socket already hold the tab to a fixed 2 WebSockets, so the visibility-pause + cap now bound how many PTY attaches (tmux clients) are live at once rather than the HTTP/1.1 pool. The unmount-on-pause seam is transport-agnostic. (`260531-rus8`, `260717-803u`)

- **Plaintext-only gate** — the entire feature is gated on `plaintext = window.location.protocol === "http:"` (`board-page.tsx`). On HTTPS/h2 (production via Tailscale) every desktop pane stays live (`paused={false}`), no `IntersectionObserver` is created, and no cap applies — behavior is byte-identical to before this change. The ~6-connection ceiling is a plaintext HTTP/1.1 artifact (h2 multiplexes; the relay WS limit is ~255), so the fix activates only where the problem exists (E2E/dev `http://localhost:3020`, raw-port `http://...` access)
- **Visibility via `IntersectionObserver`** — on plaintext origins, a single observer rooted on the `rowRef` horizontal-scroll container drives each pane's `paused` prop from viewport intersection. Panes are keyed to indices via a `data-paneIndex` attribute on each pane's root element (forwarded through a `rootRef` callback prop on `BoardPane`, kept distinct from the `paneRefs` imperative `BoardPaneHandle` so neither contract leaks into the other). The observer effect mirrors the existing wheel-handler effect's setup/cleanup discipline (`observer.disconnect()` on unmount) and re-subscribes when the pane count changes
- **Pre-warm margin** — the observer uses `RELAY_PREWARM_ROOT_MARGIN` = `` `0px ${BOARD_PANE_DEFAULT_WIDTH}px` `` (one pane-width of horizontal `rootMargin`, vertical 0) so a pane is kept live slightly before it enters and after it leaves the strict viewport, preventing pause/resume thrash (and the `[reconnecting...]` flicker) on a quick scroll-past. No debounce in v1 — add one only if thrash is observed during Playwright tuning
- **Live-pane cap** — simultaneously-live (unpaused) relay panes are capped at `MAX_LIVE_RELAY_PANES = 4` (named constant, not a magic number), backstopping the observer for the wide-monitor case where more panes fit on-screen than the budget allows (`1 SSE + 4 relay + headroom` stays under 6). When visibility alone would leave more than the cap live, the **least-recently-focused** visible panes are paused first. The selection logic is the pure `selectLivePanes` helper in `app/frontend/src/components/board/select-live-panes.ts` (colocated unit tests), consuming the visible-index set, the focused index, the most-recently-focused order, and the cap; `DesktopRow` passes `paused={!livePanes.has(idx)}` (and short-circuits to `paused={false}` when `livePanes === null`, i.e. on secure origins). The MRU order folds the current `focusedIndex` to the front during render (`useMemo` keyed on `focusedIndex`) so cap eviction never sees a stale focus
- **Focused pane always live** — `selectLivePanes` adds `focusedIndex` unconditionally before filling the remaining slots, so the focused pane is exempt from both visibility-pause and the cap. This preserves `Cmd+]`/`Cmd+[` cycling (cycling to an off-screen paused pane re-selects it → unpauses → re-mounts → imperative `focus()` via `paneRefs`) and BottomBar targeting of the focused terminal
- **Composes with the sibling change** — `260531-m3pl` removes the xterm chunk-fetch pressure from the runtime connection budget while this change bounds the persistent relay streams; together they fit the board route under the 6-connection cap on plaintext origins (the original board-route E2E hang root cause). `MobileCarousel` is untouched — it already suspended correctly

### Mobile Single-Pane Carousel

Below the `min-width: 640px` breakpoint (matching the existing project mobile convention), the BoardPage renders a single-pane swipe carousel:

- One pane fills the viewport width
- Touch swipe left/right cycles in `orderKey` order; threshold 40px on `touchstart` → `touchend` `clientX` delta
- **Off-screen panes pause** by unmounting their `TerminalClient` so the WebSocket closes; on swipe-in, the pane re-mounts and the terminal reattaches
- A pagination dot strip indicates the current pane index (no wrap on edges in v1)

### Sidebar Boards Section (`app/frontend/src/components/sidebar/boards-section.tsx`)

Renders **at the very top of the sidebar** — the section order is **Boards → Servers → Sessions**. Visible on every route that mounts `<Sidebar>` (`/$server/...` and `/board/$name`). The board route reuses the same `BoardsSection` component for board switching; there is no separate BoardPage listing. (`260509-17m3`)

- **Always visible**, regardless of `boards.length` or current route
- **Hint mode** — when `boards.length === 0`, the body shows a one-line hint `Pin a window to start a board` (`text-xs text-text-secondary`) verbatim from 4vuv's copy. Applies on every route, not only on `/board/<name>` — placing Boards at the top would cause a layout shift if the section hid/showed dynamically (Servers would jump up, then back down when the first board materializes)
- **First board materializes** — hint replaced by a single board row in place; no other section's vertical position shifts
- **Last board removed** — section reverts to hint mode; no layout shift to ServerPanel or Sessions

Each row: board name (left, truncate with ellipsis), pin count (right, muted), highlighted background when current route matches `/board/<name>`. Clicking the row navigates to `/board/<name>`. **Drag-reorderable** (`260708-a2qd`): rows render `orderedBoards` from the shared `useBoardListReorder` hook with `getTileProps(b.name)` spread onto each, and the dragged row dims via `opacity-50` — see § Board-list drag reorder.

**Dynamic default-open + header PinIcon**: the `CollapsiblePanel` uses `defaultOpen={boards.length > 0}` (storageKey `runkit-panel-boards`) so the panel opens live once the first board exists and a fresh pin surfaces where it landed, while an explicit user toggle always wins — this falls out of `useLocalStorageBoolean(storageKey, defaultValue)`, which consults `defaultValue` only when no stored key exists and resyncs its effect on `defaultValue` change (see § Sessions-pane scope → Sessions-scope hooks for the shared-hook family — `useLocalStorageBoolean` and its enum sibling). The panel `headerRight` renders the shared outline `PinIcon` (`components/pin-icon.tsx` — the same glyph the window-row pin button and board-tile-header unpin use) leading the `{boards.length}` count, visually linking the window-row pin affordance to where pins land; the icon stays present in zero-board hint mode (the count is dropped there, the icon is not). BOARDS keeps its name (the "Board" vocabulary is load-bearing — `/board/$name`, the `Board:` heading/palette, `/api/boards`); discoverability comes from default-open + the glyph, not a rename to "PINNED WINDOWS". (`260718-gxrq`)

### Sidebar Pin Icon on Window Rows

`window-row.tsx` gains a pin icon button that follows the existing icon-on-hover pattern in the sidebar:

- **Hover-revealed** (always visible on touch devices via `coarse:opacity-100`)
- **Filled** when the window is pinned to ANY board; **outline** when not pinned (computed via `useWindowPins(server, windowId)` which watches every board). The glyph is the shared thumbtack `PinIcon` (`components/pin-icon.tsx`) — the same component the board tile header renders in its `slashed` unpin variant (§ Board Tile Header). **Accent-colored** when the row is pinned to the currently-viewed board (`isPinnedToActiveBoard`), monochrome `text-text-secondary` otherwise — this glyph carries the active-board cue (there is no left border; § Row Anatomy, § Active-Board Highlight in Sessions Tree)
- **Click opens `PinPopover`** (`app/frontend/src/components/sidebar/pin-popover.tsx`) anchored to the icon: an optional **"Go to {board}" navigation row** at the top when the window is pinned, then the list of existing boards (each row pins or unpins on click, ordered last-used-first — see below), plus an inline "Pin to new board…" text input with an adjacent **Pin button** — the mouse submit path, mirroring Enter exactly (`handleSubmitNew`: non-empty input pins to that name, empty input pins to the ↵-hinted last-used board; disabled when Enter would be a no-op). Enter validates against the board-name regex and creates the board on first pin. Validation errors surface inline. Outside-click + Escape dismiss. Sizing is sidebar-compact: `min-w-[160px] max-w-[220px]`, `text-xs` rows at `min-h-[24px] coarse:min-h-[36px]` (matching BoardsSection row density). (`260718-co9z`)
- **Pinned-row → board navigation is a TWO-STEP** (indicator → popover → "Go to {board}" row): a pinned window's pin indicator is a path to the owning board, but navigation lives on a dedicated popover row rather than hijacking the indicator's click (§ Design Decisions → Pin-indicator navigation is a popover row). A window has exactly one pin-session → exactly one board, so the row names that single board. `PinPopover` takes a `pinnedBoard?: string` + `onNavigateToBoard?(board)` — `sidebar/index.tsx` derives the reverse `windowId → board` lookup by extending `useWindowPins` (the per-board pin-map aggregation) and wires `onNavigateToBoard` to navigate to `/board/{board}`. Keyboard/palette-reachable per Constitution V. (`260718-co9z`)

**Cold-start & last-used friction reduction** (`260718-gxrq`): the popover removes the invent-a-name-then-type friction of a cold start and makes bare Enter meaningful once boards exist.
  - **Cold start (`boards.length === 0`)** — the new-board input is pre-filled with the default board name `main` (`DEFAULT_BOARD_NAME`) and its text is selected on autofocus (`inputRef.current.select()`), so a bare **Enter** immediately pins to a new board `main` (the existing `handleSubmitNew` path — no new submit logic) while typing any character replaces the selection, preserving the invent-a-name path. `ValidBoardName` accepts `main`. When boards exist the input stays empty (placeholder unchanged).
  - **Existing-board ordering** — the board list renders via `orderBoardsLastUsedFirst(boards, readLastPinnedBoard())` (`lib/last-pinned-board.ts`): the last-used board moves to the front when it is still a live board; remaining boards keep their `boards`-prop order; a stale value (board gone) is ignored. `lastUsed` is read once via `useMemo` when the popover opens (stable for its lifetime).
  - **Empty-input Enter → last-used** — when boards exist, the input is empty, and a valid last-used board exists (`emptyEnterTarget`), Enter pins to it and closes the popover; otherwise it stays a no-op (current behavior). Unreachable on cold start (input pre-filled). The last-used row (rendered first) carries a small `↵` hint (`aria-label="press Enter to pin here"`) so Enter's target is visible; an already-pinned board additionally shows a `✓`.
  - **Last-used persistence** — written on every successful pin from any entry point by `usePinActions.pin` → `writeLastPinnedBoard(board)` (see § Pin last-used preference), NOT by the popover itself.

### Active-Board Highlight in Sessions Tree

When the current route is `/board/<name>`, the cue for a window pinned to **that specific board** is the **accent-colored pin glyph** — NOT a left border (the row carries no accent border since the axis split; see § Row Anatomy). `WindowRow` renders the persistent filled pin glyph accent-colored when `isPinnedToActiveBoard`, monochrome otherwise. Pins to other boards show a monochrome filled glyph. The pin icon's filled state (pinned to ANY board) is independent of the accent. On non-board routes, no window is pinned-to-active-board, so all pins render monochrome.

### Pin Entry Points

| Entry point | Location | Notes |
|-------------|----------|-------|
| Sidebar pin icon | `WindowRow` (every server's window rows in the unified sidebar — server routes and board routes alike) | Hover-revealed; popover with board picker + inline input (cold-start prefill + last-used-first ordering + empty-Enter-to-last-used) (`260718-gxrq`) |
| Command palette | `boardActions` block in `app.tsx` (AppShell mount) and BoardPage's own mount | Direct `Pin: Current Window to <board>` per unpinned board + `Pin: Current Window to new board…` (opens the popover) — the keyboard-first pin path (Constitution V). See § Boards Command Palette (`260718-gxrq`) |
| Board pane header | `BoardHeader` (only on `/board/<name>`) | Per-pane unpin button (a pin-glyph SVG, § Board Tile Header) — no confirmation (pin is cheap to restore) (`260715-6jwn`) |

There is no right-click context-menu pin entry — no context-menu pattern exists in the sidebar to extend, and the three entry points above cover all flows.

### Board Tile Header

`BoardHeader` (`components/board/board-header.tsx`) renders each board tile's header: a **home crumb** + an **unpin button**. The crumb is `{session} › {window}` — the top-bar crumb vocabulary (`›` separator) — where `{session}` is the pinned window's HOME session (dual presence keeps a pinned window linked into a visible session). `BoardHeader` takes a resolved `homeSession?: string` prop; `board-page.tsx` derives it at render time from the `homeSessionByKey` join (a `useMemo` over `ctx.sessionsByServer` mapping each `server:windowId` → its owning `ProjectSession.name`) and threads it through `board-pane.tsx`. When `homeSession` is absent (legacy pin / home died — window not in the snapshot) the header **falls back to window-only** (`{windowName} · {server}` / window name). The whole header is the drag handle for board pane reorder (`dragHandleProps`, § Board Pane Reorder); the unpin button opts out (`draggable={false}` + `e.stopPropagation()` on click) so a click there unpins rather than starting a drag, and does not refocus the pane. `aria-label={`Unpin ${windowName || windowId} from board`}`, `title="Unpin from board"`, no confirmation dialog (pin is cheap to restore — contrast the confirm-gated top-bar Kill, § Board Kill Confirm Dialog). Wired from `board-page.tsx`'s `onUnpin` per tile (`POST /api/boards/{name}/unpin`). (`260718-co9z`)

**Pin-glyph icon**: the button renders the shared **`PinIcon`** (`components/pin-icon.tsx`) in its **`slashed`** variant — the thumbtack outline crossed by a diagonal `line` = "remove the pin", not a text `×`. A `×` would read as a destructive close/kill, misleading since the top-bar ✕ is a (confirm-gated) window-kill (§ Close pane button / § Board Kill Confirm Dialog); the slashed pin truthfully signals the safe, reversible unpin. `PinIcon` is THE single pin shape for every board-pin affordance: the sidebar window-row pin button renders the same component (`filled` = pinned-to-any-board, outline = not pinned), so pin and unpin read as two states of one affordance. Hand-rolled inline SVG (16×16 viewBox rendered at 12px so strokes pixel-align, `stroke="currentColor"` `strokeWidth={1.5}`, round caps/joins) per the project's no-icon-library pattern (matching top-bar `SplitButton`/`HelpLink`). The `slashed` variant is always unfilled — a currentColor slash over a currentColor fill would vanish in the overlap. Non-icon behavior: non-draggable, stopPropagation, aria/title, no-confirm. (`260715-6jwn`)

### Boards Command Palette (`Board:` prefix)

`boardActions: PaletteAction[]` is composed in a dedicated `useMemo` block in `app.tsx`, between `windowActions` and `viewActions`:

```ts
const paletteActions = useMemo(
  () => [...sessionActions, ...windowActions, ...boardActions, ...viewActions, ...terminalFontActions, ...themeActions, ...configActions, ...updateActions, ...serverActions, ...pushActions, ...windowSwitchActions, ...agentActions],
  [...]
);
```

(`pushActions` is the Web Push opt-in block — see § Notifications (Web Push opt-in); `updateActions` is the `run-kit: Dismiss Update Notice` block — see § Update Notification, folded in after `statusRefreshActions`, followed by `checkActions` (the two `run-kit: Check for Updates…` commands — § On-demand check commands), then `maintenanceActions` (`run-kit: Update Now`/`Restart Daemon`) then `versionActions` (`run-kit: Version — v…` — see § Steady-state version surfaces) before `serverActions`; `windowSwitchActions`/`agentActions` compose last.) (`260715-ifco`)

| Entry | Visibility | Action |
|-------|------------|--------|
| `Board: Switch to <name>` (one per board, `(current)` on the active one) | Always | Navigate to `/board/<name>` |
| `Pin: Current Window to <board>` (one per board the window is NOT already pinned to, ordered last-used-first) (`260718-gxrq`) | Only when `sessionName && currentWindow && server` | Direct pin via `usePinActions.pin` — the keyboard-first pin path (Cmd+K → type → Enter; §2c success toast is the feedback). Built by the pure `buildPinActions` (`lib/palette-pin.ts`) — see § Pin palette actions |
| `Pin: Current Window to new board…` (`id: pin-current-new-board`) | Only when `sessionName && currentWindow && server` | Dispatches `pin-popover:open` to the matching `WindowRow` (free-text entry needs the popover — the palette has no value input); it carries the popover-opening role for pinning to a new board (`260718-gxrq`) |
| `Board: Unpin Current Window` | Only when current window is pinned to ≥1 board | Unpins from all boards the current window is pinned to (single-action — no per-board picker in v1) |
| `Board: Leave Board View` | Only on `/board/<name>` | Navigate to last viewed window route, or `/` if none |
| `Board: Cycle Pane Focus →` | Only on `/board/<name>` and ≥1 pane | Same as `Cmd+]` |
| `Board: Cycle Pane Focus ←` | Only on `/board/<name>` and ≥1 pane | Same as `Cmd+[` |
| `Board: Unpin Focused Pane` (`260704-9o7k`) | Only on `/board/<name>` and ≥1 pane | Unpins the focused entry via the shared `unpinFocused` handler (`onSelect: unpinFocused`) — non-destructive, NOT a kill. Keyboard parity for the **tile-header pin-glyph unpin** (the top-bar ✕ is a kill), not the ✕ (`260715-6jwn`) |
| `Board: Split Focused Pane Vertical` (`260715-6jwn`) | Only on `/board/<name>` and ≥1 pane | `executeSplit(focusedPane.server, .windowId, true, .cwd)` — `splitWindow` with `horizontal: true`, mirroring the terminal *palette*'s Vertical→`horizontal:true` mapping (the documented top-bar-chip-vs-palette flag divergence, left out of scope). Keyboard parity for the board SplitButtons (Constitution V) |
| `Board: Split Focused Pane Horizontal` (`260715-6jwn`) | Only on `/board/<name>` and ≥1 pane | `executeSplit(focusedPane.server, .windowId, false, .cwd)` — `horizontal: false`; mirror of Vertical |
| `Board: Kill Focused Pane` (`id: board-kill-focused`) | Only on `/board/<name>` and ≥1 pane | `requestKillFocused` — opens the **kill confirm dialog** (§ Board Kill Confirm Dialog) rather than firing immediately; confirmed Kill is a window-kill (`killWindow` → `POST /api/windows/{id}/kill`) whose `onSettled` schedules `refetch()`. Keyboard parity for the board ✕ (Constitution V) (`260718-co9z`) |
| `Board: Move up` / `Board: Move down` (`260708-a2qd`) | Only on `/board/<name>`, boundary-hidden (not first / not last) | Reorder the CURRENT board in the board list — keyboard/touch parity for the board-list drag (Constitution V). Computes the full order via `computeMoveOrder` and POSTs `setBoardOrder`; see § Board-list drag reorder + § Command Palette Move up/down |
| `Board: Move Focused Pane Left` (`260708-rmiq`) | Only on `/board/<name>` when `focusedIndex > 0` (hidden at the left edge — not disabled) | Moves the focused pane one slot left — fires the same single `reorder(...)` POST as DnD, computing `before`/`after` via `computeMoveNeighbors` (§ Board Pane Reorder). No wraparound. Keyboard parity for the drag reorder (Constitution V) |
| `Board: Move Focused Pane Right` (`260708-rmiq`) | Only on `/board/<name>` when `focusedIndex < entries.length - 1` (hidden at the right edge) | Moves the focused pane one slot right — mirror of Move Left |
| `Board: Toggle Autofit (on/off)` (`260708-738w`, `id: board-toggle-autofit`) | Only on `/board/<name>` (label reflects the current state) | Flips the per-board desktop autofit preference (same state the top-bar `BoardAutofitToggle` reflects — Constitution V parity). Desktop layout only; a no-op on the mobile carousel. See § Board Autofit Toggle |

**Limits**: The right-click context menu pin entry is not implemented (use sidebar pin icon, command palette, or board pane header). Hover-to-focus is disabled. Pane reorder ships via DnD + the Move Focused Pane Left/Right palette entries above (§ Board Pane Reorder). (`260708-rmiq`)

The AppShell palette mount carries `Board: Switch to <name>` + the `Pin: Current Window to <board>` direct-pin set + `Pin: Current Window to new board…` + `Board: Unpin Current Window` (`260718-gxrq`). The BoardPage's own palette mount (`boardRouteActions` useMemo in `board-page.tsx`) carries `Switch to <name>` + `Leave Board View` + the boundary-hidden `Board: Move up/down` (`260708-a2qd`) + the entries-gated `Cycle Pane Focus →/←` + `Unpin Focused Pane` (`260704-9o7k`) + the entries-gated `Board: Split Focused Pane Vertical/Horizontal` + `Board: Kill Focused Pane` (`260718-co9z`) + the boundary-gated `Move Focused Pane Left/Right` (`260708-rmiq`; Left pushed only when `focusedIndex > 0`, Right only when `focusedIndex < entries.length - 1`; the cycle/unpin/split/kill/move-pane entries all sit inside a single `entries.length > 0` guard) + the always-present `Board: Toggle Autofit (on/off)` (`260708-738w`, § Board Autofit Toggle — parity for the top-bar `BoardAutofitToggle`, outside the `entries.length > 0` guard) — board-route-only entries that AppShell's palette can't surface because the board route does not render AppShell. The split/kill/unpin actions all consume shared `board-page.tsx` handlers rather than re-deriving state (parsimony): the `focusedPane` memo (`entries[focusedIndex]` → `{server, windowId, cwd}`, cwd from the active pane, hoisted above `boardRouteActions`) feeds the split executors (`executeSplit`, `useOptimisticAction`-wrapped `splitWindow` with `addToast` on error) and the kill opener `requestKillFocused` (which routes through the confirm dialog whose confirmed Kill runs `executeKillWindow` — `killWindow` — scheduling `refetch()` via `onSettled`, § Board Kill Confirm Dialog), and the shared `unpinFocused` callback backs both the palette unpin and (via the tile header) the header unpin — **plus** the globally-meaningful actions duplicated in because the board mounts its own palette: the `Go:` nav trio (`Go: Back` / `Go: Forward` / `Go: Host` via `buildNavActions("board", "", …)`, § `Go:` palette parity), the terminal-font trio (Increase / Decrease / Reset terminal font — the board's panes are live terminals, § Terminal Font Size), then `View: Refresh Page`, `Help: Documentation`, and `...updateEntries` (`buildUpdateActions`, § Update Notification) — with `...checkEntries` (the two `run-kit: Check for Updates…` commands, § On-demand check commands), `...maintenanceEntries`, and `...versionEntries` LAST. The returned array composes as `[...switchEntries, ...conditional, ...navEntries, ...fontEntries, refreshEntry, helpEntry, ...updateEntries, ...checkEntries, ...maintenanceEntries, ...versionEntries]` — the nav trio sits after the board-specific entries and before the font trio, mirroring AppShell's `navActions` group ordering. `server` is `""` (board mode never emits `Go: tmux Server` — its gate is `mode === "terminal" && server`), so `onTmuxServer` is an unreachable no-op. The board is the degraded-relay recovery scenario — N live relay WebSockets — and a top-bar RefreshButton also renders in board mode (L3 always-block), so the palette refresh entry is the keyboard-parity form. Below `sm` the top-bar UpdateChip is hidden, so the board palette is a phone user's only update surface on `/board/$name`. (`260703-p29w`, `260704-hmd0`, `260704-9o7k`, `260713-4zap`, `260719-i996-nav-actions-board-wiring`)

### Pin palette actions (`Pin:` prefix)

`buildPinActions` (`app/frontend/src/lib/palette-pin.ts`) is the pure, dependency-free builder for the command-palette pin actions, following the `lib/palette-move.ts` / `lib/palette-version.ts` / `lib/palette-view.ts` convention (label composition, exclusion, and ordering are unit-testable without mounting the shell). Signature `buildPinActions(boards, alreadyPinned, lastUsed, onPin, onOpenNewBoardPopover): PaletteAction[]`:

- One **direct-pin** action per board the current window is NOT already pinned to — `id: pin-current-<board>`, label `Pin: Current Window to <board>`, ordered last-used-first via `orderBoardsLastUsedFirst` (over the already-pinned-filtered set). `onSelect` → `onPin(board)`.
- The **new-board variant** last — `id: pin-current-new-board` (`PIN_NEW_BOARD_ACTION_ID`), label `Pin: Current Window to new board…`, `onSelect` → `onOpenNewBoardPopover()`. Always present (the only free-text entry seam).
- Edge cases: window pinned to every board, or zero boards → only the new-board variant.

**Wiring** (`app.tsx` `boardActions` useMemo): gated on `sessionName && currentWindow && server` so the actions are available on the terminal/server route for the current window. `onPin` calls `usePinActions.pin(server, windowId, board)`; `onOpenNewBoardPopover` dispatches the `pin-popover:open` CustomEvent (`{ detail: { server, windowId } }`) that the matching `WindowRow` handles. `alreadyPinned` = `currentWindowPinnedBoards` (derived from the cross-board pin map); ordering uses `readLastPinnedBoard()`. The per-board entries provide the direct keyboard pin (Constitution V); the new-board variant carries the popover-opening role. (`260718-gxrq`)

### Pin last-used preference (`lib/last-pinned-board.ts`)

Client-side "last board a window was pinned to" preference — per-client only (Constitution II, no backend persistence), `runkit-*` key convention (`LAST_PINNED_BOARD_KEY = "runkit-last-pinned-board"`, alongside `runkit-terminal-font-size`, `runkit-update-dismissed`). Reads/writes are best-effort try/catch-noop (mirroring `lib/window-view.ts`) so private mode / quota / SSR never throw.

- `readLastPinnedBoard(): string | null` — value NOT validated against the live boards list here; callers filter it (a board disappears when its last pin is removed).
- `writeLastPinnedBoard(name: string): void` — called at the **single** pin site inside `usePinActions.pin` (see § Hooks (Frontend)) on every successful pin, so all entry points (popover, palette) keep the preference consistent.
- `orderBoardsLastUsedFirst(boards, lastUsed): BoardSummary[]` — returns `boards` with a valid live last-used board moved to the front; a stale/absent `lastUsed` (board gone, or `null`) is ignored and input order preserved; the input array is never mutated (fresh array on reorder, same reference on no-op). Consumed by both the popover ordering and `buildPinActions`.

### Post-pin success feedback + toast optional action

`usePinActions.pin` surfaces success feedback (before this it toasted only on error). On a successful pin it fires `addToast("Pinned to <board>", "info", { label: "View board", onSelect: () => navigate to /board/<board> })` — placed in the hook (not per call site) so every pin entry point gets the same feedback; the hook runs inside router context so it obtains `useNavigate` directly. `unpin`/`reorder` stay error-only.

This required a minimal extension to the **toast system** (`components/toast.tsx`, see § Error toast system): `ToastEntry`/`addToast` gain an optional `action?: { label: string; onSelect: () => void }` as a **THIRD positional argument** — `addToast(message, variant?, action?)`, NOT an options object — which preserves all existing positional call sites with zero churn. The action renders as a keyboard-focusable `<button>` inside the toast body (the toast body is already `pointer-events-auto`); selecting it dismisses the toast then runs `onSelect`.

### Command Palette View actions (`View:` prefix)

`viewActions: PaletteAction[]` (`useMemo` in `app.tsx`) is the AppShell palette's `View:`-prefixed block, composed into `paletteActions` between `boardActions` and `terminalFontActions` (see § Boards Command Palette). Its static entries are:

| Entry | Visibility | Action |
|-------|------------|--------|
| `View: Text Input` | Only when `sessionName` is set (a terminal is in view) | Toggles the docked compose strip (`toggleComposeStrip`) — palette parity for the `>_` chip (§ Docked Compose Strip) |
| `View: Terminal` / `View: Web` / `View: Chat` | Each shown only when its lens is **available** (`availableViews(currentWindow)`, which folds in the `chatProvider` gate) **AND not the current** (`resolvedView`) view; `shortcut` hint = `` Ctrl+` `` for `View: Chat` (and `View: Terminal` when LEAVING chat), else `⌘.` | `switchView(view)` — the per-viewer lens switch (no `@rk_type` mutation). Built by the ONE pure `buildViewActions(available, resolved, onSwitch)` (`lib/palette-view.ts`); see § Window Views (Lens Model) → Palette parity. There is no `@rk_type`-mutating `toggle-iframe-terminal` action (`260714-t97o`, `260714-r7rq`) |
| `View: Fixed Width (900px)` / `View: Full Width` | Always (label reflects `fixedWidth` state) | `toggleFixedWidth` |
| `View: Refresh Page` | Always (ungated) | `window.location.reload()` — a full page reload (`260703-p29w`) |

**`refresh-page` is appended ungated after `toggle-fixed-width`** — a full-page reload is meaningful on every AppShell route (tmux Server `/$server`, Terminal `/$server/$window`), unlike the terminal-only top-bar `RefreshButton` (§ Chrome (Top Bar)). It is the keyboard-reachable form of that recovery affordance (constitution V).

**Dual-mount duplication** — the app mounts **two** CommandPalettes (AppShell's, driven by `paletteActions`; and the board route's own, driven by `boardRouteActions`) and the board route does NOT render AppShell, so a globally-meaningful action is **registered in both** to be reachable everywhere (§ Design Decisions → Palette actions are duplicated across the two mounts). `refresh-page` follows the terminal-font-trio precedent (Increase/Decrease/Reset terminal font, § Terminal Font Size): both the trio and `refresh-page` live in `app.tsx`'s AppShell blocks AND in `board-page.tsx`'s `boardRouteActions` (§ Boards Command Palette). The `run-kit: Update…`/`Dismiss Update Notice` actions (§ Update Notification) follow the SAME convention — built by the shared pure `buildUpdateActions` helper (`lib/palette-update.ts`) and folded into BOTH `app.tsx`'s `updateActions` and `board-page.tsx`'s `boardRouteActions` — with the extra motivation that below `sm` the top-bar UpdateChip is hidden, so the board palette is a phone user's only update surface. The **Host page (`/`) mounts NO CommandPalette** (`HostOverviewPage` has no palette), so `refresh-page` is unreachable there. The reach comments at `app.tsx` `viewActions` and the `top-bar.tsx` `RefreshButton` docblock name the scope (AppShell palette + board palette; the Host page mounts none). (`260713-4zap`)

### Command Palette `PR: Refresh Status` action

`PR: Refresh Status` is the keyboard-first parity (Constitution §V) for the PANE-header refresh button (§ Collapsible Panels → WindowPanel). It triggers the same `refreshStatus()` → `POST /api/status/refresh` best-effort kick of both PR pollers (fresh state via SSE).

It follows the established **pure-builder** convention (mirrors `lib/palette-view.ts` / `lib/palette-update.ts`): the label/id live in `buildStatusRefreshAction(onRefresh)` (`lib/palette-status-refresh.ts`, colocated `.test.ts`) — a single `{ id: "status-refresh", label: "PR: Refresh Status", onSelect: onRefresh }` action whose body is the caller-supplied `onSelect`. `app.tsx` memoizes it as a `statusRefreshActions: PaletteAction[]` group (`buildStatusRefreshAction(() => void refreshStatus().catch(() => {}))`, empty deps — the callback closes over the static import) and folds it into the AppShell `paletteActions` aggregation (between `configActions` and `updateActions`, in both the array spread and its dependency list). **AppShell-only** (not dual-mounted into `board-page.tsx`'s `boardRouteActions`) — the refresh is server-global but the affordance is labeled around the PANE panel, which the board route does not render; the top-bar/PANE surfaces cover the board user. The label is `PR:`-prefixed (scope honesty — it refreshes PR/status freshness, not "all pane stats"; the other PANE registers are already fresh within ~7.5s).

### Hooks (Frontend)

| Hook | File | Returns |
|------|------|---------|
| `useBoards()` | `hooks/use-boards.ts` | `{ boards, isLoading, error }`. Initial `listBoards()` on mount; subscribes to `board-changed` SSE on every server returned by `listServers()` (boards are server-scoped, but the board LIST is summarized across servers, so it attaches all to catch each one's pin/unpin/reorder events); 50ms debounce coalesces rapid events; preserves last good value on transient error (`260602-qn62`) |
| `useBoardEntries(name)` | `hooks/use-boards.ts` | `{ entries, isLoading, error, refetch }`. Initial `getBoard(name)`; subscribes on all known servers (the board list spans servers, so a pin/unpin on any server may affect this board); same debounce + error tolerance. `refetch` (= `fetchEntries`) forces a re-fetch bypassing the SSE debounce — the board-mode kill self-heal (a window-killing ✕ collapses a pin-session with no `board-changed` event) calls it to drop the now-dead tile (`260715-6jwn`) |
| `usePinActions(board?)` | `hooks/use-pin-actions.ts` | `{ pin, unpin, reorder }` stable callbacks; optimistic — SSE re-broadcast reconciles. `pin` on success writes last-used (`writeLastPinnedBoard`) and fires the `info` "Pinned to <board>" + "View board" toast (`260718-gxrq`, § Post-pin success feedback); `unpin`/`reorder` toast on error only (`reorder` rethrows so the caller can roll back its optimistic order) |
| `usePaneWidths(boardName, sidebarWidth)` | `hooks/use-pane-widths.ts` | `{ getWidth, setWidth }`; reads/writes `localStorage["runkit:board-widths:<name>"]`; clamps to `[280, viewport - sidebar]`; default 480px |
| `useBoardAutofit(board)` (`260708-738w`) | `hooks/use-board-autofit.ts` | `{ autofit, toggleAutofit }`; per-board desktop autofit preference in `localStorage["runkit:board-autofit:<board>"]` ("on" sentinel; OFF removes the key); default off; reloads on `board` change (mirrors `usePaneWidths`). Never touches `runkit:board-widths:<board>`. See § Board Autofit Toggle |
| `useIsMobile()` | `hooks/use-is-mobile.ts` | `boolean`; `matchMedia("(max-width: 640px)")` listener |
