| `useActiveBoardName()` | `hooks/use-active-board.ts` | active board name from `/board/<name>` route, else `null` |
| `useWindowPins(server, windowId)` | `hooks/use-window-pins.ts` | list of boards the window is pinned to; drives the pin-icon filled state |
| `useNow()` | `hooks/use-now.ts` | current epoch seconds (`Math.floor(Date.now()/1000)`); self-ticks every 1s via `setInterval` (cleared on unmount), re-rendering ONLY the calling leaf. Display-only clock — NOT data polling. Scope to duration leaves so the tick never re-renders ancestors; see § Render Performance (`260613-ect6`) |
| `useUpdateNotification()` (`260713-4zap`) | `contexts/session-context.tsx` (exported alongside the provider) | `{ qualifies, showChip, tools, key, singleRunKit, latest, current, updateNow, dismissUpdate, daemonVersion, brew, forceUpdateNow, restartNow }` — the DERIVED update-notification display shape read by the top-bar `UpdateChip` + the palette `buildUpdateActions`/`buildMaintenanceActions` callers (and the connection-dot title). Reads `SessionContext` via `useContext` DIRECTLY (provider-tolerant — never throws outside the provider; each field falls back). `tools` = matched-tool set (`?? EMPTY_TOOLS` frozen module constant, so no per-render array churn); `qualifies = !isDev && tools.length > 0`; `showChip = qualifies && key !== updateDismissedKey` (composite-key dismissal); `singleRunKit` gates the single-run-kit `⬆ v{latest}` wording, `latest`/`current` non-null only then. Self-contained-consumer pattern (mirrors `usePushSubscription`). See § Update Notification |

## Notifications (Web Push opt-in)

Browser Web Push lets `rk notify` (and any process on the box) deliver an OS notification that reaches the user **even when the RunKit PWA tab is closed**. The end-to-end backend/delivery model lives in `architecture.md` § Web Push Notifications; this section covers the frontend opt-in surface. (`260615-xd9r`)

**The opt-in is a Cmd+K palette entry — NOT a bell.** Per Constitution §V (Keyboard-First) and §IV (Minimal Surface Area, no new route/settings page), the entire opt-in gesture is a single command-palette action. The label reflects subscription state and is **terminal-themed text**, never a bell icon:

| Palette label | When | Action |
|---------------|------|--------|
| `Notifications: Enable push` | Not yet subscribed | Runs the enable flow: `Notification.requestPermission()` → on `granted`, `getVapidPublicKey()` (`GET /api/push/vapid-public-key`) → `registration.pushManager.subscribe({userVisibleOnly: true, applicationServerKey})` → `subscribePush(sub)` (`POST /api/push/subscribe`) |
| `Notifications: Enabled ✓` | Already subscribed | Reflects state; the `✓` is a Unicode checkmark (terminal-themed glyph, not a bell) |

**Wiring**: `usePushSubscription()` (`app/frontend/src/hooks/use-push-subscription.ts`) returns `{ state, actions }` where `actions` is the `pushActions: PaletteAction[]` block; it is threaded into `app.tsx`'s `paletteActions` useMemo (spread just before `windowSwitchActions` — see § Boards Command Palette for the composition). The flow logic is the self-contained `app/frontend/src/lib/push.ts` module (`registerServiceWorker()`, `enablePushSubscription()`, `getPushState()`) plus the `getVapidPublicKey()`/`subscribePush()` client functions in `api/client.ts` — a separate module rather than inlining into the 1600-line, SSE-coupled `app.tsx`. The service worker (`public/sw.js`) is registered on app load from `main.tsx`.

**Fail-silent / secure-context**: every path is throw-free. `registerServiceWorker()` is guarded by `'serviceWorker' in navigator` and no-ops on unsupported / insecure-context environments. The enable flow aborts silently (a toast is acceptable) when permission is denied or push is unsupported / the context is insecure, sending no subscription. Web Push (service worker + `PushManager`) requires a **secure context — HTTPS or `localhost`**; the user typically hits run-kit on `localhost:3000` or behind a TLS proxy (both secure), but raw-IP plaintext access simply cannot subscribe (silently).

## Update Notification

Notifies the web-UI user when a newer release of ANY shll-toolkit tool (run-kit, shll, wt, idea, tu, hop, fab-kit) crosses its per-tool notify threshold, and offers a one-click upgrade that runs a SCOPED `shll update <matched…>` (fallback `rk update` self when shll is absent) — brew-upgrading the matched tools and restarting the daemon when run-kit is among them. **In-app ONLY — explicitly NO Web Push** (user-decided: Web Push is reserved for waiting agents; update notices must not buzz phones). Two surfaces — a top-bar L3 chip + command-palette actions — both self-contained consumers of one context hook, mirroring the `NotificationControl`/`usePushSubscription` precedent (no props threaded through `RootTopBar`→`TopBar`). The backend origin (SSE `event: version`/`event: update-available`, `POST /api/update`, `internal/updatecheck`) is in [architecture.md](/run-kit/architecture.md) § SSE Hub / § API Layer; this section is the frontend surface.

### Context state + `useUpdateNotification()` hook

`SessionContext` (`contexts/session-context.tsx`) owns the update state (it already owns the server-global SSE pool + `?metrics=1` stream, and `version`/`update-available` are server-global like `server-order`/`board-order`, so this reuses the exact fan-out — no second context). It exposes:

- `daemonVersion: string | null` — the running daemon version from `event: version` (no leading `v`), `null` until first seen.
- `updateAvailable: UpdateAvailable | null` — the current toolkit-update verdict from `event: update-available`, `null` when none. `UpdateAvailable = { tools: UpdateTool[], key: string, current: string, latest: string }` where `UpdateTool = { tool, current, latest, updateAvailable?, notable? }`: `tools` is the **FULL per-tool verdict list** — every tool with a pending update INCLUDING sub-threshold rows, each carrying the optional `updateAvailable?: boolean` (installed < latest) and `notable?: boolean` (crosses the notify threshold) flags parsed from the extended SSE payload; a MISSING flag is treated as `true` (an old-daemon payload listed only matched tools, so all its rows count as notable). Chip/palette consumers read the NOTABLE subset via `useUpdateNotification`'s filter. `key` = the composite dismissal key (sorted `tool@latest` pairs over the NOTABLE set, comma-joined); `current`/`latest` = the legacy run-kit-row fields, populated only when run-kit is in the notable set (transitional not-yet-reloaded-frontend compat).
- `updateDismissedKey: string | null` — the composite-key dismissal from localStorage `runkit-update-dismissed` (const `UPDATE_DISMISSED_KEY`), lazily read in a try/catch on mount.
- `updateNow(): Promise<void>` — thin wrapper over the `triggerUpdate()` client helper (`POST /api/update`; rejects on non-2xx).
- `dismissUpdate(): void` — writes the current `updateAvailable.key` to localStorage `runkit-update-dismissed` + sets `updateDismissedKey`; a no-op on an empty key.
- **`brew: boolean`** — whether the daemon is a Homebrew install, from the `event: version` `brew` field. Tracked in React `useState` (`isBrew`, drives palette visibility → must re-render, unlike the reload-decision refs below), **default `false` until the first version event is observed** (so the brew-gated `run-kit: Update Now` palette entry stays hidden on the brief pre-connect window; mirrors the `qualifies` absent-data-hidden gating). Set inside `applyVersion`.
- **`forceUpdateNow(): Promise<void>`** — thin wrapper over `triggerForceUpdate()` (`POST /api/update` body `{"force":true}`; rejects on non-2xx). Same shape as `updateNow`.
- **`restartNow(): Promise<void>`** — thin wrapper over `triggerRestart()` (`POST /api/restart`; rejects on non-2xx).

The `version`/`update-available` listeners are added on **BOTH** stream kinds — the per-server pool AND the dedicated `?metrics=1` subscription — server-global, applied idempotently (no `data.server` filter), exactly like `server-order`/`board-order`. Both call the pure-ish `applyVersion` / `applyUpdateAvailable` callbacks; malformed events are skipped. **`applyVersion(version, boot, brew)`** parses the payload as `{ version?, boot?, brew? }` **tolerantly** — `boot` passed only when `typeof data.boot === "string"` (else `null`), `brew` as `data.brew === true` (defaults `false`) — so an older daemon's boot-less/brew-less payload never breaks parsing or flips brew true. The `update-available` parse maps each `tools[]` row's optional `updateAvailable`/`notable` booleans onto `UpdateTool` — carried ONLY when the daemon sends real booleans (an old daemon's flag-less payload leaves them `undefined`, which consumers treat as `true`). **`applyUpdateAvailable(next)`** stores `next` but **dedups by composite `key`** (a re-delivery of the same matched set does not churn consumers) — AND handles a **CLEARED payload** (empty `key`) by clearing the stored state so the chip hides. It MUST NOT early-return on an empty key: a siblings-only `shll update` never restarts the daemon, so the post-remediation re-check's cleared `update-available` is the ONLY signal that clears the consumed match; an early return would leave a consumed match advertised forever.

**Tolerant `useUpdateNotification()` hook** (exported from `session-context.tsx`) — reads the context via `useContext(SessionContext)` DIRECTLY (not `useSessionContext`, so it **never throws outside the provider**; every field falls back — `updateNow`/`forceUpdateNow`/`restartNow` → `() => Promise.resolve()`, `dismissUpdate` → `() => {}`, `brew` → `false`). It returns the DERIVED display shape the chip + palette consume, so the gating logic lives in one place:

- `isDev = daemonVersion === DEV_VERSION` (`"dev"`).
- `tools` = the **NOTABLE subset** of `updateAvailable?.tools`, computed in a `useMemo`: `all.filter((t) => t.notable !== false)` (a missing/undefined flag counts as notable — old-daemon compat), returning `all` unchanged (stable referential identity) when nothing filters out so a no-op filter never mints a fresh array. The payload's `tools` is the FULL verdict list (incl. sub-threshold rows the incl.-patches check surfaces), but the chip/palette/dismissal machinery reads only this notable subset — so the chip stays policy-driven (a patch-only finding never lights it). The empty base is a **module-level frozen `EMPTY_TOOLS` constant** (`Object.freeze([])` cast through `unknown` to the mutable `UpdateTool[]` contract — frozen at runtime for a real no-mutation guarantee, typed mutable so the cast doesn't ripple through `updateChipToolSummary`/`buildUpdateActions` consumers) so `?? EMPTY_TOOLS` never mints a new array per render (a fresh `[]` would break referential memoization downstream).
- `key = updateAvailable?.key ?? null`.
- `singleRunKit = tools.length === 1 && tools[0].tool === "run-kit"` (`RUN_KIT_TOOL`) — the one shape that keeps the historical single-version chip/palette wording.
- `latest = singleRunKit ? tools[0].latest : null` / `current = singleRunKit ? tools[0].current : null` — the run-kit-row versions, surfaced ONLY for the single-run-kit `⬆ v{latest}` chip label + its transition title. Null otherwise (a multi/non-run-kit chip uses the count form + per-tool detail). The palette carries no version-bearing entry — `run-kit: Update Now` is a static label.
- **`qualifies = !isDev && tools.length > 0`** — the frontend trusts the server's `update-available` verdict for the per-tool threshold decision (the backend already applied it); it only additionally suppresses the `dev` daemon and requires a non-empty matched set. It does NOT re-run any semver compare.
- **`showChip = qualifies && key !== updateDismissedKey`** — the chip's composite-key dismissal gate. A later check with a DIFFERENT key (a newly-matching tool or a newer latest) re-shows the chip, because the changed key re-broadcasts `update-available` → `updateDismissedKey` no longer equals `key`.
- Returns `{ qualifies, showChip, tools, key, singleRunKit, latest, current, updateNow, dismissUpdate, daemonVersion, brew, forceUpdateNow, restartNow }`. `daemonVersion` is surfaced raw because `buildMaintenanceActions` does its own `version === "dev"` gate.

### Reload guard — `shouldReloadOnVersion` (post-restart auto-reload, boot-aware)

After a one-click upgrade the daemon restarts, which drops the state socket; the reconnect replays a **different** `version` global event (a set-once cached slot delivered once after `hello` over `/ws/state` — see `architecture.md` § State Socket), and the open tab is stale (it embeds the old frontend assets baked into the old binary). The guard auto-reloads it exactly once. The `StateSocket`'s resubscribe-on-reconnect replays the global slots, so the `version` listener fires on every reconnect. The guard also fires on a same-version restart (a plain `POST /api/restart`, a config-change/wedge-recovery restart, or a restart initiated from SSH) via the per-process `boot` id — so a tab that reconnects to a **new process at the same version** is not left silently running stale in-memory state: (`260714-3law`, `260716-qf3j`)

- The pure exported predicate is **4-arg**: `shouldReloadOnVersion(firstVersion: string | null, firstBoot: string | null, nextVersion: string, nextBoot: string | null): boolean`. Logic, in order: (1) `firstVersion === null` → `false` (**never reload on first connect** — no reload loop); (2) `nextVersion !== firstVersion` → `true` (a version change means new assets); (3) **same version** → reload on a **boot change** UNLESS the version is `"dev"`: `nextVersion === DEV_VERSION` returns `false` (the **air-recompile storm guard** — under `just dev`, air recompiles the backend on every save, minting a fresh boot id each time; reloading every dev tab on every recompile would be a reload storm), else `nextBoot !== null && nextBoot !== firstBoot`. A **null `nextBoot`** (older daemon, mixed-version window) never triggers the boot branch. (`260713-4zap`, `260714-3law`)
- `applyVersion(version, boot, brew)` (the `version`-listener callback): sets `daemonVersion` + `isBrew`; if `shouldReloadOnVersion(firstVersionRef.current, firstBootRef.current, version, boot)` → `location.reload()` (and returns); else, **only on the first-ever version** (`firstVersionRef.current === null`), stamps BOTH `firstVersionRef.current = version` and `firstBootRef.current = boot`. Both `firstVersionRef` and `firstBootRef` (new in `3law`) are `useRef` (not state — the reload decision must not re-render) so `applyVersion` stays referentially stable.
- Coverage this buys: update (version change), plain restart (boot change, same version), every open tab (the version slot is replayed per SSE connect), and restarts initiated from SSH or crash-recovery (the signal is server-originated, not client-action-originated).

### Top-bar L3 UpdateChip (`UpdateChip` in `top-bar.tsx`)

A self-contained chip in the L3 right cluster, **leading `NotificationControl`** (the L3 order is Update → Notification → Theme → Refresh → Help → connection dot). Reads `useUpdateNotification()`. It is a registry candidate: its bar/menu presence is 100% registry-driven (registry `hidden: !showChip` keeps it out of the candidate set when it wouldn't render, so it never reserves width or an empty slot). Below `sm` it does not vanish; under width pressure it overflows into the chevron menu, where its function merges into the fixed version row (§ Right cluster overflow / § Steady-state version surfaces → surface 5). The palette update surface provides keyboard-first parity; the menu also reaches the update surface on phones. (`260715-h1ck`) The chip IS the **promoted/single-action form** of the unified update button whose resting form is the overflow menu's version + ⟳ row; the split is verdict-derived — the chip renders in-bar when `showChip` and bar space allow, otherwise the update surface appears on the version row. It stays single-action (no ⟳ segment): checking is a resting-row affordance only, never on the promoted chip (`260720-ml7k`).

- **Hide gate**: `if (!showChip || tools.length === 0) return null` — the hide conditions (no qualifying update / dismissed-for-key / daemon is `dev`) are folded into `showChip` inside the hook.
- **Single/multi presentation** (R15): the visible label is `⬆ v{latest}` when the single matched tool is run-kit (`singleRunKit`), else a count form `⬆ updates (N)` for any other single tool OR multiple tools. The chip runs a SCOPED update of exactly the matched tools, so the `title`/`aria-label` must say WHICH tools move: `restLabel = singleRunKit && current ? `Update run-kit: v{current} → v{latest}` : `Update: ${updateChipToolSummary(tools)}``, where `updateChipToolSummary` composes the per-tool `tool v{a} → v{b}` transitions (a tool with no known current degrades to `tool → v{latest}`). Accent styling (`border-accent-green text-accent-green` + `rk-glint` CRT-glint hover — the button hover vocabulary, § Hover-Animation Vocabulary).
- **Click → one-click trigger** via the shared **`useUpdateClick()`** hook (`hooks/use-update-click.ts`), consumed by BOTH the chip and the overflow-menu version-row update surface so the updating-state + failure catch/toast is ONE implementation, never a mirrored copy. `triggerUpdate` early-returns if already `updating`, records the composite `key` at click time (`clickKeyRef`), sets `updating`, then `void updateNow().catch(...)`. On a request FAILURE (409 not-brew / no-match / network) it clears `updating` + shows an error toast. The busy state renders a `<LogoSpinner size={12}>` + `<span>{"updating…"}</span>` — the busy label is a JS string expression (a real `…` U+2026), NOT raw JSX text (JSX text does not process JS escape sequences, so a raw `…` would render six literal chars; `update-chip.test.tsx` asserts the exact visible text `updating…`).
- **Two `updating`-clearing paths** (R13): (1) run-kit IN the spawned scope → the daemon restarts, the state socket drops, and the reconnect's differing version reloads the tab (discarding this state); (2) SIBLINGS-ONLY scope → NO daemon restart, so no reload comes — the post-remediation re-check (R17, architecture § internal/updatecheck) broadcasts a cleared/changed `update-available` whose composite `key` differs from the click-time key, and a `useEffect` keyed on `key` clears `updating` when `key !== clickKeyRef.current` (including the cleared empty key). A FAILED brew upgrade leaves the key unchanged, so `updating` persists until a page reload / the palette force path — the accepted residual.
- **Dismiss `✕`**: a small sibling button (rendered only when `!updating`, `aria-label="Dismiss update notice"`) → `dismissUpdate()` (composite-key localStorage). Dismissal silences only the chip; the palette action remains (keyboard-first recoverability, §V).

### Palette parity — `run-kit:` actions via `buildUpdateActions` (`lib/palette-update.ts`)

Keyboard-first parity (§V): the pure helper `buildUpdateActions(qualifies, tools, onDismiss): UpdatePaletteAction[]` (in `lib/palette-update.ts`, unit-testable, mirroring `lib/palette-move.ts`) returns, when `qualifies && tools.length > 0`, the **single** entry:

- `{ id: "run-kit-dismiss-update", label: "run-kit: Dismiss Update Notice", onSelect: onDismiss }` — the keyboard mirror of the chip's `✕`; `onDismiss` writes the composite key.

and an empty array otherwise (signature: `(qualifies, tools, onDismiss)` — no update callback). There is **no version-bearing update entry here** — the update action is `run-kit: Update Now` in `buildMaintenanceActions` (§ Maintenance palette entries), THE single update action (see § Design Decisions → Single static `Update Now`). **Gated on `qualifies` ALONE — the palette deliberately IGNORES chip dismissal** (`qualifies`, NOT the chip's `showChip`): dismissal silences the ambient chip, but the palette is deliberate discovery. The per-tool `updateChipToolSummary` helper (consumed by the chip + overflow-menu aria) is the single exported source in this module, so the top bar and the menu can never drift (R15 / A-024).

**Dual-mount duplication** (the board-palette convention, § Command Palette View actions → Dual-mount duplication): the app mounts TWO CommandPalettes and the board route does NOT render AppShell, so a globally-meaningful action must be registered in both.

- **AppShell palette** (`app.tsx`): an `updateActions` block (a `useMemo` over `buildUpdateActions(qualifies, tools, dismissUpdate)`, alongside `viewActions`) folded into `paletteActions` between `statusRefreshActions` and `checkActions`.
- **Board palette** (`board-page.tsx` `boardRouteActions`): `buildUpdateActions` is duplicated in as `updateEntries`, appended near-last (the tail is `[...switchEntries, ...conditional, ...navEntries, ...fontEntries, refreshEntry, helpEntry, ...updateEntries, ...checkEntries, ...maintenanceEntries, ...versionEntries]` — the check entries follow the update entry, then maintenance, then version) — because below `sm` the top-bar UpdateChip is hidden, so on a phone `/board/$name` the palette is the ONLY update surface. (`260714-3law`, `260720-n2ai`)

The Host page (`/`) mounts no palette, so it carries no update palette action (pre-existing scope-out — its chip still renders in the mode-invariant right cluster).

### On-demand check commands — `buildCheckActions` + `composeCheckToast` + `useUpdateCheck` (`260720-n2ai`; two-backend split `260720-wb3n`)

Two on-demand check commands make "is anything updatable right now?" reachable without waiting on the ambient 6h chip or firing a blind force-update — keyboard-first (§V), reporting via the existing toast system (§ Post-pin success feedback + toast optional action for the toast primitive). The pure builder `buildCheckActions(version, onCheck, onCheckIncludingPatches): UpdatePaletteAction[]` (`lib/palette-update.ts`, unit-tested) returns:

- `{ id: "run-kit-check-updates", label: "run-kit: Check for Updates", onSelect: onCheck }` — reports tools crossing their notify threshold (`notable`).
- `{ id: "run-kit-check-updates-patches", label: "run-kit: Check for Updates (incl. patches)", onSelect: onCheckIncludingPatches }` — reports every tool with any pending update, annotating sub-threshold rows.

Both POST the same `/api/updates/check` endpoint but select **TWO BACKENDS** (`260720-wb3n`): the default check runs shll's `released` manifest source (POST body `{}`), while incl.-patches requests the FRESH `github` release-tags source (`checkForUpdates("github")` → body `{"source":"github"}`) — a SIDE-CHANNEL query the daemon answers without touching the cached verdict/chip. The two commands thus become "two backends", not "same data, two filters": the default can report all-up-to-date while incl.-patches lists updates, purely from the shll.ai manifest's ~1-day lag behind a just-cut release (the github source is the workaround). **Hidden on the `dev` sentinel** (`version === "dev"` → `[]`, same gating pattern as `buildMaintenanceActions`; a `null` version — no version event yet — counts as non-dev). **No brew gate** — checking is harmless without a remediation path (unlike `Update Now`).

**`composeCheckToast(tools, includePatches, source = ""): { message, updatable }`** (pure, unit-tested) composes the result toast over the verdict list: the default view filters `notable`, the incl.-patches view filters `updateAvailable` with sub-threshold rows annotated `(patch — below notify threshold)` (e.g. `tu v0.9.1 → v0.9.2 (patch — below notify threshold)`), reusing `updateChipToolSummary`'s per-tool `tool v{a} → v{b}` shape; an empty filtered set composes `All tools up to date` (`updatable: false`). The `source` argument is the ECHOED report backend from the check response (`"released"`/`"github"`; optional, default `""` for old daemons — keeping today's behavior). **When `source === "github"` the sub-threshold annotation is SUPPRESSED**: that backend carries no notify policy, so every row lands `notable=false`, and a github minor bump (e.g. `run-kit 3.8.7 → 3.9.1`) would otherwise be mislabeled a sub-threshold patch. The `updateAvailable`/`notable` filtering is unchanged — only the annotation keys off the source.

**Shared `useUpdateCheck()` hook** (`hooks/use-update-check.ts`) wires the POST→toast flow ONCE for both palette mounts AND the overflow-menu resting-row check affordance (the same anti-drift extraction as `use-update-click.ts`, § Design Decisions → Shared check-flow hook): it returns `{ runUpdateCheck, checking }`. `runUpdateCheck(includePatches)` maps `includePatches === true` → `checkForUpdates("github")` (the fresh github source) and the default check → `checkForUpdates()` (released), passing the response's echoed `result.source` into `composeCheckToast` so the sub-threshold annotation keys off what actually ran (`POST /api/updates/check`, tolerant parse, rejects on non-2xx with the server message), then shows ONE result toast (deliberately NO intermediate "checking…" toast — the endpoint responds synchronously ~1-2s). **`checking: boolean`** is the in-flight UI value (drives the overflow menu's ⟳ spinner/disabled form, § Steady-state version surfaces → surface 5). Single-flight is enforced by a **`useRef` flag checked synchronously** at the top of `runUpdateCheck` (early-return when set), with `checking` state purely driving the spinner — so a same-tick double-click can't slip past the not-yet-flushed state, and `runUpdateCheck` keeps a **stable referential identity** across the in-flight transition (`board-page.tsx` memoizes a large palette-action array on it; adding `checking` to its deps would churn that array mid-check). Both the ref and the state clear in a `.finally` on success AND failure. The result toast:

- an **info** toast with the `composeCheckToast` summary;
- when something updatable was reported AND the daemon can actually update (**`brew && daemonVersion !== "dev"`** — the same gate as the `Update Now` palette entry), the toast's **action slot carries "Update Now"**, triggering the same `forceUpdateNow()` force-update flow (a `.catch` on it surfaces an `"error"` toast);
- on a failed check (502 shll-missing, 409 dev, network) an **error** toast surfaces the server's message — the manual check is fail-LOUD, unlike the fail-silent ambient loop.

Both palette mounts consume the hook: AppShell (`app.tsx`) memoizes `checkActions = buildCheckActions(daemonVersion, () => runUpdateCheck(false), () => runUpdateCheck(true))` (folded into `paletteActions` right after `updateActions`); the board route (`board-page.tsx`) builds the same `checkEntries` via the shared hook.

### Maintenance palette entries — `buildMaintenanceActions` (`lib/palette-update.ts`)

Two **palette-only** maintenance actions, independent of the qualifying-update gate that governs `buildUpdateActions` — they make **update** and **daemon restart** reachable from the web (remote/mobile over Tailscale, no SSH), per Constitution V (keyboard-first) and IV (no new chrome). There is **no chip, no confirmation dialog, and no dedicated toast** — both fire immediately on select, and the SSE drop followed by the boot/version-driven tab reload IS the success feedback (only a rejection surfaces a toast).

The pure builder `buildMaintenanceActions(brew: boolean, version: string | null, onForceUpdate, onRestart): UpdatePaletteAction[]` (co-located with `buildUpdateActions` in `lib/palette-update.ts`, same test surface) computes `isDev = version === "dev"` and returns:

- `{ id: "run-kit-force-update", label: "run-kit: Update Now", onSelect: onForceUpdate }` — **THE single update action** in the palette: a force update (POST `/api/update` `{"force":true}`, a full-roster `shll update`; idempotent, and it picks up patch-only bumps a scoped match set would skip). Included ONLY when **`brew && !isDev`**. NOT gated on a qualifying update, so it reaches patch releases and works before any check has run. Brew-gated because a non-brew install cannot self-upgrade (the backend brew 409 would reject it anyway).
- `{ id: "run-kit-restart", label: "run-kit: Restart Daemon", onSelect: onRestart }` — included whenever **`!isDev`** (**NO brew requirement** — restart works for any install method).

Neither appears on a `dev` daemon (both gated on `!isDev`). `Update Now` is the ONE update entry in the palette — a static label; version detail lives in the check-result toasts and the chip summary (see § Design Decisions → Single static `Update Now` for why there is no dynamic `Update to v{X}` entry).

**Dual-mounted** per the same board-palette duplication convention as `buildUpdateActions` (below `sm` the top-bar chip cluster is hidden, so board routes on phones need palette parity — and there is no chip surface for these two at all):

- **AppShell** (`app.tsx`): a `maintenanceActions` `useMemo` over `buildMaintenanceActions(brew, daemonVersion, …)` (reading `brew`/`daemonVersion`/`forceUpdateNow`/`restartNow` from `useUpdateNotification()`), folded into `paletteActions` after `checkActions`. Each action wraps `forceUpdateNow`/`restartNow` in a `.catch` toast-on-failure with **`"error"` severity** (messages `"Update failed"` / `"Restart failed"`).
- **Board** (`board-page.tsx` `boardRouteActions`): `maintenanceEntries` via the same builder + gating, appended after `checkEntries` (before `versionEntries`), with the same `.catch` toast handling but **no severity arg** (mirroring the board's existing convention).

### Steady-state version surfaces

The `UpdateChip` above renders **only when a qualifying update is pending** and names only the TARGET version, so the running version is otherwise **invisible in the web UI** — a user filing a bug report or verifying a restart had to SSH in for `rk --version`. `260715-ifco` adds **four passive, chrome-level surfaces** that expose the *current* `daemonVersion` in steady state (frontend-only — the version already reaches every tab via `event: version`; no backend, no new routes/pages/buttons per Constitution IV, palette-first per V) — and `260715-h1ck` adds a **fifth**, the overflow menu's fixed version row (surface 5 below). All **degrade gracefully on a null `daemonVersion`** (hide/omit, never a `vundefined` placeholder) and show the **`dev` sentinel as-is** (`run-kit dev`, not `vdev`) — pure display, unlike the dev-gated update/restart actions.

**Shared `displayVersion` helper + `lib/palette-version.ts`.** A new pure, dependency-free module `app/frontend/src/lib/palette-version.ts` (mirroring the `lib/palette-update.ts` pattern, colocated `palette-version.test.ts`) exports:

- **`displayVersion(version: string): string`** — the single frontend source of the v-prefix convention, mirroring the backend `displayVersion()` (`app/backend/cmd/rk/root.go:16-21`): prefixes `v` to a numeric version, leaves `dev` and any already-`v`-prefixed string bare (idempotent — never `vdev` / `vv0.6.2`). Reused by all three display surfaces below (avoids the magic-string conditional per-site). Chosen to live in the palette module rather than a standalone `lib/version.ts` — the palette builder already needs it and it is the new dependency-free home.
- **`buildVersionAction(version: string | null, onSelect: () => void): VersionPaletteAction[]`** — returns `[]` when `version` is null (omit, no placeholder), else a single `{ id: "run-kit-version", label: `run-kit: Version — ${displayVersion(version)}`, onSelect }`. The LABEL carries the version, so typing "version" in the palette answers "what am I on?" **without selecting anything**. `VersionPaletteAction` is a local type mirroring `palette-update.ts`'s shape.

**1. Command-palette version entry** (the primary discovery surface, §V). `buildVersionAction` is **dual-mounted** — the same board-palette duplication convention as the update actions (§ Dual-mount duplication), and for the same reason: below `sm` the top-bar right cluster is hidden, so on a phone `/board/$name` the palette is the ONLY version surface.
  - **AppShell** (`app.tsx`): a `versionActions` `useMemo` over `buildVersionAction(daemonVersion, …)`, folded into `paletteActions` **after `maintenanceActions`, before `serverActions`**.
  - **Board** (`board-page.tsx` `boardRouteActions`): `versionEntries` via the same builder, appended **last** after `maintenanceEntries` (`[...switchEntries, ...conditional, ...navEntries, ...fontEntries, refreshEntry, helpEntry, ...updateEntries, ...checkEntries, ...maintenanceEntries, ...versionEntries]`).
  - **Gated on non-null `daemonVersion` INCLUDING `dev`** — `buildVersionAction`'s only gate is the null check (pure display; the entry is present for a `dev` daemon).
  - **On select**: copies the **DISPLAYED form** (`v0.6.2` / `dev` — what-you-see-is-what-you-copy, matches the label; NOT the raw `daemonVersion`) via `lib/clipboard.ts` `copyToClipboard`, then toasts. AppShell: `addToast(ok ? "Version copied" : "Copy failed", ok ? "info" : "error")`. Board: `addToast("Version copied", "info")` on success / `addToast("Copy failed")` (no severity arg) on failure — matching the board's own `updateEntries`/`maintenanceEntries` toast convention.

**2. Connection-dot version title** — the top-bar dot's hover `title` folds in `Connected — run-kit {displayVersion(daemonVersion)}`; full mechanics in § Chrome (Top Bar) → Connection dot.

**3. Host-page footer stamp** (`host-overview-page.tsx`) — a small passive BIOS/boot-style footer line `run-kit {displayVersion(daemonVersion)}` at the **bottom of the scroll container, after the SERVICES `</section>`** (out of the zone hierarchy — a POST-footer, on-brand with the CRT/terminal aesthetic). `text-xs text-text-secondary font-mono`, no border, no interaction, **no hover treatment** (passive means passive — the hover-animation vocabulary categories don't apply to inert text). Reads `daemonVersion` from `useSessionContext()` and renders **nothing when null** (`{daemonVersion && (…)}`, absence not a hidden placeholder). The Host page `/` is the only route with no top-bar version surface on phones, and its BIOS-footer aesthetic fits the stamp best.

**4. UpdateChip transition title** — the pending-update chip's `title`/`aria-label` show `v{current} → v{latest}`; mechanics in § Top-bar L3 UpdateChip and the `current` field in § Context state + `useUpdateNotification()` hook.

**5. Overflow menu's fixed version row** (`260715-h1ck`, `top-bar-overflow-menu.tsx`) — the top-bar overflow chevron's menu **always** contains a fixed version row as its last item (so the chevron renders even when nothing overflows; full mechanics in § Right cluster → overflow chevron menu). It reuses the same `displayVersion(daemonVersion)` + `copyToClipboard` machinery as the palette version action: renders `RunKit v{version}`, click copies the DISPLAYED form and toasts (`"Version copied"` / `"Copy failed"`); renders plain `RunKit` — no `v`, no `vundefined` — when `daemonVersion` is null. This is the sixth home of `displayVersion` and a chrome (not palette) version surface reachable on touch at any width.

The row has TWO forms, chosen by the **verdict-derived** `asUpdateSurface` computed in `TopBarOverflowMenu` from `useUpdateNotification`: `asUpdateSurface = tools.length > 0 && (updateOverflowed || (qualifies && !showChip))`. The `updateOverflowed` prop (`showChip && the update-chip entry is in the overflow set`, computed in `top-bar.tsx`) covers the undismissed-overflowed case; the `qualifies && !showChip` disjunct (`260720-ml7k`) covers the **dismissed-pending** case. Placement between this row and the in-bar `UpdateChip` (surface 4) is ALWAYS derivation — from `showChip` + overflow measurement — never imperatively moved (§ Design Decisions → Dismissed-pending shows the menu update surface).

- **Update-surface form** (the surface-4 UpdateChip's overflow twin): `asUpdateSurface` true → the row FLIPS from copy-mode to update-mode — `RunKit v{current} → v{latest} ⬆` for the single-run-kit match, else the count form `Toolkit updates (N) ⬆`; it is a `role="menuitem"` whose click triggers the update instead of copying, and no separate UpdateChip menu row is added (its function merges here). Both the chip and this row consume the shared `useUpdateClick()` hook (`hooks/use-update-click.ts`) — updating-state + failure catch/toast is ONE implementation (spinner + `updating…` while in flight), never a mirrored copy. The aria/summary reuses the shared `updateChipToolSummary` (single source, no bar↔menu drift).
- **Resting form** (the unified update button's resting version row, `260720-ml7k`): `asUpdateSurface` false → the version copy button PLUS a dev-gated ⟳ "Check for updates" affordance. The ⟳ renders whenever `!asUpdateSurface && daemonVersion !== DEV_VERSION` (a `null` version counts as non-dev — the same gate as the palette check entries). It is a **plain, non-`menuitem` control** (`tabIndex={-1}`) so the container's role-keyed close handler does not fire — the menu stays open across the ~1-2s check and the in-flight spinner/single-flight state stays visible (§ Design Decisions → Check affordance is a non-menuitem control). Arrow-nav still reaches it via the `button:not([disabled])` focusables selector. It uses the lucide `rotate-cw` SVG in the 24px/`coarse:30px` bordered-square step-button treatment (the refresh vocabulary, same glyph as `RefreshButton`). Click runs `runUpdateCheck(false)` — the plain notable check through the shared `useUpdateCheck` hook (info toast via `composeCheckToast`, error toast on failure; NO incl.-patches variant, that stays palette-only). While `checking` it shows a `LogoSpinner size={12}` and is disabled (single-flight; see surface's hook above).

**Chevron attention badge** is keyed on the **undismissed-overflowed case ONLY** — `showBadge = updateOverflowed && tools.length > 0`, unchanged from `h1ck`. It deliberately does NOT light for the dismissed-pending update surface: the surface itself appears (deliberate discovery, like the palette's `qualifies` gate) but the ambient badge stays silenced (dismissal silences ambient chrome).

**`copyToClipboard` success signal.** `lib/clipboard.ts` `copyToClipboard` returns `Promise<boolean>` — `true` on a successful copy (Clipboard API OR the `execCommand` non-secure-context fallback), `false` when both fail. Callers that `void`-ignore the return (`terminal-client.tsx`, `status-panel.tsx`) are unaffected; the palette-version `onSelect` consumes the boolean to toast confirmation vs. error (fail soft with an error toast in a non-secure context). The return-value cases (Clipboard-API success, `execCommand`-fallback success, total failure) are unit-tested in `terminal-client.test.ts` (the home of the `copyToClipboard` describe block).

## Shell Grid Layout

The `<Shell>` wrapper (`app/frontend/src/components/shell/shell.tsx`) is the shared layout for `AppShell` and `BoardPage` (the Host page `/` uses a plain `flex-col h-full` instead — no Shell). **The Shell grid carries NO `topbar` row** — the TopBar mounts once in the persistent root layout, full-width above the Shell (see § Chrome (Top Bar) → persistent root mount). The visual stack (full-width bar over sidebar+content) is preserved. (`260707-4vq2`)

The **desktop** (`≥ 640px`) grid is sidebar+content over bottombar:

```
gridTemplateAreas: "sidebar content" / "sidebar bottombar"   (rows: 1fr auto)
```

`gridTemplateColumns` stays `${sidebarWidth}px 1fr` when `sidebarOpen` else `0 1fr` (a `150ms ease-out` collapse transition, zero-width column when closed — no rail). The **mobile** (`< 640px`) branch is single-column `gridTemplateAreas: "content" "bottombar"` (rows `1fr auto`), with the sidebar rendered as an `absolute` overlay whose grid child spans `gridRow: "1 / 3"` (the content+bottombar rows; the Shell grid has no topbar row — see § Sidebar Mobile). The `sidebar` grid area is **Shell-owned** — `Shell` renders the desktop `<aside style={{ gridArea: "sidebar" }}>` itself from `sidebarChildren` (see § Sidebar Desktop); consumers place only the `content` and `bottombar` areas via `style={{ gridArea: "content" | "bottombar" }}`. (`260707-4vq2`, `260719-rwqf`)

**Shell height is `100%`** — Shell fills the root layout's `flex-1` content region rather than sizing itself to the viewport. Shell does not call `useVisualViewport()` or consume `--app-height` directly (both live in `RootWrapper` — see § iOS Keyboard Support). `useSidebarKeyboardToggle` (Cmd+\ / Ctrl+\) is registered in Shell — the chord is live only on routes that mount a `<Shell>` (AppShell + BoardPage). (`260707-4vq2`)

## Chrome (Top Bar)

The full-width top bar is the app's primary chrome and doubles as the navbar. **It mounts ONCE at the persistent root layout, above the router `<Outlet>` — not once per page** (see § Persistent root mount below). `TopBar` (`app/frontend/src/components/top-bar.tsx`) accepts a `mode: "terminal" | "board" | "server" | "host"` prop (default `"terminal"`) selecting the left-nav content; the left nav is a breadcrumb bar. Everything below (per-mode breadcrumbs, center heading, right-cluster pyramid, connection dot) describes `TopBar`'s internal rendering. (`260702-6m46`, `260707-4vq2`, `260715-zs1y`)

### Persistent root mount (`RootTopBar` / `AppLayout`)

`TopBar` mounts once at the persistent root layout and re-renders in place across route changes (§ Design Decisions → TopBar mounts once at the root layout).

**Where it mounts.** A **pathless layout route** (`id: "app-layout"`, `router.tsx`) uniformly parents every page route (index, server, terminal, board), so every navigation keeps the match chain `[root, app-layout, <leaf>]`. Its component `AppLayout` (`app.tsx`) sits at a **stable match depth with a stable route id and is never remounted** across navigation; it renders a flex column — `<div className="app-root flex flex-col" style={{ height: "var(--app-height, 100vh)" }}>` — with `RootTopBar` in a `shrink-0` wrapper above a `flex-1 min-h-0` content region. The bar keeps a stable React identity and re-renders (props change, no unmount) as the URL flips. The pathless layout normalizes tree depth (§ Design Decisions → TopBar mounts once at the root layout). The `AppLayout` wrapper is a plain `div`, NOT `<header>` — `TopBar` already renders its own `<header>` banner landmark, so a second would nest two `role="banner"` landmarks.

**Suspense blast radius.** The `<Suspense fallback={null}>` boundary wraps ONLY the `<Outlet>` content region (inside `AppLayout`), not the header. So when the lazy board chunk loads, only the page body blanks — the bar stays painted.

**Prop delivery — two channels.** `TopBar`'s inputs split by how synchronously they must resolve:

- **Route-derived (synchronous, at root)**: `RootTopBar` (`app.tsx`) derives `mode` + `boardName` from `useMatches()` — a deepest-first walk over route params (`window` ⇒ `terminal`, `name` ⇒ `board` + `boardName`, `server` ⇒ `server`, none ⇒ `host`; param names are unique across the tree, the same walk `SessionContext` uses for `currentServer`). This flips the instant the URL changes, so the heading never waits on the incoming page's mount — critical for the lazy board (`Board: <name>` renders from the URL param while the chunk still loads). `mode`/`boardName` are deliberately NOT in the slot.
- **Page-registered (a slot context, `contexts/top-bar-slot-context.tsx`)**: pages publish their data/handler props — `sessions`, `currentSession`, `currentWindow`, `sessionName`, `windowName`, `isConnected`, `sidebarOpen`, `server`, `onNavigate`, `onToggleSidebar`, `onCreateSession`, `onCreateWindow`, plus board extras (`paneCount`, `serverCount`, `waitingPaneCount`, `boards`, `focusedPane` — the focused-tile split target — `onRequestKill` — the board ✕'s kill-dialog opener — and `autofit`/`onToggleAutofit` for the board autofit toggle, § Board Autofit Toggle) — via `useRegisterTopBarSlot(...)` (an effect: publish on mount/update, **clear to `null` on unmount**, last-writer-wins). This follows the `FocusedTerminalProvider` precedent (referentially-stable dispatcher held in a `useRef`, `useMemo`'d context value) and keeps the heavy handlers where they live — `AppShell`'s `navigateToWindow` (View-Transitions gate) and `handleCreateSessionInstant` (optimistic ghosts) are published by reference; **no logic lives at root**. (`260708-738w`, `260715-6jwn`, `260718-co9z`)

**Tolerant-empty defaults.** When no page has registered yet (first frame after navigation, or a lazy chunk still loading), the slot value is `null` and `RootTopBar` renders the route-derived mode with the tolerant-empty prop shape every `TopBar` mode already supports (`sessions=[]`, `currentSession=null`, `currentWindow=null`, `sessionName/windowName/server=""`, `sidebarOpen=false`, no-op callbacks). No crash, no stale props from the prior page (the clear-on-unmount guarantees this).

**Not-found is a dedicated boolean channel.** `TopBarSlotContext` carries a `notFound` flag SEPARATE from the page-data `slot`. `NotFoundPage` (`router.tsx`) — the `app-layout` route's `notFoundComponent`, rendered inside the `<Outlet>` below the persistent bar — calls `useSignalTopBarNotFound()` (sets `true` on mount / `false` on unmount); `RootTopBar` reads `useTopBarNotFound()` and forces `mode="host"` (nulling `boardName`) BEFORE the route-param walk. This is required because TanStack Router's fuzzy not-found handling RETAINS the partially-matched params in `useMatches()` (e.g. `/board/x/y` keeps `name=x`), so the param walk alone would derive `board` mode ("Board: x") over the not-found body. A separate boolean keeps `NotFoundPage` — which owns no TopBar data — from publishing the full slot shape, and avoids coupling to a router-internal field + hardcoded route-id string. Because `RootTopBar` sits ABOVE the `<Outlet>`, the in-Outlet signal is inherently one render behind: a ~1-frame "Board: x" flash before the effect lands is unavoidable without reading router internals — not user-perceptible, and the settled state is unaffected. (The `/a/b/c` shape is a DIFFERENT arm: it renders `AppShell`'s `ServerNotFound` early-return, not `NotFoundPage`, so `notFound` stays false there and the `server`/`terminal` mode derivation is kept.)

**Per-page registration.** No page mounts `<TopBar>`; each registers into the slot context instead: `AppShell` registers its terminal/server data (the `terminal` vs `server` distinction is derived at root); `HostOverviewPage` registers just `isConnected: hostMetricsConnected` (wrapper `flex flex-col h-full`); `BoardPage` registers the board extras (`boardName`, counts, `boards`, `focusedPane`, `onRequestKill: requestKillFocused` — the kill-dialog opener — `isConnected: boardConnected`; keeps the `HELP_URL` import for its palette action). Edge pages (`NotFoundPage`, `ServerNotFound`, `ServerWaiting`) center with `h-full` so they fit the content region below the persistent bar without overflow. (`260718-co9z`)

**Achievable-invariant note (e2e).** No component in the persistent chain (`RootWrapper`/`AppLayout`/`RootTopBar`/`TopBar`) remounts across navigation, so the bar stays continuously present with a per-route heading — this is what `tests/e2e/top-bar-persistence.spec.ts` asserts (mount-effect stability + per-route heading), NOT strict DOM-node identity. TanStack Router 1.168's per-match Suspense re-commit recreates the header host node on the `→ /` (index-route) transition; that is a router-internal reconciliation artifact that does NOT remount the component and does NOT blank the bar (the heading renders synchronously from route state), so it is not a user-visible flicker. The spec's brand-crumb hop is a RELOAD BOUNDARY — the brand is a raw `<a href="/">` TanStack Router does not intercept, a full document navigation — so only the client-side hops carry the no-remount claim.

**Non-goals.** Sidebar/BottomBar/Shell stay per-page (they still remount on `/$server` ↔ `/board/$name`); `TopBar`'s internal rendering across all four modes is unchanged; frontend-only (no backend/API/tmux change).

`app.tsx`, `board-page.tsx`, and `host-overview-page.tsx` (Host page `/`) register into the slot context rather than rendering `<TopBar>` directly (see § Persistent root mount above). The right-section control cluster is a **strict 3-level cumulative pyramid**: a stable always-block pinned right renders in every mode, with terminal+board extras and terminal-only extras growing leftward — so no shared button ever changes screen position between pages. Only which levels appear gates on mode; see § Right cluster below. (`260704-9o7k`)

**Layout** (`border-b-[3px] border-border` — a 3px structural seam, see § Border-Width System): a single line, a **3-column CSS grid `grid grid-cols-[1fr_auto_1fr] items-center gap-2 py-2`**. `1fr auto 1fr` makes the CENTER cell truly centered regardless of asymmetric left/right widths. LEFT cell = a flex wrapper holding the hamburger (first, outside the nav) + `<nav aria-label="Breadcrumb">` (the nav ends at the parent — see per-mode below); CENTER cell = the **universal `PageType: name` page heading, FILLED IN EVERY MODE** (terminal `WindowHeading` + ▾ window switcher / board display heading + ▾ board switcher / server display heading / solo `Host`; § Chrome (Top Bar) center cell); RIGHT cell = the control cluster (`justify-self-end`). No Line 2. The header itself carries `px-3` (the center cell is `flex items-center justify-center min-w-0`, no flex `gap` — the boot sweep owns the prefix→name spacing via its own space cell). (`260703-5ilm`, `260704-pr0p`)

**Left cluster** — the `1fr` left grid cell is a flex wrapper (`flex items-center gap-1.5 min-w-0`) holding, in order, the **hamburger** then the **breadcrumb nav**. The hamburger is a sibling BEFORE the nav (outside the `nav[aria-label="Breadcrumb"]` landmark — a drawer toggle is not a breadcrumb item); `min-w-0` lets the nav shrink below its content inside the `1fr` column. The center heading's true centering is untouched by the wrapper. (`260720-ap63`)

**Hamburger** — the sidebar toggle (`aria-label="Toggle navigation"`, a Notion-style rounded-rect pictogram whose left column fills when `sidebarOpen`), the FIRST element of the left cluster (standard drawer-toggle position — VS Code / Slack), rendered before and outside the breadcrumb nav. Present on every mode that has a sidebar; `hasSidebar` is DERIVED as `mode !== "host"` (no separate prop) — the host mode is the only sidebar-less mode, so it gets no hamburger (the brand shifts left ~30px there; no ghost slot is reserved). It joins the top-bar button-control size vocabulary: `min-w-[24px] min-h-[24px] coarse:min-w-[30px] coarse:min-h-[30px]` (24px fine / 30px coarse — the same 24/30 the right-side cluster uses, NOT the bottom-bar's 36px), plus `shrink-0`. Hover treatment is `rk-glint` (borderless at rest, so hover = green icon + sweep only). (`260720-ap63`)

**Brand root crumb** (all modes, the nav's FIRST child): the logo icon (`/icon.svg`, always visible) + `hidden sm:inline` "RunKit" wordmark wrapped in a single `<a href="/">` (`aria-label="RunKit home"`). It is the breadcrumb's root crumb, so the `›` separator starts after it. This IS the home affordance — there is no separate "Host" crumb and no right-side "RunKit" anchor. The brand carries the `LINK_CRUMB_CLASS` bordered-chip treatment (see § Crumb Affordance Vocabulary) and `rk-brand-glitch` hover. Below `sm` it collapses to the bare icon so long crumbs still fit the single-line 375px topbar. (`260702-6m46`, `260720-ap63`)

**Separator** — `›` (U+203A, `aria-hidden`, `BreadcrumbSeparator`), the palette-label convention (`<session> › <name>`) between every crumb level. No `/` separator. (`260702-6m46`)

**Host** (`/`, `mode="host"`): brand crumb ONLY — no hamburger, no crumbs, no terminal-font control, no split/close buttons, and **no fixed-width button** (terminal-only; the 900px effect never applied to the Host page — `host-overview-page.tsx` never reads `fixedWidth`). Renders only the L3 always-block (Notification / Theme / Refresh / Help) **plus the connection dot**, which reflects **host-metrics stream health** — `host-overview-page.tsx` passes `hostMetricsConnected` from `useSessionContext()` (see § Right cluster → connection dot and architecture.md § Server-independent host-metrics subscription). Session/server-dependent props are passed empty (`sessions=[]`, `currentSession=null`, `currentWindow=null`, `sessionName=""`, `server=""`, no-op callbacks) — the same tolerant-empty shape board mode uses. The Host page's page identity is the **solo `Host` heading in the top-bar center cell** (a `PageHeadingDisplay` with `prefix=""` + `name="Host"` + `solo` — primary-medium, visible at all breakpoints; § center cell), plus the in-page `Host Overview` SectionHeading (§ Page Overview Headings). A "RunKit Host" doubled word is avoided — it would duplicate the adjacent brand crumb. (`260704-9o7k`, `260704-pr0p`, `260715-zs1y`)

**tmux Server** (`/$server`, no `$window`, `mode="server"`): the left cluster is **hamburger + brand** — nothing more (the breadcrumb nav holds just the brand crumb). The server name is the **`tmux Server: <server>` heading in the CENTER cell** (a display-only `PageHeadingDisplay`, no rename), NOT a left-nav leaf (move-don't-copy: the current-page leaf is the centered heading; a name never appears twice in the bar). "Dashboard" appears nowhere. (`260702-6m46`, `260704-pr0p`)

**Terminal** (`/$server/$window`, `mode="terminal"`): the left cluster is hamburger + brand + `›` + server link + `›` + **session dropdown — and the breadcrumb ENDS THERE** (the hamburger precedes the brand, outside the nav) (the window identity lives in the centered `WindowHeading`, not the breadcrumb chain). The server crumb here is a plain `<a href="/$server">` (a link back to the tmux Server page, `LINK_CRUMB_CLASS` chip, `truncate max-w-[16ch]`) — NOT a dropdown (server switching stays in the command palette, `Server: Switch to …`). The session crumb is a `BreadcrumbDropdown` (session switch jumps to the session's first window; `+ New Session` action; session `max-w-[16ch] truncate` (matches the server crumb); the session name is snapshot-derived from the active `@N`, not a URL segment). **The window switcher lives in the center cell** — a label-less bare-`▾` `BreadcrumbDropdown` (`title="Window"`, `windowItems` + `+ New Window` action) sitting beside the `WindowHeading` (name-click = edit, `▾`-click = switch), so the window name is never duplicated in one bar. The centered `WindowHeading` carries a static prefix sibling span (§ Window Heading) — the two-tone `PageType: name` identity, `Window:` in every lens. See § Chrome (Top Bar) center cell / § Breadcrumb Dropdowns → Window switcher. No type-prefix words ("SERVER"/"tmux Server"/"session") — crumbs are instance names only; position conveys the level. The level IS named on hover via native `title` tooltips in the canonical vocabulary: brand `title="Host"`, server crumb `title="tmux Server"` (both link and leaf variants), session dropdown trigger `title="Session"` and the window switcher `title="Window"` (via BreadcrumbDropdown's optional `title` prop). (`260529-jad6`, `260703-5ilm`, `260704-pr0p`, `260714-uco1`)

**Center cell — the universal `PageType: name` page heading** (filled on every mode). The outer center `<div className="flex items-center justify-center min-w-0">` (no flex `gap` — the boot sweep's own `sp` space cell separates prefix from name) stays centered in the grid; it wraps an **inner anchor `<div className="flex items-center justify-start min-w-0 sm:min-w-[28ch]">`** — a `sm:`-gated min-width with LEFT-aligned content so the heading's left edge stops drifting as the instance name length changes (below `sm` the min-width is absent — space is scarce at 375px). The browser-history arrows + hierarchy ▾ live INSIDE this anchored box (§ Center-heading stable anchor + nav affordances). It renders per mode: (`260703-5ilm`, `260704-pr0p`, `260714-uco1`)

- **terminal** (`mode === "terminal" && currentWindow`): `<HistoryNav>` ◀ ▶ + `<HierarchyDropdown mode="terminal">` (left of the prefix) + `<WindowHeading>` (static `Window: <window>`, editable name — see § Window Heading) + the relocated bare-`▾` window switcher.
- **board** (`mode === "board" && boardName`): `<HistoryNav>` + `<HierarchyDropdown mode="board">` + a `<PageHeadingDisplay prefix="Board:" name={boardName}>` (display-only — boards have no rename API) + the `<BoardSwitcher>` ▾ (moved here from the left `BoardModeBreadcrumb`).
- **server** (`mode === "server" && server`): `<HistoryNav>` + `<HierarchyDropdown mode="server">` + `<PageHeadingDisplay prefix="tmux Server:" name={server}>` (display-only).
- **host**: `<HistoryNav>` + `<PageHeadingDisplay prefix="" name="Host" solo>` — a solo type word, no instance name, primary-medium, visible at all breakpoints; NO hierarchy ▾ (the root has no ancestors).

The type-prefix constants live once in `top-bar.tsx`: `WINDOW_PREFIX = "Window:"`, `BOARD_PREFIX = "Board:"`, `TMUX_SERVER_PREFIX = "tmux Server:"`, `HOST_SOLO = "Host"` (title case). Because the cell lives in the `auto` middle grid column, it stays centered under the topbar regardless of the breadcrumb / control-cluster widths. The `WindowHeading` (and the display headings) are deliberately NOT keyed on the route identity (no remount `key`) so they persist across window/page switches — that is what lets the boot sweep replay on navigation and keeps an in-progress inline edit alive (an external windowId/server switch mid-edit CANCELS the stale edit instead, since committing the typed name onto the newly-navigated window would rename the wrong one). (`260714-uco1`, `260715-zs1y`)

### Center-heading stable anchor + nav affordances

Four affordances on the top-bar center heading, all inside the anchored center box (§ Chrome (Top Bar) center cell), no new routes and no backend surface: (`260714-uco1`)

- **Stable left anchor.** The outer center cell stays `justify-center` in the grid; an INNER container `flex items-center justify-start min-w-0 sm:min-w-[28ch]` reserves a `sm:`-gated min-width with LEFT-aligned content, so the heading's left edge stops drifting as the instance name length changes (min-width over fixed-width+truncate — long names grow rightward, accepted). Applies uniformly across all four modes; below `sm` the min-width is absent (375px). The `28ch` value is monospace-exact, visually tuned. The inline-rename `<input>` is `text-left` so the name does not jump on edit entry (§ Window Heading → edit).
- **Hierarchy ▾ dropdown** (`HierarchyDropdown`, reuses `BreadcrumbDropdown`). A bare-`▾` sibling of the rename button, bound LEFT of the prefix (reads `▾ Window: name`), listing EXACTLY the current page's ANCESTOR chain — no lateral jumps. Terminal: `tmux Server: {server}` (→ `/{server}`) then `Host` (→ `/`); board & server: `Host` only; **solo Host: not rendered** (the root has no ancestors). `hidden sm:inline-flex` — below `sm` it rides with the hidden prefix span (the hamburger/sidebar covers mobile nav). Being a sibling of the rename button, clicking it never enters inline edit. Navigation routes through the typed `useNavigate()` (params validated). It is intentionally redundant with the left breadcrumb.
- **Browser-history ◀ ▶ arrows** (`HistoryNav`). Fixed-width bordered `rk-glint` icon buttons (`coarse:` touch sizing, `aria-label`s) rendered LEFT of the prefix inside the anchored box on ALL FOUR modes (history is global). They call TanStack Router's `useRouter().history.back()` / `.forward()` — BROWSER HISTORY, explicitly NOT sibling-window cycling. Being fixed-width they never shift the heading's text anchor. Forward is always-active (browser-chrome style — `canGoForward` is not reliably exposed, so a dim/disabled state is omitted; a no-forward click is a harmless no-op). **Within-server window hops retrace**: user-initiated window switches **push** history entries (`navigateToWindow` — see § URL as Resumable Bookmark → optimistic navigate), so Back/Forward step through every within-server hop, not only server boundaries. No dedup — `w1→w5→w1` yields three entries. History Back/Forward bypasses `navigateToWindow` (raw `router.history.back()/forward()`), so no slide transition plays on arrow navigation; the landed window's tmux is realigned for free by the deep-link intent effect (§ URL as Resumable Bookmark, contract 1 — its `hasAlignedToUrlRef` guard re-arms on every `windowParam` change). (`260715-m4xy`)
- **`Go:` palette parity** (Constitution V) via the pure `lib/palette-nav.ts` builder `buildNavActions(mode, server, handlers)` (+ colocated `palette-nav.test.ts`), mirroring `palette-move.ts`/`palette-view.ts`. Returns the two history actions (`Go: Back`/`Go: Forward`, ALWAYS) followed by the route-appropriate ancestor entries: `Go: tmux Server` when `mode === "terminal" && server`, then `Go: Host` **unconditionally** (the Host root is an ancestor of every palette-bearing mode — only the `terminal` extra differs). `NavMode` is `"terminal" | "board" | "server"` — the **palette-bearing subset of `TopBarMode`**: the root Host route mounts no palette, so there is no `host` mode (`TopBarMode` keeps its `"host"` member; only `NavMode` narrows). **Dual-wired** (§ Dual-mount duplication): `app.tsx`'s `navActions` `useMemo` folds it into the AppShell `paletteActions` composition with `mode = windowParam ? "terminal" : "server"`; `board-page.tsx`'s `boardRouteActions` wires its own `buildNavActions("board", "", …)` call (§ Boards Command Palette) — the board route does not render AppShell, so the trio would otherwise be missing on `/board/$name` despite the top-bar arrows rendering there. Both pass `router.history.back/forward` + `navigate(...)` bodies. No new app-level keybindings (browser-native Alt+←/→ already cover history). (`260714-uco1`, `260719-i996-nav-actions-board-wiring`)

**Board** (`/board/$name`, `mode="board"`): the left cluster is hamburger + brand + a **counts/hint span ONLY** (`BoardModeInfo` — `{N} pane[s] · {M} server[s] · ⌘[⌘] cycle`, no leading `›` because the hint is not a crumb). The board name + ▾ switcher live in the center heading (`Board: <board>` display + `<BoardSwitcher>`; § center cell); there is no left `Board ▸` home button (the brand crumb is the home affordance, and a left `Board` word would duplicate the centered type word — move-don't-copy). Right cluster: the two L1 **SplitButtons** (wired to the focused tile's window via `focusedPane`) + the L2 controls (Aa + the board-only **autofit toggle** between Aa and ✕ + ✕, where the board ✕ is a **confirm-gated window-kill** of the focused tile's window — the ✕ opens the kill dialog with a default-focused `Unpin instead` escape, § Board Kill Confirm Dialog; unpin lives on the tile-header pin-glyph + palette — see § Right cluster / § Close pane button / § Board Tile Header / § Board Autofit Toggle) and the L3 always-block including the connection dot, which shows an **AND over the board's attached servers** (green iff ≥1 entry AND every distinct attached server's `isConnectedByServer` slice is connected; `board-page.tsx` derives `boardConnected` and passes it). (`260702-6m46`, `260704-pr0p`, `260704-9o7k`, `260715-6jwn`, `260718-co9z`)

**Mobile (`< sm`)** — the brand collapses to the bare icon and intermediate crumbs (server link + session, plus their `›` separators, wrapped in `hidden sm:flex` spans) are hidden, leaving brand icon + the centered heading. The leaf is the **center-cell heading in EVERY mode**: Terminal → `WindowHeading` (the mobile leaf AND primary rename affordance, `coarse:min-h-[30px]` touch target), tmux Server → the `tmux Server: <server>` display heading, Board → the `Board: <board>` display heading, Host → the solo `Host`. **The two-tone `PageType:` prefix is hidden below `sm`** (`hidden sm:inline`) so mobile keeps just the name — EXCEPT the solo `Host` word (a name-equivalent, not a prefix), which stays visible at all breakpoints. The `▾` window/board switcher stays visible on mobile with its `+ New Window` / board-switch action. Long names truncate in the center cell (`max-w-[16ch]` on mobile, `sm:max-w-[28ch]`) — never wrap or squeeze neighbors. The topbar stays a single line at 375px (the documented invariant in `fab/project/context.md`). (`260704-pr0p`)

**Mid-width overlap degradation.** Between the `sm` breakpoint (640px) and ~900px (the common sidebars-open / half-screen browser-pane case), a deterministic **degradation ladder** (class-only in `top-bar.tsx`, no API/routing/backend change) keeps the left breadcrumb from painting over the centered heading: (`260715-q8ey`)

1. **Crumbs truncate first.** The two left-nav crumb wrapper spans (server-link crumb + session crumb) each gained `min-w-0` so the `truncate max-w-[16ch]` already present on their inner anchor / `BreadcrumbDropdown` trigger finally engages. **`min-w-0`-chain rule**: a nested flex item defaults to `min-width: auto`, which blocks `truncate` from shrinking the item until an explicit `min-w-0` is added at that level — the crumb text had been overflowing the nav box because the intervening wrapper span, not the anchor, was the blocked link in the chain. `BreadcrumbSeparator` and the brand chip stay `shrink-0` — the protected identity floor inside the nav; the hamburger sits outside the nav and carries its own `shrink-0`.
2. **Server crumb hides below `md`.** The server-link crumb wrapper is `hidden md:flex … min-w-0` — the first element to give way, because the hierarchy ▾ inside the heading prefix already lists `tmux Server: {server}` → `Host`, so the left server crumb is redundant navigation at cramped widths. The **session crumb stays at `sm+`** (it owns the session switcher + `+ New Session` action). (`260714-uco1`)
3. **Nav clips at its explicit floor.** The `<nav aria-label="Breadcrumb">` carries an explicit breakpoint-aware floor `min-w-[46px] sm:min-w-[150px]` plus `overflow-hidden`. The floor budgets only nav content — the hamburger sits outside the nav and carries its own `shrink-0` + min sizes: below `sm` the floor guarantees just the bare brand icon; at `sm+` also a session-crumb sliver. The left cell's TOTAL floor (hamburger + gap + nav floor) is what holds the left budget. **Clip-backstop rule**: `overflow-hidden` converts any residual overflow past the shrunk floor into a clean clip at the nav's right edge instead of paint-over overlap — overlap becomes structurally impossible, not merely unlikely. The `min-w-[46px] sm:min-w-[150px]` values hold across the full Playwright sweep (375 / 640 / 700 / 768 / 1024px) with the 30px coarse hamburger, no clip or wrap regression — the top-bar-overlap spec is the harness. (A clipped child keeps a layout box wider than its clipping parent, which is expected; the meaningful proofs are the no-intersection assertion + computed `overflow:hidden`, not a layout-box comparison.)

**Center protection.** The center `auto` grid column is protected by holding its bounded **content floor**, NOT by a magic pixel min-width. The center cell's OUTER wrapper (`flex items-center justify-center`) carries no `min-w-0`, so the `auto` column can not be squeezed below the heading's content. That floor is *bounded* because the heading name spans carry `max-w-[16ch] sm:max-w-[28ch] truncate` (WindowHeading button + PageHeadingDisplay) and the history ◀ ▶ / hierarchy ▾ / window & board ▾ controls are fixed-width `shrink-0`. The inner box's **`sm:min-w-[28ch]` stable anchor stays at `sm:` (NOT `md:`)** — the right cluster absorbs squeeze instead. Net effect: squeeze lands on the left (and right) `1fr` columns; the center heading is never compressed into overlap across the 640–900px band. (`260715-q8ey`)

**Right-cluster degradation.** The right cluster is registry-driven and its `1fr` grid track is squeezable via `min-w-0` on the cell, so under width pressure controls collapse into a chevron menu instead of clipping (full mechanics in § Right cluster → overflow chevron menu below). It uses an explicit fit computation + move-to-menu, NOT `overflow-hidden` — a partial `overflow-hidden` on the right cluster would clip the *wrong* end (flex overflow spills toward inline-end, dropping the L3 always-block / connection dot first). The cell carries `min-w-0` but deliberately NO `overflow-hidden` (the only content that can exceed a very-narrow track is the always-present exempt chevron+dot block, which must stay visible/clickable per R6). Regression coverage lives in `tests/e2e/top-bar-overlap.spec.ts` (+ `.spec.md`): at ~700×800 with long window + session names, nav-box ∩ heading-box is empty and crumbs are ellipsised; server crumb toggles across `md`; 375px stays single-line; 1024px+ keeps the anchor intact. The width-sweep spec `tests/e2e/top-bar-overflow.spec.ts` (+ `.spec.md`) is the right-cluster's regression proof (see § Right cluster). (`260715-q8ey`, `260715-h1ck`)

**Right cluster** (`flex items-center justify-end gap-3 min-w-0`) — a **strict 3-level cumulative pyramid**, growing LEFTWARD from a stable always-block pinned right, so no shared button ever changes screen position between pages. The pyramid is consumed by a priority+ overflow menu (§ Right cluster → overflow chevron menu below): the L1→L2→L3 order encodes DROP priority (L1 drops first, L3 last) and the whole cluster is registry-driven, not hardcoded JSX. The tiers: (`260704-9o7k`, `260715-h1ck`)

| Level | Gate | Buttons (left → right) |
|---|---|---|
| **L1** — splits terminal+board, FixedWidthToggle terminal-only (`260715-6jwn`) | splits: `currentWindow` (terminal) OR `mode === "board" && focusedPane` (board); FixedWidthToggle: `mode === "terminal"` | SplitButton (vertical) · SplitButton (horizontal) · **FixedWidthToggle (terminal-only)** |
| **L2** — terminal + board | `mode === "terminal" \|\| mode === "board"` | TerminalFontControl (Aa) · **BoardAutofitToggle (board-only, between Aa and ✕)** · **ClosePaneButton (✕ — terminal: close-pane; board: confirm-gated window-kill via `onRequestKill`, `260718-co9z`)** |
| **L3** — always (all four modes) | none | **UpdateChip (⬆ v… — leading, conditional: hidden unless a qualifying, un-dismissed, non-dev update is pending — `260713-4zap`)** · NotificationControl (🔔) · ThemeToggle (◐) · **RefreshButton (⟳)** · HelpLink (?) · **connection dot (●)** |

Each control carries the shared `rk-glint` chip styling (`min-w-[24px] min-h-[24px] coarse:min-w-[30px] coarse:min-h-[30px]`). There is no per-control `hidden sm:flex` breakpoint cliff: controls do not vanish below `sm`; under width pressure they overflow into the chevron menu at any width (§ Right cluster → overflow chevron menu). L1's absence on non-terminal pages just widens the gap to the breadcrumb; the L3 always-block keeps its fixed right edge (the brand anchor lives in the left nav as the root crumb). Mode deltas: (`260702-6m46`, `260704-9o7k`, `260715-h1ck`)

- **L3 order is user-specified**: Notification → Theme → Refresh → Help, then the dot as the **right-most status terminator** (not a button). The conditional **UpdateChip leads the block** (Update → Notification → Theme → Refresh → Help → dot) — it renders only when a qualifying, un-dismissed, non-`dev` update is pending, so its absence just tightens the gap (§ Update Notification). (`260713-4zap`)
- **RefreshButton** is L3 — renders in every mode (a reload is meaningful everywhere): plain click `window.location.reload()`, Shift+click `forceReload()`. See § Refresh button.
- **FixedWidthToggle** is L1 (terminal-only). The 900px `maxWidth` wrapper lives in AppShell (`app.tsx`), which renders both `terminal` AND `server`, so **the tmux Server page keeps the constraint and the `View: Fixed Width` palette access** — only the tmux Server page button is absent (it is a no-op on Board/Host, which never read `fixedWidth`). See § Command Palette View actions.
- **TerminalFontControl (Aa)** gates on the L2 predicate `mode === "terminal" || mode === "board"` (a terminal-bearing surface: the single window or a board pane).
- **ClosePaneButton (✕) is mode-branched** (one component): terminal ✕ is a real close-pane (`closePane`) of the current window's active pane; board ✕ routes through `onRequestKill` to open the **kill confirm dialog** whose confirmed action is a window-kill of the focused tile's window (with an `Unpin instead` escape). Unpin lives on the tile header + palette, not the ✕. See § Close pane button / § Board Kill Confirm Dialog. (`260715-6jwn`, `260718-co9z`)
- **BoardAutofitToggle is board-only, INSIDE L2**: a toggle rendered **between Aa and ✕** in the L2 cluster, gated `mode === "board" && onToggleAutofit` (narrower than the L2 predicate — it does NOT appear on terminal). Mirrors `FixedWidthToggle` (`aria-pressed`, `rk-glint`, `coarse:` sizing) and flips the per-board desktop autofit preference. See § Board Autofit Toggle. (`260708-738w`)

**Overflow chevron menu (priority+ degradation).** The pyramid above is consumed by a browser-toolbar-style priority+ overflow menu: as the right `1fr` track shrinks, controls drop into a dropdown behind an always-visible down-chevron rather than clipping or vanishing. Registry + measurement live in `top-bar.tsx`; the chevron/menu component is `components/top-bar-overflow-menu.tsx`; the fit math is `lib/top-bar-overflow.ts` (+ colocated `.test.ts`). (`260715-h1ck`)

- **Ordered registry drives the cluster.** The right cluster is built from an ordered `RegistryEntry[]` (`{ id, tier — implicit in position, modes: TopBarMode[], hidden?, barRender: () => ReactNode, menuRender: () => ReactNode }`), one entry per control in drop order — **`view-switcher` LEADS the list** (terminal-only, first-to-drop), then the pyramid: L1 split-vertical · split-horizontal · fixed-width; L2 terminal-font · autofit · close-pane; L3 update-chip · notification · theme · refresh · help. One ordered source drives BOTH the bar (first-that-fit render `barRender` as icon buttons) and the menu (the rest render `menuRender` as labeled rows), so bar↔menu can never drift. Filtered per render by `modes.includes(mode)` and the optional `hidden` predicate (an entry with `hidden` true renders NOWHERE — not bar, not menu, not the measurement probe): `view-switcher` `hidden: !(mode==="terminal" && currentWindow && onSelectView && availableViews && availableViews.length > 1)`; `notification` `hidden: pushUnsupported`; splits/fixed-width `hidden: !currentWindow`; autofit `hidden: !(mode==="board" && onToggleAutofit)`; `update-chip` `hidden: !showChip` (kept out of the candidate set entirely so it never reserves an empty slot). Gating is 100% registry data — no per-item `hidden sm:flex` empty-flex-item gap hack. (`260717-6anu`)

- **Drop order = registry consumed from the LEFT; surviving buttons never shift.** Overflow eats the **`view-switcher` FIRST** (it leads the list), then L1, then L2, then L3, leftmost-within-tier first — so the surviving in-bar set is a SUFFIX of the registry order and every survivor keeps its exact screen position (the pyramid invariant; the pill keeps its leftmost in-bar position while it survives). Implementation: the fit function reverses the measured widths (L3-end first), `computeVisibleCount` greedily fits from the tail, and the returned N trailing candidates stay in-bar while the leading `candidates.length − N` overflow into the menu (in registry order). `visibleItems = candidates.slice(splitAt)`, `overflowItems = candidates.slice(0, splitAt)`. (`260717-6anu`)

- **Exempt items never overflow**: the exempt set is only the **overflow chevron itself** and the **connection dot** — the ViewSwitcher is the first *candidate* (§ ViewSwitcher chip; it drops first, before L1). The chevron+dot render in a **trailing block** (`trailingRef`, chevron immediately LEFT of the dot — the dot keeps its right-most status-terminator role); their measured width is the only thing RESERVED before candidates are placed. So `reserved = trailing + RIGHT_GAP_PX` (the trailing block plus one `gap-3` joining it to the last candidate); the pill's width is contributed by the probe row like every other candidate. (`260717-6anu`)

- **Attention badge**: when an attention-bearing item is overflowed — today only the UpdateChip, i.e. `showChip && overflowItems` contains `update-chip` (`updateOverflowed`) — the chevron carries a small accent-green dot so the update signal isn't lost when the chip is hidden into the menu. No badge when the chip is in-bar or no qualifying update.

- **Always-present menu + fixed version row.** The chevron renders even when nothing overflows, because the menu ALWAYS ends with a fixed `RunKit v{version}` row (§ Steady-state version surfaces → surface 5): click copies the displayed version + toasts; plain `RunKit` when `daemonVersion` is null. When a qualifying update is pending AND the UpdateChip is overflowed, that row FLIPS to the update surface (`RunKit v{current} → v{latest} ⬆`, click = `updateNow()`) and no separate UpdateChip menu row is added (the `update-chip` entry's `menuRender` returns `null` by design). The chip and the version-row update surface share the `useUpdateClick()` hook so the updating-state + failure toast can't drift.

- **Menu-row representations** (`menuRender` closures): view-switcher → **one `View: {label}` row per available view** (`View: Terminal`/`View: Web`/`View: Chat`) via `ViewSwitcherMenuRows` in tty-first `orderViews()` order, active row inverse-video accent-green + `aria-pressed`, click = `onSelectView(view)` + close (§ ViewSwitcher chip → overflow representation); splits → "Split vertical" / "Split horizontal"; fixed-width → "Fixed width" `role="menuitemcheckbox"` (checked=`fixedWidth`); terminal-font (Aa) → an inline `−`/`+` stepper `role="group"` row operating on `terminalFontSize` within `TERMINAL_FONT_BOUNDS` (does NOT reopen the Aa popover); autofit → "Autofit panes" checkbox row; close-pane → "Close pane" in BOTH modes (a real close-pane, not the board "Unpin pane" label) honoring the same disabled conditions; notification → NotificationControl's own dropdown FLATTENED into direct "Enable notifications" / "Send test notification" rows; theme → "Theme: {current}" cycle row (shares the extracted `cycleTheme()` with the in-bar ThemeToggle — review M5); refresh → "Refresh page" row (Shift+click force-reload preserved; the "page" word disambiguates from the `Status: Refresh` palette action, `260715-jykd`); help → "Help / Documentation" external `HELP_URL` link.

- **Menu a11y mirrors `BreadcrumbDropdown`**: `role="menu"` panel / `role="menuitem"`/`menuitemcheckbox` rows, `position: fixed` anchored to the trigger rect (top just below, right-aligned — no ancestor `overflow-hidden` clips it, no new dependency), Escape closes + refocuses the chevron, ArrowUp/ArrowDown move focus, outside `mousedown` closes, glued to a moving trigger via scroll/resize reflow. **Row-click close keys on the target's ROLE, not the row wrapper** (review S1): a click landing on a `role="menuitem"`/`menuitemcheckbox` closes the panel (single-shot action), but the font stepper's `−`/`+` are plain buttons inside a `role="group"`, so repeated stepping does NOT close the menu.

- **Measurement mechanism** (in `top-bar.tsx`, collapse-first, no hysteresis): the right cell is given `min-w-0` so its `1fr` grid track is squeezable (the left/center floors make the track width grid-determined — no feedback loop, no oscillation). **The cell must FILL the `1fr` track — `flex … justify-end … min-w-0`, NOT `justify-self-end`** (M1, load-bearing): `justify-self-end` content-sizes the box, which both deadlocks the fit (with collapse-first `visibleCount=0` the box measures only the exempt block → budget < 0 forever) and never fires the ResizeObserver on window resize (a content-sized box's width doesn't track the viewport); default grid stretch fills the track and `justify-end` right-aligns content inside it.
