A single `ResizeObserver` observes the cell + a hidden off-screen `inert`/`aria-hidden` **probe row** (renders every candidate's `barRender` so real widths are always known — buttons vary by ViewSwitcher/UpdateChip/`coarse:` sizing, nothing hardcoded; the ViewSwitcher is a candidate IN this probe row) + the trailing chevron/dot block (the only reserved node), so reserved/candidate width changes (the ViewSwitcher's probe width changing when it gains a segment or the active segment shifts, the UpdateChip's `⬆ v{latest}` label width changing) re-fit too even though they don't resize the outer cell (S2). The measure effect's dep array retains `availableViews`/`activeView` because the ViewSwitcher's probe width varies with segment count and the active segment. The pure `computeVisibleCount(availableWidth, itemWidths, reservedWidth, gap)` (front-consuming greedy fit, `gap` charged between rendered items only, clamp `[0, len]`, 0 for a non-positive budget) is unit-tested in isolation. Collapse-first: `visibleCount` starts at 0 (`useState(0)`) and is set in a `useLayoutEffect` before paint, so no flash of overflowing buttons. The cell carries `min-w-0` but deliberately **NO `overflow-hidden`** — the only content that can exceed a very-narrow track is the always-present exempt chevron+dot block, which must stay visible/clickable (R6); `.app-shell`/`header` clip any horizontal page overflow. (`260717-6anu`)

- **Keyboard path (Constitution V)**: the menu is a pointer affordance; the command palette exposes every affected action (the menu is itself keyboard-operable per its a11y contract). Coverage: `lib/top-bar-overflow.test.ts` (fit edge cases), `top-bar.test.tsx` / `update-chip.test.tsx` (chevron presence, menu open, version-row states, a working menu action), `view-switcher.test.tsx` (the `ViewSwitcherMenuRows` per-view rows in `orderViews()` order, active marking + aria, click callback, single-view `null`), and the width-sweep e2e `tests/e2e/top-bar-overflow.spec.ts` (+ `.spec.md`) — 1280→…→375px asserting no overlap, monotonic drop, menu = exactly the dropped controls + version row, exempt items always visible, a menu action firing, and (on a multi-view window) the view-switcher FIRST-to-drop with its per-view `View:` menu rows + row activation switching the lens. The e2e is the regression proof for the M1 fit-wiring (jsdom's zero widths mean the Vitest layer can't catch fit defects). (`260717-6anu`)

**Connection dot** (`role="status"`, `aria-live="polite"`, green `bg-accent-green` / gray `bg-text-secondary`, `aria-label` Connected/Disconnected) — the right-most element, in **ALL four modes**. It carries a hover **`title`** that folds in the running version — a computed `dotTitle`: `Disconnected` when `!isConnected`, else `Connected — run-kit {displayVersion(daemonVersion)}` when `daemonVersion` is known, else bare `Connected` (the version fragment is OMITTED until the first `version` event so the title is never `vundefined`). `daemonVersion` is read via `useUpdateNotification()` (already imported for the UpdateChip); `displayVersion` from `lib/palette-version`. The **`aria-label` stays the concise `Connected`/`Disconnected`** — the version is hover-discovery detail, not screen-reader-essential state on the live region. Its meaning is per-page "this page's live data is flowing", derived by each caller and passed as `isConnected`. (`260704-9o7k`, `260715-ifco`)

**A dot reads Connected only when the state socket is connected AND the page's relevant subscription has ACKED.** A bare socket connection is not enough — the subscription must have received its `ack` (the fresh snapshot). Per-caller derivation: (`260716-qf3j`)

- **Terminal / tmux Server**: the current server's slice `isConnected` (`isConnectedByServer.get(server)` mirrored through ChromeProvider) — now true iff the socket is up AND that server's `subscribe` acked (its slice flips Connected on `ack`, and back on the socket-level disconnect debounce). Reconnect nuance (nice-to-have, `A-011`): on socket re-open a previously-acked server flips Connected before its fresh re-ack lands (ms-scale window).
- **Host**: `hostMetricsConnected` from `useSessionContext()` — the dedicated `metrics` subscription's debounced ack-health when no server is attached, else true iff any attached server subscription is connected (per-server metrics fan-out); architecture.md § Server-independent host-metrics subscription.
- **Board**: `boardConnected` — AND over the board's attached servers (green iff ≥1 entry AND every distinct attached server's slice is connected, i.e. subscribed-and-acked).

**Help link** (`HelpLink` in `top-bar.tsx`): an external-docs chip in the L3 always-block, after `RefreshButton` (Refresh sits between Theme and Help) and before the connection dot. It is a registry candidate (`id: "help"`) — it overflows into the chevron menu as a "Help / Documentation" row when it doesn't fit. An **`<a>`, not a button** — it navigates externally to the exported `HELP_URL` constant (`https://shll.ai/run-kit`) with `target="_blank"` + `rel="noopener noreferrer"`, so the live dashboard (terminals, SSE) is never unloaded. Carries the shared cluster chip styling verbatim (`rk-glint` glint hover + `min-w-[24px] min-h-[24px] coarse:min-w-[30px] coarse:min-h-[30px] rounded border border-border text-text-secondary hover:border-text-secondary`) and a 14px inline `currentColor` `?` SVG glyph matching the sibling icons; `aria-label`/`title` "Help — run-kit docs". `HELP_URL` is defined once in `top-bar.tsx` (mirroring the `NOTIFICATIONS_HELP_URL` precedent) and **exported** so the palette action reuses the same constant — the two cannot drift. The palette counterpart is the `Help: Documentation` action (`id: "help-documentation"`), registered in `app.tsx`'s `configActions` next to `Help: Keyboard Shortcuts` — so it reaches the **AppShell palette only** (Terminal + tmux Server), NOT the board route's own `boardRouteActions` (which carries only `refresh-page` + the terminal-font trio) and NOT the Host page (mounts no palette). **The chip itself renders on every route** (mode-invariant right cluster); it is only the *palette* affordance that is AppShell-scoped. Unit-tested in `top-bar.test.tsx` (asserts `href`, `target="_blank"`, `rel` containing `noopener`, and an accessible name); no dedicated e2e — a static anchor in existing chrome has no interactive flow to drive. (`260704-hmd0`, `260704-9o7k`, `260715-h1ck`)

**Split buttons** (`SplitButton` in `top-bar.tsx`): Two inline components calling `splitWindow(server, windowId, horizontal, cwd)` from `api/client.ts`. Custom SVG icons (square-split pattern). Best-effort error handling — tmux may reject if pane is too small. `POST /api/windows/{windowId}/split` with `{ "horizontal": bool }`. **Rendered on terminal AND board mode** (L1). Terminal: `server`/`windowId` come from `currentWindow`, `server` read from `useSessionContext()`. Board: fed by the slot's `focusedPane` — a `mode === "board" && focusedPane && (...)` block renders the same two `SplitButton`s wired to the **focused tile's** `{server, windowId, cwd}`. Window IDs are server-unique, so targeting a pinned window's ID works even though it lives in a hidden `_rk-pin-*` session; the split lands relative to that window's active pane and renders live inside the tile. Absent when the board is empty (no `focusedPane`); same `hidden sm:flex` gating as terminal. (`260715-6jwn`)

**Close pane button** (`ClosePaneButton` in `top-bar.tsx`): the L2 ✕ chip — **mode-branched** between a terminal close-pane and a board window-kill. Props: `server?`, `windowId?`, `disabled?: boolean`, `onClosed?: () => void`, `onRequestKill?: () => void` (board routing), `label = "Close pane"`. (`260718-co9z`)
- **Terminal mode**: the optimistic close-pane path — `closePane(server, windowId)` via `useOptimisticAction`, spinner (`LogoSpinner`) + `disabled` while `isPending`. `POST /api/windows/{windowId}/close-pane` → `tmux.KillActivePane`. Rendered only when `currentWindow` exists; also "Pane: Close" in the palette. Terminal-mode ✕ semantics are UNCHANGED (out of scope of `260718-co9z`).
- **Board mode**: when `onRequestKill` is present (registered by `BoardPage`) the ✕ calls it INSTEAD of `closePane`, opening the **kill confirm dialog** (§ Board Kill Confirm Dialog) rather than firing immediately; the confirmed action is a window-kill (`killWindow`), not a close-pane, with an `Unpin instead` escape. Its label/aria/tooltip become "Kill". `disabled={!focusedPane}` so the ✕ is disabled on an empty board. The confirm gate + escalation exist because a board pane's blast radius — the whole window everywhere, including its home session — is otherwise illegible. (`260715-6jwn`, `260718-co9z`)
- **Self-heal seam**: post-kill board refetch rides `executeKillWindow`'s own `onSettled` in `board-page.tsx` (§ Board Kill Confirm Dialog), not an `onClosed` callback on this button. The self-heal covers the no-`board-changed`-on-kill gap: killing a window collapses its single-window pin-session with no `board-changed` SSE event — fired only by pin/unpin/reorder — so the refetch lets `getBoard` drop the vanished tile and an emptied board fall out of `GET /api/boards`.

X-shaped close icon SVG (`width="14" height="14" viewBox="0 0 24 24"`), shared `rk-glint` chip styling. It is the L2 registry `close-pane` candidate — it renders in-bar when it fits and overflows into the chevron menu as a "Close pane" (terminal) / "Kill" (board) row honoring the same disabled conditions (board `disabled={!focusedPane}`). Unpin is not on the ✕ — it lives on the tile-header pin-glyph button (§ Board Tile Header) and the `Board: Unpin Focused Pane` palette action (§ Boards Command Palette), both driven by the shared `unpinFocused` handler in `board-page.tsx` (`unpin(entries[focusedIndex].server, .windowId, name)`, `POST /api/boards/{name}/unpin`). (`260715-h1ck`)

**Board autofit toggle** (`BoardAutofitToggle` in `top-bar.tsx`): the L2 cluster's **board-only** toggle, rendered **between `Aa` (`TerminalFontControl`) and `✕` (`ClosePaneButton`)** but gated on `mode === "board" && onToggleAutofit` (narrower than the terminal+board L2 predicate — it never renders on the Terminal route). Props: `autofit: boolean`, `onToggle: () => void`. Mirrors the `FixedWidthToggle` vocabulary — `aria-label="Toggle board autofit"`, `aria-pressed={autofit}`, shared `rk-glint` glint hover + `coarse:` touch sizing, `title` reflecting on/off ("Autofit on (panes fill the row)" / "Autofit off (fixed pane widths)"). Clicking it flips the per-board desktop autofit preference; the palette counterpart `Board: Toggle Autofit (on/off)` flips the SAME state (Constitution V parity). It is wired from `BoardPage` through the top-bar slot context (`autofit` + `onToggleAutofit`) → `RootTopBar` (`app.tsx`) → `TopBar` props (tolerant-empty: absent `onToggleAutofit` ⇒ no toggle). The behavior it controls (equal-share flex layout, hidden resize handles, non-destructive stored-width round-trip) lives in § Board Autofit Toggle. (`260708-738w`)

**Refresh button** (`RefreshButton` in `top-bar.tsx`): part of the **L3 always-block** — a reload is meaningful on every page, rendered between `ThemeToggle` and `HelpLink`. It is a registry candidate (`id: "refresh"`) — it renders in-bar in all four modes when it fits and overflows into the chevron menu as a "Refresh page" row otherwise. A **plain `<button type="button">`** whose `onClick` does a **full page reload** — plain click `window.location.reload()`; **Shift+click force-reloads** via the exported `forceReload()` helper (a `fetch(location.href, { cache: "reload" })` that overwrites the document's HTTP cache entry, then `reload()` in `.finally` so it fires even offline — Chrome Shift+reload semantics. The fetch races a 3s timeout (`Promise.race`, then `clearTimeout` in `.finally`) so a **stalled** socket that never resolves *or* rejects still reloads — `.catch` alone covers rejection but not an indefinite hang). `aria-label` "Refresh page", `title` "Refresh page (Shift+click: force reload)", carrying the shared cluster className (`min-w-[24px] min-h-[24px] coarse:min-w-[30px] coarse:min-h-[30px] rounded border border-border …`) and a 14×14 `aria-hidden` stroke SVG (lucide `rotate-cw` — a circular arrow + top-right arrowhead, `stroke="currentColor" strokeWidth="2"`, round caps/joins) matching the sibling split/close glyphs. It is the in-app recovery affordance for degraded terminal views (stale relay / wedged xterm / SSE drift) where browser chrome is out of reach (PWA/standalone/kiosk). Deliberately **NO spinner / `useOptimisticAction` / `isPending` / `LogoSpinner`, NO `disabled` state, and NO confirmation** (unlike Split / Close) — the page unloads synchronously so a spinner would never meaningfully render, and the reload is non-destructive by design (constitution II/VI: all client state re-derives on load; tmux sessions are unaffected). The same action is reachable from the command palette as "View: Refresh Page" (see § Boards Command Palette / § Command Palette View actions below). It is a full reload rather than a targeted relay-reconnect (§ Design Decisions → Refresh is a full page reload). (`260703-p29w`, `260704-9o7k`, `260715-h1ck`)

**Toolbar button color convention**: All toolbar buttons (top bar and bottom bar) use `text-text-secondary` as their default foreground color. Active toggle states (Ctrl/Alt modifiers when armed, FixedWidthToggle when active) use `text-accent` with accent background. Hover state uses `hover:border-text-secondary` (border highlight). This convention applies to: compose button, theme toggle, fixed-width toggle, split buttons, close pane button, Esc, Tab, Ctrl, Alt, Fn trigger, arrow pad, and ⌘K.

### Window Heading (`WindowHeading` in `top-bar.tsx`)

The centered, highlighted, editable window heading — the single most important identity on the Terminal route (the tmux window name, e.g. `riff-gallant-jackal`). It gives the window name the prominence of a document title (mental model: browser-tab / editor title bar) and makes rename lowest-friction direct manipulation. Lives in the top bar's center grid cell (§ Chrome (Top Bar) center cell); renders only when `mode === "terminal" && currentWindow`. It is the terminal instance of the universal `PageType: name` heading — a static prefix span sits OUTSIDE the rename button, and the name is driven by the shared boot-sweep primitive (`useBootSweep`/`SweepCells`, § Hover-Animation Vocabulary → boot sweep). **The prefix is a static `Window:` in every lens** (§ Heading is a static `Window:`): `WindowHeading` takes a `prefix` prop, but the sole call site passes the CONSTANT `WINDOW_PREFIX` — the heading does not vary by lens (the `ViewSwitcher` shows the lens — the overflow-registry chip or, when collapsed, its `View:` menu rows). (`260704-pr0p`, `260714-uco1`, `260717-6anu`)

**Two-tone prefix**: the `Window:` prefix (static in every lens) renders `text-text-secondary` as a **static sibling span outside the rename button/input** (`hidden sm:inline` — mobile keeps just the name) — clicking it never starts an edit, and the button's `aria-label` stays clean. The name keeps `font-semibold text-text-primary`. The prefix's frame states (dim ahead of cursor / typed behind) come from the boot sweep's `prefix` half. (`260704-pr0p`, `260714-uco1`)

**Three states** (one component):

- **display** — a `<button aria-label="Rename window {name}" title="Click to rename">` rendering the name (via `<SweepCells>` at rest → plain text) at `text-sm font-semibold text-text-primary` (weight-600 + primary color IS the "highlighted" rest state; the surrounding crumbs are secondary, so weight+color alone read as highlighted — no background). `max-w-[16ch] sm:max-w-[28ch] inline-flex items-center coarse:min-h-[30px]` (mobile-leaf touch target), with the name inside an inner `min-w-0 truncate` span — truncation MUST live on the span, not the button: `text-overflow` is inert on a flex container, and flex centering clipped long names on BOTH ends with no ellipsis (`riff-blustery-whale` → `iff-blustery-whal`). Left-anchored, so long names keep their head and cut at the tail; the button itself stays centered in the grid cell. Click enters edit.
- **boot sweep** — the JS sweep from `useBootSweep` (§ Hover-Animation Vocabulary → boot sweep). One inverse-video accent-green cursor at `DECODE_FRAME_MS = 28`ms/cell sweeps `Window:` + space + name; over the prefix it types (TypedLabel states), over the name it churns `DECODE_GLYPHS`. The heading container does NOT flip `text-accent-green` for the whole scramble — green lives ONLY on the per-cell churn/cursor spans inside `SweepCells`; each resolved cell settles to its own REST color (`restCellClass`: prefix → `text-secondary`, name → semibold `text-primary`), so the left-to-right two-tone reveal is visible instead of a uniform green flash. **Guards**: (a) a `DECODE_HOVER_INTENT_MS = 140`ms hover-intent delay before the sweep starts (cursor transit toward the right buttons doesn't replay it); (b) edit-start stops the sweep and the input binds to the real `name`/`draft` state, never the scrambled DOM text; (c) the sweep replays once whenever the **DISPLAYED name changes** — a `prevNameRef` **seeded `null`** effect keyed on the incoming `name` prop. The null seed plays the sweep ONCE on mount (first name resolution flips `prevNameRef` from `null`), so route navigation between page types animates — AND a committed rename, an SSE external rename, and window navigation all replay through the same name-change mechanism. This is why the instance is NOT remounted per window — a fresh mount would re-seed `prevNameRef` to `null` and replay every time / double-play. Skipped entirely under `prefers-reduced-motion` (`prefersReducedMotion()` reads `window.matchMedia`, guarded for jsdom — the rest state IS the reduced-motion state). (`260704-pr0p`)
- **edit** — an identically-styled inline `<input aria-label="Window name">` (monospace, `text-left font-semibold text-text-primary`, `border-b border-accent`; `text-left` so the name does not jump horizontally on edit entry given the left-anchored heading), width sized in `ch` and growing with content (`Math.max(draft.length + 1, 3)ch`), `autoFocus` + select-on-focus. **Enter commits, Escape cancels, blur commits**; empty/whitespace-only trim on commit = cancel (matches the sidebar/dialog trim guard); an unchanged name is also a no-op. Commit calls the shared `useWindowRename()` hook (§ Shared window rename below) — optimistic store rename + toast on error — then optimistically sets the display; the name-change effect replays the sweep when the store-driven `name` prop settles. (`260714-uco1`)

**Keyboard path (Constitution V)**: the command-palette `Window: Rename` action dispatches a `window-heading:rename` `CustomEvent` (mirroring `theme-selector:open`); a document-level listener in `WindowHeading` enters inline edit. There is no rename modal dialog — the inline edit (heading + sidebar) is the only window-rename surface; see § Keyboard Shortcuts (the palette rename action) and § Component Conventions (the shared `Dialog`). Only the SESSION rename dialog lives in `app.tsx`.

**External-switch cancel**: a `prevIdentityRef` effect keyed on `${server}:${windowId}` cancels an in-progress edit when the window identity changes out from under it (another client / tmux switching the route) — committing the typed name onto the newly-navigated window would rename the wrong window.

### Display-only page headings (`PageHeadingDisplay` in `top-bar.tsx`)

The board/server/host siblings of `WindowHeading` — a `PageHeadingDisplay({ prefix, name, solo?, ariaLabel })` that renders the same `PageType: name` two-tone identity via the SAME `useBootSweep`/`SweepCells` primitive, but with NO rename affordance (boards/servers have no rename API; the host mode has no instance). The static prefix span is `hidden sm:inline` (same mobile rule as terminal); the `solo` variant (host) renders the single word primary-medium and visible at all breakpoints. Hover replays the sweep behind the 140ms intent; mount + displayed-name-change replay via the same `null`-seeded `prevNameRef` effect; reduced motion skips. **A11y**: the identity carries a STABLE `aria-label` (the churn glyphs are `aria-hidden` inside `SweepCells`) placed on a `role="group"` wrapper — `aria-label` is prohibited on the implicit `role="generic"` of a bare `<div>`/`<span>`, so `role="group"` is what makes it a valid, screen-reader-stable accessible name. No `<h1>` is added to the top bar. (`260704-pr0p`)

**Tests**: `top-bar.test.tsx` covers the heading display/edit states (click → input, Enter commits via `renameWindow`, Escape/empty-trim cancel), the `window-heading:rename` CustomEvent entering edit, AND per-mode heading coverage (terminal `Window:` prefix sibling, board `Board:` + board switcher in the center, server `tmux Server:`, solo `Host`; board left nav shows only counts/hint — no `Board ▸`, no left board name; server left nav has no `aria-current` leaf). E2e `tests/e2e/window-heading.spec.ts` (+ sibling `.spec.md`, per the constitution's Test Companion Docs rule) covers, documented 1:1 in the `.spec.md`: the terminal heading renders the name once with a static `Window:` prefix sibling (NOT a trailing breadcrumb crumb); click → inline input → Enter commits (sidebar + heading reflect the new name); Escape cancels (window id unchanged); the palette `window-heading:rename` CustomEvent enters inline edit; the 375px bar stays single-line with no horizontal overflow; hover-treatment classes present and unchanged under `reducedMotion: "reduce"`; the board/server/host centered headings render with their prefixes; the `[ SESSIONS▊ ]` section-heading shape; a motion-opted-in **boot-sweep** e2e (hover the heading → an `.rk-typed-cursor` cell attaches → resolves to rest, since the units stub `matchMedia` to reduced-motion and never exercise the sweep behaviorally); and a reduced-context check that the sweep never starts (JS-gated). (`260704-pr0p`, `260714-uco1`)

### Shared window rename (`useWindowRename`, `hooks/use-window-rename.ts`)

`useWindowRename()` returns `execute(server, session, windowId, newName)` — the ONE optimistic window-rename action, used by BOTH the top-bar `WindowHeading` AND the sidebar inline rename (`sidebar/index.tsx:398`), so the two surfaces rename identically. It stamps the window store's `pendingName` (`renameWindow`) on `onOptimistic`, rolls back via `clearRename` on failure with a toast, and clears the pending marker on settle (SSE snapshot then becomes authoritative). The captured `(server, session, windowId)` is held in a `lastRenameRef` so rollback/settle target the right entry even if the caller re-renders between execute and resolution. Callers own their own trim/empty-name guards before calling (rename is unconditional inside the hook). Session rename is NOT part of this hook — it keeps its own dialog/inline path (§ Sidebar → Session rename). (`260703-5ilm`)

### Hover-Animation Vocabulary

A site-wide motion map where each treatment encodes **exactly one** category of element, so motion carries meaning instead of noise. The shared color cue: **the animated element turns `--color-accent-green` while it animates** (the brand chip on glitch-hover, the boot-sweep cursor + name-churn cells, both caret variants, the stepping brackets — user-requested — including the glint: the sweep strip is accent-green-tinted and the hovered chip's border + glyph flip green for the hover duration, the "green line"). **Scope note**: the boot-sweep green is PER-CELL — only the single cursor cell and the unresolved name-churn glyphs are green; the heading container does NOT tint green wholesale, so resolved cells settle to their own rest color and the two-tone reveal reads left-to-right (`260704-pr0p`). All utilities live in `globals.css` (beside the `logo-chase` keyframes / `coarse` variant; Tailwind CSS 4). Under `@media (prefers-reduced-motion: reduce)` the contract is **animations zeroed, not styling removed**: the CSS gate zeroes every keyframe animation (classes stay in the DOM — that is the test seam), the JS treatments (decode, typed sweep) skip themselves by reading the same media query, and static hover styling (e.g. the glint's green border/glyph flip) remains — a color change is not motion. No pixel assertions in tests — treatments are asserted via class-presence + reduced-motion emulation, plus one behavioral guard for the caret (below).

| Category | Treatment | Mechanism |
|----------|-----------|-----------|
| **Brand** | glitch | `.rk-brand-glitch` on the top-left "RunKit" brand anchor — one-shot `@keyframes rk-glitch` RGB-split `text-shadow` (~300ms, `steps(2)`, ±2px split) on `:hover`, plus `color: var(--color-accent-green)` for the hover duration (the color snap is what makes the glitch read at 11.5px; the split is texture — the shadow alone was barely visible). Wordmark hidden below `sm`, so on mobile only the icon jitters (accepted). |
| **Top-bar page heading** | boot sweep | JS in `top-bar.tsx` — the shared `useBootSweep` hook + `SweepCells` renderer (see § Window Heading / § Display-only page headings), NOT a CSS class. ONE inverse-video accent-green cursor at `DECODE_FRAME_MS` (28ms/cell) sweeps `PageType:` + space + `name`: over the PREFIX it types like TypedLabel (`rk-typed-off` ahead / `rk-typed-cursor` cursor cell / `text-secondary` resolved); over the NAME the cells right of the cursor churn `DECODE_GLYPHS` in accent-green from frame 0, each locked to its true char as the cursor arrives, resolved cells settling to semibold `text-primary` (spaces preserved). Reuses the `rk-typed-*` cell classes + `DECODE_*` constants — no class of its own. (`260703-5ilm`, `260704-pr0p`) |
| **Section headings** | brackets + caret | `.rk-bracket-group` scoped to `SectionHeading`'s inner bracket cluster ONLY (not the row/rule/`side`). On group `:hover` the `.rk-bracket-open`/`.rk-bracket-close` spans step outward `translateX(∓3px)` + turn `--color-accent-green` (transform only — no layout shift), and a `.rk-bracket-caret` (always-reserved `1ch` cell, accent-green, transparent at rest so the closing bracket never shifts) blinks `▊` (`@keyframes rk-caret-blink`, 1.06s `steps(1)`). Moved from the retired `PageHeading` to the in-page section labels by `260704-pr0p`. See § Section Heading. |
| **Section labels** | typed sweep | `TypedLabel` (`components/typed-label.tsx`) — on hover the label fades (`.rk-typed-off`, 26% opacity) and an inverse-video cursor (`.rk-typed-cursor`, accent-green cell OVER the character — a terminal block cursor sitting on text) sweeps from the FIRST cell, "typing" each character back to full brightness (`.rk-typed-on`); after the pass the label holds bright (`rk-typed-done`) until pointer-leave. Fixed ~350ms TOTAL pass regardless of length (per-cell = 350/len clamped 20–60ms) so all labels read as one gesture; width never changes (the cursor occupies its cell). JS-driven (the frame states are the `globals.css` `.rk-typed-*` classes); reduced motion skips the sweep entirely in JS. Applied to the sidebar panel titles (`collapsible-panel.tsx`) and the sidebar `Sessions` region heading (`sidebar/index.tsx`) directly, and — inside the `SectionHeading` brackets — on the tmux Server page's `Sessions` heading (`session-tiles.tsx`) and the four Host-page zone `h2`s (Host Health / Boards / Tmux Servers / Services, `host-overview-page.tsx`), where the typed sweep and the brackets+caret hover compose on one element (`260704-pr0p`). The sidebar labels are deliberately NOT bracket targets (typed-sweep only). Decorative — headings stay non-interactive-looking at rest. |
| **Buttons** | CRT glint + green line | `.rk-glint` — `position:relative; overflow:hidden` + an `::after` skewed accent-green highlight strip sweeping across the button face on `:hover` (`@keyframes rk-glint-sweep`, ~450ms one-shot), plus `.rk-glint:hover:not(:disabled)` flipping border + glyph to `--color-accent-green` (unlayered rule, so it beats the chips' Tailwind hover utilities without touching call sites; chosen over a fill/inverse cell so hover never reads as the armed state's solid accent fill). Applied to every top-bar right-cluster chip (SplitButton, ClosePaneButton, TerminalFontControl, NotificationControl, ThemeToggle, FixedWidthToggle, BoardAutofitToggle, HelpLink) AND the bottom-bar `KBD_CLASS` buttons. `overflow:hidden` is verified safe — the font/bell popovers are SIBLINGS of their trigger buttons, not children, so clipping never clips a popover. |

**Typed-sweep note**: the section-label treatment is the `TypedLabel` typed sweep (no CSS-only hover caret); the e2e guard asserts the sweep behaviorally (cursor cell attaches → `rk-typed-done` lands → unhover resets). The `.rk-bracket-caret` is a separate, reserved `1ch` blinking caret cell inside the bracket group, carried by `SectionHeading`. The section labels compose BOTH vocabularies on one element: the typed sweep (TypedLabel, inside the brackets) AND the brackets+caret hover (the `rk-bracket-group` cluster around them). (`260704-pr0p`)

### Theme System

> Full spec: [`docs/specs/themes.md`](../../specs/themes.md) — architecture, ANSI palette structure, tmux colour mapping, import script usage, persistence model.

Palette-based theme model: each theme defines a `ThemePalette` with 22 canonical terminal colors — `foreground`, `background`, `cursorColor`, `cursorText`, `selectionBackground`, `selectionForeground`, plus 16 ANSI colors (indices 0-15) as a fixed-length readonly tuple. The `Theme` type has shape `{ id, name, category, palette }` — no `colors` or `themeColor` properties (both replaced by derivation from palette).

20 built-in themes (14 dark + 6 light) defined in `app/frontend/src/themes.ts` with canonical ANSI palettes sourced from iTerm2-Color-Schemes / official theme repos. Three consumers derive from the same palette:

1. **Web UI CSS** — `deriveUIColors(palette, category)` produces 8 `UIColors` keys (`bgPrimary`, `bgCard`, `bgInset`, `textPrimary`, `textSecondary`, `border`, `accent`, `accentGreen`). Derivation: `bgPrimary` = background, `bgCard` = lighten/darken background, `bgInset` = darken background, `textPrimary` = foreground, `textSecondary` = ansi[8] (bright black), `border` = blend(fg, bg, 0.25), `accent` = ansi[4] (blue), `accentGreen` = ansi[2] (green). Color utility helpers (`hexToRgb`, `rgbToHex`, `lightenHex`, `darkenHex`, `blendHex`) are module-private. CSS custom properties (`--color-bg-primary`, etc.) applied via inline styles on `document.documentElement.style` overriding `globals.css` fallbacks.
2. **xterm.js canvas** — `deriveXtermTheme(palette)` produces an xterm.js `ITheme` with all 22 colors mapped (background, foreground, cursor, cursorAccent, selectionBackground, selectionForeground, and 16 named ANSI colors black through brightWhite). Terminal content (syntax highlighting, colored prompts, git diff output) matches the selected theme.
3. **tmux chrome** — `configs/tmux/default.conf` uses ANSI `colour{N}` indices (colour0-colour15) instead of hardcoded hex. Because tmux renders its chrome as escape sequences that xterm.js interprets, changing the xterm.js ANSI palette automatically themes tmux status bar, pane borders, and pane-border-format. No runtime `tmux set -g` calls needed — the tmux.conf is static.

`data-theme` attribute set to theme's `category` ("dark" or "light") for CSS branching. Theme preferences persisted to both backend API (`GET/PUT /api/settings/theme` writing `~/.rk/settings.yaml`) and localStorage as synchronous cache. Three settings: `theme` (mode: `"system"` or specific ID), `theme_dark` (preferred dark theme, default `"default-dark"`), `theme_light` (preferred light theme, default `"default-light"`). localStorage keys: `runkit-theme`, `runkit-theme-dark`, `runkit-theme-light`. On init, API is canonical source; localStorage is the fast fallback if API fails. Unrecognized `theme` values fall back to `"system"`, while unrecognized `theme_dark`/`theme_light` values fall back to `"default-dark"`/`"default-light"`. PUT accepts partial updates (load-then-merge).

**ThemeToggle** (top bar): Normal click cycles `system → default-light → default-dark`. **Ctrl+Click / Cmd+Click** dispatches `"theme-selector:open"` CustomEvent to open the theme selector.

**Theme Selector** (`app/frontend/src/components/theme-selector.tsx`): Modal overlay matching CommandPalette structure (fixed z-50, backdrop, max-w-lg at 20vh). Search input filters by name (case-insensitive). Themes grouped under "Dark" / "Light" category headers. Arrow key navigation wraps and skips headers. Mouse hover and arrow navigation trigger live preview via `previewTheme()` — CSS custom properties update in real-time. Enter confirms (persists to API + localStorage), Escape/outside-click reverts to original theme via `cancelPreview()`. Opens via `"theme-selector:open"` custom event (same pattern as `"palette:open"`). Theme rows display multi-color palette swatches showing background plus representative ANSI colors (red, green, yellow, blue, magenta, cyan) instead of a single-color swatch.

**Command palette**: "Theme: Select Theme" action dispatches `"theme-selector:open"`. Individual "Theme: System", "Theme: Light", "Theme: Dark" quick-switch actions retained.

**ThemeProvider** (`app/frontend/src/contexts/theme-context.tsx`): `useTheme()` returns `{ preference, resolved, theme, themeDark, themeLight }`. `useThemeActions()` returns `{ setTheme, previewTheme, cancelPreview }`. Preview applies colors to DOM without persistence. Cancel reverts to the last persisted theme. Uses stable `actionsRef` pattern for callback identity. On init: calls `getThemePreference()` from API (returns `{ theme, themeDark, themeLight }`), falls back to localStorage / defaults if API fails. Per-mode theme resolution: in `"system"` mode, resolves to the user's preferred dark or light theme based on OS `prefers-color-scheme`, falling back to `DEFAULT_DARK_THEME` / `DEFAULT_LIGHT_THEME` if the stored ID is invalid. `setTheme` with a specific theme ID saves it to the matching per-mode slot (by `category`), keeps preference as `"system"` (preserving OS auto-toggle), and persists all three values to API and localStorage. `setTheme("system")` resets to system mode without changing per-mode prefs. Backend is canonical source of truth; localStorage is the fast fallback.

### Breadcrumb Dropdowns

Session and window name text are the dropdown triggers. Clicking/tapping the name opens the respective dropdown. No split click-target pattern — the name itself is the trigger. The session name shown in the breadcrumb is the **snapshot-derived** owning session of the active `@N` (there is no `$session` in the URL), not a URL segment. (`260529-jad6`)

**Session dropdown**: Lists all tmux sessions. Current session highlighted with `text-accent`. Selecting navigates to the session's first window by its window ID (`/{server}/{windows[0].windowId}` — 2-segment). First item: `+ New Session` action — triggers instant session creation (no dialog).

**Window switcher**: Lists all windows in the current session. Current window highlighted (`w.windowId === currentWindow.windowId`). Selecting navigates to `/{server}/{windowId}` (2-segment). First item: `+ New Window` action (creates new window in current session). It renders as a **label-less bare-`▾` `BreadcrumbDropdown`** in the top bar's center cell, beside the centered `WindowHeading` (name-click = edit, `▾`-click = switch); the window name lives once in the heading. Carries `title="Window"` and stays visible on mobile. See § Chrome (Top Bar) center cell / § Window Heading. (`260529-jad6`, `260703-5ilm`)

**Board switcher** (`BoardSwitcher` in `top-bar.tsx`): the board mode's `▾` dropdown — lists the cross-server boards + a `← Sessions` navigate action — sits beside the centered `Board: <board>` display heading, mirroring the window switcher's center-cell placement. The board name is display-only (no rename API); the `▾` is the sole board affordance in the bar. The left nav keeps only the pane/server counts + `⌘[⌘] cycle` hint (`BoardModeInfo`). See § Chrome (Top Bar) center cell / Board. (`260704-pr0p`)

**Action items in dropdowns**: `BreadcrumbDropdown` accepts an optional `action` prop of type `{ label: string; onAction: () => void }`. When provided, the action item renders before the selection list, separated by a divider (`border-t border-border`). Action items use `text-text-primary` styling (not `text-accent`), close the dropdown on click, and are excluded from ArrowUp/ArrowDown keyboard navigation among selection items.

**Optional `secondaryAction`**: a second leading action of the same `{ label, onAction }` shape, rendered below `action` and above the divider — **only honored when `action` is also present**. Its sole call site is the terminal-mode window-switcher dropdown, which renders `+ New Window` (`action`) and `+ New Agent` (`secondaryAction`) as two stacked leading buttons. The two actions occupy dropdown indices `0..offset-1` (leading actions) with selection items following at `offset..N-1`; `actionRefs` is an array and the focus-index `offset` is the count of present leading actions — so the keyboard-nav index math generalizes to N leading actions while every **other** call site (session switcher, board switcher) that passes only `action` keeps its single-action behavior. This minimal second-prop shape is chosen over a generic `actions: []` array (only one call site needs two actions, and an array would churn every call site plus the focus-index logic). See § Spawn-Agent Dialog. (`260713-sbk1`)

**Dropdown component** (`app/frontend/src/components/breadcrumb-dropdown.tsx`): Reusable dropdown with outside-click dismiss, Escape dismiss, ArrowUp/ArrowDown keyboard navigation, ARIA `role="menu"`/`role="menuitem"`. Styled with `bg-bg-primary border-border shadow-2xl`, matching bottom-bar Fn key dropdown pattern. Name text serves as the trigger (44px on touch devices via `coarse:min-h-[44px]`), wrapped in a `min-w-0 truncate` span. When the trigger has a label (`icon` prop set) it renders a **persistent `▾` caret** after the label (`aria-hidden`, `ml-1 shrink-0 text-base` — 16px, user-tuned for visibility) — the always-visible "opens a menu" affordance distinguishing dropdown crumbs from link crumbs (`260702-6m46`; see § Crumb Affordance Vocabulary). A label-less trigger already IS a bare caret (`▾` fallback) and gets no second one. Long names truncated via `max-w-[240px]`.

Connection indicator: green/gray dot only (no text label), driven by `isConnected` from ChromeProvider (set by each page from `useSessions`).

**Open menu escapes any `overflow:hidden` ancestor via `position: fixed`.** The open `role="menu"` element renders **`position: fixed` anchored to the trigger's viewport rect** — it measures `buttonRef.getBoundingClientRect()` on open and positions its top-left at `rect.bottom + gap` / `rect.left`, recomputing (or closing) on `scroll`/`resize` (capture-phase, so a scrolling ancestor container is heard) so it never detaches from the moving trigger. **The reusable invariant — clip-backstop vs. contained popover**: when you add `overflow-hidden` (or `overflow-clip`) to a container that also *holds* a popover, a plain `absolute` popover inside it gets **both clipped AND focus-scroll-displaced** — `overflow:hidden` turns the container into a scroll box, and the menu's focus-on-open `scrollIntoView` then scrolls the whole container's content out of its own clip box. This is exactly the bug the `q8ey` nav clip-backstop (§ Center-heading … → degradation ladder step 3) introduced on the session-switcher menu (empirically: post-clip the menu landed off-viewport at y≈-75 with an empty hit-test; pre-clip it rendered visible at y≈37). The nav clip is a user-approved requirement, so the resolution is to let the menu **escape the clip context**, not weaken the clip — and `position: fixed` is viewport-relative, so no `overflow:hidden` ancestor can clip it. `overflow-clip` on the container would have fixed only the focus-scroll (a clip box is not a scroll container), not the clipping itself. Because the escape lives in the shared `BreadcrumbDropdown` component, it applies identically to **all four call sites** (session crumb, hierarchy ▾, window switcher, board switcher); it keeps `z-50`, the `min-w-[160px] max-w-[240px]` sizing, and the existing click-outside / Escape / Arrow-key focus behavior. **Rule for future clips**: adding `overflow-hidden` to any container that contains a popover requires that popover to escape via fixed/portal positioning, or the popover breaks. (`260715-q8ey`)

### Crumb Affordance Vocabulary

Breadcrumb crumbs advertise their interactivity WITHOUT hover — a two-affordance vocabulary where every remaining crumb is interactive (the current-page LEAF lives in the centered heading, not the left nav, § Chrome (Top Bar), so the "you are here" signal is the centered heading itself, not a no-affordance crumb). The cases: (`260704-pr0p`)

- **Link crumbs** (brand, server link) — carry the shared `LINK_CRUMB_CLASS` constant (`top-bar.tsx`): a **bordered chip** (`rounded border border-border hover:border-text-secondary px-1.5 py-0.5 text-text-secondary hover:text-text-primary transition-colors`), reusing the right cluster's "bordered = clickable" language. The user compared three candidates live (chip / accent color / dotted underline) and picked the chip; the unused variant definitions were removed at lock-in. *(Accent color was rejected — hue is reserved by the StatusDot phases; dotted underline was rejected — it left the mobile icon-only brand with no affordance, and text-decoration doesn't propagate into an anchor's flex children, so the wordmark needed a `[text-decoration:inherit]` patch that the chip doesn't.)*
- **Dropdown triggers** (session — and the window/board switchers) — carry the persistent `▾` caret inside `BreadcrumbDropdown` (see § Breadcrumb Dropdowns). Signals "opens a switcher", distinct from "navigates". The **window switcher** AND the **board switcher** are bare-`▾` `BreadcrumbDropdown`s in the top bar's center cell beside their headings (§ Chrome (Top Bar) center cell), using the same caret affordance. (`260703-5ilm`, `260704-pr0p`)
- **Current-page leaf** — there is NO leaf crumb in the left nav; the current page's identity is the **centered `PageType: name` heading** (the tmux Server page's identity is the centered `tmux Server: <server>`). The heading carries the "you are here" role. (`260704-pr0p`)

*Why not hover-only cues*: a `hover:text-text-primary` cue is invisible to first-time users and absent entirely on touch. (`260702-6m46`)

### Section Heading (`section-heading.tsx`)

A shared `SectionHeading({ label, side?, className? })` renders a one-line **bracketed BBS-menu-tag** SECTION heading — `[ SESSIONS▊ ]──────────── side`. The bracket idiom names in-page SECTIONS; page identity lives in the top-bar center heading (§ Chrome (Top Bar), § Canonical page names — Vocabulary Split). (`260704-pr0p`)

- **Structure**: an outer `<div className="flex items-center gap-3 min-w-0">` (a div, NOT a span — it contains an `<h2>`, and a span may not contain flow content). The inner `rk-bracket-group flex items-center gap-1.5 min-w-0 shrink-0 max-w-[60%]` cluster holds: the `[` open bracket, an `<h2 className="text-xs uppercase tracking-wide text-text-secondary">` wrapping `<TypedLabel text={label} />` (so the section-label typed-sweep lives INSIDE the brackets — § Hover-Animation Vocabulary), the always-reserved `▊` caret cell, then the `]` close bracket. A `flex-1 min-w-4 border-t border-border` fills the middle as the rule (a CSS border — responsive, no literal `─` glyphs to overflow at 375px); an optional right-aligned `side` slot (`text-sm text-text-secondary truncate shrink-0`) sits after the rule when provided.
- **Accessibility**: the `[`/`]` brackets, the `▊` caret cell, and the rule are `aria-hidden`; the `<h2>` is the accessible structure and its accessible name is the label text ONLY (uppercase styling). No `<h1>` anywhere (the top bar adds none either — § Display-only page headings).
- **Bracket hover treatment** (brackets+caret = section-heading vocabulary): the inner bracket cluster carries `rk-bracket-group`, scoping the hover treatment to THIS cluster ONLY — the rule and `side` slot are outside it and never trigger it. On group hover the `[`/`]` spans (`.rk-bracket .rk-bracket-open`/`.rk-bracket-close`) step outward `translateX(∓3px)` + turn accent (transform only, no layout shift), and the **always-reserved `.rk-bracket-caret` cell** (fixed `1ch`, transparent at rest, sitting AFTER the label and BEFORE the closing bracket → `[ SESSIONS▊ ]`) blinks its `▊`. All disabled under `prefers-reduced-motion`. See § Hover-Animation Vocabulary. (This reserved-caret is NOT the section-label typed sweep, which lives in the `TypedLabel` inside the brackets — the two vocabularies compose on this one element.)
- **tmux Server page** (`/$server`): a page-level `<SectionHeading label="tmux Server Overview" />` heads the scroll area (§ Page Overview Headings), then `<SectionHeading label="Sessions" side={"{N} sessions, {M} windows"} />` precedes the session-tile grid (`session-tiles.tsx`). The server-view stats ride the `Sessions` heading's `side` slot, right-aligned after the rule.
- **Host-page zones** (`/`): a page-level `<SectionHeading label="Host Overview" />` heads the scroll container (§ Page Overview Headings), above the four zone `<h2>`s — `Host Health` / `Boards` / `Tmux Servers` / `Services` — each `<SectionHeading label=... className="mb-2" />` (`host-overview-page.tsx`). The zone headings' `side` slots stay **empty** (reserved for the server-view stats relocation, plan assumption #4); each zone's existing inline metadata (live hostname / `{N} boards` / `{N} servers`) stays in the zone BODY at its `text-xs` sizing right below the heading — NOT in `side`. (`260704-pr0p`, `260715-zs1y`)
- **Tests**: `section-heading.test.tsx` asserts the `<h2>` accessible name equals the label (brackets/caret/rule `aria-hidden`), the optional `side` slot renders after the rule, and the `TypedLabel` is present inside the brackets. `host-overview-page.test.tsx` asserts no level-1 heading exists, the four zone `<h2>` labels render in order (Host Health → Boards → Tmux Servers → Services), and the `Host Overview` page heading renders.

### Page Overview Headings

Two page-level in-page `SectionHeading` headings sit at the TOP of their page's scroll container, above the page's first zone/section, reusing the `SectionHeading` component (§ Section Heading) — both inherit `SectionHeading`/`TypedLabel` `prefers-reduced-motion` behavior (static under reduced motion): (`260715-zs1y`)

- **"Host Overview"** — on `/` (`host-overview-page.tsx`), the first child inside the `overflow-y-auto` scroll container, ABOVE the HOST HEALTH zone (so the page reads `[ HOST OVERVIEW ]` then the four zones). Distinct from the top-bar center-cell solo `Host` identity heading — this is the in-page overview label, that is the chrome page-type identity.
- **"tmux Server Overview"** — on `/$server` (`session-tiles.tsx`, the no-window `SessionTiles` view), the first child of the scroll area, ABOVE the existing `[ SESSIONS ]` `SectionHeading`. It renders **only** in the no-window `/$server` view; navigating into a window (`/$server/$window`) does not mount `SessionTiles`, so the heading is absent there. Distinct from the top-bar `tmux Server: <server>` center-cell identity heading.

Coverage: `host-overview-page.test.tsx` asserts the "Host Overview" heading renders; `tests/e2e/window-heading.spec.ts` (+ `.spec.md`) asserts both "Host Overview" (`/`) and "tmux Server Overview" (`/$server`) in-page headings.

**FixedWidthToggle** (in the top-bar right cluster): part of the FixedWidth → Notification → Theme block (before the right-most connection dot; see § Chrome (Top Bar) for the full cluster order). Self-contained component using `useChrome()`/`useChromeDispatch()` — fixed-width is a viewport preference, not a per-window setting. Touch target: `coarse:min-h-[30px] coarse:min-w-[30px]`. It is the L1 registry `fixed-width` candidate (gated `modes: ["terminal"]`, `hidden: !currentWindow` per the pyramid table above, which is authoritative): its menu row is a "Fixed width" `role="menuitemcheckbox"` reachable below `sm`. (`260509-17m3`, `260704-9o7k`, `260715-h1ck`)

**TerminalFontControl** (`top-bar.tsx`, placed near `FixedWidthToggle`): a compact combo `[−] {size} [+]` + reset for the global terminal font preference (see § Terminal Font Size). Self-contained sub-component (mirrors the `FixedWidthToggle` function-component shape) reading `useChromeState()`/`useChromeDispatch()` and `TERMINAL_FONT_BOUNDS`. (`260613-oo89`) The − button is disabled at `min` (8), the + button at `max` (24); the value label shows the effective size; reset calls `resetTerminalFont`. aria-labels `Decrease terminal font` / `Increase terminal font` / `Reset terminal font`; established top-bar `coarse:36px`-square touch sizing.

### Sidebar Kill Controls

- **Session row ✕**: Always-visible ✕ button on session rows with red hover. Normal click opens confirmation dialog: "Kill session **{name}** and all {N} windows?" **Ctrl+Click / Cmd+Click** bypasses the confirmation dialog and kills immediately (best-effort `.catch(() => {})`).
- **Window row ✕**: Hover-reveal ✕ button on window rows (always visible on touch devices via `coarse:opacity-100`). Normal click opens confirmation dialog: "Kill window in **{session}**?" **Ctrl+Click / Cmd+Click** bypasses the confirmation dialog and kills immediately (best-effort `.catch(() => {})`).

The Ctrl+Click force-kill pattern matches the established "modifier = power action" convention: ThemeToggle uses Ctrl+Click to open the theme selector instead of cycling. Modifier detection uses `e.ctrlKey || e.metaKey` (Ctrl on Linux/Windows, Cmd on macOS).

## Sidebar

`app/frontend/src/components/sidebar/` — session/window tree navigation. The sidebar is decomposed into an orchestrator and seven sub-components:

- `index.tsx` — `Sidebar` orchestrator; owns all state (`collapsed`, `killTarget`, `editingWindow`, `editingSession`, `dragSource`, `dropTarget`, `sessionDropTarget`) and all `useOptimisticAction` hooks. Accepts `metrics` and `isConnected` props for HostPanel
- `session-row.tsx` — `SessionRow` (exported as `memo(SessionRowInner)`); renders the session header row (chevron, name) plus a **trailing hover-revealed icon cluster** in fixed order `[🎨 palette/color] [🤖 bot spawn] [+ create window] [✕ kill]` — the bot button (`gsmu`) sits immediately **LEFT of `+`** so `+`/`✕` keep their muscle-memory edge positions; handles cross-session drag-over styling; all event handlers passed as props (stable identity-arg `useCallback`s — see § Render Performance). **Session-row icon cluster** (the spawn-agent trigger): each icon button shares the same affordance classes as its palette sibling (`text-text-secondary hover:text-text-primary opacity-0 group-hover:opacity-100 coarse:opacity-100`, `min-h-[24px] coarse:min-h-[36px]`). The **bot button** (`onSpawnAgent && (…)`) renders **only when an `onSpawnAgent?: (server, session) => void` handler is present** (mirroring the optional `onColorChange` pattern), carries `aria-label={`Spawn agent in ${session.name}`}`, and on click does `e.stopPropagation()` then `onSpawnAgent(server, name)` — passing the ROW's explicit `{server, session}` (the spawn target). Its glyph is `BotIcon` from `sidebar/icons.tsx` — a lucide-style `bot` (robot head: antenna + rounded head with two eye dots + side ports) stroke SVG matching the `PaletteIcon` idiom (`stroke="currentColor"`, `strokeWidth={2}`, `aria-hidden`, 24-unit viewBox + 13px default size). **Prop threading** (`gsmu`): `onSpawnAgent` is optional on `SidebarProps` → threaded through `ServerGroupProps`/`ServerGroupInner` → `SessionRow` (mirroring `onColorChange`); the board-route sidebar passes NO handler, so the bot button is hidden there (Non-Goal — later wiring is cheap via the optional prop). See § Spawn-Agent Dialog for the dialog it opens.
- `window-row.tsx` — `WindowRow` (exported as `memo(WindowRowInner)`); renders a single window row (a leading unified `<StatusDot>` + name) plus the absolutely-positioned hover-icon cluster (pin / color swatch / kill); handles drag-and-drop and inline rename display; all event handlers passed as props. **Row Minimalism**: no trailing status cluster (no fab stage word, no `WindowDuration`/`TickingDuration` duration leaves or their per-second `useNow()` tick); the leading `<StatusDot>` is the row's ONLY status signal, so the component is purely presentational except for its hover-icon state (§ Window rows / Row Minimalism). The icon cluster is inert at rest (`pointer-events-none` + hover/coarse/focus restore). Renders no full PR line — its single leading dot carries all status: the palette-v3 two-family ladder + additive waiting halo (§ Status Dot). (`260706-y1ar`, `260715-jykd`)
- `collapsible-panel.tsx` — `CollapsiblePanel`; reusable collapsible container with header (title + chevron) and localStorage open/closed state persistence via `storageKey` prop. Two modes: (a) legacy `max-height` CSS transition when `resizable` is absent/false (preserves existing Window/Host panel behaviour); (b) resizable mode (opt-in via `resizable` prop) — renders a 6px `ns-resize` drag handle at the bottom, persists user-set height to `localStorage[${storageKey}-height]`, and supports `defaultHeight`/`minHeight`/`maxHeight` props. `maxHeight` accepts a number or a `calc(100vh - Npx)` string form (parsed at drag time using `window.innerHeight`). Mobile breakpoint (`@media (pointer: coarse), (max-width: 639px)`) hides the drag handle and pins the content area to the `mobileHeight` prop (default 56px). All localStorage access wrapped in try/catch. **Header tint**: `tint` prop (`RowTint | null`) paints the header background. By default (legacy mode) the header uses `tint.base` with a `tint.base` ↔ `tint.hover` swap on hover. When `tintOnlyWhenCollapsed` is set, the tint is applied only while the panel is collapsed — and the shade switches to `tint.selected` with the hover swap disabled (stays flat), because in that mode the header is standing in for the selected item inside and a less-saturated hover would read as an inverted effect. `ServerPanel` is the only current consumer of `tintOnlyWhenCollapsed`; the legacy `base`/`hover` behavior is preserved for forward compatibility
- `status-panel.tsx` — `WindowPanel` (exported as both `WindowPanel` and deprecated `StatusPanel`); wraps the identity rows (`tmx`, `cwd`, `git`) plus the **four orthogonal signal registers** (`out`/`agt`/`fab`/`PR` — L0/L1/L2/L3, 3-char prefix vocabulary) in a `CollapsiblePanel` with copyable row interactions (via the file-private `CopyableRow`); see § Pane panel four-register view. The `PR` (L3) register is **ungated from `fabChange`** — shows for ANY pane with a derived `prNumber` (universal derivation); its interaction is **open-first** (the one row that isn't click-to-copy) — with a PR URL the row body is a real anchor (file-private `PrLinkRow`) opening the PR in a new tab (always-visible inline `↗`), and copy is role-swapped to a hover-revealed right-side icon (reusing the window-row icon-cluster gating); without a URL it stays a plain `CopyableRow` copying the segment text. See § PR Status. The panel's `headerRight` leads with a unified `<StatusDot win={win} />` before `{win.name}` — an at-a-glance status summary that survives panel collapse; see § Status Dot (`260703-41ks`, `260706-y1ar`)
- `host-panel.tsx` — `HostPanel`; hostname header + SSE dot inside a `CollapsiblePanel`, delegating the metric rows to the shared `HostMetrics` component (see § HostPanel). Keeps the `!metrics` "No metrics" branch
- `host-metrics.tsx` — `HostMetrics`; the shared layout-agnostic presentational component rendering the CPU sparkline / memory gauge / disk+uptime / load rows for a `MetricsSnapshot` via `lib/sparkline.ts` + `lib/gauge.ts`. Consumed by both `HostPanel` (sidebar) and the `/` HOST HEALTH zone (`260701-vshd`; see § HostPanel)
- `server-panel.tsx` — `ServerPanel`; swatch-style grid of server tiles (Mock A) inside a `CollapsiblePanel` with `title="Server"`, `storageKey="runkit-panel-server"`, `defaultOpen={true}`, `resizable={true}`, `defaultHeight={140}`, `minHeight={80}`, `mobileHeight={56}`. Its expansion state is purely the tile grid's own visibility — `runkit-panel-server` is `CollapsiblePanel`'s private persistence and no sidebar code path outside it reads that key; the sessions-pane scope is a separate, explicit state (§ Sessions-pane scope). The active server name is rendered in the panel's `headerRight` slot with `truncate text-text-primary font-mono` (matching the WindowPanel/HostPanel header-right convention); the `LogoSpinner` follows the name when `refreshing` is true. The panel also passes `tint={activeTint}` + `tintOnlyWhenCollapsed` so the collapsed header background matches the selected server's `rowTints.get(activeColor).selected` shade (same body tint used by the active tile inside the panel) — collapsed and expanded readings agree, and the header hover stays flat at the selected shade. Desktop grid: `repeat(auto-fill, minmax(72px, 1fr))`, 6px gap — tiles expand to fill the sidebar width, multi-row, scrolls internally when overflowing the user-set height. Each tile is a focusable `<button role="option">` with a 4px top color stripe (ANSI tint via `rowTints.get(color).base`, neutral `--color-border` for tiles without an assigned color), 11px truncated name, 10px `{N} sess` meta. Active tile: `aria-current="true"` + inset accent ring + `rowTints.get(color).selected` body tint (accent-subtle fallback for untinted active server). Hover-revealed `.actions` cluster (color-picker `■` + kill `✕`) rendered as a sibling to the tile button (not nested — avoids invalid button-in-button) with `group-hover:flex` on the outer wrapper; the cluster is shown on **every** tile (the color/kill affordances gate on `onColorClick`/`onKill` being passed, and `ServerPanel` passes `onKill` to every tile unconditionally — `server-panel.tsx:165` — not just the active one), and the entire cluster is hidden on `pointer: coarse`. Mobile layout (`@media (pointer: coarse), (max-width: 639px)`): single-row grid via `grid-auto-flow: column`, `grid-auto-columns: 88px`, `overflow-x: auto; overflow-y: hidden`, `scroll-snap-type: x mandatory` — swipe horizontally, tap to select. Active tile `scrollIntoView({ block: 'nearest', inline: 'nearest' })` on mount when mobile layout active. `ServerInfo` shape (`{name, sessionCount, rank?}` — `rank` added by `260705-bpnr`) flows through from `/api/servers`. **Drag-reorder** (`260705-bpnr`): regular server tiles are draggable via the shared `useServerReorder` hook (see § Server-tile drag reorder) — infra tiles are excluded (not draggable, not drop targets); the dragged tile dims via `opacity-50`. **Infra-server name de-emphasis** (`260705-uh8f-deemphasize-infra-servers`): the tile name span carries `text-text-secondary` (not the usual `text-text-primary`) when `isInfraServer(name)` (from `@/api/client`) — greyed, not disabled. Hover/click/active-selection and the kill ✕ are unchanged, so the infra tile stays fully attachable (useful for reading daemon logs) and never reads as dead/disconnected. See § Infra-server de-emphasis
- `server-selector.tsx` — `ServerSelector` (legacy); owns its own dropdown state (`serverDropdownOpen`, `refreshingServers`, `serverDropdownRef`); pinned-bottom server dropdown with outside-click dismiss. Retained for backwards compat — `ServerPanel` is the primary server-switcher in the current UI
- `kill-dialog.tsx` — `KillDialog`; stateless; renders the kill confirmation dialog for sessions and windows using `<Dialog>`

Consumers import `@/components/sidebar` as before — Vite resolves directory imports to `sidebar/index.tsx` automatically.

### Infra-server de-emphasis

**Infrastructure** tmux servers — the `rk-daemon` socket (hosting the run-kit daemon itself, backend `ServerSocket`, `app/backend/internal/daemon/daemon.go`) and any `rk-test-*` socket (the isolated test-socket umbrella, backend `IsTestServerName`, `app/backend/internal/tmux/tmux.go:1342`) — are de-emphasized (greyed + sorted-last) but NOT hidden (§ Design Decisions → Infra servers are greyed, not hidden). (`260705-uh8f`)

**Identification lives in one frontend home** (`app/frontend/src/api/client.ts`, near the `ServerInfo` type): an exported `DAEMON_SERVER = "rk-daemon"` constant, a module-private `TEST_SERVER_PREFIX = "rk-test-"` (the one frontend home of that literal, mirroring the backend `IsTestServerName`), an exported `isInfraServer(name)` (true for the exact daemon socket or any `rk-test-` prefix), and an exported `compareServers(a, b)`. Identification is name-based, not a backend `isDaemon` flag (§ Design Decisions → Infra servers are greyed, not hidden). Consumers import these; magic strings are never re-derived at call sites.

**`compareServers` ordering**: regular servers first (alphabetical), then infra servers (alphabetical within their class). Comparison is plain byte-order lexicographic (`a.name < b.name`), NOT `localeCompare` — this mirrors the backend's `sort.Strings` byte order so the regular-server segment renders byte-identical to before this change. `rk-test-*` sockets sort within the infra class.

**Single sort choke point** — `app/frontend/src/contexts/session-context.tsx` `fetchServers`: the fetched array is sorted once at the sole `setServers` ingestion point (`setServers(Array.isArray(data) ? [...data].sort(compareServersRanked) : [])` — note the `[...data]` copy: the sort is non-mutating, and the fresh reference each fetch matches production behavior, where `listServers` already returns a fresh array). Every consumer of `ctx.servers` inherits the effective ordering from this one place: the Sidebar Server-panel tile grid (`server-panel.tsx`), the Sessions-tree per-server `ServerGroup`s (`sidebar/index.tsx`), the Host-page TMUX SERVERS zone (`host-overview-page.tsx`), and the command-palette `Server: Switch to {name}` entries (`app.tsx`). **The backend does not sort** — `/api/servers` stays alphabetical (an asserted API contract, `servers_test.go:143`); display order is a frontend concern. `servers[0]` (the Host page's "Open in window" target, `host-overview-page.tsx`) prefers a real workspace over `rk-daemon` (see § SERVICES Zone on `/`). (`260705-bpnr`)

**Rank-aware comparator composition**: the choke-point sort key is **(infra-class, rank, name)** via `compareServersRanked(a, b)` (exported from `client.ts` beside `compareServers`), which **wraps** `compareServers` — the infra-last class pin and the byte-order intra-class ordering are preserved; rank is a secondary key inserted ONLY inside the regular class. Its logic: for a cross-class pair OR two infra servers it defers ENTIRELY to `compareServers` (infra ignore rank — their intra-class order stays byte-alphabetical); for two regular servers rank is primary — a ranked server sorts before any unranked one, two ranked sort by `rank` ascending, two unranked fall back to byte-order name. An **all-regular-unranked** list is byte-alphabetical, identical to `compareServers`. The rank on each `ServerInfo` comes from the `/api/servers` `rank` field (`@rk_server_rank`, see `architecture.md` / `tmux-sessions.md`). `session-context.tsx` imports `compareServersRanked`. (`260705-bpnr`)

**Live re-sort without refetch** — SessionContext listens for the server-global `event: server-order` on BOTH the per-server pool streams and the dedicated `?metrics=1` stream (identical payload on every stream, since the event is host-global). The `applyServerOrder(order)` handler stamps each named server's `rank` from its index in `order`, drops the rank of any server not listed (so it falls to the unranked tail), then re-sorts the held `servers` array with the same `compareServersRanked` — a state update, NO `/api/servers` refetch. Churn is bounded to explicit reorder events (not per-tick SSE), so no dedup guard is needed. See § Server-tile drag reorder below for the write path.

**Grey (de-emphasized, not disabled) treatment**: the tile **name** text renders `text-text-secondary` instead of `text-text-primary` when `isInfraServer(name)`, on two surfaces — the Sidebar Server tile (`ServerTile`, `server-panel.tsx`) and the Host-page TMUX SERVERS tile (`host-overview-page.tsx`). Applied **uniformly** to all infra servers (`rk-daemon` and `rk-test-*`). Hover, click, active-selection, and the kill ✕ are all unchanged — the tile stays fully attachable (reading daemon logs is legitimate) and MUST NOT read as dead/disconnected. The infra de-emphasis is a SERVER-tile treatment only — it does not touch the Sessions-tree `ServerGroup` header, which carries its own per-server tint treatment (§ Per-server `ServerGroup`s → Server-group header tint); an infra server's group header tints from its color (or the gray sentinel) like any other.

**Kill guard for `rk-daemon`** (`app.tsx`): the server-kill confirm Dialog is NOT `kill-dialog.tsx` (that stateless dialog handles sessions/windows only). The server-kill confirm is the `killServerTarget` Dialog in `app/frontend/src/app.tsx` ("Kill tmux server?"), the single choke point for **both** kill entry paths — the server-tile ✕ (`onKillServer` → `setKillServerTarget(name)`) and the command-palette `Server: Kill` (`setKillServerTarget(server)`). When `killServerTarget === DAEMON_SERVER`, the dialog renders an extra `text-red-400` warning line ("**rk-daemon** hosts the run-kit daemon serving this dashboard — killing it takes the dashboard down"); a regular target shows no warning. The ✕ affordance is **kept** on every tile (including `rk-daemon`) — hiding the tile ✕ would leave the palette path unguarded and would remove a legitimate capability (an operator may intentionally kill/restart the daemon server), which is why the guard is a dialog warning, not a capability removal. This parallels the change's own de-emphasize-don't-hide principle.

### Render Performance (memo tree + leaf-scoped `useNow`)

The sidebar tree does not re-render on every SSE session tick. The session SSE stream fires several times/sec; each tick produces a fresh `slicesByServer` Map in `session-context.tsx`, which churns the derived `sessionsByServer`/`sessionOrderByServer`/`isConnectedByServer` Maps (intentional fresh refs, documented in that file). Three coupled parts keep the whole tree (every `ServerGroup`/`SessionRow`/`WindowRow`) from re-rendering on each tick; **all three are load-bearing — undoing any one silently re-breaks the perf win with no test catching it.** (`260613-ect6`)

**1. Row components are `React.memo`'d.** `WindowRow` (`memo(WindowRowInner)`, `window-row.tsx:354`), `SessionRow` (`memo(SessionRowInner)`, `session-row.tsx:200`), and `ServerGroup` (`memo(ServerGroupInner)`, `index.tsx:1280`) are each wrapped in `memo` (bare named import from `react`). **These are the first — and currently only — `React.memo` usages in the frontend.**

**2. The per-second `now` tick lives in a leaf `useNow()` hook (`hooks/use-now.ts`), NOT a threaded prop.** `useNow()` returns `Math.floor(Date.now()/1000)` and self-ticks every 1s. It is consumed by **one** leaf: `WindowContent` in `status-panel.tsx` (feeds the L0 `out` register's elapsed via `getOutputLine`). The sidebar tree does not tick per-second at all — there is no `WindowDuration` leaf inside `WindowRow` and no `nowSeconds` prop threaded through `ServerGroup`→`WindowRow`/`WindowPanel` (a value that changes every render threaded into a memoized child defeats the memo). **Do NOT reintroduce a `nowSeconds` prop on these components, and do NOT re-add a per-second tick to `WindowRow`.** The bottom panel (`WindowContent`) is a single instance, so its per-second re-render is negligible and does not touch the memoized `ServerGroup`/`SessionRow`/`WindowRow` tree. (`260706-y1ar`)

**3. Handler/array props are referentially stable, so the memos actually skip.** Per-row/per-group handlers are identity-arg `useCallback`s in `Sidebar` (taking `server`/`session`/`windowId` as arguments, following the existing `toggleSession` pattern — `handleSessionRowKill`/`handleWindowRowKill`/`handleSessionColorChange`/`handleWindowColorChange`/the drag handlers, `index.tsx:723-749` and the rename/drag block above), so a leaf calls a stable callback with its own identity rather than receiving a fresh closure. The Map/array context props (`rowTints`, `ansiPalette`, `allBoards`, `pinnedSet`, `pinnedToBoard`, `isPinnedToActiveBoardFor`) are verified stable across session ticks (sourced from `useMemo`/`useWindowPins`, changing only on theme/board events).

**THE SUBTLE INVARIANT (R6a — most regression-prone):** the three handler props `Sidebar` *receives from its parents* — `onSelectWindow`, `onCreateWindow`, `onCreateSession` — MUST be `useCallback`s **at their source in the parents**, because both parents (`AppShell` in `app.tsx`, `BoardPage` in `board-page.tsx`) consume `useSessionContext()` and therefore re-render on **every** SSE tick. An inline arrow re-added at either parent recreates these references each tick and silently defeats `ServerGroup`'s memo for **every** group (including the currently-viewed one), with **no test catching it** — the initial implementation memoized the rows but missed this caller-side leak, and review caught it as rework. The stable callbacks are `handleSidebarSelectWindow`/`handleSidebarCreateWindow`/`handleSidebarCreateSession` (`app.tsx:1116-1154`) and `handleSelectWindow` (`board-page.tsx:363`). **Root-cause fix:** `handleCreateSessionInstant` (`app.tsx:583`) and board-page's `handleCreateSession` (`board-page.tsx:145`) read churning values (`currentWindow`, `isSessionCreatePending`, `ctx.sessionsByServer`) via **render-time-mutated refs** (`currentWindowRef`/`isSessionCreatePendingRef`/`sessionsByServerRef`, set `ref.current = value` on each render) — the same `dialogOpenRef`/`orderOverrideRef` idiom used elsewhere — so the callbacks stay referentially stable across ticks instead of taking those churning values as `useCallback` deps.

**Why the memo skip is cross-server, not full per-row:** `updateSlice` (`session-context.tsx:216-227`) builds a `new Map(prev)` and replaces only the **changed** server's slice via `next.set(server, ...)`; every other server's slice object — and its `slice.sessions` array ref — carries over unchanged. So a tick on server B leaves server A's `sessions` prop referentially identical, and `ServerGroup`'s memo skips A's whole subtree. The currently-ticking server's own rows DO still re-render on its own data tick (correct — its `sessions` ref changed); the `useNow` leaf is what additionally isolates the pure clock tick from even that server's row bodies.

**Related invariants (cross-linked, not re-described here):** the derive-over-store session-order pattern (`orderOverrideRef ?? sseOrder` + render-time `arraysEqual` reconcile — see § Session drag-and-drop reorder; no whole-Map watcher effect); the triage signals (`fabDisplayState === "failed"` red stage *text* + `isFailish` PR-fail signal — see § Window rows; the failed-state *dot* is a phase-hue dashed ring + red center, § Status Dot); and single-source `isSelected` selection (URL window-id first, `isActiveWindow` fallback — see § URL as Resumable Bookmark). The intra-`WindowRow` `useMemo`s (`tint`/`uncoloredSelectedTint`/`borderColor`/`buttonStyle`/`buttonClass`) apply. (`260609-ebks`, `260615-0hsz`)

**Desktop** (`>= 640px`): `Shell` renders the sidebar `<aside style={{ gridArea: "sidebar" }} aria-label="Sidebar">` itself (rows 2–3, below the full-width topbar — see § Shell Grid Layout), gated `!isMobile && sidebarOpen && !!sidebarChildren` and wrapping `sidebarChildren` in a `flex-1 min-w-0 overflow-hidden` content wrapper. Consumers pass `sidebarChildren` (and, optionally, `sidebarResizeHandle`) rather than grid-area-placing their own aside. Drag-resizable panel, default 220px width. Width persisted to `localStorage` key `runkit-sidebar-width` via `persistSidebarWidth(width)` (called once at drag-end; `setSidebarWidth` updates in-memory state per-pointermove). Constraints: min 160px, max 400px. The drag handle is passed through Shell's `sidebarResizeHandle?: ReactNode` slot and rendered at the aside's right edge (after the content wrapper): a `w-[3px]` visible bar (the 3px structural seam — see § Border-Width System; `bg-border hover:bg-text-secondary`) with `col-resize` cursor, driven by pointer events (unified mouse/touch/pen). Its grabbable area is extended ~8px LEFTward into the sidebar via an invisible `before:` pseudo-element (`before:absolute before:inset-y-0 before:-left-2 before:right-0` — pointer events on a pseudo hit its element, so the drag/hover handlers fire unchanged) so the thin visible bar is still easy to grab; it cannot extend rightward over the terminal because the `<aside>` is `overflow-hidden`. The handle is hidden when `sidebarOpen === false` — the only re-open affordance is the hamburger at TopBar.left. Collapse animation: `grid-template-columns 150ms ease-out` (zero-width column when closed; no 48px rail). Drag-handle wiring is AppShell-only — AppShell passes the handle (with all its drag state/handlers) through the slot; BoardPage passes none, so its aside carries a `border-r border-border` seam instead (Shell applies the border only when no handle is present) and drag-resize is intentionally absent on the board route (the dimension lives in `ChromeContext` and is shared). (`260702-6m46`, `260719-rwqf`)

**Mobile** (`< 640px`, the project `sm:` Tailwind breakpoint / `useIsMobile()` hook): Sidebar renders as an overlay positioned via `gridRow: "2/4"` inside the `<Shell>` (NOT `fixed inset-0`) — backdrop and `<aside>` use `position: absolute` so the topbar stays visible during overlay open (matches the existing project convention recorded in `fab/project/context.md`). Backdrop classes include `absolute z-40 bg-black/50`; aside classes include `absolute left-0 z-50 w-[88%] max-w-[320px] bg-bg-primary shadow-2xl` plus `role="dialog" aria-modal="true"`. Open/close is driven by the single `sidebarOpen` boolean. Dismissal: tapping the backdrop, tapping a destination row (auto-closes after navigation), the explicit close affordance at TopBar.left (the hamburger), or **Escape**. (`260509-17m3`, `260613-o20f`)

**Shared modal focus trap** (`useFocusTrap`): `useFocusTrap(containerRef, active, onEscape)` (`app/frontend/src/hooks/use-focus-trap.ts`) is the single focus-cycle contract, consumed by **three** surfaces — the Shell mobile drawer, `Dialog` (`components/dialog.tsx`), and `CommandPalette` (`components/command-palette.tsx`). It focuses the container's first focusable on activation, calls `onEscape` on a **document-level** Escape (so Escape fires regardless of which element inside the container has focus), and contains Tab/Shift+Tab within the container (wrap at the boundaries, `preventDefault` only there). The `document` `keydown` listener attaches only while `active` and is removed on deactivate/unmount; `onEscape` is read through a stable `onEscapeRef` so a fresh closure each render still fires the latest. **No focus-return on close** across any consumer.

- **Shell mobile drawer**: `Shell` attaches a `drawerRef` to the `<aside>` (`role="dialog" aria-modal="true"`) and drives the hook with `active = isMobile && sidebarOpen && !!sidebarChildren` — the mobile overlay only; the desktop sidebar is a grid region and is NEVER trapped. Escape → `setSidebarOpen(false)` (additive to the backdrop/destination/hamburger dismissals above).
- **`Dialog`**: a leaf modal that only mounts while open, so it drives the trap with the constant `useFocusTrap(dialogRef, true, onClose)` — `dialogRef` on the `role="dialog" aria-modal="true"` div, Escape → `onClose`.
- **`CommandPalette`**: `useFocusTrap(paletteRef, open, () => setOpen(false))` — `paletteRef` on the `role="dialog" aria-modal="true"` div. The hook owns Escape (document-level — closes from any focused element inside), Tab containment, and initial focus; the `<input>` is the palette's **sole** focusable (option rows are non-focusable `role="option"` divs), so the hook's focus-first lands on it and Tab wraps to it. The palette's own input `onKeyDown` retains only ArrowUp/ArrowDown/Enter list navigation.

(`260613-o20f`, `260719-dsw9-focus-trap-adoption`)

**Nested-modal deference** (R10): while a nested **modal** dialog — a `[role="dialog"][aria-modal="true"]` **descendant** of the trap container — is open, `hasNestedDialog(container)` detects it and the trap stands down entirely: its `handleKeyDown` early-returns before both Escape and Tab. So a single Escape dismisses only the topmost modal, and the container-wide Tab wrap can't pull focus out of the nested dialog into the elements behind it. This applies to every `useFocusTrap` consumer; the live case is the drawer — `KillDialog`→non-portaled `Dialog` renders inside the Sidebar tree, hence inside the `<aside>` — while `Dialog` and `CommandPalette` are leaf modals today, so their stand-down is dormant (correct semantics if one ever nests). The container itself carries `role="dialog"` but is correctly excluded: `querySelector` returns descendants only, backed by an explicit `!== container` guard. **The `aria-modal="true"` part of the selector is load-bearing** (`260613-o20f` PR review): `PinPopover` carries `role="dialog"` but is NON-modal (no `aria-modal`, no internal Tab-trap) — matching it would have made the trap stand down for a layer that doesn't contain focus itself, letting Tab escape the container and regressing the `aria-modal` contract; restricting to modal dialogs keeps the trap live for `PinPopover`/`SwatchPopover`. (Those two popovers attach capture-phase `document` keydown listeners with `stopPropagation`, which independently suppress the trap's bubble-phase Escape listener — so there's no Escape collision with them even though they are not caught by `hasNestedDialog`.)

**Resize separator cursor convention**: Horizontal separator (server↔session panel divider, inside `CollapsiblePanel`) uses `cursor-row-resize`; vertical separator (sidebar↔terminal, in `app.tsx`) uses `cursor-col-resize`. Both are the double-arrow-with-middle-bar vocabulary (not `ns-resize`/`ew-resize`). Hover highlight on both uses full-opacity `hover:bg-text-secondary`.

**Document-body cursor override during drag**: Thin drag handles lose their `:hover` cursor once a drag starts because the pointer moves off the narrow strip. Both handlers work around this by writing `document.body.style.cursor = "<axis>-resize"` on drag start and `""` on drag end — so the cursor persists at document level across the whole gesture, regardless of where the pointer lands. Both handlers (horizontal `CollapsiblePanel` and vertical sidebar-width) drive this from pointer-event handlers; the vertical handler migrated to pointer events so the corner affordance's `preventDefault()` on pointerdown wouldn't suppress the mouse compatibility events the vertical drag would otherwise rely on. `CollapsiblePanel`'s unmount cleanup also clears the body cursor to prevent a leaked cursor if the component unmounts mid-drag (navigation, hot-reload). Future thin-handle drag affordances should follow this pattern rather than relying on element-level `:hover`.

**Multi-axis corner affordance**: Both sidebar drag handlers use independent document-level listeners (horizontal tracks `clientY` only, vertical tracks `clientX` only) with independent state refs, so they coexist without coordination.
