The corner element at the separator intersection exploits this: its pointerdown invokes the horizontal handler, then the vertical handler, then writes `document.body.style.cursor = "nwse-resize"` last so the diagonal cursor wins over the axis-specific writes. Corner visibility is coupled to the horizontal handle's `showDragHandle` (`resizable && isOpen && !isMobile`) — same guard, no separate source of truth. Wired via optional props: `app.tsx` → `Sidebar` (`onSidebarResizeStart`) → `ServerPanel` (`onSidebarResizeStart`) → `CollapsiblePanel` (`onCornerPointerDown`). All optional at every level so other `CollapsiblePanel` consumers (WindowPanel, HostPanel, mobile drawer) render the default single-handle path unchanged.

**Padding**: `px-3 sm:px-6` (matches top bar and bottom bar chrome padding).

**Sessions header**: The Sessions panel in `sidebar/index.tsx` is a plain always-open `<div>` (intentionally not a `CollapsiblePanel` — the session tree is a core always-visible nav surface). Its header row uses `text-text-secondary` as the baseline text color, with the "Sessions" label rendered via `TypedLabel`. The right edge of the header (an `ml-auto` cluster) carries, in order: the current-session name (rendered `truncate text-text-primary font-mono` when both `currentServer` and `currentSession` are non-null — mirroring the ServerPanel `headerRight` pattern) followed by the scope chip. No background tint on this header — per-server tints live on the `ServerGroup` headers below.

**Scope chip**: A keyboard-focusable `<button>` at the far right edge of the SESSIONS header (after the current-session name) that toggles the sessions-pane scope (`all` ⇄ `current`) via the `useSessionsScope` setter. It reads clearly at rest — a small monospace text chip showing `ALL` (scope `all`) or `CUR` (scope `current`) — because a `current`-filtered list with no visible indicator would look like servers vanished. Idiom: `font-mono text-[10px] tracking-wide`, a `border-border rounded-sm` box, `text-text-secondary hover:text-text-primary` (the standard header-button treatment). Its accessible name is the state-stable `aria-label="Toggle sessions scope"` (so tests/AT stay robust across flips); the `title` tooltip is state-descriptive ("Showing all servers — click to show current server only" / vice versa). No `CollapsiblePanel` refactor of the header — the chip slots directly into the hand-rolled div.

**Per-server `ServerGroup`s**: Below the Sessions header, the sidebar renders one `ServerGroup` per server in `servers` (the list returned by `/api/servers`). Each group is a `CollapsiblePanel`-style collapsible whose header carries the server name and a palette → plus → close action cluster (§ Server-group header action cluster; the `+` creates a session against that section's server regardless of `currentServer`); the body contains that server's session tree, fed by `sessionsByServer.get(server)` and ordered by `sessionOrderByServer.get(server)`. Per-server slice isolation is the rule — drag-and-drop, rename, kill, ghost reconciliation, and optimistic-action keys all carry the server they originated on so cross-server overlays do not leak.

**Default collapse + persistence**: By default the `currentServer` group is open and all other groups are collapsed. User toggles persist per-server in `localStorage["runkit-panel-sessions-{server}"]`. On board routes (`currentServer === null`) no group is the implicit default — collapse follows persisted state, falling back to all-collapsed. The legacy single-server `runkit-panel-sessions` key is migrated best-effort into the current server's namespaced key on first read when `currentServer` is non-null; if the user first lands on a board route, the migration is skipped (acceptable per the spec's "best-effort, no error if missing" rule). Expanding a non-current server's group also calls `attachServer(name)` on the provider so its slice starts populating from SSE. **`toggleServerSection`'s `setServerSectionsOpen` updater MUST be pure** — it MUST NOT `localStorage.setItem` or call `attachServer` inside the updater body. Under React 19 StrictMode (active via `main.tsx`, dev + e2e) updaters are double-invoked, so a `localStorage` write inside the updater is observed by the second pass (`readServerOpen` re-reads it), inverting the computed `next` and turning a single Expand click into a net no-op (the group never opens). Instead, snapshot `current = readServerOpen(server)` once, compute `next = !current`, run the persist + lazy `attachServer` side-effects ONCE outside the updater, then commit a pure functional update that derives `next` from `prev` (falling back to the pre-write `current` snapshot for an untouched group, never a fresh `readServerOpen`) for batch-safety. Established by `260602-mss7-fix-sidebar-group-expand`.

**Sessions-pane scope** (which servers' `ServerGroup`s the Sessions Pane lists) is an **explicit persisted state**, independent of the SERVER panel's expansion. It lives in localStorage key `runkit-panel-sessions-scope` with values `all | current`, default `all`; any unrecognized stored value reads as `all`. The state is owned by `useSessionsScope()` (`hooks/use-sessions-scope.ts`) — a thin wrapper over the generic `useLocalStorageEnum` (§ Sessions-scope hooks below) exporting `SESSIONS_SCOPE_KEY`, the `SessionsScope` type, and the `SESSIONS_SCOPES` tuple. The SESSIONS-header scope chip, the session-list render, and the command-palette entry are sibling subscribers of that one key, so a flip on any surface re-renders the others in the same tab.

**Scope behaviors**:

- **`all`** (default): the Sessions Pane iterates the full `servers` array; every server renders as a `ServerGroup` with per-server collapse state (`runkit-panel-sessions-{server}` via `readServerOpen`) applied as usual.
- **`current`** (resolvable): when scope is `current` AND `currentServer !== null` AND `currentServer` is present in the `servers` list, the pane renders exactly one `ServerGroup` (the entry whose `name === currentServer`), omitting all other groups from the DOM (absent, not CSS-hidden), and **force-opens** it (`isOpen={true}` passed regardless of `localStorage["runkit-panel-sessions-{currentServer}"]`) so the filtered view always shows content rather than a degenerate collapsed header. The force-open is **render-time only** — the persisted per-server key is never written by it, and chevron clicks still flow through `toggleServerSection(currentServer)` so the persisted state advances (taking visible effect when scope returns to `all`). Other servers' persisted collapse states sit dormant while filtered out — never cleared or overwritten.
- **`current` fallback-to-all**: when scope is `current` but no current server resolves — a board route (`currentServer === null`) OR a stale/deleted route param not in the `servers` list — the pane **falls back to rendering all servers**. There is no dead-end hint in this case — the `current` scope is never a dead-end or an empty pane.

The `currentOnly` gate in `index.tsx` is exactly `sessionsScope === "current" && currentServer !== null && servers.some((s) => s.name === currentServer)`; when true, `visibleServers` filters to the current server and each group's `isOpen` is forced true, otherwise `visibleServers` is the full list and `isOpen` reads `readServerOpen`. The transition between the all-servers tree and the current-only tree snaps in the next React commit — no group-list-level animation (only the per-group `CollapsiblePanel` body transitions remain). Empty `servers` still renders the "No servers" empty state regardless of scope.

**Scope chip** — see § Scope chip above. **Palette entry**: a single `sessionsScopeActions` block in `app.tsx` (composed into `paletteActions`) with one target-labeled toggle — `Sessions: Show current server only` when scope is `all`, `Sessions: Show all servers` when `current` — following the `Noun: Verb` idiom and satisfying Constitution V (keyboard reachability, palette as primary discovery).

**Sessions-scope hooks**: `useLocalStorageEnum<T extends string>(storageKey, defaultValue, allowedValues)` (`hooks/use-local-storage-enum.ts`) is the generic string-enum sibling of `useLocalStorageBoolean` — same in-module pub/sub keyed on the storage key (so same-tab siblings re-render on a write, which localStorage alone does not trigger), same `storage`-event subscription for free cross-tab parity, same try/catch guard around every localStorage access (SSR/privacy mode). Values outside `allowedValues` (including unset) resolve to `defaultValue`. `allowedValues` MUST be a stable reference (a module-level constant) — it is a `useEffect` dep and inline arrays would churn; all current consumers pass the `SESSIONS_SCOPES` constant. `useSessionsScope()` is the thin scope-specific wrapper over it. (`useLocalStorageBoolean` remains in use by `CollapsiblePanel`'s own open/closed persistence — including `ServerPanel`'s.)

**Server-group header tint (Variant D)**: Every `ServerGroup` header in the SESSIONS pane renders as a filled bar carrying that server's color — the tint is applied to the full-width header row container (the `group flex items-stretch w-full` div holding the flex-1 expand/collapse toggle button and the trailing action cluster — § Server-group header action cluster below), NOT just the current server. Fill and text resolve through the SAME dual-keyed descriptor maps the SERVER tiles use (§ Color Tinting) — no parallel resolution path, no hardcoded hexes: `rowTints.get(key)` for the fill, `rowBorders.get(key)` (contrast-guarded accent hex) for the text and top border. The lookup key is the raw stored `serverColor` descriptor when `rowTints` has an entry for it, else the `UNCOLORED_SELECTED_KEY` gray sentinel (`index.tsx:1523` — covers both an unassigned color and an unrecognized descriptor); the uncolored fallback carries the identical heavier treatment so colored and uncolored groups read as the same element class.

- **Current server** = deeper `headerTint.selected` (40%) fill + `text-text-primary` text, flat on hover (a lighter `hover` (22%) shade would read as an inverted effect — the same rule `CollapsiblePanel` applies to its `tintOnlyWhenCollapsed` selected-shade header, § Sidebar `collapsible-panel.tsx`).
- **Other servers** = `headerTint.base` (14%) fill + the guarded `rowBorders` accent hex as text (set inline, not a `text-*` class); hover deepens to `headerTint.hover` (22%) and restores to `base` on leave, applied imperatively via `onMouseEnter`/`onMouseLeave` background mutations (`index.tsx:1549` — the established dynamic-background pattern shared with window/session rows and `CollapsiblePanel`, avoiding CSS-specificity fights). Only non-current headers carry the hover swap.

**Heavier treatment**: the toggle button is `min-h-[26px]` on fine pointers / `coarse:min-h-[28px]` touch floor (the coarse floor must not shrink), `font-semibold`, `text-[10px] uppercase tracking-wider`; the header container carries a **1px top border in the resolved `rowBorders` accent** (`borderTop`, `index.tsx:1547`) separating consecutive groups. The `<section>`'s neutral `border-b border-border last:border-b-0` (`index.tsx:1532`) is left to carry the section separation, and the header bar has no separate background-only hover state (all shading rides the tint). Since every header is weight 600, the current-server distinction rides entirely on tint strength (`selected` vs `base`) and text (`text-text-primary` vs the guarded accent), not weight.

**Scope boundary — header surface only**: color appears ONLY on the header bar. The left gutter belongs to the window-marker vocabulary (§ Left-Edge Label Zone, `markerStripeStyle`) and stays untouched — this is why the rejected full-height group stripe was not chosen. No color wash on group body rows, and session rows, window rows, agent-activity tints, and the SERVER panel tiles are unchanged. Header semantics are preserved: `aria-labelledby`/`aria-expanded`, the `data-server`/`data-current-server`/`aria-current` attributes, the chevron disclosure, and the header's action cluster (§ below) all carry over. The tint tracks `currentServer` reactively (server-route switches re-paint without remounting the group); no tint is drawn distinctively when `currentServer === null` (board routes / index) — those headers simply render as non-current. (`260720-t1ca`)

**Server-group header action cluster** (palette → plus → close): the tinted header hosts a three-button cluster at its right end, in fixed DOM order palette, plus, close — the header both *displays* the server's color and *hosts* the server's actions, so a user working entirely in the SESSIONS pane (independent of the SERVER panel's expansion — § Sessions-pane scope) reaches server color and server kill on the element that shows the color. The cluster occupies the right-end slot; the toggle button keeps `flex-1 min-w-0` and stays the dominant click target.

- **Palette** (`PaletteIcon`, `aria-label` `Set color for server {name}`): hover-revealed with the touch fallback `opacity-0 group-hover:opacity-100 coarse:opacity-100` (the header container carries the plain `group` that drives it — no ancestor claims `group`). Toggles a per-group local `showColorPicker` boolean (not the SERVER panel's keyed `colorPickerFor` map — a header renders exactly one group) opening a **color-only** `SwatchPopover` (no `onSelectMarker`). The popover is portalled to `document.body` at `position: fixed` coordinates anchored at the palette button (right-aligned `right: innerWidth - rect.right`, flip-above via a `useLayoutEffect` with the ServerTile's ~100px height heuristic), escaping the session list's `overflow-y: auto` clip — the same portal treatment the SERVER tiles use. A swatch pick funnels through the shared `handleServerColorChange` (below) then closes.
- **Plus** (`aria-label` `New session on {name}`, unchanged behavior — `onCreateSession(server)` instant create): always visible.
- **Close** (`✕`, `aria-label` `Kill server {name}`, `hover:text-red-400`): always visible; calls the `onKillServer(server)` prop, inheriting the parents' kill-confirmation dialogs, daemon warning, navigation-after-kill, and `killServer` API (app.tsx / board-page.tsx `killServerTarget` — § Sidebar Kill Controls). No new dialog, handler, or endpoint; header-kill and tile-kill share one path.

Deliberate divergence from the SERVER tiles: the actions are NOT hidden on mobile (no `showActions = !isMobile` gate) — coarse pointers have no hover, so palette/plus/close all stay reachable on touch, mirroring the session-row `+ ✕` convention. Icon legibility on the tinted fill rides a cluster **wrapper** carrying the header's text treatment (inline contrast-guarded `headerAccent` for non-current headers / `text-text-primary` for the current one); buttons **inherit** that color at rest so their own Tailwind `hover:` classes win (an inline `style.color` on a button would beat any hover class). Known parity quirk carried over from the ServerTile picker: re-clicking the palette while the popover is open double-fires (outside-mousedown close, then toggle reopen), so the palette cannot self-close. (`260721-x4sf`)

**Single shared server-color write seam**: server color is written through ONE handler — `handleServerColorChange` (a `useCallback` in `Sidebar`) — passed to BOTH the SERVER-panel tiles and every SESSIONS-pane `ServerGroup` header, so the two color-picking surfaces funnel through the same code, not parallel paths. It updates `serverColors` optimistically (the header tint and the tile stripe repaint immediately — server user-option color mutations emit no control-mode event, so covered servers otherwise wait on the 12s safety poll, § tmux-sessions `row-color-safety-poll-latency`) then POSTs via `setServerColorApi`, toasting on failure. The picked family reaches it already mapped to its legacy descriptor through the `SwatchPopover` write seam (§ SwatchPopover — `familyToLegacy`).

**`ServerGroup` memo contract with the action-cluster props**: the header cluster added two props to the memoized `ServerGroup` (`React.memo(ServerGroupInner)`), both referentially stable so an SSE tick on one server does not re-render every other server's group. `onServerColorChange` is the shared `handleServerColorChange` `useCallback` (stable identity). `onKillServer` is the `Sidebar` prop passed through unchanged — and it is stable end-to-end only because BOTH `Sidebar` parents wrap it in an identity-arg `useCallback` (`handleSidebarKillServer` in `app.tsx` and `board-page.tsx`, over the stable `setKillServerTarget` setter); an inline arrow at the parent would churn a fresh identity every tick and defeat the memo skip for all groups. See § Render Performance for the group-memo tree.

**Cross-server window navigation**: Clicking a session name or window row in a non-current server's group navigates to that server's route (`/$server/$window`) via `navigate({ to: "/$server/$window", params: { server: thatServer, window } })`. The provider picks up the new `currentServer` via `useMatches()` on the next route match — no explicit `setCurrentServer` call. The previously-current server's group remains rendered (per default-collapse rules); its EventSource and slice persist so re-visiting is instant.

**Cross-server drag-and-drop is rejected**: Dragging a window from one server's group and dropping it on another server's session/group fires a toast `"Moving windows across tmux servers isn't supported yet"` and skips any move API call. tmux's `move-window` does not span servers, so cross-server move is a separate problem. Within-server drag-and-drop (window reorder within a session, cross-session window move within the same server, session reorder within the same server) is preserved verbatim.

**Session rows**: Chevron toggle (left, expands/collapses window list), session name (selects the session's first window via `onSelectWindow(server, session, windows[0].windowId)` → `selectWindow(server, windowId)`), + new window button (right), ✕ kill button (right, always visible). Click session name fires the select mutation for the first window's `@N`; the URL follows on the next SSE snapshot to `/$server/<windowId>` (2-segment); click chevron toggles expand/collapse. The session-level `+` button triggers instant session creation against the parent group's server (calls `onCreateSession` → `executeCreateSessionInstant`), not a dialog. The window-level `+` button triggers instant window creation (existing `executeCreateWindow` behavior, passes `activeWin?.worktreePath` as CWD).

**Window rows** (**Row Minimalism**): Single line with a leading unified `StatusDot` + window name (left) — **and nothing else in the status role**. There is no trailing status cluster (no fab stage-word span, no duration text); the leading `StatusDot` is the row's ONLY externally visible status signal (its core hue = journey, shape = health, additive halo = `waiting`), and the freed width goes to the window name. The exact stage word + durations live in the `StatusDotTip` hover-card and the PANE panel's register view (their recovery path). Hover-reveal action icons (pin / color / kill) are ACTIONS, not status. All rows have `border-l-2` (transparent when not selected to prevent layout shift). (`260706-y1ar`) Currently selected window highlighted with `bg-accent/10` + `border-accent` + `font-medium` + `rounded-r`. Selection compares the URL window ID against `win.windowId` (falling back to `isActiveWindow` when no URL window) — clicking a row fires `selectWindow(server, win.windowId)` (a pure tmux mutation; window ID is a self-contained tmux target, so no session arg); the selection state and URL update follow on the next SSE snapshot. See § URL as Resumable Bookmark for the full sidebar-click contract. The session row (parent) gains a `waiting`-count badge — see § Attention Surfacing.

**Current-row focus on mobile drawer open**: `Sidebar` attaches `navRef` to its `<nav aria-label="Sessions">` and runs a `useEffect` (reading `useIsMobile()` + chrome `sidebarOpen`) that, when the drawer is visible on mobile, queries `[data-window-id] [aria-current="page"]` then `scrollIntoView({ block: "nearest" })` + `focus()`es that row — landing the keyboard user on their current context. Deferred via `requestAnimationFrame` so it takes precedence over the focus trap's first-focus (committed in `Shell`'s effect). The selector is scoped to WINDOW rows: the active `BoardsSection` row also carries `aria-current="page"` but has no `[data-window-id]` ancestor, so it is excluded — board routes (no selected window) no-op and the trap's first-focusable focus stands. Mirrors the `server-panel.tsx:77-82` mount-scroll pattern. This effect ALSO syncs the roving cursor: it `setRovingKey(key)`s the `[data-window-id]` row it focuses so the tab-stop (`tabIndex={0}`) and the DOM-focused row don't desync — see § Keyboard Navigation & Tree ARIA below. (`260613-o20f`, `260613-wt1v`)

1. **Leading status dot (unified `StatusDot`) — the row's ONLY status signal**: the row's single leading dot is `<StatusDot win={win} />` (`status-dot.tsx`, see § Status Dot). It is the palette-v3 **two-family ladder**: a fab window shows its cool pipeline phase (blue intake → green apply→review-pr collapsed → purple PR) with a shape for health (ring/solid/dotted-ring+red-center/rounded-square); a plain window with a fresh `agentState` shows the warm ad-hoc-agent hue (yellow working → orange PR); a plain window with neither shows the monochrome gray floor (solid = active, ring = idle). A `waiting` window of ANY tier gets an **additive constant-yellow halo** (core hue + shape untouched). A failed fab stage renders as a dotted ring **in its phase hue** with only a small red center dot (no whole-dot red tint). Pure CSS + the `rk-waiting-halo` keyframe. (`260615-0hsz`, `260706-y1ar`)

2. **Row Minimalism — no trailing status cluster**: the row has no fab stage-word span and no duration text (`WindowDuration`/`TickingDuration` leaves + their per-second `useNow()` tick). The leading `StatusDot` is the sole status signal; the freed width goes to the window name. The exact stage word + durations are the tip's + PANE panel's job (their recovery path — see § Status Dot hover-card, § Pane panel four-register view). The tip keeps the exact stage label regardless. (`260706-y1ar`)

3. **PR status — the PR phase of the leading `StatusDot`**. The high-value PR signal lives in the single LEADING `StatusDot` (§ Status Dot), reached when `statusDotState(win)`'s ladder returns a PR phase — `pr` (purple) for a `fabChange && prNumber` window, `agentPr` (orange) for a `fresh-agent && prNumber` window (D1 per-family ownership). A plain floor pane's PR never owns the dot; the derived PR still shows in the PANE panel L3 register + the tip's "Open PR" link (universal derivation, Principle X). The PR status shape reuses `prShape`/`prDotState` unchanged (`merged`→`done`, `fail`→`failed`, `pending`→`ring`, `healthy`→`solid`; closed-unmerged never owns the dot post-D1). **Still NOT the full PR line** — full PR detail lives in the PANE panel's L3 register (§ Pane panel four-register view).

4. **Hover-icon cluster** (pin / color swatch / kill) — absolutely-positioned container (`absolute right-2 top-1/2 -translate-y-1/2 flex items-center gap-1 z-10`) rendered as a sibling of the row button (avoids nested interactive elements); the row button reserves `pr-[68px]` when the pin is wired (`pr-11` otherwise) so labels don't run under the icons. **Inert at rest**: the container carries `pointer-events-none` plus `group-hover:pointer-events-auto coarse:pointer-events-auto has-[:focus-visible]:pointer-events-auto`, so on fine pointers a stray click near the row's right edge falls through to the row-select button instead of hitting an invisible kill/pin/swatch target (deliberate icon clicks are unaffected — any mouse interaction hovers the row first, restoring interactivity). Each hover-revealed `opacity-0` button (pin's not-pinned branch, color swatch, kill) carries `focus-visible:opacity-100` so keyboard focus never sits on an invisible control — the reveal is per-button because a container-level `opacity-100` cannot reveal children carrying their own `opacity-0` (element opacity is independent/multiplicative); the container-level `has-[:focus-visible]:pointer-events-auto` restores interactivity while a child is focused. The `pr-[68px]` reservation, `coarse:opacity-100` always-visible icons on touch, and the pin's permanent visibility when pinned-to-any apply. Window metadata lives in the Pane panel's rows (`status-panel.tsx`), not a per-row info popover. (`260612-epqk`)

**Empty state**: When no sessions exist (`sessions.length === 0`), the sidebar displays "No sessions" text with a centered `+ New Session` button. The button triggers instant session creation (same as the sidebar `+` button and breadcrumb dropdown `+ New Session` action). With no active window, `cwd` is omitted and the name falls back to `session`.

**Inline rename** (double-click — windows and sessions): Both window names and session names in the sidebar support double-click inline rename. The pattern is identical for both:

- Double-clicking a name `<span>` replaces it with a text `<input>` pre-filled with the current name, auto-focused with all text selected.
- Enter or blur commits the rename if the trimmed value is non-empty and differs from the original name. Empty or unchanged input dismisses the editor without an API call.
- Escape cancels editing. A `cancelledRef` / `sessionCancelledRef` prevents blur from committing after an Escape (or cross-cancel).
- Single-click behavior is preserved (navigate to window / navigate to session's first window) — only `onDoubleClick` triggers editing.

**Window rename**: the sidebar's inline window rename goes through the **shared `useWindowRename()` hook** (`hooks/use-window-rename.ts`) — the same hook the top-bar `WindowHeading` uses, so both surfaces rename identically. The hook's `execute(server, session, windowId, newName)` runs the optimistic store rename (`windowStore.renameWindow`), rolls back via `windowStore.clearRename` + toast on API failure, and clears the pending marker on settle; SSE reconciles the canonical updated name once the server event arrives. See § Shared window rename. (The sidebar owns its own trim/empty-name guard before calling `execute`.) (`260703-5ilm`)

**Session rename**: calls `renameSession(server, oldName, newName)` via `useOptimisticAction`. The UI updates immediately via `markRenamed("session", server, oldName, newName)`; on API failure it rolls back via `unmarkRenamed(server, oldName)` (`lastRenameSessionRef` snapshots `{ server, name }` together for cross-server-safe rollback). Toast error on failure. The dialog-based session rename in `app.tsx` is an alternate path — inline editing is an additional one.

**Cross-cancellation**: Only one inline edit (window or session) may be active at a time. Starting any new inline edit cancels the currently active one without committing it. `handleStartEditing` (window edit) sets `sessionCancelledRef.current = true` and clears `editingSession` before activating the window input; `handleStartSessionEditing` sets `cancelledRef.current = true` and clears `editingWindow` before activating the session input. This ensures blur on the cancelled input is a no-op.

**Window drag-and-drop reorder**: Window items in the sidebar are `draggable={true}` (ghost windows excluded). Uses native HTML5 drag-and-drop — no external library (constitution IV). Drag state managed via `dragSource` and `dropTarget` state in `Sidebar`. On `dragStart`, sets `dataTransfer` with JSON `{ session, index, windowId, name }` and `effectAllowed: "move"`. The `windowId` and `name` fields serve cross-session optimistic operations; within-session drops use only `session` and `index`. Within-session drops: drop indicator is a 2px accent-colored top border (`borderTop: 2px solid var(--color-accent)`) on the hovered window item when source and target differ. On `drop`, uses `useOptimisticAction` to immediately swap window indices in the Zustand store via `swapWindowOrder(session, srcIndex, dstIndex)`, then fires `moveWindow(server, srcWindowId, dstIndex)` API call in the background (server captured at drop-handler time; the move targets the source by its stable `windowId` and the destination by position). The optimistic action's arg tuple is `(server, session, srcWindowId, srcIndex, dstIndex)` — `session`/`srcIndex` retained for the store-side swap/rollback, while the API call uses only `srcWindowId` + `dstIndex`. `onSelectWindow` is called immediately (not deferred to API success). On API failure, `onAlwaysRollback` reverses the swap via `swapWindowOrder(session, dstIndex, srcIndex)` and shows a toast error. SSE reconciliation naturally clears the optimistic state when `setWindowsForSession` replaces all entries with server-confirmed data. Same-position drops are no-ops (source === target check). All drag visual state (drop indicators) cleared on `dragEnd` and `drop` — handles both successful drops and cancelled drags (Escape, drag outside sidebar).

**Cross-session drag-and-drop**: Dropping a window onto a different session's header moves it to that session. `handleDragOver` accepts drag events on session headers when the dragged window is from a different session. Visual feedback: the session header shows an accent border (`border-accent`) when a valid cross-session drop is hovering. The drag data payload includes `{ session, index, windowId, name }` — `windowId` and `name` serve optimistic store operations (within-session drop ignores the extra fields). On drop, `handleSessionDrop` calls `executeMoveToSession` (a `useOptimisticAction` instance) with all six arguments `(server, srcSession, srcIndex, windowId, windowName, dstSession)`. The optimistic lifecycle:

- **`onOptimistic`**: calls `killWindow(srcSession, windowId)` to hide the window from the source session, `addGhostWindow(dstSession, windowName)` to show it in the target (using the source window's display name, not a placeholder), and navigates to `/$server` immediately. The `optimisticId` is stored in a ref for rollback.
- **`action`**: calls `moveWindowToSession(server, srcSession, srcIndex, dstSession)` — the API client function with `server` as the first positional argument.
- **`onAlwaysRollback`** (API failure): calls `restoreWindow(srcSession, windowId)` to un-hide in source + `removeGhost(optimisticId)` to remove from target. Toast: "Failed to move window to session".
- **`onAlwaysSettled`** (success): clears the ref. SSE reconciliation handles final state — `setWindowsForSession` removes the entry from the source (not in incoming list), adds it to the target (new incoming entry), and reconciles the ghost (new `windowId` not in ghost's `snapshotWindowIds`).

Same-session header drops are ignored (not a valid cross-session target). Within-session window-to-window drag-and-drop is unchanged. The sidebar handles the move internally — no `onMoveWindowToSession` prop or `handleMoveWindowToSession` callback in `app.tsx` (the sidebar imports `moveWindowToSession` directly from `@/api/client`, matching the pattern of other sidebar API calls).

**Session drag-and-drop reorder**: Session header rows are themselves draggable (the row root, not the chevron / name button) — except optimistic ghost sessions, which set `draggable={false}` because they have no canonical name to persist yet. The reorder feature shares the SAME `<SessionRow>` `onDragOver` handler used by cross-session window drops; the two are disambiguated by `dataTransfer.types`: window drags use the default JSON payload, session reorder drags use a custom MIME `application/x-session-reorder` (so a window-drag never accidentally triggers a session reorder, and vice versa). Native HTML5 drag-and-drop, no external library (Constitution IV).

The persisted order lives server-side in tmux user-option `@rk_session_order` (see `tmux-sessions.md` § "Server-Scoped User Options"), broadcast to all connected clients via SSE event `session-order`. Frontend pipeline:

- **Source of truth**: `SessionContext.sessionOrder: string[]` populated from the SSE `session-order` event handler in `session-context.tsx` (`es.addEventListener("session-order", ...)`). The handler ignores events whose `server` field doesn't match the current `server` prop — defense-in-depth alongside the backend's per-server filtering.
- **Render-time order computation**: `Sidebar` derives `orderedSessions` via `useMemo` over `sessions` and an effective order. Sessions absent from the saved order render at the bottom in their natural sequence (`Number.POSITIVE_INFINITY` rank) so newly created sessions never disappear from the sidebar.
- **Snappy drag (derive-over-store)**: The transient drag override is held in a server-keyed `orderOverrideRef = useRef<Record<string, string[]>>({})` (NOT React state), and the displayed order is *derived at render* as `orderOverrideRef.current[server] ?? (sessionOrderByServer.get(server) ?? [])` — `handleSessionReorderStart`/`handleSessionReorderOver` compute the new order via `splice` and write it into the ref for instant visual feedback. Because writing a ref does not re-render, the handlers call a minimal `forceRender` nudge (`useReducer((x) => x + 1, 0)`). The override clears via a **per-server, render-time SSE-equality reconcile**: while computing each visible server's props, if `arraysEqual(orderOverrideRef.current[server], sseOrder)` the override is deleted and `localOrder` rendered as `null` in the same pass (no nudge needed — the displayed output is unchanged). The per-server equality check (NOT a whole-`sessionOrderByServer`-Map watcher `useEffect`, which would re-run on every unrelated SSE slice tick — sessions/metrics/connection fire a fresh Map reference several times a second) fires only on the relevant server's echo, so unrelated churn triggers no reconcile work; **do not reintroduce a whole-Map watcher.** No **data** snap-back: the override outlives the debounced PUT until that server's SSE order echoes the new arrangement, so the *order* never reverts. (`260609-ebks`)
- **`dragover` MUST accept the drop even on the self-target row**: `handleSessionReorderOver` MUST call `e.preventDefault()` + `dropEffect = "move"` for a valid same-server session-reorder drag *even when hovering the dragged row itself* (`sessionDragSource.name === targetName`), then bail with no reorder math. HTML5 DnD registers a release as an accepted drop only when the LAST `dragover` before mouse-up was `preventDefault()`ed; insert-before splicing lands the dragged row under the cursor, so the dragged row's OWN element is the **common terminal hover state** at release. Bailing early there (folding the self-name check into the leading guard) leaves the final `dragover` uncancelled → no `drop` fires → `dragend` sees `dropEffect: "none"` → the browser plays its native **cancelled-drag snap-back ghost** flying back to the drag origin, contradicting the visibly-succeeded reorder (the data stuck via the debounce). **Guard order (invariant across both this handler and `useServerReorder.onDragOver` — see § Server-tile drag reorder)**: source/scope guard (`!sessionDragSource || sessionDragSource.server !== server`, confines the drag to one server's group) + MIME guard (`application/x-session-reorder`) come BEFORE acceptance; the self-target no-op (`if (sessionDragSource.name === targetName) return;`) comes AFTER `preventDefault()`. Do NOT re-fold the self-name check back into the leading guard — that is exactly the snap-back regression. Session-reorder keeps **debounce-only persistence** — even though `drop` also fires on session rows, there is no session drop-flush (the row's own `onDrop={handleSessionDrop}` is the window-move handler and no-ops safely on a reorder payload: empty `application/json` → `JSON.parse` throws → `catch` → return). (`260705-i41e`)
- **Debounced PUT**: 250ms trailing debounce via `orderPutTimerRef` + `setTimeout`. Drag events fire on every cursor frame; coalescing avoids one HTTP call per frame. `handleSessionReorderEnd` (dragend) does NOT cancel the pending timer — a fast drag-and-release within 250ms still flushes via the timer, otherwise the user's edit is lost.
- **Drag visual**: Source row gets `opacity-50` while it is the drag source (driven by the `isDragSource` prop on `<SessionRow>`).

`<SessionRow>` exposes optional drag props (`draggable`, `isDragSource`, `onDragStart`, `onDragEnd`) — present for the new feature, absent for any future caller that doesn't want session reorder. The row root passes them straight through to the underlying `<div>`.

**Test ergonomics**: `session-context.tsx` exports a `StandaloneSessionContextProvider` test helper that accepts a partial multi-server shape (`sessionsByServer`, `sessionOrderByServer`, `isConnectedByServer`, `metricsByServer`, `currentServer`, etc.) and synthesizes the full context value without opening any network connection. Tests requiring SSE-driven behavior use the full `SessionProvider` with a stubbed `EventSource`; `MockEventSource` is keyed by URL so per-server streams can be driven independently (see `session-context.test.tsx` for the pattern).

**Drop-acceptance unit-test seam**: session-reorder drop acceptance is asserted through the `renderSidebar` harness in `index.test.tsx`. The idiom: render via `renderSidebar`, `fireEvent.dragStart` the `[data-session-row="{server}:{name}"]` row (seeds `sessionDragSource` and writes the MIME onto a shared mutable `dataTransfer` bag mirroring the hook test's `makeDragEvent`), then `fireEvent.dragOver(row, { dataTransfer })` on the SAME row. **`fireEvent.dragOver` returns `false` when the handler called `preventDefault()`** — that boolean is the drop-acceptance assertion (`expect(notPrevented).toBe(false)` + `dataTransfer.dropEffect === "move"`), no native-method stub needed. A source-guard negative case (`dragOver` with the MIME but NO prior `dragStart` → returns `true`, not accepted) proves the guard fires before acceptance. The window-move `handleSessionDragOver` no-ops when its `dragSource` is null, so a prevented default on a session-reorder dragover is attributable solely to `handleSessionReorderOver`. (`260705-i41e`)

**Server-tile drag reorder**: the two server-tile grids — the Sidebar `ServerPanel` (`server-panel.tsx`) and the Host-page TMUX SERVERS grid (`host-overview-page.tsx`) — are drag-reorderable, sharing ONE lifted hook `useServerReorder(servers, onError)` (`app/frontend/src/hooks/use-server-reorder.ts`) so neither grid copy-pastes the handler logic. (`260705-bpnr`) It mirrors the § Session drag-and-drop reorder pattern verbatim: native HTML5 DnD (no external library, Constitution IV), a custom MIME `application/x-server-reorder` (`SERVER_REORDER_MIME` — so a server drag never collides with the `application/x-session-reorder` session drag or the default-JSON window drag), insert-before splice semantics on `dragOver`, and the derive-over-store optimistic override.

- **Effective-order input**: the hook takes the already-`compareServersRanked`-sorted `ctx.servers` and returns `{ orderedServers, getTileProps(name), isDragging, draggingName }`. Consumers render `orderedServers` (the transient optimistic order during a drag, else the authoritative list) and spread `getTileProps(name)` onto each tile.
- **Infra excluded**: only REGULAR servers participate. `getTileProps` returns `{ draggable: false }` (no drop handlers) for `isInfraServer(name)` tiles — they are neither draggable nor valid drop targets, and the reorder POST carries only the regular-class order (rank `i` → i-th regular server; infra ignore rank server-side, so omitting them is correct and keeps them pinned last).
- **Derive-over-store optimistic override**: the transient dragged order lives in `overrideRef = useRef<string[] | null>` (of regular server NAMES), NOT React state — so writing it doesn't re-render; a minimal `forceRender` (`useReducer((x)=>x+1,0)`) drives the optimistic repaint (the same idiom as the sidebar session reorder). `onDragStart` seeds the override with the current regular order; `onDragOver` splices the dragged name to the target position. The override clears via a **render-time equality reconcile**: once the authoritative regular order element-wise equals the stored override (via `namesEqual`), the round-trip has landed and the ref is dropped (mutating a ref during render is safe — output unchanged, no nudge). **No data snap-back on drag-end** — the override outlives the debounced POST until the SSE `server-order` echo re-sorts `ctx.servers` to match, which triggers the reconcile, so the *order* never reverts.
- **`onDragOver` MUST accept the drop even on the self-target tile**: `onDragOver` MUST call `e.preventDefault()` + `dropEffect = "move"` for a valid same-hook server-reorder drag *even when hovering the dragged tile itself* (`dragName === targetName`), then bail with no reorder math. HTML5 DnD registers a release as an accepted drop only when the LAST `dragover` before mouse-up was `preventDefault()`ed; insert-before splicing lands the dragged tile under the cursor, so the dragged tile's OWN element is the **common terminal hover state** at release. Folding the self-target check into the leading guard leaves the release-over-self `dragover` uncancelled → no `drop` fires → `dragend` sees `dropEffect: "none"` → the browser plays its native **cancelled-drag snap-back ghost** flying the tile back to the drag origin, reading as failure even though the reorder visibly succeeded and persisted (the data stuck via the debounce). **Guard order (invariant, shared verbatim with the sidebar `handleSessionReorderOver` — see § Session drag-and-drop reorder)**: originating-instance guard (`!dragName` — the hook is instantiated by BOTH `ServerPanel` and the Host-page grid; a null-`dragNameRef` instance did not start the drag and must not accept it) → infra guard (`isInfraServer(targetName)`, infra tiles are non-targets) → MIME guard (`SERVER_REORDER_MIME`) — all BEFORE acceptance; then `preventDefault()` + `dropEffect = "move"`; then the self-target no-op (`if (dragName === targetName) return;`) AFTER acceptance. Do NOT re-fold the self-target check back into the leading `!dragName` guard — that is exactly the snap-back regression. (`260705-i41e`)
- **Debounce + drop-flush**: reorder writes go through a `SERVER_ORDER_DEBOUNCE_MS = 250` trailing debounce (`putTimerRef`), coalescing a rapid drag-over sweep into one `setServerOrder(order)` POST — mirroring the sidebar's `SESSION_ORDER_DEBOUNCE_MS`. `onDrop` flushes any pending debounced POST immediately so the write isn't lost if the SSE echo races the timer. The self-target drop acceptance (above) is what lets releasing over the source tile fire `onDrop`, which flushes and clears the timer (single POST, no double-post). A **mount-scoped unmount cleanup effect** (`useEffect(() => () => clearTimeout(putTimerRef.current), [])`) clears a pending timer so a drag ending right before the grid unmounts never fires a stray post-unmount write (mirrors `sidebar/index.tsx:258-262`). (`260705-i41e`)
- **Drag-source feedback**: both grids dim the dragged tile via `opacity-50`, driven by `isDragging && draggingName === name` (the session-reorder `isDragSource` treatment). Do NOT delete the `isDragging`/`draggingName` fields — they are the drag-affordance seam wired into both grids.
- **Non-drag paths**: the Sessions-tree per-server `ServerGroup`s and the palette `Server: Switch to {name}` entries FOLLOW the order (via the `compareServersRanked` choke point) but expose no server drag affordance. Touch devices get no drag (HTML5 DnD doesn't fire on touch — the palette `Server: Move up/down` are the touch/keyboard path; see § Command Palette Move up/down). Coverage: the hook's logic (MIME discrimination, insert-before splice, infra exclusion, override seed/reconcile, debounce/drop-flush, **self-target drop acceptance + drop-on-source flush**) is Vitest-covered in `use-server-reorder.test.ts`; the API+SSE slice is the `server-reorder.spec.ts` e2e (a live-drag e2e is infeasible under the single-infra-server e2e harness `RK_SERVER_ALLOWLIST=rk-test-e2e`, so it is descoped to Vitest, mirroring the `fixme`'d session-drag e2e). **The native snap-back ghost animation is browser-chrome-level and NOT observable via Playwright synthetic DnD** — the drop-acceptance (`preventDefault`/`dropEffect`) is the only testable seam, so it has unit coverage only, no e2e. (`260705-i41e`)

**Board-list drag reorder**: the BOARDS list itself is drag-reorderable on its two user-named surfaces — the Sidebar `BoardsSection` rows (`sidebar/boards-section.tsx`) and the Host-page BOARDS zone tiles (`host-overview-page.tsx`) — sharing ONE lifted hook `useBoardListReorder(boards, onError)` (`app/frontend/src/hooks/use-board-list-reorder.ts`). It is a near-verbatim mirror of § Server-tile drag reorder (`useServerReorder`), with the same derive-over-store optimistic-override discipline, and is DISTINCT from the within-board PIN reorder (`/api/boards/{name}/reorder`, § Boards View) — this reorders the boards, not the panes inside one. (`260708-a2qd`)

- **Effective-order input + return shape**: the hook takes the already-backend-sorted board list (the `GET /api/boards` response order via `useBoards`, which is itself the display order — see `architecture.md` `/api/boards`) and returns `{ orderedBoards, getTileProps(name), isDragging, draggingName }`. Consumers render `orderedBoards` (the transient optimistic order during a drag, else the authoritative list) and spread `getTileProps(b.name)` onto each row/tile.
- **Custom MIME**: `application/x-board-list-reorder` (`BOARD_LIST_REORDER_MIME`) — distinct from `application/x-server-reorder`, `application/x-session-reorder`, and the board-pane window-move payload, so a foreign-MIME drag over a board row/tile is ignored (MIMEs never cross-fire).
- **No infra exclusion**: unlike `useServerReorder`, EVERY board is draggable and a valid drop target — `getTileProps` returns the full handler set for every name (there is no board analog of the infra-server class).
- **Derive-over-store optimistic override**: the transient dragged order of board NAMES lives in `overrideRef = useRef<string[] | null>` (NOT React state); a minimal `forceRender` (`useReducer((x)=>x+1,0)`) drives the optimistic repaint. `onDragStart` seeds the override with the current order; `onDragOver` splices the dragged name to the target position (insert-before). The override clears via a **render-time name-equality reconcile** (`namesEqual`): once the authoritative `boards` order element-wise equals the stored override the round-trip has landed and the ref is dropped (mutating a ref during render is safe — output unchanged, no nudge). **No snap-back on drag-end** — the override outlives the debounced POST until the SSE `board-order` echo re-fetches `boards` to match (see propagation below), which triggers the reconcile.
- **`onDragOver` accepts the drop on the self-target tile BEFORE the self-target bail** — the same snap-back guard-order as the server hook: originating-instance (`!dragNameRef.current`) → MIME (`BOARD_LIST_REORDER_MIME`) BEFORE acceptance, then `preventDefault()` + `dropEffect = "move"`, then the self-target no-op (`if (dragName === targetName) return;`) AFTER acceptance. Bailing before `preventDefault()` on the release-over-self path would leave the drop uncancelled → native cancelled-drag snap-back ghost + a starved `onDrop` flush. Do NOT re-fold the self-target check into the leading guard. (`260705-i41e`)
- **Debounce + drop-flush**: reorder writes go through a `BOARD_ORDER_DEBOUNCE_MS = 250` trailing debounce (`putTimerRef`), coalescing a rapid drag-over sweep into one `setBoardOrder(order)` POST (mirroring `SERVER_ORDER_DEBOUNCE_MS`); `onDrop` flushes any pending POST immediately so the write isn't lost if the SSE echo races the timer. A mount-scoped unmount cleanup effect (`useEffect(() => () => clearTimeout(putTimerRef.current), [])`) clears a pending timer so a drag ending right before the list unmounts fires no stray post-unmount write.
- **Drag-source feedback + error toast**: both surfaces dim the dragged row/tile via `opacity-50` (`isDragging && draggingName === b.name`), and both pass `useToast().addToast` as the hook's `onError` handler so a failed reorder POST surfaces a toast — matching the server-panel / Host-page precedent.
- **Propagation (server-global re-sort)**: `api/boards.ts` has `setBoardOrder(order)` (POST `/api/boards/order`); `session-context.tsx` exposes a `subscribeBoardOrder` seam on BOTH the per-server pool streams AND the dedicated `?metrics=1` stream (so a zero-attached-server Host page still hears reorders, since the event is host-global); `useBoards` subscribes and reuses its `scheduleRefetch`/`REFETCH_DEBOUNCE_MS` machinery to re-fetch `/api/boards` on a `board-order` event — the backend-sorted response is the single display-order source, so a reorder on one client re-sorts every other client live (NO client-side order reducer). The top-bar BoardSwitcher dropdown and every other `useBoards` consumer inherit the order passively.
- **Non-drag / keyboard path**: the palette `Board: Move up/down` (see § Command Palette Move up/down) is the keyboard + touch path (HTML5 DnD doesn't fire on touch). Coverage: the hook logic is Vitest-covered in `use-board-list-reorder.test.ts` (override lifecycle, render-time reconcile, debounce/flush, self-target accept, foreign-MIME ignore) plus BoardsSection + Host-page wiring tests; the API + rank-aware-sort + server-global-SSE slice is the `board-list-reorder.spec.ts` e2e (endpoint/SSE-surface form, mirroring `server-reorder.spec.ts` — the live synthetic drag is Vitest's; see § E2E host-global filesystem state for its `~/.rk/settings.yaml` save/restore).

**Server selector footer** — pinned at the bottom of the sidebar below the scrollable session tree, separated by `border-t border-border`. Displays `Server: {name}` with a dropdown trigger. Clicking opens a dropdown listing all available tmux servers (from `GET /api/servers`); the current server is highlighted with `text-accent`. Selecting a different server calls `setServer(name)`, which updates localStorage (`runkit-server`), reconnects SSE, and navigates to `/`. The session tree area is `flex-1 min-h-0 overflow-y-auto` above the pinned footer.

### Keyboard Navigation & Tree ARIA

The session/window tree is a **W3C-APG two-level disclosure tree** with roving-tabindex arrow navigation, scoped entirely to the Sessions tree DOM (never `document`, never the terminal — no xterm.js key conflict). Builds on the Wave-2 memo tree (§ Render Performance) and preserves its SSE-tick invariant. Frontend-only — no backend/API/route/tmux changes.

**Tree ARIA roles** (two levels — decided; the server group stays structural, NOT a treeitem):
- The scrollable Sessions region (`<div role="tree" aria-label="Session tree">`, `index.tsx:1070`) carries `role="tree"`; the outer `<nav aria-label="Sessions">` stays the separate landmark, so the landmark and the tree widget don't collide on one element.
- **Session rows** (`SessionRow`, `session-row.tsx:113-128`) are `role="treeitem"` `aria-level={1}` with `aria-expanded={!isCollapsed}` (lifted onto the treeitem from the chevron), `aria-setsize`/`aria-posinset` (position among `orderedSessions`), and `data-session-row="${server}:${name}"` as the stable focus handle. `aria-controls={windowGroupId}` is emitted **ONLY while expanded** — the `role="group"` window list is mounted only when `!isCollapsed`, so a collapsed row pointing `aria-controls` at an unmounted id would be invalid ARIA (SF-5, enforced via `aria-controls={isCollapsed ? undefined : windowGroupId}`).
- **Window rows** (`WindowRow`, `window-row.tsx:204-217`) are `role="treeitem"` `aria-level={2}` LEAF nodes (no `aria-expanded`) with `aria-setsize`/`aria-posinset` (position among `session.windows`), reusing their existing `data-window-id` handle.
- The **window-list container** (`<div role="group" id={windowGroupId}>`, `index.tsx:1597`) is `role="group"`; that id — `windowGroupId` = `windows-${server}-${session.name}` (`index.tsx:1549`) — is threaded down for the parent session's `aria-controls`. The wrapper carries no left margin — window rows are full-bleed, and the 12px hierarchy indent lives inside each row's left padding (§ Left-Edge Label Zone). Server-group `<section>` headers stay structural wrappers — server collapse/expand remains mouse/Tab-button only for v1.

**Roving-tabindex arrow nav**: exactly one tree row carries `tabIndex={0}` (the roving row), the rest `-1` (`tabIndex={rovingKey === key ? 0 : -1}`, threaded as a single primitive into the memo'd rows so an arrow press flips `tabIndex` on only the two affected rows — the Wave-2 memo skip is preserved). The keydown handler is on the `role="tree"` container (`handleTreeKeyDown`) and early-returns when the target is an `<input>`/`<textarea>`/`isContentEditable` (so a row's rename input keeps Enter=commit / Escape=cancel and arrows move the caret). Bindings (APG-standard, each `preventDefault()`s):
- **ArrowDown/ArrowUp** — next/prev visible row; **stop at the ends (no wrap)**; flow **continuously across all open server groups** as one flat list.
- **ArrowRight** — collapsed session → expand (focus stays, via `toggleSession`); expanded session → first window child; window → no-op (leaf).
- **ArrowLeft** — expanded session → collapse; window → parent session row (scans upward for the nearest `aria-level="1"`); collapsed session → no-op (no parent treeitem — the server header is a wrapper).
- **Enter AND Space** — activate. Derives the target from a typed `RowIdentity` discriminated union (`identityForKey`) and calls `onSelectWindow(server, session, windowId)` / `onSelectWindow(server, session, firstWindowId)` **DIRECTLY** — NOT a synthesized `.click()` or a magic-string `aria-label` match (SF-2). Ghost/optimistic rows (`ghost` flag or empty `windowId`) are a no-op (SF-3), mirroring the drag-path `isGhostWindow` guard; an empty session (no first window) is likewise a no-op.
- **Home/End** — first/last visible row.

**THE LOAD-BEARING INVARIANT (most regression-prone)**: the roving cursor is a `rovingKey` STRING (the row's `data-window-id` / `data-session-row`), NOT a numeric index — so it survives expand/collapse and SSE add/remove without ever pointing at a stale or wrong row, and the "session, then descend into its windows, across groups" order falls out of DOM order for free (`getVisibleRows` reads `[role="treeitem"]` straight from the tree at keypress time). The key-normalization effect (resets `rovingKey` to the first visible row when it matches no rendered treeitem) is gated on `[rovingKey, rowsVersion]`, where `rowsVersion` (a `useReducer` counter) is bumped by `registerGroupRows` **ONLY when a server group's visible-row-SET signature changes** (the `|`-joined ordered row-key string — window add/remove, collapse/expand, rename), NOT on the several-per-second passive SSE activity ticks. This preserves the Wave-2 #262 invariant: **an SSE tick must NOT change roving state or steal focus.** A tick recomputes `rowSlice`/`rowSignature` but the signature STRING is unchanged → no bump → the normalize effect doesn't run (no full-tree `querySelectorAll`, no `setRovingKey`). The only `row.focus()` is gated by `focusMovedRef`, set `true` only on an actual keypress-driven move, so a passive re-render never pulls focus into the sidebar. DOM focus + `scrollIntoView({ block: "nearest" })` on a roving change reuse the CommandPalette/ThemeSelector "Keyboard-Navigable List Scroll Pattern" (§ Keyboard-Navigable List Scroll Pattern). Roving focus is INDEPENDENT of the URL-based `isSelected`/`aria-current="page"` selection (§ URL as Resumable Bookmark) — do not conflate them. The mobile-drawer focus effect (§ Window rows → Current-row focus on mobile drawer open) likewise `setRovingKey`s the row it focuses so its DOM focus and the tab-stop stay in sync (SF-4).

**APG caveats**: the inner per-row buttons (chevron, name, +, ✕, pin, swatch, kill) remain natively `Tab`-focusable rather than being subsumed under the single tree tab stop — a deliberate keyboard-first choice (every control stays reachable) over strict APG purity. `role="tree"` wraps the server `<section>` wrappers (which are not themselves treeitems). The implementation reuses the scroll half of the named list-scroll pattern but deliberately diverges from its `selectedIndex` numeric-state model in favor of the `rovingKey` string + DOM enumeration (see § Keyboard-Navigable List Scroll Pattern's third-consumer note).

### Collapsible Panels (Bottom-Aligned)

Two collapsible panels are pinned at the bottom of the sidebar below the scrollable session tree, above the server selector. Layout order top-to-bottom: server selector -> session list (`flex-1 overflow-y-auto`) -> Window panel -> Host panel. Combined height target ~140px when both open.

**CollapsiblePanel** (`app/frontend/src/components/sidebar/collapsible-panel.tsx`) — reusable wrapper used by both Window and Host panels. Props: `title` (string), `storageKey` (string for localStorage persistence), `defaultOpen` (boolean, default `true`), `children` (ReactNode), `headerRight` (ReactNode rendered inside the toggle button, right-aligned — the StatusDot+name slot; clicking it toggles the panel), and `headerAction` (ReactNode rendered OUTSIDE the toggle button at the header's right edge, whose clicks are **stopped from toggling the panel** — the purpose-built seam for an interactive control like the PANE-header refresh button, see WindowPanel below). Header is always visible: the title (`TypedLabel` — the section-label typed-sweep hover treatment, `260703-5ilm`, see § Hover-Animation Vocabulary) + chevron (`&#x25B8;` U+25B8) that rotates 90 degrees on toggle via CSS `transform: rotate()` with `transition-transform duration-150`. Content area uses `max-height` transition (`duration-150 ease-in-out`) for smooth expand/collapse. `overflow: hidden` during transition, `visible` when fully expanded (accessibility). Collapse state persisted to `localStorage[storageKey]` on every toggle. Each panel has `border-t-[3px] border-border first:border-t-0` (a 3px structural seam — see § Border-Width System — so panels partition cleanly; the resizable drag handle is transparent by default, letting the next panel's 3px top border be the sole visible inter-panel line).

**WindowPanel** (`app/frontend/src/components/sidebar/status-panel.tsx`) — collapsible panel with `title="Pane"`, `storageKey="runkit-panel-window"`, `defaultOpen={true}`. **PANE-header refresh button** (`PaneRefreshButton`, with an `idle | spinning | check` feedback state machine): passed as `CollapsiblePanel`'s `headerAction` (NOT `headerRight` — `headerAction` is the seam whose clicks are stopped from toggling the panel; `headerRight` is the StatusDot+name slot inside the toggle button). It kicks a server-side on-demand refresh of BOTH PR pollers via `refreshStatus()` → `POST /api/status/refresh` (see architecture.md § API Endpoints). **Feedback state machine**: a single `useState<"idle" | "spinning" | "check">` (discriminated over the three mutually-exclusive visuals; consumed by tests via a `data-state` attribute). The button **spins from CLICK until the server-global `status-refresh` SSE completion event, NOT until the POST settles** (the POST 202s in ~ms while the real `gh` work runs 1–10s detached). It branches on the tri-state 202 body: `started`/`coalesced` → `spinning` (no distinct coalesced visual — the in-flight pass's one completion event clears both); `throttled` → skip spinning and `flashCheck()` immediately ("already fresh"; no event will come). Completion is delivered via `useSessionContext().subscribeStatusRefresh` (subscribed ONLY while `spinning`, so an unrelated tab's completion doesn't flash an idle button); on fire it transitions `spinning → check` (a brief post-completion checkmark, `REFRESH_CHECK_MS = 1000`, auto-reverting to `idle`, mirroring the same-file `COPY_FEEDBACK_MS` cadence). A **15s UI fallback** (`REFRESH_FALLBACK_MS = 15000`, well under the 60s `statusRefreshTimeout` backend bound) clears a stuck spinner if the event is missed — **armed at click ENTRY, not inside `.then`** (a started/coalesced completion event can beat the POST settle, so arming in `.then` would restart a timer `flashCheck()` already cleared → a phantom checkmark ~15s later). A `refreshStatus()` rejection (non-2xx via the shared `throwOnError`) is swallowed back to `idle` (clearing the fallback) so a network failure never leaves a stuck spinner. All timers are cleared on every transition and on unmount. Renders `animate-spin` on the `lucide` rotate-cw SVG in `spinning`, a checkmark SVG (`data-testid="pane-refresh-check"`, `text-accent`) in `check`, the static rotate-cw icon in `idle`; 14×14 SVGs, 24/30px touch target (`coarse:`), `data-testid="pane-refresh"`, `data-state`, `aria-label`/`title="Refresh PR status"`. Follows the top-bar/board `RefreshButton` **CRT-glint** vocabulary (`rk-glint` — § Hover-Animation Vocabulary). It **renders whenever the PANE header renders, including with no window selected** — the refresh is server-global (both pollers are viewer-wide), so gating on window selection would add nothing. Best-effort/fire-and-forget: server-side coalescing + a min-interval throttle make it safe to over-fire (the fallback still clears any spinner). Scope-honest: labeled around PR/status freshness (the other PANE registers out/agt/fab are already fresh within ~7.5s). The `subscribeStatusRefresh` context seam it consumes is a `Set`-of-handlers ref + `fireStatusRefresh` fired from BOTH the per-server pool ES block AND the `?metrics=1` metrics-stream ES block in `session-context.tsx`, mirroring `subscribeBoardOrder`/`fireBoardOrder` (the event is host-global, so both streams carry it). Palette parity: the `PR: Refresh Status` action (§ Command Palette `PR: Refresh Status` action) is unchanged — a pure POST kick with no shared button state to hook. The `headerRight` slot renders `<StatusDot win={win} /> {win.name}` (in a `flex items-center gap-1.5 truncate text-text-secondary font-mono` span) — the unified status dot (see § Status Dot) leads the header so the window's status (palette-v3 two-family ladder + waiting halo) stays glanceable even when the panel is collapsed; hovering/focusing the dot opens the custom `StatusDotTip` hover-card (§ Status Dot). Displays the identity rows `tmx` (pane index + ID), `cwd` (shortened path), `git` (branch), then the **four orthogonal signal registers** `out` (L0 activity + elapsed) / `agt` (L1 `agentState` + duration) / `fab` (L2 change · stage · displayState) / `PR` (L3 derived PR, ungated) — the 3-char register view (§ Pane panel four-register view). The L1 `agt` register (`getAgentLine`) is `null` when `!win.agentState`, else `${agentState} ${agentIdleDuration}`; a blocked pane shows `waiting <dur>` (the pierce rule: it shows independently of the flowing-output L0 register). No window selected -> "No window selected" in secondary text. `StatusPanel` is exported as a deprecated alias. (`260715-jykd`, `260715-nwla`, `260616-37ub`, `260706-y1ar`, `260706-4h26`)

**Board-route PANE fallback — follows the focused tile.** The window `WindowPanel` renders is derived in `BottomPanels` (`sidebar/index.tsx`), not passed by the route: the route-selected window (`currentServer`/`currentSessionName`/`currentWindowId`) wins when present; otherwise `BottomPanels` consumes `useFocusedPane()` (§ Focused-pane context) and resolves the board's focused tile. On `/board/$name` the route has no `server` param so `currentServer` is `null` and no route window exists — the focused-tile fallback is the only source. Resolution (pure helpers in `app/frontend/src/lib/focused-pane-window.ts`): `resolveFocusedWindow(sessions, windowId)` scans `ctx.sessionsByServer.get(focusedPane.server)` for a window whose `windowId` matches — a **hit** yields the fully-enriched home-session copy (out/agt/fab/PR registers all live), which works because board pins are LINK-based with dual home+pin membership so the pinned window's home-session copy flows through the sessions SSE stream (§ tmux-sessions link-based board pin-sessions). A **miss** is a pin-only window (home session died while the window stayed pinned — absent from the stream); `thinWindowFromFocusedPane(focused)` then synthesizes a thin `WindowInfo` from the published board-entry data (`windowName` + `panes`: paneId/paneIndex/cwd/command/isActive/gitBranch, active pane = `isActive` else first) with `activityTimestamp: 0` (`getOutputLine` guards on a truthy timestamp, so `out` shows the pane command with no fabricated idle duration) — the tmx/cwd/git rows and `out` register render, the enrichment-only agt/fab/PR registers are honestly absent. Both branches render through the unchanged pure `WindowPanel` (a `WindowInfo | null` component — no board types or fallback markup added to `status-panel.tsx`). An empty board publishes `null`, so the panel keeps its "No window selected" state. (`260720-zx4i`)

**Copyable rows**: The `tmx`, `cwd`, `git`, and `fab` rows are interactive `<button type="button">` elements that copy their underlying value to the clipboard on click or keyboard activation (Enter/Space). Copy values per row:

| Row | Copy value | Source |
|-----|------------|--------|
| `tmx` | Pane ID (e.g., `%5`) | `activePane.paneId` |
| `cwd` | Full unshortened path (e.g., `/home/sahil/code/run-kit`) | `activePane.cwd ?? win.worktreePath` |
| `git` | Branch name | `activePane.gitBranch` |
| `fab` | Change ID (e.g., `lc2q`) | `fabChange.id` (parsed from `win.fabChange`) |

Non-interactive rows: `run` (process-only, when no fab state) and `agt` remain plain text — no hover affordance, no focus ring, no copy behavior. Rows with empty values (`tmx` with empty pane ID, `git` when no branch) are also non-interactive.

**`cwd` deleted-directory marker**: when the active pane's `cwdMissing` flag is set (the backend `os.Stat` found the pane's cwd no longer exists — typically an archived change whose worktree was deleted out from under a still-live tmux window), the `cwd` row keeps the shortened stale path as a breadcrumb but recolors the whole value `text-red-400` and appends a `(deleted)` tag (`data-testid="cwd-deleted"`); the row `title` reads `<full-path> (no longer exists)`. It uses **color over dimming** — a vanished cwd is more notable, not less, so it reuses the panel's failure-red token (the same `text-red-400` the `pr` fail-ish row uses) rather than the dimmed `text-text-secondary` of a normal path. The row stays copyable (still copies the stale full path). The marker is **self-healing**: it only shows while tmux still reports the deleted path; once the shell's cwd recovers to a real directory the backend stat succeeds, `cwdMissing` clears, and the row reverts to its normal style. This is the minimal honest signal — run-kit does NOT close or rename the orphaned tmux window (Constitution §VI forbids tearing down tmux windows). Backend derivation: `architecture.md` § `internal/sessions` (`resolveCwdMissing`). (`260614-nj74`)

**Register icons** (the pane panel is the four-register view — § Pane panel four-register view; these inline spinner glyphs lead their register line, `aria-hidden`): `BrailleSnake` (`braille-snake.tsx`, `⣾⣽⣻⢿⡿⣟⣯⣷`, 80ms) → the `out` (L0) register; `StarTwinkle` (`star-twinkle.tsx`) → the `agt` (L1) register; `ClockSpinner` (`clock-spinner.tsx`) → the `fab` (L2) register; the L3 `PR` register uses the Nerd Font git-pull-request glyph (`ICON_CLASS`). Each follows the same pattern: `useState(0)` frame counter + `useEffect` with `setInterval` + cleanup on unmount, rendered as `<span aria-hidden="true">`. (`260706-y1ar`)

**Inline feedback**: After a successful copy, the row's prefix label swaps to `copied ✓` for 1000ms, then reverts. A single `copiedRow` state variable tracks which row was last copied — only one row shows feedback at a time. Clicking a different row immediately moves the indicator.

**Hover affordance**: Interactive rows render `cursor: pointer` and a subtle background tint (`bg-bg-inset` or equivalent) on hover.

**Keyboard accessibility**: Button elements have visible focus state (outline/ring) and are keyboard-activatable (Enter/Space). Styling is reset to preserve the panel's compact plain-text aesthetic — no default button chrome (padding, border, background removed in rest state).

**Text-selection guard**: The click handler checks `window.getSelection()?.toString()` — if the user has an active text selection (e.g., from drag-selecting text), the copy action is suppressed, preserving native text-selection UX.

**Clipboard utility**: Copy operations use `copyToClipboard()` from `app/frontend/src/lib/clipboard.ts` — see [Clipboard Utility](#clipboard-utility).

**HostPanel** (`app/frontend/src/components/sidebar/host-panel.tsx`) — the sidebar host-metrics view inside a `CollapsiblePanel` with `title="Host"`, `storageKey="runkit-panel-host"`, `defaultOpen={true}`. Accepts a single `isConnected: boolean` prop. It owns only the chrome — the hostname header (truncated, on the left) + SSE indicator (green `bg-accent-green` / gray `bg-text-secondary` dot on the right, connection health) — and the `!metrics` "No metrics" branch; the metric ROWS are delegated to the shared `HostMetrics` component.

**Metrics source — server-scoped with host-global fallback.** `HostPanel` reads `metrics = useMetrics() ?? useHostMetrics()`: the current-server-scoped `useMetrics()` wins when present, falling back to the host-global metrics broadcast (`useHostMetrics()`, available on EVERY route — the same source the `/` HOST HEALTH zone consumes). On `/board/$name` there is no `currentServer`, so `useMetrics()` is `null` by construction and the panel renders the host-global snapshot instead of "No metrics"; on a `/$server/...` route the two arrive on the same tick so the fallback is harmless. **Connection dot source** is derived by `BottomPanels` (not by `HostPanel`): `isConnected` = the current server's subscription health (`ctx.isConnectedByServer.get(currentServer)`) when a server route is active, else `ctx.hostMetricsConnected` (host-metrics source health) when `currentServer` is `null` — so the board-route dot reflects host-metrics health rather than the always-false server-scoped signal. The `isConnected` prop's semantics are "health of whatever source feeds this panel". (`260720-zx4i`)

**Shared `HostMetrics` component** (`app/frontend/src/components/host-metrics.tsx`) — a single **layout-agnostic** presentational component `HostMetrics({ metrics }: { metrics: MetricsSnapshot })` renders the metric rows, so the two host views (sidebar `HostPanel` + the `/` HOST HEALTH zone) stay visually consistent (§ Design Decisions → HostMetrics is a shared component). It ALWAYS receives a non-null snapshot — the caller owns the surrounding layout chrome AND the `!metrics` empty state. It exports the `formatUptime`/`formatDisk` helpers and holds the `MemoryLine`/`LoadLine` sub-components. Rows (all `text-xs font-mono`), rendered via `lib/sparkline.ts` + `lib/gauge.ts`: (`260701-vshd`)

1. **CPU sparkline** — `cpu` label + braille sparkline (`text-accent`) + current percentage (`text-text-primary`). Sparkline rendered by `sparkline()` from `@/lib/sparkline.ts`
2. **Memory gauge** (`MemoryLine`) — `mem` label + filled/empty block gauge + `formatMemory` `used/total` text. Gauge color: green < 70%, yellow 70-90%, red > 90%. Uses `gaugeBar()`, `gaugeColor()`, `formatMemory()` from `@/lib/gauge.ts`. A `ResizeObserver` measures the container to size the gauge char-count responsively
3. **Disk + uptime** — `dsk` label + `formatDisk` `used/totalG` + ` · up ` + `formatUptime` (`Nd Nh` or `Nh Nm` if < 1 day). All `text-text-secondary`
4. **Load averages** (`LoadLine`) — `ld` label + three percentages (1/5/15 min) normalized as `(load / cpuCount) * 100`. Any percentage > 90% renders in `text-red-500`

See § Design Decisions → HostMetrics is a shared component.

### Focused-pane context (`contexts/focused-pane-context.tsx`)

The publication channel that lets the sidebar PANE panel follow the board's focused tile (§ Collapsible Panels → Board-route PANE fallback). `FocusedPaneProvider` is mounted in `RootWrapper` (`app.tsx`) alongside `TopBarSlotProvider`, so the registered value survives navigation and is readable from both the AppShell and board sidebars. Shape mirrors `top-bar-slot-context`: a referentially-stable dispatcher (held in a `useRef`), a `useMemo`'d context value, `useFocusedPane()` (read hook; throws outside the provider) and `useRegisterFocusedPane(pane)` (register hook: an effect publishes the memoized value on mount/change and clears to `null` on unmount, last-writer-wins). The published `FocusedPane` value is `{ server, windowId, windowName, panes: BoardPaneInfo[] } | null`: the focused tile's identity PLUS the board entry's thin pane data (from the `getBoard` join), so the pin-only thin render (§ Collapsible Panels) has everything it needs at the consumer with no second data channel and no board-API knowledge in the sidebar. `BoardPage` registers `entries[focusedIndex]` (memoized so the effect re-runs only when the focused entry changes); an empty board registers `null`, and navigating away clears it. This is distinct from `FocusedTerminalContext` (which registers the focused xterm's imperative send/focus handle for the compose strip) — this context carries declarative pane identity/data, not a terminal handle — and from the top-bar slot's `focusedPane` field (the `{server, windowId, cwd}` split target for the palette/top-bar ✕), which stays a separate, thinner channel. (`260720-zx4i`)

### HOST HEALTH Zone on `/` (Host-page host-console home)

`HostOverviewPage` (`app/frontend/src/components/host-overview-page.tsx`, route `/`) renders a **HOST HEALTH** zone ABOVE the tmux-server tile grid, inside the scroll container (`div.flex-1.min-h-0.overflow-y-auto`, which carries `pt-6` so the gap below the pinned TopBar matches the `mb-6` inter-section rhythm). This makes `/` — the only route that is about the BOX, not a session — a machine console. The zones render in top-to-bottom order **HOST HEALTH → BOARDS → TMUX SERVERS → SERVICES** (each an uppercase-labelled `<section>`; the server-tile grid has a "Tmux Servers" heading + inline server count, SERVICES last after the tiles; see § BOARDS Zone, § SERVICES Zone on `/`). A page-level `Host Overview` `SectionHeading` heads the scroll container above these zones (§ Page Overview Headings). Each zone heading is a `[ LABEL▊ ]────` `SectionHeading` (§ Section Heading); the Host page's identity is the solo `Host` heading in the top-bar center cell. Read-only awareness view; nothing here mutates host state (Constitution IV). (`260701-vshd`, `260701-5d0z`, `260702-6m46`, `260704-pr0p`, `260715-zs1y`)

- The zone (`<section aria-label="Host health">`) shows a `<SectionHeading label="Host Health" className="mb-2" />` (§ Section Heading), then the live `hostname` (from `useHostMetrics()`) in the zone BODY as a `text-xs text-text-secondary font-mono truncate mb-2` line right below the heading (NOT in the SectionHeading `side` slot, which stays empty on Host-page zones), then the shared `HostMetrics` component (CPU sparkline+current, memory gauge, load 1/5/15 normalized, disk used/total, uptime). (`260702-6m46`, `260704-pr0p`)
- It consumes **`useHostMetrics()`** (the server-independent hook — see architecture.md § Server-independent host-metrics subscription), NOT `useMetrics()` (which is `null` on `/` — there is no `currentServer`). Metrics update on each `event: metrics` tick; on a bare `/` with zero servers attached, freshness is the fast ~2.5s (`legacyPollInterval`) cadence, because `safetyIntervalEffective` treats a sentinel-only slice as the exception and returns the fast interval rather than the 12s backstop (the on-connect cached snapshot renders immediately) — see architecture.md § API Layer `/api/sessions/stream`.
- **Empty state**: when `useHostMetrics()` is `null` (pre-first-tick, or a non-Linux zero-valued host), the zone renders a graceful `No metrics` affordance (never a blank/broken layout), mirroring `HostPanel`'s `!metrics` branch.
- The server-tile grid below (create / open / count) and the `+ New Server` affordance function normally. **Infra-server name de-emphasis**: each tile's name `<div>` renders `text-text-secondary` (instead of `text-text-primary`) when `isInfraServer(name)` — the same greyed-not-disabled treatment as the Sidebar Server tile; the tile stays fully clickable/attachable. See § Infra-server de-emphasis. (`260705-uh8f`)

### BOARDS Zone on `/` (Host page)

`HostOverviewPage` renders a **BOARDS** zone (`<section aria-label="Boards">`) BETWEEN HOST HEALTH and TMUX SERVERS. A board aggregates windows across tmux servers, so the box-level Host page (not any single tmux Server page) is its list's natural home; it sits above TMUX SERVERS per the page's general→specific flow. (`260702-6m46`)

- **Data source**: the existing **`useBoards()`** hook (`plain /api/boards` fetch + the shared SSE pool — NO new API/endpoint; the same hook `board-page.tsx` and the sidebar consume). Returns `{ boards, isLoading }`.
- **Heading row**: a `<SectionHeading label="Boards" className="mb-2" />` (§ Section Heading). The board count / `loading…` is NOT in the SectionHeading `side` slot (reserved for the server-view stats) — it stays in the zone BODY, a `text-xs text-text-secondary font-mono mb-2` line right below the heading (`loading…` before the first fetch via `isLoading`, else `{N} board(s)`). (`260704-pr0p`)
- **Tiles**: one `<button>` per board (same tile idiom as the server tiles — `bg-bg-card border border-border rounded p-4 hover:border-text-secondary min-h-[60px]`) showing the board name + `{N} pin(s)`; clicking navigates to `/board/$name`. **Drag-reorderable**: tiles render `orderedBoards` from the shared `useBoardListReorder` hook (same instance seam as the sidebar) with `getTileProps(b.name)` spread onto each and the dragged tile dimmed `opacity-50` — see § Board-list drag reorder. (`260708-a2qd`)
- **Always visible**: the section renders even with zero boards — the empty state shows the sidebar's "Pin a window to start a board" hint (mirroring `BoardsSection`) instead of the section appearing/vanishing with the first/last board.
- **Not a shared component**: the tile markup is NOT shared with the sidebar `boards-section.tsx` (a parallel surface; the sidebar section drives the actual sidebar).

### SERVICES Zone on `/` (Host-page host-console home)

`HostOverviewPage` renders a **SERVICES** zone (`<section aria-label="Services">`) as the LAST zone, below the TMUX SERVERS tile grid, inside the same scroll container. It surfaces the host's listening TCP **ports** as tiles — a listening port is a HOST property (owned by no tmux window/session), so `/` (the box-level console) is its home, mirroring the HOST HEALTH rationale. The backend (`internal/ports`) passively enumerates and broadcasts **ALL** listening ports (procfs on Linux, lsof on darwin) with best-effort process attribution on BOTH platforms — no probing, no HTTP filter (see architecture.md § `internal/ports`). A tile is therefore **not guaranteed to speak HTTP**; the frontend does NO protocol guessing and applies no client-side denylist. Read-only awareness view; the only action opens a port's UI in a tmux window (Constitution IV — nothing mutates host state directly). (`260701-5d0z`, `260703-8y2a`, `260715-vfcz`)
