- **Data source**: **`useHostServices()`** (its own `HostServicesContext`, separate from `HostMetricsContext` so the ~2.5s services stream doesn't cascade re-renders into metrics-only consumers). It rides the SAME server-independent broadcast as host metrics — the `event: services` frame arrives on every stream (the dedicated `?metrics=1` stream on a bare `/`, and each per-server stream's fan-out), deduped on the raw payload string (`applyHostServices`). Returns `[]` (never null) before the first tick, so consumers map over it unconditionally. See architecture.md § API Layer `/api/sessions/stream` (`event: services`) and § Server-independent host-metrics subscription.
- **Tiles**: each `Service` (from `@/types` — `{ port, process?, pid? }`) renders a row keyed by `svc.port` showing `:{port}` (mono) + the optional `process` name. **Process attribution is best-effort on BOTH platforms**: macOS populates `process`/`pid` from lsof; Linux joins lsof attribution onto its procfs port set and populates them where lsof can attribute the port, leaving them absent (bare tile) for ports lsof can't see (e.g. root-owned `sshd :22` under a non-root lsof) — see architecture.md § `internal/ports`. Empty state: a graceful `No services` affordance when the list is empty (pre-first-tick, nothing listening, or an unsupported platform where the collector returns `[]` — Windows/BSD; macOS and Linux both enumerate). (`260715-vfcz`)
- **"Open in window" action** (`handleOpenInWindow`): opens the port's UI in an `@rk_type=iframe` tmux window via the existing `/proxy/{port}/` reverse proxy (`createWindow(server, session, "port-{port}", undefined, "iframe", "/proxy/{port}/")` — the `rkType`/`rkUrl` args become the `@rk_type`/`@rk_url` window options), then navigates to `/$server` (the new window surfaces via SSE). The window **name** is `port-{port}`, NOT `:{port}` — tmux rejects colons and periods in window names (`validate.ValidateName`); the tile still *displays* `:{port}`. Since `/` is server-less, it resolves a **target (server, session)**: `servers[0]` + that server's first session from the SSE cache (`sessionsByServer`), else an authoritative `getSessions()` fetch (the per-server stream is usually not attached yet on a fresh `/` load, so the cache can be empty even when sessions exist — fetching avoids a duplicate-name 500 on `new-session`), else an instant `"services"` session created on the fly (`createSession`). An `openingRef` guard debounces a double-click into a single create flow. `servers[0]` reflects the infra-last sort applied in `session-context.tsx` `fetchServers` (see § Infra-server de-emphasis), so a real workspace is preferred over `rk-daemon` as the "first-listed server" target. (`260705-uh8f`)
- **Button gated SOLELY on server existence**: the "Open in window" button is `disabled` with `title="Create a server first"` ONLY when `servers.length === 0` (there is no target to host the iframe window); otherwise it is enabled regardless of port number. The tile still renders in the disabled case.
- **Well-known-port de-emphasis**: with the SERVICES zone showing ALL listening ports, well-known/system ports (`port < 1024`, the reserved range — `sshd:22`, `smtp:25`, …) are visually de-emphasized, mirroring the `isInfraServer` server-tile treatment: their `:{port}` renders grey (`text-text-secondary` instead of `text-text-primary`) and they sort **last as a class**. `isWellKnownPort(port) = port < 1024`; the `orderedServices` `useMemo` partitions `hostServices` into regular vs. well-known, sorts each sub-group by port ascending, and concatenates (regular first) — so regular tiles keep their port-ascending order and well-known tiles trail. **Presentation-only, applied at render in `host-overview-page.tsx`**: the backend snapshot stays port-sorted; this is a frontend concern (parallel to the `session-context.tsx` infra-last server sort — see § Infra-server de-emphasis). Every tile, well-known or not, renders with its "Open in window" button. (`260715-vfcz`)
- **No HTTP gate anywhere**: there is no client-side HTTP-likely heuristic (no `NON_HTTP_PORTS` denylist, no `isLikelyHttpPort(port)`, no disabled branch, no `"Not a web service"` tooltip, no `handleOpenInWindow` guard) and no denylist or HTTP gate on the server; **do not re-add one**. The backend broadcasts ALL listening ports and does no probing, so a tile is not guaranteed to be a web service; **opening a non-HTTP port yields a user-initiated failed iframe — the iframe load IS the on-demand probe** (visible and harmless; there is no ambient probe). The empty state is `No services` (meaning "no listening ports"). `types.ts` `Service`/`ServicesSnapshot` carry no `http:` flag — there is no HTTP verdict. (`260703-8y2a`, `260715-vfcz`)

### Color Tinting — Owned Palette + Axis Split

Session rows, window rows, and server tiles support an optional color assignment that applies a full-width background tint. The palette is an **owned set of 10 fixed OKLCH hue families adapted to the active theme**: each family has a stable hue angle, and hue identity survives theme switches (a window labeled "orange" reads orange on every theme). The row's visual channels are split so labeling and selection never collide: **hue = label**, **tint depth = selection**, **left-edge marker = an independent label axis** (§ Left-Edge Label Zone). On window rows both label axes (color + marker) are set from the single left-edge Label picker; session rows and server tiles keep a right-side color affordance and have no marker.

**Owned hue families** (`themes.ts` `HUE_FAMILIES`): 10 families in stable display order, each `{ name, hue, legacy, neutral? }`. Hue angles are placed non-uniformly — tight through the discriminable red→amber region, the large gap parked in teal→blue where human hue discrimination is weakest: red 25°, orange 55°, amber 90°, olive 120°, green 150°, teal 185°, blue 250°, purple 290°, magenta 330°, slate 250° (`neutral`). `PICKER_COLOR_VALUES` is the display-ordered list of the 10 **family names** (the form new writes intend). `FAMILY_BY_NAME` / `FAMILY_BY_LEGACY` are the two lookup maps.

**Theme adaptation (full adoption)**: `themeColorStats(palette) → { L, C }` computes the mean OKLab lightness and mean chroma over `palette.ansi[1..6]`, with a chroma floor `THEME_CHROMA_FLOOR = 0.05` (near-monochrome themes stay distinguishable). A family's source hex = `oklchToHexInGamut(L_theme, C_theme, family.hue)`; slate uses a near-neutral chroma `min(C_theme × 0.2, 0.025)`. `colorValueToHex(value, palette)` resolves any stored value (family name OR legacy alias) to this adopted hex, returning `null` when it maps to no family.

**OKLCH → in-gamut hex, chroma-reduction not channel-clamp**: `oklchToHex(L, C, hueDeg)` converts polar chroma/hue to OKLab (`a = C·cos h`, `b = C·sin h`) then reuses `oklabToHex`. `oklchInGamut(L, C, hueDeg)` reports whether the triple maps inside sRGB without any channel being clamped, reusing the shared `oklabToLinearRgb(c)` matrix helper (extracted so its 18 coefficients stay in lockstep with `oklabToHex` — both consume it). `oklchToHexInGamut(L, C, hueDeg)` brings an out-of-gamut triple in by **reducing chroma stepwise** (`GAMUT_REDUCE_FACTOR = 0.92`, `GAMUT_REDUCE_MAX_STEPS = 20`) — L and hue are preserved; sRGB channel-clamping is never used because it shifts hue and would defeat the stable-hue goal.

**Legacy color values resolve 1:1 to families (zero migration)**: stored color values remain the **legacy vocabulary end-to-end** — the backend stores and validates only numeric/blend descriptors (`"4"` / `"1+3"`), and family names are frontend-side read aliases. The 1:1 map: red←`1`, orange←`1+3`, amber←`3`, olive←`1+2`, green←`2`, teal←`6`, blue←`4`, purple←`1+4`, magenta←`5`, slate←`3+4`. `resolveFamily(value)` accepts a family name OR a legacy descriptor (normalized via the file-private `normalizeLegacy`, mirroring the backend `NormalizeColorValue` rule) and returns the same family for both. `parseColorValue`/`formatColorValue` (family name form) accept both vocabularies. `familyToLegacy(name)` maps a picker family name to its legacy descriptor for the **write seam** (below); it is idempotent — an already-legacy or unrecognized input passes through unchanged.

**Pre-blended row tints, dual-keyed**: `computeRowTints(palette) → Map<string, RowTint>` pre-computes the three blended state hexes for every family, keyed under **BOTH vocabularies** — the family name AND its legacy descriptor point at the *same* tint entry — plus the `"8"` uncolored-selected sentinel. Both keys are populated because consumers (`window-row`/`session-row`/`server-panel`) look up the RAW stored value and the backend emits legacy forms, so a family-name-only map would miss every pre-existing colored row. Each family's adopted source hex (`colorValueToHex`) is saturated ×1.5 (`TINT_SATURATE_FACTOR`) before blending into the theme background at three ratios:

| State | Constant | Saturated-source ratio |
|-------|----------|------------------------|
| Base | `TINT_BASE_RATIO` | 14% |
| Hover | `TINT_HOVER_RATIO` | 22% |
| Selected | `TINT_SELECTED_RATIO` | 40% |

Selection is carried by tint **depth** alone (no left border — § Row Anatomy), so the selected ratio is 40%. The uncolored-selected gray sentinel (`"8"`, `UNCOLORED_SELECTED_ANSI`/`UNCOLORED_SELECTED_KEY`) is NOT saturated (gray is near-zero chroma) and uses the deeper `UNCOLORED_SELECTED_RATIO = 0.5` so it beats the `bg-card/50` hover. Each state gets its own concrete hex — no stacked transparent layers. The `RowTint` type (`{ base, hover, selected }`) is exported. Hover is applied imperatively via `onMouseEnter`/`onMouseLeave` style mutations to avoid CSS-specificity issues with dynamic backgrounds.

**Contrast-guardrailed borders** (`computeRowBorders(palette, category) → Map<string, string>`): each family's adopted source hex passed through a WCAG contrast guardrail, dual-keyed (family name + legacy descriptor + `"8"` sentinel) exactly like `computeRowTints`. `adjustBorderForContrast(border, bg, isDark, BORDER_MIN_CONTRAST)` nudges **only the OKLab lightness L** (lighten on dark themes, darken on light) in `0.03` steps until the border clears `BORDER_MIN_CONTRAST = 3.0` against the background or hits a 24-step cap; **hue and chroma are preserved** so the color keeps its identity. Window rows do not use these for a selection border; **server tiles** use them for their stripe/edge, and **the left-edge marker stripe uses them as its guarded family color** (`markerColor`, § Left-Edge Label Zone — the Label picker's marker CELLS deliberately do not: they draw in the theme foreground, see § Unified side-by-side Label picker). `sidebar/index.tsx` computes `rowTints` + `rowBorders` once per theme via `useMemo` and threads them to `WindowRow`/`ServerPanel`.

**OKLab + WCAG color-math helpers** (`themes.ts`): `hexToOklab` / `oklabToHex` (Björn Ottosson 2020 coefficients; `oklabToHex` and `oklchInGamut` share the `oklabToLinearRgb` matrix helper), the sRGB↔linear `srgbToLinear` gamma step, `relativeLuminance` (WCAG 2.x) and `contrastRatio(hex1, hex2)` (1..21), and `adjustBorderForContrast`. OKLab is the chosen lightness/distinctness space; WCAG is the separate legibility standard.

**SwatchPopover** (`app/frontend/src/components/swatch-popover.tsx`): one shared component, **one universal square style** — no rounded variant, no `square` prop. The color section renders the **10 families** from `PICKER_COLOR_VALUES` laid out 4-wide (rows of 4/4/2) plus a full-width `Clear color` first row. Props are STRINGS: `selectedColor?: string`, `onSelect(color | null)`, `onClose()`, plus the marker extension `selectedMarker?`, `onSelectMarker?(marker)` (no `markerColor` — marker stripes draw in the theme foreground, not a row-dependent color). **Color write seam** — every color emit funnels through `familyToLegacy` (the file-private `emit` callback: `onSelect(familyToLegacy(value))`), so a picked family name is stored as its legacy descriptor (`"orange"` → `"1+3"`); `null` (Clear) passes through untouched. This keeps stored values in the legacy vocabulary end-to-end — the backend validators (`ValidateColorValue`) accept only numeric/blend forms, so a raw family-name write would 400. Each swatch's fill is its `computeRowTints` `selected` tint (falling back to `colorValueToHex` then `theme.palette.foreground`); the selected swatch is matched by `resolveFamily(selectedColor)?.name` so a legacy-stored value highlights the right family. The listbox **autofocuses on mount** (`containerRef.current?.focus()` in a mount effect, mirroring pin-popover) so arrow-key nav works immediately after the `Window: Label` palette action — the sole keyboard path to the marker section. Dismisses on selection, Escape, or outside click.

**Universal square style**: every caller gets the same vocabulary — zero border radius on the container and all cells (no `rounded-md`/`rounded-sm`), a hard offset block shadow `3px 3px 0 rgba(0,0,0,.35)` (not `shadow-lg`), 3px gaps (`gap-[3px]`), 18px cells (`w-[18px] h-[18px]`), and 1px selection/focus outlines (`ring-1 ring-text-secondary`). There is a single style literal per axis — no dual class-string branches, no `SQUARE_GRID_COLS`/`DEFAULT_GRID_COLS` split. Session/server rows and the palette color actions render square like the window-row picker.

**Unified side-by-side Label picker**: when `onSelectMarker` is supplied (`showMarkers`), the popover renders two side-by-side sections divided by a **vertical hairline** (`w-px bg-border mx-1.5 self-stretch`) — markers LEFT (a 1-column `flex flex-col gap-[3px]` of 4 cells), colors RIGHT (the 4-wide grid). The layout pairs the two axes row-for-row:

```
∅   │  [   Clear color    ]     ← row 0: removal row
▐░  │  c1  c2  c3  c4           ← row 1: dotted  + colors 1–4
▐█  │  c5  c6  c7  c8           ← row 2: solid   + colors 5–8
▐▓  │  c9  c10  .   .           ← row 3: double  + colors 9–10 (2 dead cells)
```

- **Row 0 is the removal row**: the `∅` no-marker cell (marker column) beside a `Clear color` button spanning the 4 color columns (`col-span-4`).
- **Rows 1–3** pair the dotted / solid / double marker cells with color rows of 4/4/2. Marker cells draw stripes via the shared `markerStripeStyle` helper in the **theme foreground** on `bg-bg-inset` cells — deliberately NOT the row's guarded family color: picker cells communicate *shape*, a row-color-dependent stripe repaints the marker column on color changes (contradicting the independent-axes model), and the gray sentinel rendered near-invisible on uncolored rows (the common first-labeling case). The row GUTTER stripe keeps the guarded family color (§ Left-Edge Label Zone). The empty cell shows a `∅` glyph (10px); the current state carries `aria-selected` + a `ring-1 ring-text-primary` outline. Selecting a cell calls `onSelectMarker` **directly with the exact state** (no cycling — any state is one click; `""` clears).
- Marker cell order mirrors `MARKER_STATES` (`["", "dotted", "solid", "double"]`) via `MARKER_CELLS` — `∅` in row 0, the three non-empty states beside the three color rows.
- **Load-bearing coincidence** (marked with a code comment): the 1:1 marker-row ↔ color-row pairing works only because the 10 `PICKER_COLOR_VALUES` laid out 4-wide make exactly 3 color rows — the same count as the 3 non-empty `MARKER_STATES`. Changing `PICKER_COLOR_VALUES`' length or `MARKER_STATES` breaks the pairing (and the keyboard grid).

**Color-only callers get the pure square grid**: with the marker props absent the left marker column and vertical hairline are simply not rendered — the color section stands alone with its full-width `Clear color` first row over the 10 swatches (rows of 4/4/2). Same square style; no separate layout branch.

**Keyboard navigation — conceptual 5-column grid**: focus is a `{row, col}` `GridPos` pair (not a linear item index). `col` 0 = the marker column (valid only when `showMarkers`), cols 1–4 = the color columns; `row` 0 = the removal row, rows 1–3 = color rows. ArrowLeft/ArrowRight cross the hairline (col 1 ↔ col 0) and step within the color columns; ArrowUp/ArrowDown move within a column. The `Clear color` button is a **single spanning focus target** occupying cols 1–4 of row 0 (canonicalized to col 1; `focusOnClear = row === 0 && col >= 1`). Off-grid moves and the two dead cells (row 3, cols 3–4) clamp to the nearest valid cell via `maxColorCol(row)` — no crash, focus stays valid (`maxColorCol(3) === 2`). Enter/Space activates the focused cell (`activate`): col 0 → `onSelectMarker(MARKER_CELLS[row])`, row 0 → `emit(null)` (Clear), else → `emit(PICKER_COLOR_VALUES[colorIndexAt])`. **Initial focus FOLLOWS SELECTION**: the selected color swatch, or the `Clear color` cell (row 0 — already `aria-selected` in that state) when uncolored, never an arbitrary swatch; the marker column is reached via ArrowLeft. **Focus-visible semantics**: the focus ring (`ring-text-secondary`, visually quieter than the `ring-text-primary` selection ring) renders only after the first arrow key (`keyboardActive` flag) — the listbox autofocuses on mount, so an always-on ring showed mouse users a phantom highlight. The selected item is marked with the brighter `ring-text-primary` (colors additionally show a ✓; the uncolored state rings `Clear color`). Color-only mode is the same grid minus column 0.

**Window-row left-edge trigger**: the combined Label picker opens from the window row's left-edge label zone (§ Left-Edge Label Zone) or the `Window: Label` palette action — it is not a right-edge hover indicator. Session rows and server tiles still surface their color picker via a right-edge hover palette icon (visible on hover on desktop, always on touch via `coarse:opacity-100`).

**Command palette actions**: "Session: Set Color" opens the color-only SwatchPopover. The window **label** action is `window-label` / `Window: Label`, which dispatches an imperative `label-popover:open` CustomEvent (`{ detail: { server, windowId } }`) for the current window — the matching `WindowRow` listens and opens its combined picker (mirroring the `pin-popover:open` pattern used by "Board: Pin Current Window") to set both color and marker in one picker. The color-only `window-set-color` / `Window: Set Color` action (which opens the color-only SwatchPopover via `setShowColorPicker("window")`) is a separate registered action. Every color write path flows through the `familyToLegacy` write seam so stored values stay legacy; "Clear color" sends `null`, and clearing the marker sends `null` through `setWindowMarker`.

**Storage**: stored color values are the **legacy descriptor** (`"4"` / `"1+3"`); frontend wire types are `WindowInfo.color?: string` and `ProjectSession.sessionColor?: string` (`src/types.ts`). Window and session colors are ephemeral tmux user options (`@color` per window, `@session_color` per session — survive session lifetime, not tmux-server restarts), set via `setWindowColor`/`setSessionColor` in `client.ts`. Server colors persist in `~/.rk/settings.yaml`. **No color storage/API/backend migration** — the owned-palette rewrite is frontend-only for color. See architecture.md § Data Model for the backend storage/validation contract.

### Row Anatomy — Selection & Board-Pin Cues (`window-row.tsx`)

The window row's visual channels are orthogonal: **hue = label** (family tint), **tint depth = selection**, **left-edge zone = the independent marker axis + the Label-picker trigger** (§ Left-Edge Label Zone). Selection and the board-pin cue are borderless — the sidebar window row carries no left accent border.

**Full-bleed row box**: the row `<button>` (`window-row.tsx:238`) spans the sidebar **edge-to-edge** — every box-anchored visual layer (family tint via `buttonStyle`, hover fill, 40% selection tint, the `isDragOver` box-shadow, and the `inset-0` scanline overlay) reaches the physical sidebar left edge with no gutter. The 12px hierarchy indent lives inside the button's left padding (`pl-[30px]` = 12px indent + 18px content padding), not as a group margin on the window-list wrapper — so the status dot and window name sit at a fixed 30px from the sidebar edge (dot leading edge) while the box itself extends to the seam. The wider scanline band on selected+double rows follows from the box reaching the edge and is intended.

**Selection = tint depth + typography, borderless**: a selected colored row deepens to the 40% family tint (`rowTints.get(color).selected`); an uncolored selected row uses the gray sentinel's deeper 0.5 tint. The name goes `font-medium` + `text-text-primary`. There is **no** left accent border on selection.

**Board-pin active-board cue on the pin glyph** (not a border): the persistent filled pin glyph — already `opacity-100` + filled whenever the window is pinned to any board (`isPinnedToAny`) — renders **accent-colored** when the row is pinned to the currently-viewed board (`isPinnedToActiveBoard`), and monochrome `text-text-secondary` otherwise. `isPinnedToActiveBoard` implies `isPinnedToAny`, so the accent branch is always the persistent (never hover-gated) glyph. This is load-bearing because link-based pinning keeps pinned rows visible in SESSIONS: the cue distinguishes "pinned to the board you're viewing" from "pinned to some board" with zero new elements, leaving the left-edge zone for the marker + Label picker. See § Active-Board Highlight in Sessions Tree, § Sidebar Pin Icon on Window Rows. (`260718-co9z`)

### Left-Edge Label Zone (`window-row.tsx` `LabelZone`)

The whole 26px to the left of the status dot on each window row is ONE interactive target that opens the combined **Label picker** (colors + marker). It consolidates both of the row's label axes on the left edge — hue and the independent 4-state marker — leaving the right hover cluster for actions (pin + kill). The marker is an abstract label axis, orthogonal to hue and selection; its four states are deliberately unnamed in the UI (todo/doing/done for one user, priority for another).

**One 26px target, opens the picker — never cycles, never selects**: clicking anywhere in the zone opens the combined Label picker anchored at the row's bottom-left (an `absolute left-0 top-full z-50` wrapper; the row root stays overflow-free so the `top-full` popover is not clipped even on a selected+double row). The click `stopPropagation`s so it does not select the row, and coexists with drag-reorder. Cursor is `pointer` (menu-opener semantics). The zone is enabled on non-ghost rows wired with both the color and marker write seams plus a `server` (`labelZoneEnabled`).

**Zone geometry**: an absolute `z-20` sibling positioned `left-0` spanning `LABEL_ZONE_WIDTH = 26`px (full row height). Because the row box is full-bleed (§ Row Anatomy), `left-0` IS the physical sidebar edge — the zone needs no negative offset, so the coordinate expression is a plain `left-0` overlay. The zone's absolute span (sidebar x = 0…26) is 26px of the true sidebar edge. The palette-icon home is a 12px band (`ICON_ZONE_WIDTH = 12`) inset `ICON_EDGE_INSET = 12`px off the physical edge (sidebar x = 12…24) — past the widest (double, 4+6=10px) marker stripe, so the hover icon sits beside the stripe rather than over it. The button content is padded clear with `pl-[30px]` (12px hierarchy indent + 18px content padding) so the leading StatusDot + name start 4px past the zone's inner edge — the dot keeps its own hover-card and click-to-select, and the dot + name keep their exact x-positions (no content shift). Active on coarse pointers — touch gets direct label access (no `coarse:pointer-events-none`).

**Hover affordance — palette icon + two-stage zone glow**: at rest the zone is transparent with no icon. On ROW hover (`group-hover`) the shipped `PaletteIcon` (~11px, in the 12px icon zone at `left: ICON_EDGE_INSET = 12`px, beside the edge-anchored stripe rather than over it) fades to ~65% and the whole zone glows ~12% family color; when the ZONE ITSELF is hovered the icon reaches full opacity and the glow deepens to ~24% (`color-mix`). The icon is drawn in the row's guarded family color (`markerColor`) on colored rows and inherited monochrome on uncolored rows. The icon container keeps an explicit `z-10` (the stripe is a DOM sibling rendered before it) as a guard so any residual overlap layers icon-over-stripe deterministically inside the zone's own `z-20` stacking context, not by incidental sibling order. `aria-label="Set window label"` names the zone for pointer AT users and test selection.

**Marker stripe is display-only**: the marker renders as a left-edge stripe (3px dotted / 3px solid / 6px double in the guarded family color, gray uncolored) via the shared `markerStripeStyle` helper, anchored near-flush at the sidebar's physical left edge — `left: STRIPE_EDGE_INSET = 4`px (`window-row.tsx:474`, `:530`), `right: 0`. `dotted` is a fixed-rhythm `repeating-linear-gradient` (3px dash / 3px gap, `background-size: 3px 100%`), NOT `border-left: dotted` — a dotted border distributes dots per-element and restarts at every row, so stacked dotted rows showed seams while solid/double merged; the gradient's 6px period divides the 24px (36px coarse) row height exactly, so the rhythm carries across adjacent rows. It is purely a display of current state — clicking it opens the picker; it does not cycle. `themes.ts` owns `MARKER_STATES = ["", "dotted", "solid", "double"]` and the `markerStripeStyle(state, color)` helper, shared by this stripe and the Label picker's marker cells so the stripe vocabulary lives in exactly one place. Markers are available on all rows including uncolored ones.

**Marker/color plumbing**: `WindowInfo.marker?: string` (`src/types.ts`) carries the state from the `@rk_marker` window option (architecture.md § `@rk_marker`). `setWindowMarker(server, windowId, marker | null)` in `client.ts` delegates to `setWindowOptions({"@rk_marker": ...})` (empty/`null` clears). `sidebar/index.tsx` owns `onColorChange` + `onMarkerChange` handlers, prop-drilled through `ServerGroup` to `WindowRow`; the Label picker passes the **exact** picked color and marker state straight to these (no cycling — any state is one click). The `Window: Label` palette action opens this same picker via an imperative `label-popover:open` CustomEvent that the matching `WindowRow` listens for (`{ detail: { server, windowId } }`, mirroring the `pin-popover:open` pattern); the row registers both listeners in one `useEffect`. **Scope: window rows only** — session rows and server tiles get the owned-palette color affordance but no marker and no left-edge label zone.

### Easter Egg — Double-Marker Scanlines (`globals.css` `.rk-scanlines`)

A window row whose marker is `double` gets a static CRT scanline overlay across its full width, making `double` the one marker state readable from across the sidebar. Selecting such a row brings the scanlines alive.

**Static scanlines**: `.rk-scanlines::before` paints a `repeating-linear-gradient(to bottom, {marker color}@24% 0 1px, transparent 1px 3px)` reading the family color from the `--rk-marker-color` custom property (set on the row when `double`). The overlay is a **dedicated absolutely-positioned inner element** (`absolute inset-0 z-[5] overflow-hidden pointer-events-none`), NOT the row root — `overflow-hidden` on the root would clip the row's `top-full` pin/color popovers, so clipping lives on the overlay and the root stays free to overflow. The overlay sits above the tint/button background (`z-5`), below the `z-10` icon cluster and `z-20` gutter. Pure static CSS — it does not touch the status pyramid's animation channel (the waiting halo stays unambiguous).

**Selected + double retro animation**: when a double-marker row is ALSO selected, the class `rk-scanlines-crawl` is added, animating a slow downward crawl of the gradient period (`@keyframes rk-scanline-crawl`, `background-position-y` 0 → 3px, 2.4s linear infinite) plus an occasional CRT refresh band — a soft ~12px gradient band in the marker color rolling top→bottom via `::after` (`@keyframes rk-scanline-band`, 7s cycle with a rest phase then a ~2.8s sweep, `pointer-events: none`). Static again when deselected. **Both animations move `background-position-y`, never `transform`** — an animated translateY range grows the compositor layer beyond the row box (ancestor clips ignored), and the HTML5 drag-ghost snapshot of a selected+double row then carries a sliver of the neighboring row along with it; a background sweep cannot paint outside the element's own box. The band is a `no-repeat` `background-size: 100% 12px` gradient on an `inset-0` `::after`, parked at `background-position-y: -12px` (outside the box paints nothing) and swept to `calc(100% + 12px)` (band top at box bottom — fully exited).

**Reduced motion**: inside the existing `@media (prefers-reduced-motion: reduce)` block, `.rk-scanlines-crawl::before { animation: none }` and `.rk-scanlines-crawl::after { animation: none; display: none }` — the crawl and band are fully zeroed (static scanlines only, band hidden). The base rules PRECEDE the reduced-motion block so its equal-specificity overrides win by source order, mirroring the `rk-waiting-halo`/`rk-waiting-seam` discipline.

### Braille Sparkline Renderer

`app/frontend/src/lib/sparkline.ts` — converts an array of float values (0-100 range) into a Unicode braille sparkline string. Uses 8 vertical levels from the U+2800-U+28FF braille range filling bottom-to-top: `⣀⣄⣤⣦⣶⣷⣾⣿` (level 0 = `⣀`, level 7 = `⣿`). Values linearly interpolated across 8 levels. Zero-filled buffer renders as repeated `⣀`. Exported as `sparkline(samples: number[]): string`.

### Memory Gauge Renderer

`app/frontend/src/lib/gauge.ts` — utilities for the memory gauge visualization:
- `gaugeBar(ratio: number): string` — builds a filled/empty block string (`█` filled, `░` empty) from a 0-1 ratio. Fixed width of 10 characters
- `gaugeColor(percent: number): string` — returns a Tailwind color class: `text-green-500` (< 70%), `text-yellow-500` (70-90%), `text-red-500` (> 90%)
- `formatBytes(bytes: number): string` — compact human-readable size (`3.1G`, `512M`, `128K`)
- `formatMemory(used: number, total: number): string` — compact `used/total` string (e.g., `3.1G/8G`)

### Clipboard Utility

`app/frontend/src/lib/clipboard.ts` — shared `copyToClipboard(text: string): Promise<boolean>` function. Primary path uses `navigator.clipboard.writeText()`; fallback uses `document.execCommand('copy')` for non-secure contexts (HTTP). All callers (terminal copy, Pane panel row copy) import from this module (§ Steady-state version surfaces for the boolean success signal).

CWD display (line 1) uses `shortenPath()` to shorten the active pane's `cwd` (falls back to `worktreePath`):
- Home substitution: `/home/<user>/…` → `~/…`, `/Users/<user>/…` → `~/…`, `/root/…` → `~/…` (exact home dir → `~`). Handles Linux and macOS conventions.
- Truncation: if the path (after home substitution) has more than 2 non-empty segments, it is truncated to `…/<second-to-last>/<last>`. Paths with ≤ 2 segments are not truncated.
- Examples: `/home/sahil/code/org/repo/src` → `…/repo/src`; `/home/sahil/code/org` → `~/code/org`; `/var/log/nginx` → `…/log/nginx`.
- The `title` attribute on the CWD element always contains the original unmodified `activePaneCwd` — hover to see the full path.

## Session Creation Pattern

### Instant Creation (Primary)

All primary session creation entry points create a session immediately without a dialog. Implemented by `executeCreateSessionInstant` in `app.tsx`.

**Algorithm**:
1. Derive a name from the active window's `worktreePath` using `deriveNameFromPath(worktreePath)` (exported from `create-session-dialog.tsx`). If the result is empty (CWD is `/`, `~`, or `worktreePath` is undefined), the name is `session`.
2. Deduplicate against `sessions`: if the name is taken, try `{name}-2`, `{name}-3`, … up to `{name}-10`. If all are taken, use `{name}-11` (best-effort).
3. Call `createSession(server, derivedName, worktreePath)`. If no active window exists, call `createSession(server, "session")` (no `cwd` — tmux defaults to server CWD).
4. The session appears in the sidebar via the existing optimistic/ghost mechanism.

**Entry points** (all call `onCreateSession` → `executeCreateSessionInstant`):
- Sidebar `+` button (session level)
- Sidebar empty-state `+ New Session` button
- `SessionTiles` "+ New Session" dashed-border tile (the density view on `/$server`)
- Top-bar breadcrumb session dropdown `+ New Session` item
- Cmd+K "Session: Create" action

**Name derivation utilities**: `deriveNameFromPath` and `toTmuxSafeName` are exported from `app/frontend/src/components/create-session-dialog.tsx` so `app.tsx` can import them without duplicating logic.

### Folder-Prompted Creation (Secondary, via Cmd+K)

Two secondary entry points open `CreateSessionDialog` for users who want to specify a starting directory:

- **"Session: Create at Folder"** — opens `CreateSessionDialog` (mode `"session"`, default). The dialog's path input is pre-filled with `currentWindow.worktreePath` via the `defaultPath?: string` prop added to `CreateSessionDialogProps`. If no active window, the field starts empty.
- **"Window: Create at Folder"** — opens `CreateSessionDialog` with `mode="window"` and `session={currentSession}`. In window mode: title changes to "Create window at folder", session name input hidden, confirming calls `createWindow(server, session, undefined, cwd)` — **no name**, so tmux auto-names the window to the chosen folder's basename via `automatic-rename-format` (see [tmux-sessions](/run-kit/tmux-sessions.md) § Managed Window Creation). This flow sets no optimistic ghost, so there is no ghost label to derive. (`260707-j66b`)

`CreateSessionDialog` gains three optional backward-compatible props:
- `defaultPath?: string` — pre-fills the path input
- `mode?: "session" | "window"` — controls dialog behavior (default `"session"`)
- `session?: string` — required in window mode to pass to `createWindow`

### Deprecated: Dialog-First Flow

There is no `showCreateDialog` / `openCreateDialog` / `closeCreateDialog` API in `use-dialog-state.ts`; `CreateSessionDialog` is not opened by the sidebar `+` button or the primary "Session: Create" palette action. Use "Session: Create at Folder" in Cmd+K for folder-prompted session creation.

### Unnamed `+ New Window` — Folder Auto-Naming

The `+ New Window` action does **not** pin the window name to `"zsh"` — it calls `createWindow` with **no name**, so tmux auto-names the window to its folder basename and live-updates it (the tmux-layer convention lives in [tmux-sessions](/run-kit/tmux-sessions.md) § Managed Window Creation). A hardcoded name would leave a sidebar full of windows as indistinguishable "zsh" rows. (`260707-j66b`)

**All three unnamed-window call sites:**

1. **Sidebar `+ New Window`** (`app.tsx`, the `create-window` "Window: Create" palette action) — `createWindow(srv, session, undefined, activeWin?.worktreePath)`. Its optimistic-ghost label becomes the **raw** (unsanitized) basename of the creation cwd via the local `rawBasename(cwd)` helper (falls back to `"window"` when no cwd). This is deliberately **NOT** `deriveNameFromPath` — that runs `toTmuxSafeName` (`.`→`_` etc.), but tmux's `#{b:pane_current_path}` uses the unsanitized basename, so the ghost must match the raw form tmux will actually display.
2. **Palette "Window: Create at Folder"** (`create-session-dialog.tsx`, `mode="window"`) — `createWindow(server, session, undefined, cwd)`; this flow sets **no** optimistic ghost, so no label is derived.
3. **Board-route `+ New Window`** (`board-page.tsx`) — `createWindowApi(srv, sess)` (no name, no cwd — the backend resolves a default; this action registers no ghost). Identical behavior to the same button on `/$server`.

**Client contract**: `createWindow(server, session, name?, cwd?, rkType?, rkUrl?)` in `api/client.ts` makes `name` optional and **omits it from the JSON body when absent/empty** (matching the existing omit-when-absent handling for `cwd`/`rkType`/`rkUrl`). Explicit names are still sent — the deliberate-name paths are unchanged: **iframe/service windows** (`Window: New Iframe Window`, `createWindow(..., name, undefined, "iframe", url)`), the `port-N` "Open in window" service windows (`server-list-page.tsx`), and `rk riff`.

**E2E** (`app/frontend/tests/e2e/new-window-unnamed.spec.ts` + sibling `.spec.md`): asserts, via route interception on `POST /api/sessions/*/windows`, that the `+ New Window` request body carries **no `name` key** — a deterministic frontend→API seam. (The visual auto-rename is NOT asserted: the e2e tmux server is created with a bare `new-session` and `CreateWindow` never sources the config there, so `automatic-rename-format` isn't reliably applied on that server; the tmux-native naming is covered by the config + Go arg-builder tests instead.) (`260707-j66b`)

**Ghost TTL backstop** (`GHOST_WINDOW_TTL_MS = 15_000`, exported from `src/store/window-store.ts`): an optimistic ghost row is **claimed** only when a NEW windowId (one not in the ghost's `snapshotWindowIds`) arrives for its `(server, session)` via SSE (`setWindowsForSession`, oldest-ghost-first). Ordinary creates confirm within one SSE tick (~1-2s), and a *failed* create's caller rollback calls `removeGhost`. But if a create **succeeds somewhere else** — e.g. a tmux target ambiguity routes the window into a different session (exact-match session targets prevent this at the backend, see [tmux-sessions](/run-kit/tmux-sessions.md) § Exact-Match Session Targets) — no rollback fires and no claim ever arrives, stranding a permanently greyed, pulsing, unclickable row. `addGhostWindow` therefore arms a `setTimeout(() => get().removeGhost(optimisticId), GHOST_WINDOW_TTL_MS)`: the unclaimed ghost self-clears after 15s (comfortably past any legitimate claim). `removeGhost` is **idempotent** (filters by `optimisticId`), so a timer firing after the ghost was already claimed or rolled back is a no-op. This is a generic frontend backstop for the "no rollback, no claim" strand, independent of the backend root-cause fix. Two fake-timer unit tests cover TTL expiry and the claimed-ghost no-op. (`260717-hikh`)

## Bottom Bar (Shell-level, Shared Across Routes)

Single row of `<kbd>` styled buttons, rendered at shell level via `<Shell>`'s `bottombar` grid area on every route that mounts `<Shell>` — single-terminal, board, and tmux Server (no-window) alike. Width tracks the right grid column (page width minus sidebar). Styled with `border-t-[3px] border-border` (the 3px structural seam — see § Border-Width System) and `px-1.5 h-[48px]`. Layout: `Tab Ctrl Alt Fn▴ ArrowPad | >_ ⌘K ⌨`. The hostname is shown in the sidebar Host panel, not the bottom bar; Escape lives in the Function key dropdown's extended-keys section. The `>_` button (conditionally rendered when `onOpenCompose` is provided) is an `aria-pressed` accent toggle for the docked compose strip (§ Docked Compose Strip), not a modal trigger. (`260509-17m3`, `260702-6m46`)

`BottomBarProps` contains no `wsRef`. Input handlers read `focused?.wsRef` from `FocusedTerminalContext` and send ANSI escape sequences through it. The component is byte-identical across single-terminal and board routes (same JSX, same callbacks: `onOpenCompose`, `onFocusTerminal`, `onScrollLockChange`) — board panes are terminals, so the input toolbar applies identically. When `focused === null` (Dashboard route, no active terminal), input handlers natural-no-op via the existing `wsRef.current?.readyState !== OPEN` guard — no error, no toast.

**Modifier toggles** (Ctrl, Alt): Sticky armed state with visual indicator (`accent` bg). Click to arm, auto-clears after next key is sent. Click again while armed to disarm. Multiple modifiers can be armed simultaneously. No Cmd (`⌘`) toggle — on desktop users hold the real Cmd key; on mobile Cmd combos aren't used in terminal workflows.

**Armed modifier bridging**: When modifiers are armed, a capture-phase `keydown` listener intercepts physical keypresses and translates them to terminal escape sequences (Ctrl+letter → control characters, Alt → ESC prefix). Sends via WebSocket, preventing xterm from receiving the unmodified key. Ignores real Cmd/Ctrl/Alt held by the OS.

**ArrowPad** (`arrow-pad.tsx`): Combined directional pad replacing individual arrow buttons. Sends ANSI escape sequences (`[A/B/C/D`). With modifiers, use xterm parameter encoding (`[1;{mod}X`). Modifier parameter: 1 + (alt?2:0) + (ctrl?4:0).

**Function key dropdown** (F▴): Opens a combined popup above the button. Top section: F1-F12 in a 4-column grid. Divider (`border-t border-border`). Bottom section: Esc, PgUp, PgDn, Home, End, Ins, Del in a 3-column grid (3x3, 7 items). Escape uses `sendSpecial` (preserves Ctrl re-arm semantics); other extended keys use `sendWithMods`. Closes after each selection, on outside click, or on Escape.

**Special keys** (Tab in bottom bar, Esc in Fn menu): Direct send via `sendSpecial`. Ctrl is not consumed for Esc/Tab (Esc IS Ctrl+[, Tab IS Ctrl+I in terminal semantics) — Ctrl stays armed for the next key. Alt prefix with ESC (Meta convention).

**All buttons**: 33px min-height / 35px min-width on fine pointers (`min-h-[33px] min-w-[35px]` — reduced from 36×36 to give the row air), full 36×36 touch target on coarse pointers (`coarse:min-h-[36px] coarse:min-w-[36px]`). Row gap is `gap-1.5` (6px) on fine pointers, `coarse:gap-1` (4px) on touch — so the 375px single-row budget is byte-identical to before. `text-xs`, `<kbd>` element styling.

**Focus preservation**: All bottom bar buttons that send terminal input or toggle modifier state have `onMouseDown={(e) => e.preventDefault()}` via a shared `preventFocusSteal` handler. This prevents the browser from shifting focus away from xterm.js's hidden textarea when buttons are tapped, keeping the on-screen keyboard visible on iOS/touch devices. The CmdK button is excluded (it intentionally opens a dialog that takes focus). The ArrowPad handles focus preservation independently via its own `onMouseDown` handler.

### Docked Compose Strip

`ComposeStrip` (`components/compose-strip.tsx`) is a single **global**, sticky text-input surface docked at the bottom of the terminal area, immediately **above** the bottom-bar keys. It is a plain `<div>` in the shell footer — no backdrop, no `role="dialog"`/`aria-modal`, no focus trap, no Escape-closes, no close-on-send, no terminal dimming. A real `<textarea>` gives mobile autocorrect/IME (xterm is a `<canvas>` with neither) and a stable home for pasting large text blocks over a laggy relay.

**Two distinct send paths** (do not conflate): the compose strip rides the **relay WebSocket as raw bytes** — a submit sends `text + "\r"`, an insert sends bare `text` (no `\r`), over the focused terminal's `wsRef` (the muxed RelayMux stream, same path as BottomBar keystrokes), no backend endpoint. The **chat-send** path is entirely separate — `POST /api/windows/{id}/chat/send` with named-buffer paste + NOVELTY echo probe + probe-and-submit-gated Enter + per-`(server,paneID)` lock (see [chat](/run-kit/chat.md) § send path). Compose does NOT use that machinery. The two surfaces DO share the pointer-aware Enter policy (one `classifyComposeEnter` + `useCoarsePointer`), but not the delivery mechanism.

**Toggle + persistence.** The strip's enablement is the `composeStripEnabled` chrome preference (ChromeContext, `localStorage["runkit-compose-strip"]`, `"true"` sentinel — the `terminalFontSize`/`fixedWidth` pattern; see § Terminal Font Size). Two parity affordances flip it: the bottom-bar `>_` chip (`aria-pressed={composeStripEnabled}` + the ctrl/alt pressed-state vocabulary `bg-accent/20 border-accent text-accent` when on, `text-text-secondary` off; `preventFocusSteal` preserved) and the `View: Text Input` palette action (`toggleComposeStrip`). The caller gates the mount (`{composeStripEnabled && <ComposeStrip />}` in `app.tsx` and `board-page.tsx` footers). Toggling grows/shrinks the footer grid row by the strip's height, which the terminal container's existing `ResizeObserver` picks up → `fitAndSync` (FitAddon `fit()` + tmux resize) — the same reflow class as a font-size change; no dedicated refit effect.

**Live target.** The strip sends to the **currently-focused** pane's `wsRef` from `FocusedTerminalContext`, read live at send time — never a target snapshotted at open. A persistent surface that outlives many focus changes would, with a frozen target, silently send to a stale/closed pane. The wrong-pane risk is instead mitigated by an always-visible `→ {window}` target label, resolved in layers: window-store name by `server:windowId` (live — tracks renames) → the `windowName` the registrant carried into `FocusedTerminalContext` (board entries have a server-derived `windowName`; the store only covers servers whose sidebar group has delivered sessions, so board panes from other servers would otherwise label as `@N`) → raw windowId. With `focused === null` (e.g. the `/$server` tiles route) the strip renders **disabled** with a "no target" label and never sends.

**Send semantics — pointer-aware, shared with the chat send form.** The keydown routes through the shared pure `classifyComposeEnter` (`lib/compose-keys.ts`) fed the live `useCoarsePointer()` value (`hooks/use-coarse-pointer.ts`) — the SAME hook + classifier the chat send form uses, so the two surfaces cannot diverge (divergence is a defect; see [chat](/run-kit/chat.md) § Send-form input box and § Design Decisions → Pointer-aware Enter). The `send(submit: boolean)` callback delivers `ws.send(submit ? text + "\r" : text)` over the focused terminal's `wsRef`, guarded on `wsRef.readyState === WebSocket.OPEN`:
- **Fine pointer**: Enter = submit (`text + "\r"`), Shift+Enter = newline (unchanged).
- **Coarse pointer (touch)**: Enter = newline (NOT intercepted — the textarea default; the Send button submits).
- **Cmd/Ctrl+Enter = submit ALWAYS**, all devices (the escape hatch for a hardware keyboard on a touch device).
- **Alt+Enter = insert-without-submit ALWAYS** — `ws.send(text)` with **NO trailing `\r`** (the trailing `\r` IS the Enter press, so omitting it stages the raw text bytes in the pane's input box without submitting). Precedence: non-Enter/IME-composing → default; meta/ctrl → submit; alt → insert; shift → default; coarse → default; else → submit.

Enter is guarded against IME composition (`e.nativeEvent.isComposing`); empty/whitespace-only is a no-op (bare Enter for TUI y/n prompts stays a terminal tap). Insert uses the SAME delivery guards (open WS, non-empty text) and the SAME clear-on-delivery as submit. After a **delivered** send (submit or insert) the textarea + attachments clear and the strip stays open. A **guard-blocked** send (stream not open) early-returns WITHOUT clearing — the draft is preserved. The multiline raw-bytes caveat (an embedded `\n` sent as raw bytes executes per line on a plain shell pane; Claude Code treats it as a newline insert) is documented in a code comment, not guarded — insert-only is only truly Enter-free for single-line text on non-TUI panes.

**Insert button + truthful `enterkeyhint`** (260719-mxvw). A secondary **Insert** house-chip (border-styled, `data-testid="compose-strip-insert"`, `preventFocusSteal`, disabled exactly when Send is, `coarse:min-h-[36px]`, `title` documenting the Alt+Enter chord) renders left of Send — touch users have no Alt modifier, and Constitution V's keyboard reach is met by the Alt+Enter chord. The new chords are NOT registered in the command palette (focused-textarea editing chords like the unregistered Shift+Enter; the palette steals focus from the textarea it would act on). The textarea's `enterKeyHint` tracks what Enter actually does — `"send"` on fine pointer, `"enter"` on coarse — from the same live `useCoarsePointer()` value, so a mid-session pointer-capability change updates the keydown policy and the keyboard hint together.

**Draft survives everything.** Because the mount is conditional (toggle-off unmounts it) AND per-route (the AppShell and BoardPage footers are distinct React subtrees), draft text + pending attachments live in a **module store** (`lib/compose-draft-store.ts`) read via `useSyncExternalStore(subscribeComposeDraft, getComposeDraft)` — the same module-slot + listener-set + stable-snapshot pattern as the window-switch pending mask (`window-transition.ts`). Any mounted strip instance reads the same live draft, so an unsent draft survives toggle-off/on and terminal↔board route changes. Blob-URL previews are the one piece of state kept component-local (a fresh per-mount ref, revoked on unmount, recreated lazily from the retained `File` objects on remount).

**Focus routing.** The strip NEVER steals focus (mount / toggle / after-send) — the user chooses where to type. Escape in the textarea blurs it back to the terminal (never closes the strip). `preventFocusSteal` (`onMouseDown` preventDefault) is on the Send/📎 buttons. On touch devices the ⌨ keyboard button focuses the strip's real textarea when the preference is on, via the **focus registry** in `lib/compose-strip-events.ts` (`registerComposeStripFocuser`/`focusComposeStrip` — a module registry, not a `document.querySelector('[data-testid]')`, since test ids are test-only here; the focuser returns `false` in the disabled "no target" case so `bottom-bar.tsx` falls back to `onFocusTerminal`).

**Uploads — eager, worktree-scoped, re-homed on focus change.** The strip calls `useFileUpload(focused.session, focused.windowId, focused.server)` scoped to the **live** focused target, so uploads land in that window's worktree `.uploads/` (backend `upload.go` unchanged — see § File Upload). Retained `File` objects back both previews and re-homing: when the focused target changes while attachments are pending, the held files are re-uploaded to the new worktree and the textarea path lines are rewritten (`lines.indexOf(oldPath)` splice). Re-home failure keeps the original path lines and surfaces a non-blocking inline `role="alert"` error; sending is not blocked (orphaned files in the old worktree are acceptable). Terminal drag-drop / clipboard-paste gestures (`terminal-client.tsx`) hand raw files to the strip via a document `CustomEvent` bridge (`COMPOSE_STRIP_ATTACH_EVENT` + a module hand-off queue in `compose-strip-events.ts`, drained on both the event and mount), enabling the preference first if off — no prop-drilling of upload results.

**Board-pane focus cleanup.** `BoardPane` registers itself as the focused terminal while `isFocused`, and clears `FocusedTerminalContext` on **unmount** iff it is still the registered pane (`focusedRef.current?.wsRef === wsRef`, unmount-only `[]` deps, ref-guarded so a sibling's newer registration during a focus cycle is not clobbered). Without it, leaving a board for `/$server` would strand a stale non-null target — the enabled strip would render active with a stale label and upload into the stale worktree. With it, the strip reverts to the disabled "no target" state.

### File Upload

Entry points, all on the terminal page:
- **Clipboard paste** (`Cmd+V` / `Ctrl+V`) — document-level paste listener; files in `clipboardData.files` trigger upload, text-only paste passes through to xterm
- **Drag-and-drop** — drop files onto the terminal area; `ring-2 ring-accent` border highlight during drag-over; non-file drag content ignored
- **Compose strip upload button** (📎) — in the docked compose strip action row, left of Send; opens native file picker via hidden `<input type="file">`

The paste/drop gestures live in `terminal-client.tsx` and hand raw files to the docked compose strip (enabling the `composeStripEnabled` preference first if off) via the `COMPOSE_STRIP_ATTACH_EVENT` document bridge; the strip uploads them to the **focused** target's worktree and inserts one path per line in its textarea (see § Docked Compose Strip). Server writes to `.uploads/{YYMMDD-HHmmss}-{sanitized-name}` in the target window's worktree. 50MB size limit. `.uploads/` auto-added to `.gitignore` on first use.

### iOS Keyboard Support

`useVisualViewport` hook (`app/frontend/src/hooks/use-visual-viewport.ts`) manages all viewport-related CSS side effects: adds the `fullbleed` class to `<html>` on mount (removed on cleanup), and listens to both `resize` and `scroll` events on `window.visualViewport`, setting `--app-height` (and `--app-offset-top`) CSS custom properties from `visualViewport.height`. The `scroll` listener catches iOS Safari viewport panning that doesn't trigger `resize`. **The hook is called once in `RootWrapper`** so the `--app-height` var is maintained on EVERY route — including the Host page and edge pages that mount no `Shell` — and owning the single idempotent effect at the root avoids the double-mount cleanup race a second copy in `Shell` would create. (`260707-4vq2`)

In fullbleed mode, `globals.css` pins the **`.app-root` root layout container** (`position: fixed; inset: 0; height: var(--app-height, 100vh)`) to the visual viewport regardless of document scroll — the pin lives on `.app-root` (not the per-route `.app-shell` beneath it) because the persistent TopBar lives inside `.app-root` above the content region, so pinning that container keeps the header above the content. The per-route `.app-shell` is `position: relative; height: 100%` — it fills the root layout's `flex-1` region (its `overflow: hidden` contains xterm's canvas). (`260707-4vq2`) When the iOS keyboard appears, the bottom bar stays pinned above it, the terminal shrinks, and xterm refits via the existing `ResizeObserver`. The `fullbleed` class is also present in `index.html` as a static default (FOUC prevention); the hook takes over lifecycle management at runtime.

**Keyboard toggle** (`⌨` U+2328): Right-aligned button in the bottom bar, visible only on touch devices (`hidden coarse:inline-flex`). Bidirectional toggle: when terminal is focused (detected via `document.activeElement.closest(".xterm")`), tapping blurs to dismiss the keyboard; when not focused, tapping calls `onFocusTerminal` callback which chains through `app.tsx` → `TerminalClient.focusRef` → `xtermRef.current.focus()` to summon the keyboard. Dynamic `aria-label`: "Hide keyboard" / "Show keyboard". Uses `preventFocusSteal` to avoid stealing focus on the dismiss path.

**Scroll-lock mode**: Long-press (>= 500ms) on the keyboard toggle button activates scroll-lock — a mode that prevents the soft keyboard from appearing when the terminal area is tapped, allowing uninterrupted reading and scrolling. State is a `scrollLocked` boolean in `BottomBar` (default `false`), exposed to the parent via `onScrollLockChange` callback and passed down to `TerminalClient` as a `scrollLocked` prop. When locked, a capture-phase `focusin` listener on the terminal container immediately blurs any `.xterm` element that gains focus, preventing the keyboard from appearing. Touch scroll gestures (SGR mouse sequences) are unaffected — only focus is prevented. Activating scroll-lock while the keyboard is visible auto-dismisses it (`document.activeElement?.blur()`). Optional haptic feedback via `navigator.vibrate?.(50)` on toggle (graceful no-op if unavailable).

- **Long-press detection**: `touchstart`/`touchend`/`touchmove` handlers with a 500ms timer (`LONG_PRESS_MS` constant). Touch move > 10px (`LONG_PRESS_MOVE_THRESHOLD`) cancels the long-press. On timer expiry, scroll-lock toggles and subsequent `touchend`/`click` are suppressed via a ref flag. Desktop click behavior is unaffected (touch events only).
- **Tap in locked mode**: Tapping the keyboard button (< 500ms) when `scrollLocked` is `true` unlocks AND summons the keyboard in one action — matches user intent without requiring a double-tap.
- **Visual indicator**: When locked, the button shows `bg-accent/20 border-accent text-accent` (same armed-state pattern as Ctrl/Alt modifier toggles) and the icon changes from `⌨` (U+2328) to `🔒` (U+1F512). `aria-label` updates to "Scroll lock on — tap to unlock".
- **State lifecycle**: Session-scoped (component-local React state, not persisted). Resets on navigation (component unmount/remount). The docked compose strip is unaffected — it has its own input field outside the terminal container.

### Terminal Touch Scroll

The terminal container div has `touch-pan-y` (CSS `touch-action: pan-y`) — allows vertical swipe gestures for scrollback access on mobile/touch devices while blocking horizontal panning (prevents page-level overflow from tmux's ~80 column minimum). The xterm.js `.xterm-viewport` has `overflow-y: scroll` and `overscroll-behavior: none` (in `globals.css`), so the browser delegates vertical touch scroll to xterm natively without page bounce. In the single-view model, fullbleed is always active — `overflow: hidden` and `overscroll-behavior: none` are applied to both `html` and `body` (via `globals.css`), preventing iOS Safari elastic bounce scrolling. The docked compose strip and bottom bar are siblings of the terminal container, not children, so their touch behavior is preserved.

## Mobile Responsive

### Breakpoints & Container Width

All zones use `px-3 sm:px-6` — reduced horizontal padding on screens < 640px. No `max-w-4xl` constraint — terminal, top bar, and bottom bar all span full width. The mobile/desktop breakpoint for the `<Shell>` topology is **640px** (matches the existing `sm:` Tailwind breakpoint and `useIsMobile()` hook): `>= 640px` uses the 2-column grid with sidebar full-height; `< 640px` uses the single-column grid with sidebar overlay. Sidebar is drag-resizable on desktop (default 220px, min 160, max 400); terminal fills remaining space via the right grid column. Terminal container has `py-0.5 px-1` padding for breathing room against border lines. Bottom bar uses `py-1.5` vertical padding.

### Touch Targets

A custom Tailwind variant `coarse:` is defined in `globals.css` via `@custom-variant coarse (@media (pointer: coarse))`. On touch devices, interactive elements are upsized per surface — `coarse:` is the mechanism, not a universal size (there is no single 44px minimum; each surface documents its own target). Upsized elements include:
- FixedWidthToggle (`coarse:min-h-[36px] coarse:min-w-[28px]`)
- Sidebar session ✕ kill buttons + window rows
- Breadcrumb name dropdown triggers
- `⋯` command palette trigger
- Hamburger icon (sidebar toggle — single state covers desktop column collapse and mobile overlay) (`260509-17m3`)

Bottom bar buttons use the full `coarse:min-h-[36px] coarse:min-w-[36px]` touch target on touch devices, `min-h-[33px] min-w-[35px]` on fine pointers (with a 6px fine / 4px coarse row gap).

### Viewport Zoom Prevention

The viewport meta tag in `app/frontend/index.html` includes `maximum-scale=1.0` and `user-scalable=no` to prevent iOS Safari from auto-zooming when text inputs (command palette, docked compose strip) receive focus. Without these directives, iOS zooms in on inputs with `font-size < 16px`, displacing the entire interface. Pinch-to-zoom is also disabled — acceptable tradeoff for a keyboard-first tool dashboard where zoom doesn't improve terminal readability. The existing `interactive-widget=resizes-content` directive is preserved (controls keyboard layout resizing, unrelated to zoom).

### Terminal Addons

Addons loaded in `init()` from **static top-of-file imports**, after `terminal.open()`, before `ResizeObserver` setup. Order: FitAddon (existing) → fit() → ClipboardAddon → WebLinksAddon → UnicodeGraphemesAddon → WebglAddon. The Unicode addon MUST precede WebGL so the renderer measures cell widths against the active Unicode 15 table on first paint.

**Static import bundling**: all six xterm-family value imports (`@xterm/xterm` `Terminal`, `addon-fit`, `addon-clipboard`, `addon-web-links`, `addon-unicode-graphemes`, `addon-webgl`) are static top-of-file `import` statements in `terminal-client.tsx`, NOT runtime `await import()`. (`260531-m3pl`) Because `terminal-client.tsx` is already router-lazy, the xterm family bundles into the already-deferred terminal-route chunk and loads **once when that chunk loads** — never as a per-pane-mount runtime module-graph fetch. This removes all six chunk fetches from the browser's per-origin connection budget at terminal-init time, fixing the board-route E2E hang: on the plaintext dev/test origin (no HTTP/2 — only negotiated over TLS), the browser caps ~6 persistent connections per origin, and long-lived streams (Vite HMR socket, pooled SSE `EventSource`, one `/relay/<wid>` WS per visible pane) already saturate the slots, so a 7th xterm chunk fetch hung pending forever → `setTerminalReady(true)` never ran → blank pane → E2E poll timeout. Masked in production over Tailscale HTTPS (h2 multiplexes). The CSS side-effect import (`@xterm/xterm/css/xterm.css`) and type-only `import("@xterm/...")` annotations are static too.

| Addon | Purpose | Notes |
|-------|---------|-------|
| `@xterm/addon-fit` | Auto-resize columns/rows | Existing — loaded first, `fit()` called immediately |
| `@xterm/addon-clipboard` | OSC 52 clipboard sequences | Custom `ClipboardProvider` accepts both `""` (empty/default, tmux's format) and `"c"` (explicit) selection targets. Rejects `"p"`, `"s"`, `"0"`–`"7"`. Provider exported as `clipboardProvider` for testability |
| `@xterm/addon-web-links` | Clickable URLs in terminal output | |
| `@xterm/addon-unicode-graphemes` | Unicode 15 + grapheme-cluster width tables | Requires `allowProposedApi: true` on the Terminal constructor; `terminal.unicode.activeVersion = "15-graphemes"` set after `loadAddon()`. Must load before the WebGL addon |
| `@xterm/addon-webgl` | GPU-accelerated rendering | The `new WebglAddon()` / `loadAddon(...)` construction is wrapped in try/catch — silently falls back to canvas renderer on GPU/WebGL-context failure. The *module load* is static (resolved at chunk load, cannot fail at `init()` time), but context creation can still throw at runtime, so the runtime guard is required (`260531-m3pl`) |

### Terminal Font Size (user-controllable global preference)

Terminal font size is a **global** user preference owned by `ChromeContext`, not a per-pane or per-window value (`260613-oo89`). The context exposes the **effective** size as `terminalFontSize: number` (what `TerminalClient` reads and the top-bar control displays); the internal preference is stored as `number | null` (null = unset) and persisted to `localStorage["runkit-terminal-font-size"]`. Effective = preference ?? device default — 11px mobile / 13px desktop via the shared `isMobileViewport()` rule (narrow-width OR coarse-pointer, NOT a CSS media query). Bounds 8–24px, step 1, exported as `TERMINAL_FONT_BOUNDS` (`{ min: 8, max: 24, step: 1 }`); all stored values clamped into `[8, 24]` on read. Helpers `clampTerminalFont`/`deviceDefaultFontSize`/`readTerminalFontSize` mirror the `fixedWidth`/`SIDEBAR_WIDTH_BOUNDS` shape.

**Mutators** (`ChromeDispatch`): `increaseTerminalFont` / `decreaseTerminalFont` step `effective ± step`, clamp, persist (try/catch noop); `resetTerminalFont` = **forget preference** (`localStorage.removeItem` → preference back to `null` → effective reverts to the device default), NOT a fixed value. First step from the unset (`null`) state operates on the device default and persists a concrete adjacent value (desktop 13 → 14).

**Applied to xterm** (`terminal-client.tsx`): `terminalFontSize` is passed as the `fontSize` option on construction (and to the `document.fonts.load` preloads); an effect keyed on it sets `term.options.fontSize = N` + calls `fitAddonRef.current?.fit()` on change (guarded against an uninitialized terminal). `fit()` recomputes rows×cols and **resizes the PTY** (the correct xterm resize path — reflows running TUIs, not a bitmap-scaled canvas). Because the value is global, **every** live `TerminalClient` reacts on change — including all mounted board-route panes. The mobile touch-scroll `LINE_HEIGHT` fallback reads `options.fontSize` live, so it tracks runtime changes.

**Control surfaces**: (1) a top-bar combo button `[−] {size} [+]` + reset (see § FixedWidthToggle), and (2) three command-palette actions — `terminal-font-increase` ("Increase terminal font"), `terminal-font-decrease` ("Decrease terminal font"), `terminal-font-reset` ("Reset terminal font"), no `shortcut`, wired to the dispatch fns. The palette actions are present on **both** the AppShell palette (`app.tsx`) and the board-route palette (`board-page.tsx`) — the setting is global and Constitution V requires the palette reachable on every route. This is the same dual-mount duplication `refresh-page` follows (§ Command Palette View actions).

**Deliberate non-decision**: `Cmd +/-` is **NOT** intercepted — browser-native whole-page zoom is retained (no global keybinding registered), avoiding the brittleness of hijacking `Cmd +/-` / `Cmd 0`.

### Terminal Font Bundling

The frontend bundles JetBrainsMono Nerd Font (patched single-file variant) as a webfont so terminal rendering is deterministic across all viewers, independent of which monospace fonts the browser happens to have installed. Without bundling, per-glyph font fallback for Nerd Font private-use-area codepoints produces visible baseline wobble within a single terminal row.

**Asset layout**: Three `.woff2` weights served from `/fonts/` — `JetBrainsMonoNerdFont-Regular.woff2` (400 normal), `-Bold.woff2` (700 normal), `-Italic.woff2` (400 italic). All three `@font-face` rules in `app/frontend/src/globals.css` expose the same `font-family: "JetBrainsMono Nerd Font"` name and MUST declare `font-display: block`. `swap` or `fallback` would let xterm measure cells against system-font metrics that persist as misalignment — xterm measures the character cell grid exactly once at `terminal.open()` and does not re-measure when a deferred font arrives. `index.html` includes a `<link rel="preload" as="font" type="font/woff2" crossorigin href="/fonts/JetBrainsMonoNerdFont-Regular.woff2" />` to overlap the Regular download with JS parsing (only Regular is preloaded — Bold/Italic are a smaller fraction of the initial paint and don't justify the extra critical-path bytes).

**Load convention before `terminal.open()`**: The init routine in `app/frontend/src/components/terminal-client.tsx` awaits a concurrent `Promise.all([document.fonts.load(...), document.fonts.load(...), document.fonts.load(...)])` for all three weights at the exact `fontPx` (`isMobile ? 11 : 13`) the Terminal will use, BEFORE `new Terminal(...)` / `terminal.open()` / `fitAddon.fit()`. Three explicit `document.fonts.load(size, family)` calls (not `document.fonts.ready`) scope the await to exactly the weights xterm will request. A fresh `if (cancelled || !terminalRef.current) return;` guard MUST follow the await. With all six xterm imports static, this font-load `await Promise.all([...])` is the **only** async boundary in `init()`, so it is the sole place a post-await unmount guard is required before `new Terminal(...)`; one post-construction dispose guard sits before `setTerminalReady(true)`. (`260531-m3pl`)

**Primary `fontFamily`**: `'"JetBrainsMono Nerd Font", ui-monospace, monospace'` — bundled webfont first, `ui-monospace` as the system-default monospace, generic `monospace` as final guard against total load failure. The older long tail (`JetBrains Mono`, `Fira Code`, `SF Mono`, `Menlo`, `Monaco`, `Consolas`) is dead code once `font-display: block` plus a successful load makes the webfont always win; do not reintroduce it. Non-terminal monospace surfaces pick up the same font automatically via Tailwind's `--font-mono` custom property (webfont-first). (`260417-hyrl`)

**Test caveat**: jsdom does not implement the FontFaceSet API. `src/test-setup.ts` stubs a minimal `document.fonts.load()` / `document.fonts.ready` surface (same pattern as the existing `ResizeObserver` stub) so unit tests that mount `TerminalClient` do not hang on the await.

### Terminal Unicode Width Handling

xterm.js defaults to Unicode 6 width tables, which classify many modern glyphs (most emojis, several Misc Symbols codepoints) as 1 cell. Modern tmux lays out its buffer using wcwidth with a newer Unicode table (typically 14/15), treating the same glyphs as 2 cells. Without alignment, subsequent characters in a row drift between tmux's intended column and xterm's rendered column, producing visible ghost/overlap artifacts — especially with the WebGL renderer.

**Resolution** (`app/frontend/src/components/terminal-client.tsx`):
1. Construct the Terminal with `allowProposedApi: true` — required to access `terminal.unicode` (a proposed-API surface in xterm v6).
2. After `terminal.open()`, `loadAddon(new UnicodeGraphemesAddon())` (statically imported) and set `terminal.unicode.activeVersion = "15-graphemes"`.
3. Load order MUST precede the WebGL addon so the renderer initialises against the Unicode 15 table on first measure.

The `addon-unicode-graphemes` package (v6-era) covers Unicode 15 and grapheme clusters (ZWJ sequences, flag emoji, skin-tone modifiers). The `unicodeVersion` Terminal constructor option is a no-op past `"6"` without the addon — the addon is what registers the newer width table. (`260418-xgl2`)

### Command Palette Mobile Trigger

The `CommandPalette` component listens for a `palette:open` CustomEvent on `document` (in addition to `⌘K`). The `⋯` button in Line 1 dispatches this event on mobile. This is the mobile equivalent of `⌘K` — physical keyboards aren't available on phones.

### Keyboard-Navigable List Scroll Pattern

Both `CommandPalette` and `ThemeSelector` use the same scroll-into-view pattern for arrow key navigation: a `listRef` on the listbox container plus a `useEffect` on `[selectedIndex, open]` that queries `[aria-selected="true"]` and calls `scrollIntoView({ block: "nearest" })`. This ensures the selected item stays visible when navigating past the `max-h-64` scroll boundary. New keyboard-navigable list components SHOULD follow this pattern.

The sidebar session/window tree is a **third consumer** (see § Sidebar → Keyboard Navigation & Tree ARIA): a `treeRef` on the `role="tree"` container plus a `useEffect` on `[rovingKey]` that resolves the roving row (`[data-window-id]`/`[data-session-row]`) and calls `scrollIntoView({ block: "nearest" })` + `focus()`. It reuses the scroll-into-view half but deliberately diverges from the `selectedIndex` numeric-state model — the roving cursor is a row-key STRING (robust to the variable-length tree's expand/collapse and SSE row churn, where a numeric index can desync); the focus call is gated by `focusMovedRef` so passive SSE re-renders never scroll/steal focus.

## Keyboard Shortcuts

### Global
| Key | Action | Context |
|-----|--------|---------|
| `Cmd+K` | Open command palette | Always |
| `Cmd+.` / `Ctrl+.` (`260714-t97o`) | Cycle the current window's view lenses (over `availableViews`, e.g. `tty→web→tty` or `tty→chat→tty`) | Terminal route — a window-level `keydown` in `app.tsx` that `preventDefault()`s so xterm doesn't also receive it, gated by `shouldSuppressViewChord` (the same non-xterm-input rule as `⌘\`). No-op when < 2 views. Documented in the Keyboard Shortcuts dialog (App section) + the `View:` palette entries. See § Window Views (Lens Model) |
| `Cmd+C` / `Ctrl+C` | Copy selection to clipboard (with selection) or send SIGINT (without selection) | Terminal focused — via `attachCustomKeyEventHandler`, `keydown` only. Uses `navigator.clipboard.writeText()` with `document.execCommand('copy')` fallback for non-secure contexts (HTTP). Selection cleared after copy via `.finally()` |
| ``Ctrl+` `` | Toggle tty↔chat view | Terminal route with a `chatProvider` window — plain Ctrl on BOTH platforms (NOT Cmd; Cmd+` is macOS window cycling). Document-level `keydown` capture (`use-chat-view-shortcut.ts`, speaks the unified `ViewName` — toggles via `switchView` between `chat` and `tty`) that fires EVEN while xterm owns focus (modeled on `useSidebarKeyboardToggle` minus its xterm-focus suppression); bails on a real INPUT/TEXTAREA/contentEditable target that is not inside `.xterm`. Enabled iff `currentViews.includes("chat")` (a chat-less window ⇒ no-op). See § Window Views (Lens Model) → shortcuts / § Chat View (`260714-r7rq`) |

No single-key shortcuts (`j`/`k`/`c`/`r`) or `Esc Esc` — these conflicted with xterm.js terminal input. All actions are accessible via `Cmd+K` command palette or top bar buttons.

Command palette actions include: create/rename/kill session, create/rename/kill window, move up/down for the current server/session/window (`260705-bpnr` — see § Command Palette Move up/down), theme switching, "Reload tmux config" (targets the active server via `?server=` param), "Create tmux server" (opens name dialog, creates session "0" in $HOME), "Kill tmux server" (confirmation dialog, kills active server, switches to next available — the dialog carries a daemon-specific warning when the target is `rk-daemon`; see § Infra-server de-emphasis → kill guard), "Switch tmux server: {name}" (one entry per available server, current marked), "Keyboard Shortcuts" (opens modal showing curated tmux keybindings from `GET /api/keybindings` + hardcoded `Cmd+K`), "Copy: tmux Commands" (opens tmux commands dialog — only visible on terminal route when `currentWindow` is available), "Notifications: Enable push" / "Notifications: Enabled ✓" (the Web Push opt-in gesture — terminal-themed label, NOT a bell; see § Notifications (Web Push opt-in)), and terminal navigation (jump to any session/window).

**Session/window creation actions in the palette**:
| Action ID | Label | Behavior |
|-----------|-------|----------|
| `create-session` | "Session: Create" | Instant creation — no dialog (see Instant Session Creation) |
| `create-session-at-folder` | "Session: Create at Folder" | Opens `CreateSessionDialog` pre-filled with `currentWindow.worktreePath`; empty if no active window |
| `create-window` | "Window: Create" | Instant window creation — the sidebar `+ New Window` path. Creates an **unnamed** window (`createWindow` called with no name), so tmux auto-names it to the active window's folder basename; the optimistic ghost is labeled with the **raw** cwd basename (see § Unnamed `+ New Window`) (`260707-j66b`) |
| `create-window-at-folder` | "Window: Create at Folder" | Opens `CreateSessionDialog` in `mode="window"` (dialog title changes, session name input hidden, confirms via `createWindow(server, session, undefined, cwd)` — no name, so tmux auto-names to the folder basename); only shown when a session is active (`260707-j66b`) |
| `create-iframe-window` | "Window: New Iframe Window" | Opens dialog with name + URL inputs; creates iframe window via `createWindow(server, session, name, undefined, "iframe", url)`; only shown when a session is active. `@rk_type=iframe` seeds "default view = web" (§ Window Views (Lens Model)) (`260714-t97o`) |

**Window rename action**: the `rename-window` action ("Window: Rename") dispatches a `window-heading:rename` `CustomEvent` (guarded on `currentWindow`), which the centered top-bar `WindowHeading` listens for and enters inline edit (mirrors `theme-selector:open`), rather than opening a modal dialog. The action stays registered (Constitution V keyboard path); there is no window rename `<Dialog>` (the SESSION rename dialog is separate). See § Window Heading. (`260703-5ilm`)

**Window move actions**: "Window: Move up" (id `window-move-up`) and "Window: Move down" (id `window-move-down`) in the `windowActions` group — the sole window-move pair, matching the up/down vocabulary of the Session / Server / Board move actions (windows render as vertical sidebar rows). Only shown when `currentWindow` exists. "Move up" excluded when the current window is at the minimum index in the session; "Move down" excluded when at the maximum index (boundary exclusion, not disabled state). On select, calls `moveWindow(server, currentWindow.windowId, targetIndex)` (source by stable window ID, destination by position) then navigates to the **same** `currentWindow.windowId` with `search: (prev) => prev` — the window keeps its ID across the reorder (only its index changes) and the current view is preserved (`260714-r7rq`), so the user stays on their window and view after the swap. The target index is computed via the shared pure helper `computeWindowMoveTarget(index, delta, minIndex, maxIndex)` (returns `null` at a boundary — no wraparound). (`260705-bpnr`, `260719-p8pv-window-move-palette-consolidation`)

**Command Palette Move up/down (server / session / window)**: a keyboard/touch reorder path parallel to the two drag surfaces, giving all THREE hierarchy levels a keyboard-reachable reorder (Constitution V). Six `PaletteAction`s, each acting on the **current** route-context entity (the `Server: Kill` current-entity semantics), grouped with their existing families in `app.tsx`, all with boundary = **hidden** (the entry is filtered out at the top/bottom of its list — no wraparound, no disabled state): (`260705-bpnr`)

- **`Server: Move up` / `Server: Move down`** (`server-move-up`/`-down`, `serverActions`) — move the current server one position within the REGULAR class (infra excluded). The new full regular-class order is computed and POSTed via `setServerOrder` (server-global `event: server-order` echo re-sorts every client). Hidden when the current server is infra (`currentRegularIdx === -1`) or at a class boundary.
- **`Session: Move up` / `Session: Move down`** (`session-move-up`/`-down`, `sessionActions`) — move the current session one position in the **effective** session order (`deriveEffectiveSessionOrder(liveNames, sseOrder)` — persisted `@rk_session_order` filtered to live names, un-ordered live sessions appended in natural order; the sidebar's transient drag override is component-local and NOT visible to the palette). Persisted via the EXISTING `setSessionOrder(server, order)` — the same primitive the sidebar session drag uses; no new backend.
- **`Window: Move up` / `Window: Move down`** (`window-move-up`/`-down`, `windowActions`) — move the current window ±1 index via `moveWindow(server, windowId, targetIndex)`, then navigate to the same stable window ID with `search: (prev) => prev` (view-preserving). The sole window-move pair. See § Window move actions above.

**`Board: Move up` / `Board: Move down`** (`board-move-up`/`-down`) — the same boundary-hidden / no-wraparound keyboard+touch path for the board list, mounted in `board-page.tsx`'s `boardRouteActions` (NOT `app.tsx`), because the board route does not render AppShell and "current board" only has meaning on a `/board/$name` route (the board owns its own palette). Each acts on the CURRENT board (the `/board/$name` param), computes the full new order via `computeMoveOrder(boardNames, currentBoardIdx, delta)` over the backend-sorted `boards`, and POSTs it via `setBoardOrder` (server-global `event: board-order` echo re-sorts every client — see § Board-list drag reorder). Hidden when the current board is first (`currentBoardIdx === 0` → only Move down) or last (only Move up); a `null` from `computeMoveOrder` is a defensive no-op. `onError` surfaces `useToast().addToast`. (`260708-a2qd`)

**Pure order-computation helpers** — the boundary gating, effective-order derivation, and swap arithmetic are extracted into `app/frontend/src/lib/palette-move.ts` (Vitest-covered `palette-move.test.ts`) so they are testable without mounting the shell; the palette action bodies are thin wrappers that call these then invoke the client mutation.
