```ts
type RenamedEntry = { type: "session"; identifier: string; newName: string; server: string };
```

API surface (session-level entries take `server` first; server-level entries are global):

| Method | Signature | Notes |
|--------|-----------|-------|
| `addGhostSession` | `(server, name) => optimisticId` | Session ghost |
| `addGhostServer` | `(name) => optimisticId` | Server ghost — global, no `server` arg |
| `markKilled("session", server, name)` | overload | Session kill |
| `markKilled("server", name)` | overload | Server kill — global |
| `unmarkKilled("session", server, name)` | overload | Mirror of `markKilled` |
| `unmarkKilled("server", name)` | overload | Mirror of `markKilled` |
| `markRenamed("session", server, name, newName)` | required `server` | |
| `unmarkRenamed(server, name)` | required `server` | |
| `useMergedSessions(real, currentServer)` | filter | Drops session-level overlays whose `server !== currentServer` |

`useMergedSessions` filters ghosts/kills/renames by `currentServer` before applying them. SSE reconciliation only inspects ghosts whose `server === currentServer` so the other server's pending state is left intact when the user switches servers and back.

**Window-store entries are NOT keyed by server** — windows cannot migrate across tmux servers (`MoveWindowToSession` operates within a single server, and there is no cross-server move API). The `windowId` (tmux `@N`) is unique per server, and `setWindowsForSession` is only ever called with data for the active server. Adding `server` to the window-store key would be defensive bookkeeping with no failure mode to defend against.

#### Why this convention exists

The convention exists to prevent an ambient-state retargeting bug: holding `server` in a module-level closure (`_getServer`) wired to `serverRef.current` dereferences live state at fetch time, so any switch between user intent and fetch dispatch silently retargets the request — most commonly via Cmd+K's near-instant server switcher between opening a rename dialog and pressing Enter. The optimistic overlay makes such a bug invisible until SSE reconciles (~2–5 s later), manifesting as random renames/kills landing on the wrong server with a flicker on rollback.

#### General rule: don't introduce ambient state for request parameters

Any value that scopes an HTTP request to a particular backend resource (server, project, account, tenant) MUST be passed as an explicit argument to the API call, captured at user-event time. Module-level mutable getters, refs read at fetch time, or context reads inside the action callback (rather than the handler) all create the same closure-race shape that this change retired. If a value travels with a mutation, it travels in the call signature — period.

The regression test in `app/frontend/src/hooks/use-dialog-state.test.tsx` flips `SessionProvider`'s `server` prop between `openRenameSessionDialog("foo")` and `handleRenameSession()` and asserts the API call uses the post-flip server (`server-B`), proving the capture point is the handler invocation, not the dialog open.


## Design Decisions

### Sessions-pane scope is explicit state, not the SERVER panel's expansion
**Decision**: The sessions-pane scope (`all | current`) is its own persisted state (`runkit-panel-sessions-scope`), read via `useSessionsScope`, with no migration from the old `runkit-panel-server` coupling; the SERVER panel defaults open and its expansion no longer affects the session list.
**Why**: "do I want to see server tiles?" and "which servers' sessions do I want listed?" are unrelated concerns that previously shared one bit — so the SERVER panel couldn't default open without permanently filtering the list, and users couldn't filter the list without paying the tile grid's vertical cost. `runkit-panel-server` encodes panel visibility, not scope intent, so carrying it over would guess wrong as often as right.
**Rejected**: Migrating the old key (encodes the wrong intent); keeping the "Select a server above…" hint with reworded text for the no-current-server case (chose fallback-to-all instead — never a dead-end).
*Introduced by*: 260720-rzg7-sessions-scope-toggle-delink

### Scope state uses a generic enum-typed localStorage hook
**Decision**: Add `useLocalStorageEnum<T extends string>` as a generic sibling of `useLocalStorageBoolean` (same pub/sub + `storage`-event mechanics, unrecognized values → default), plus a thin `useSessionsScope()` wrapper exporting the `SessionsScope` type and key constant.
**Why**: The chip, session list, and palette entry are cross-component siblings needing one reactive source; a generic hook mirrors the established boolean sibling and keeps the scope vocabulary in one importable home.
**Rejected**: Encoding scope as a boolean in the existing hook (values are semantically `all|current`, not true/false); duplicating the pub/sub logic in a scope-specific hook (needless divergence from the boolean sibling).
*Introduced by*: 260720-rzg7-sessions-scope-toggle-delink

### Route guard keys on `serversLoaded`, not `servers.length > 0`
**Decision**: `resolveServerView`'s not-found branch gates on the explicit `serversLoaded` flag, never the `servers.length > 0` proxy.
**Why**: with pre-existing servers the length proxy is already truthy while the list is stale, so the guard fired not-found immediately for a just-created server before the post-create refresh landed. The explicit flag distinguishes "list has loaded" from "list is non-empty".
**Rejected**: `servers.length > 0` as a loaded-proxy — the root-cause bug of the create-server not-found race.
*Introduced by*: 260602-3i5d-fix-create-server-not-found-race

### No bounded-fallback timer on the waiting state
**Decision**: the create-server waiting state persists until the refreshed `servers` list contains the server — cleared by an event-driven effect on the list changing, with no timer and no polling.
**Why**: synchronous near-instant backend create makes a timer speculative; a polling loop would violate the no-client-polling anti-pattern.
**Rejected**: a ~5s bounded-fallback timeout for v1. If ever added it MUST be a single `setTimeout`, never a polling loop.
*Introduced by*: 260602-3i5d-fix-create-server-not-found-race

### Pending-switch identity is `{server, @N}`, never the session name
**Decision**: `PendingSwitchTarget` keys click-intent/URL-match on `{server, windowId}` — excluding the session name, including the server.
**Why**: excluding the session name lets the selection survive a session rename or a cross-session move where `@N` survives but the session name changed (a session-name match would flip false and release pending-click suppression early, bouncing the selection). Including the server is load-bearing because tmux `@N` ids are unique only per server and `AppShell` persists across `$server` route changes without remounting — window-id-alone matching false-positives on a cross-server id collision (serverA `@5` vs serverB `@5`), which would suppress serverB's alignment and let serverA's failure bounce yank the user cross-server with a false toast.
**Rejected**: `{session, windowId}` matching (bounced the selection on rename/move); window-id-alone matching (cross-server collision).
*Introduced by*: 260529-jad6-window-api-stability, 260715-38kg-window-switch-confirmed-motion

### Fresh-switch mask teardown is a bare `tearDownMask()` at the `beginPendingSwitch` seam
**Decision**: `beginPendingSwitch` proactively clears a leftover mask/grace timer with a bare `tearDownMask()` at the top of its callback — enforcing "a fresh switch owns ALL feedback" at the one seam every pending switch passes through.
**Why**: the animated path reaches `beginPendingSwitch` (via `beginWindowSwitchGate → startViewTransition → runSwitch`) with its OWN just-opened gate current; the bare primitive clears a leftover armed mask without settling that gate, so the earned slide survives. The one shared seam means a future gateless caller inherits the fix.
**Rejected**: `abandonSwitchFeedback()` here (settles the animated path's own current gate `"superseded"` → skips the earned slide, `260715-38kg` R8); per-call-site `tearDownMask()` at the two gateless callers (spreads the invariant across callers — a future gateless caller re-introduces the leftover-mask bug).
*Introduced by*: 260719-h0x4-window-switch-stale-mask-teardown

### No `role="tooltip"` on the StatusDot hover-card
**Decision**: `StatusDotTip` advertises no `useRole({ role: "tooltip" })`.
**Why**: the W3C tooltip pattern requires a tooltip to contain NO interactive content, but this card holds real `<a>` links (PR + docs). Advertising `role="tooltip"` would lie to AT and wire a misleading `aria-describedby`.
**Rejected**: `role="tooltip"` (present in the plan, removed in review).
*Introduced by*: 260616-37ub-status-dot-tooltip

### Heading identifies the window, not the lens
**Decision**: the terminal-route center heading is a static `Window: <window>` in every lens (tty/web/chat); the active lens is shown by the `ViewSwitcher`, not the heading.
**Why**: the heading identifies the WINDOW (the substrate), per window-views.md "rows are substrates, views are lenses". Keeping the prefix constant also stops the name's anchor from jumping on a lens switch (the prefix width no longer changes with the lens).
**Rejected**: "the center page heading follows the lens" (window-views.md R4's original sentence — reversed in-spec within the change).
*Introduced by*: 260714-uco1-topbar-heading-anchor-nav

### Board pane focus tracks by key, not index
**Decision**: board pane focus is tracked by the focused pane's `server:windowId` key (`focusedKeyRef`); `focusedIndex` is reconciled from the key on every order change, and the palette `moveFocusedPane` does not bump `focusedIndex` itself.
**Why**: with `paneRefs` keyed to the authoritative order, bumping `focusedIndex` (`setFocusedIndex(i±1)`) before the SSE echo routed the imperative xterm `.focus()` into the displaced neighbour's terminal (wrong-terminal keystrokes). Key-follow reconcile keeps the focused pane's identity across own moves, own drop echoes, and remote reorders.
**Rejected**: index-follow (index bump alone) — misrouted focus before the order settled.
*Introduced by*: 260708-rmiq-board-pane-reorder

### Board imperative pane focus is gated on a true user-intent flag, not index change
**Decision**: the board's imperative `paneRefs[focusedIndex].focus()` is gated on `shouldFocusPane(intent, prev, current)` = `intent && prev !== current`, where `intent` is a `focusIntentRef` boolean set only by user-driven focus actions (keyboard cycle, palette cycle, different-pane click) and by own-move initiation through the single `reorderWithFollow` seam — never by a passive `board-changed` refetch. Index change alone does not focus.
**Why**: gating on index change alone cannot distinguish an own-move follow (wanted) from a remote-driven index reconcile (a `board-changed` from another client whose reorder/pin/unpin shifts the focused pane's index) — the latter would steal DOM focus into an xterm while the user types elsewhere, violating the "SSE must not steal focus" invariant. A true intent flag, mirroring the sidebar `focusMovedRef` literally, is set at intent sites and consumed once by the focus effect; a remote reconcile bumps the index but never moves DOM focus. The own-move follow survives the async POST→SSE-echo window by setting the flag at move initiation.
**Rejected**: index-change gating (steals focus on remote reconciles); suppressing focus on ALL order-changed re-entries (breaks the own-move follow — R6 of the reorder change); debouncing/time-windowing SSE-adjacent focus (heuristic, racy, unprincipled when a true intent signal is available). Accepted residual: a one-echo-round-trip race where a remote event interleaving before an own echo consumes the flag early — a single benign own-pane focus-follow, not a steal.
*Introduced by*: 260719-6dh9-board-focus-intent-flag

### Pin-indicator navigation is a popover row, not the indicator click
**Decision**: navigating from a pinned sidebar window row to its owning board is a two-step gesture (pin indicator → popover → "Go to {board}" row).
**Why**: the pin indicator keeps its pin/unpin *management* role; putting navigation on a dedicated popover row avoids hijacking the indicator's click.
**Rejected**: making the indicator click navigate (would collide with its management role).
*Introduced by*: 260718-co9z-link-based-board-pinning

### Palette actions are duplicated across the two mounts
**Decision**: a globally-meaningful command-palette action is registered in BOTH `app.tsx`'s AppShell blocks and `board-page.tsx`'s `boardRouteActions` — intentional duplication, not a shared source.
**Why**: the app mounts two disjoint CommandPalettes (AppShell's + the board route's own), and the board route does not render AppShell, so an action must be in both to be reachable everywhere. The Host page (`/`) mounts no palette, so such actions are unreachable there — adding a Host-page palette mount would grow UI surface against constitution §IV.
**Rejected**: a single shared action source (the two palettes have disjoint mounts); a Host-page palette mount (constitution §IV surface growth).
*Introduced by*: 260713-4zap-update-notify-one-click-upgrade

### Single static `Update Now` — no dynamic version label
**Decision**: the palette has ONE update action, the static `run-kit: Update Now` (a full-roster force update in `buildMaintenanceActions`); the former qualifying-gated `run-kit: Update to v{X}` entry and its `updateActionLabel` label composition (the single-run-kit / single-sibling / N-tools label shapes) are deleted.
**Why**: the dynamic label was multi-tool ambiguous (the update is toolkit-scoped, not single-tool) and went stale between check passes. A static label always reads true; version detail lives where it is fresh — the check-result toasts (`composeCheckToast`) and the chip's `updateChipToolSummary`. `Update Now` reaching every tool (force = full-roster `shll update`) also picks up patch-only bumps a scoped match set would skip.
**Rejected**: keeping the dynamic `Update to v{X}` label (ambiguous + stale); a 2×2 check×update / minor×patch command matrix (the update axis has only one real action — brew installs the manifest latest regardless; the minor/patch distinction exists only on the check axis).
*Introduced by*: 260720-n2ai-shll-check-updates-delegation-palette-checks

### Notable-set is the single convergence key; sub-threshold verdicts ride alongside
**Decision**: the chip visibility, the composite dismissal `Key`, and the `/api/update` argv stay derived from the NOTABLE set only; the full per-tool verdict list (incl. sub-threshold `notable:false` rows) rides the `update-available` payload but never affects Key/qualification. `useUpdateNotification` filters `tools` to the notable subset (missing flag = notable) with stable referential identity.
**Why**: keeps the chip, dismissal semantics, `use-update-click` completion signal, and `/api/update` argv byte-compatible with the pre-delegation behavior — a patch-only finding is toast-only by design (it must never light or re-dirty the chip). The ambient/released payload still carries the full per-tool verdict list so a released incl.-patches view reads sub-threshold rows off one payload; the incl.-patches command itself queries the fresh github source as a side channel (`260720-wb3n`) that likewise never dirties the chip.
**Rejected**: keying the chip/dismissal on the full `update_available` set (would light + re-dirty the chip on patch bumps and churn dismissals).
*Introduced by*: 260720-n2ai-shll-check-updates-delegation-palette-checks

### Shared check-flow hook instead of per-mount duplication
**Decision**: the on-demand check POST→toast flow (result composition, gated Update Now action slot, error mapping) lives in ONE `useUpdateCheck` hook consumed by both palette mounts; only the `buildCheckActions` label/id builder is duplicated in (per the two-mounts convention).
**Why**: mirrors `use-update-click.ts`'s anti-drift extraction for the exact AppShell↔board duplication the two-palette-mounts pattern otherwise forces — two inline copies of the toast composition + error mapping would drift.
**Rejected**: duplicating the flow inline in `app.tsx` and `board-page.tsx` (two copies of toast/error logic drift).
*Introduced by*: 260720-n2ai-shll-check-updates-delegation-palette-checks

### Github-sourced toast suppresses the sub-threshold annotation
**Decision**: `composeCheckToast` takes the echoed report `source` (optional, default `""`) and drops the `(patch — below notify threshold)` annotation when `source === "github"`; the `updateAvailable`/`notable` filtering is untouched. The frontend keys off the ECHOED report source rather than an invented client boolean.
**Why**: the github backend has no notify policy, so every row decodes `notable=false` — annotating each as a sub-threshold patch would mislabel a real minor bump (`run-kit 3.8.7 → 3.9.1`). Echoing `report.Source` doubles as a defensive check (the client reacts to what actually ran); an old daemon that omits `source` defaults to `""` and keeps today's annotated behavior.
**Rejected**: a client-side `includePatches`-implies-github boolean (fragile — decouples the annotation from what the daemon actually queried); suppressing on `includePatches` alone (a released incl.-patches view SHOULD still annotate its genuine sub-threshold rows).
*Introduced by*: 260720-wb3n-github-source-patches-check

### Dismissed-pending shows the menu update surface, not the ⟳
**Decision**: the overflow menu version row's update-surface condition is `qualifies && (updateOverflowed || !showChip)` (via `asUpdateSurface = tools.length>0 && (updateOverflowed || (qualifies && !showChip))`) — so a dismissed pending update shows the update surface rather than the resting ⟳ check affordance — while the chevron **attention badge** keeps the narrower undismissed-overflowed condition (`updateOverflowed && tools.length>0`).
**Why**: the menu is deliberate discovery (like the palette, which already ignores chip dismissal via its `qualifies`-only gate), so surfacing a known pending verdict there does not violate "dismissal silences the ambient chip" — the badge, which IS ambient, stays silenced. When a verdict is already known the update surface is the stronger, truer affordance; offering "check again" over a known pending update is a blind-affordance smell.
**Rejected**: rendering the ⟳ when dismissed (offers a redundant re-check while a pending verdict already exists); lighting the badge for the dismissed case too (would re-introduce the ambient signal dismissal is meant to silence).
*Introduced by*: 260720-ml7k-unified-toolbar-update-button

### Check affordance is a non-menuitem control (menu stays open)
**Decision**: the resting version row's ⟳ "Check for updates" affordance is a plain button (no `role="menuitem"`, `tabIndex={-1}`) inside the row, so the container's role-keyed close handler does not fire on click.
**Why**: the in-flight spinner + single-flight state is only meaningful if the menu stays open across the ~1-2s check; the font-stepper precedent (`role="group"` row, plain buttons) established this pattern for non-terminal menu actions. Arrow-key nav still reaches it (the focusables selector matches `button:not([disabled])`).
**Rejected**: `role="menuitem"` with close-on-click (hides the busy state and makes single-flight moot); an intermediate "checking…" toast (already rejected in `260720-n2ai`).
*Introduced by*: 260720-ml7k-unified-toolbar-update-button

### TopBar mounts once at the root layout
**Decision**: `TopBar` mounts a single persistent instance at the pathless `app-layout` route, above the router `<Outlet>`, and re-renders in place across route changes; a `<Suspense fallback={null}>` boundary wraps ONLY the `<Outlet>` content region, not the header.
**Why**: mounting `TopBar` per-page unmounts one instance and mounts a fresh one on cross-page navigation — a visible navbar "reload"/flicker (a component-identity problem, not an MPA→SPA gap; the app is already an SPA). A single persistent mount keeps the bar continuously present with a per-route heading; scoping Suspense to the Outlet keeps the bar painted while a lazy page chunk loads.
**Rejected**: per-page `TopBar` mounts (three instances — AppShell, HostOverviewPage, BoardPage — caused the flicker); wrapping the header in the Suspense boundary (blanked the bar on lazy load); hosting the bar directly in `RootWrapper` (the index route `/` is a direct child of the root at the same pathname, so root→index is structurally shorter than root→serverLayout→…, and React remounted the root subtree on the index transition — the pathless layout normalizes tree depth).
*Introduced by*: 260707-4vq2-lift-topbar-root-layout

### Refresh is a full page reload
**Decision**: the top-bar RefreshButton does a full page reload (`window.location.reload()`; Shift+click force-reloads), not a targeted relay reconnect.
**Why**: the reload is non-destructive by design (all client state re-derives on load; tmux sessions are unaffected) and needs no spinner because the page unloads synchronously.
**Rejected**: a `TerminalClient` `key`-bump remount to reconnect just the relay (deferred as a possible follow-up); tmux `respawn-pane` (destructive — kills the running process).
*Introduced by*: 260703-p29w-topbar-refresh-button

### Infra servers are greyed, not hidden; identified frontend-side by name
**Decision**: infrastructure tmux servers (`rk-daemon`, `rk-test-*`) are de-emphasized (greyed + sorted-last) but never hidden; they are identified frontend-side by name (`isInfraServer`), not by a backend flag.
**Why**: the backend deliberately surfaces every server so the operator sees exactly what `rk reaper` would reap (the contract at `tmux.go:1332-1341`); greying + sorting-last preserves that visibility while making the infra/workspace distinction legible. A name-based check keeps a pure display concern out of the API, and the socket name is effectively frozen (renaming it orphans deployed daemons).
**Rejected**: hiding infra servers (loses the reaper-visibility contract); a backend `isDaemon` flag on `/api/servers` (API surface for a display concern).
*Introduced by*: 260705-uh8f-deemphasize-infra-servers

### HostMetrics is a shared component
**Decision**: the host metric-row rendering lives in one layout-agnostic `HostMetrics` presentational component consumed by both the sidebar `HostPanel` and the `/` HOST HEALTH zone.
**Why**: the two host surfaces must stay visually consistent; a shared component avoids drift.
**Rejected**: duplicating the ~120 lines across the two surfaces (drift risk).
*Introduced by*: 260701-vshd-cockpit-host-console-home

### Focused-pane context carries thin board-entry data, not just identity
**Decision**: the focused-pane context value is `{ server, windowId, windowName, panes }` (tile identity + the board entry's thin pane data), not the bare `{ server, windowId, cwd }` triple the top-bar slot's `focusedPane` carries. The board route's board-entry enrichment reaches the sidebar PANE fallback through this one channel.
**Why**: the pin-only thin render (a window whose home session died while pinned, so the `windowId` lookup in `sessionsByServer` misses) needs `windowName` + `panes` at the consumer; publishing them with the identity keeps `BottomPanels` free of any board-API knowledge and avoids a second data channel. Server-side enrichment of `GET /api/boards/{name}` was rejected upstream (staleness between `board-changed` refetches + duplicates the live SSE enrichment the home-session copy already delivers), so the fill is a pure client-side join.
**Rejected**: publishing only `{server, windowId}` and having the sidebar fetch/join board entries (reintroduces board-data plumbing into the sidebar plus a fetch the board page already holds); a dedicated thin-render branch inside `WindowPanel` (would duplicate row markup and couple the pure panel to board types — instead the fallback synthesizes a partial `WindowInfo` with `activityTimestamp: 0` and renders through the unchanged `WindowPanel`).
*Introduced by*: 260720-zx4i-board-route-pane-host-panels

### Window-switch feedback stays optimistic
**Decision**: window-switch navigation stays optimistic — the heading/URL flip at click (acknowledged intent) and the sidebar highlight stays SSE-derived (confirmation); the slide plays only on confirmed-fast arrival, with a pending mask + failure bounce-back layered on.
**Why**: keeps the terminal rendering immediately while giving each visual state an honest, distinct signal.
**Rejected**: pessimistic navigation (waits for confirmation before flipping); a dimmed overlay.
*Introduced by*: 260715-38kg-window-switch-confirmed-motion
